\subsection{Mass protection from residual valley symmetry}

We now close the mass-protection question at the theorem level.

\paragraph{Setup.}
Assume that opposite-valley pairing has already been established, so that the isolated shell-relevant doubled block is
\begin{equation}
H_D(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
h_+(p) & 0\\
0 & h_-(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
h_-(p)=-h_+(-p),
\label{eq:HD_block_start}
\end{equation}
and that, after a linear change of momentum coordinates and a shell-adapted basis choice, the linearized crossing takes the standard Weyl-paired form
\begin{equation}
H_D(p)
=
\sum_{i=1}^3 v_i p_i\,\alpha_i,
\qquad
\alpha_i:=\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i.
\label{eq:HD_alpha_form}
\end{equation}
Here \(\sigma_i\) acts on the two-component Weyl doublet at each valley, while \(\tau_i\) acts on the valley pair \((+G_*,-G_*)\).

We also assume that at \(p=0\) each valley carries the same irreducible little-group representation \(\rho\), as required by opposite-valley pairing.

\paragraph{Goal.}
We want to determine all \emph{constant Hermitian operators} on the doubled block that are compatible with the residual symmetries, and then identify which of them are genuine Dirac masses.

\subsubsection{1. Classification of constant little-group-scalar operators}

Let \(K\) be a constant Hermitian operator on the doubled block. Write it in \(2\times 2\) valley-block form:
\begin{equation}
K=
\begin{pmatrix}
A & B\\
B^\dagger & D
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A,D,B\in M_2(\mathbb C).
\label{eq:K_general_block}
\end{equation}
Assume that \(K\) preserves the little-group action at the crossing point. Since the two valley blocks carry the same irreducible representation \(\rho\), Schur's lemma gives
\begin{equation}
A=a_+\,\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
D=a_-\,\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
B=b\,\mathbf 1_2,
\label{eq:Schur_reduction}
\end{equation}
with \(a_\pm\in\mathbb R\) and \(b\in\mathbb C\).
Therefore every little-group-scalar constant Hermitian operator is of the form
\begin{equation}
K
=
a_0\,\mathbf 1_4
+
a_3\,\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_1\,\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_2\,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\label{eq:K_scalar_classification}
\end{equation}
for real coefficients \(a_0,a_3,m_1,m_2\).

Thus the space of symmetry-preserving constant operators is four-dimensional, but only two of them are genuine Dirac-mass candidates.

\begin{lemma}[Classification of constant Dirac masses]
For the kinetic matrices \(\alpha_i=\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i\), the constant Hermitian matrices that anticommute with all \(\alpha_i\) are exactly
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\left\{
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\right\}.
\label{eq:Dirac_mass_space}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Take a general constant Hermitian matrix in block form
\[
M=
\begin{pmatrix}
A & B\\
B^\dagger & D
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
The condition \(\{M,\alpha_i\}=0\) for all \(i=1,2,3\), with
\[
\alpha_i=
\begin{pmatrix}
\sigma_i & 0\\
0 & -\sigma_i
\end{pmatrix},
\]
gives
\begin{equation}
\{A,\sigma_i\}=0,
\qquad
\{D,\sigma_i\}=0,
\qquad
B\sigma_i-\sigma_i B=0,
\qquad
B^\dagger\sigma_i-\sigma_i B^\dagger=0,
\label{eq:anticomm_block_eqs}
\end{equation}
for all \(i\).
Since the Pauli matrices generate \(M_2(\mathbb C)\), the first two conditions imply
\[
A=0,
\qquad
D=0,
\]
while the commutation condition implies
\[
B=b\,\mathbf 1_2
\]
for some \(b\in\mathbb C\).
Hence
\begin{equation}
M=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & b\,\mathbf 1_2\\
\bar b\,\mathbf 1_2 & 0
\end{pmatrix}
=
(\Re b)\,\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
(\Im b)\,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:M_mass_form}
\end{equation}
This proves \eqref{eq:Dirac_mass_space}.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
The terms
\[
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\]
are the \emph{only} constant Hermitian terms that open a genuine Dirac gap on the doubled block.
Indeed, for
\begin{equation}
H_D^{(m)}(p)
=
\sum_i v_i p_i\,\alpha_i
+
m_1\,\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_2\,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\label{eq:massive_HD}
\end{equation}
one has
\begin{equation}
\left(H_D^{(m)}(p)\right)^2
=
\sum_i v_i^2 p_i^2
+
(m_1^2+m_2^2),
\label{eq:massive_square}
\end{equation}
so the spectrum is
\begin{equation}
E(p)=\pm \sqrt{\sum_i v_i^2p_i^2 + m_1^2+m_2^2}.
\label{eq:massive_spectrum}
\end{equation}

By contrast,
\[
\mathbf 1_4
\]
is a trivial overall energy shift, while
\[
\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\]
is a valley-energy splitting term, not a genuine Dirac mass. Such a term must be eliminated separately by the already-isolated opposite-valley matching / energy-locking condition if one wants the crossing exactly at zero energy.

\subsubsection{2. Residual valley symmetry}

Define the valley-charge generator
\begin{equation}
Q_V:=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:Qv_def}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
[Q_V,H_D(p)]=0
\label{eq:Qv_comm_HD}
\end{equation}
for the massless doubled kinetic operator \eqref{eq:HD_alpha_form}. Hence the doubled block has a natural residual valley symmetry
\begin{equation}
\Psi \mapsto U_\theta \Psi,
\qquad
U_\theta:=e^{\,i\theta Q_V/2}.
\label{eq:valley_U1}
\end{equation}

Now compute the transformation of the two mass generators:
\begin{equation}
U_\theta
(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
U_\theta^{-1}
=
\cos\theta\,(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
+
\sin\theta\,(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2),
\label{eq:taux_rotation}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
U_\theta
(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
U_\theta^{-1}
=
-\sin\theta\,(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
+
\cos\theta\,(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2).
\label{eq:tauy_rotation}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
U_\theta
\bigl((\tau_x\pm i\tau_y)\otimes \mathbf 1_2\bigr)
U_\theta^{-1}
=
e^{\pm i\theta}
\bigl((\tau_x\pm i\tau_y)\otimes \mathbf 1_2\bigr).
\label{eq:charged_mass_ops}
\end{equation}
Thus the Dirac-mass operators carry nonzero valley charge.

Therefore, if the residual valley \(U(1)_V\) symmetry is exact, any constant Dirac mass term is forbidden.

\begin{theorem}[Mass protection from residual valley symmetry]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the low-energy doubled shell block has the form \eqref{eq:HD_alpha_form};
\item the constant operator under consideration preserves the little-group action at \(p=0\);
\item the residual valley symmetry generated by \(Q_V=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2\) is exact on the isolated doubled block.
\end{enumerate}
Then every symmetry-allowed constant Hermitian operator on the doubled block is of the form
\begin{equation}
K
=
a_0\,\mathbf 1_4
+
a_3\,\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\label{eq:K_no_mass}
\end{equation}
and in particular the Dirac-mass coefficients vanish:
\begin{equation}
m_1=m_2=0.
\label{eq:masses_zero}
\end{equation}
Hence no constant Dirac mass term is allowed, i.e. mass protection holds.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By \eqref{eq:K_scalar_classification}, every constant little-group-scalar Hermitian operator is
\[
K=a_0\,\mathbf 1_4+a_3\,\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2+m_1\,\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2+m_2\,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]
Exact \(U(1)_V\) invariance requires
\[
U_\theta K U_\theta^{-1}=K
\qquad
\text{for all }\theta.
\]
The terms proportional to \(\mathbf 1_4\) and \(\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2\) are invariant, while
\eqref{eq:taux_rotation}--\eqref{eq:charged_mass_ops} show that the pair
\[
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\qquad \tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\]
rotates nontrivially and is therefore not invariant unless
\[
m_1=m_2=0.
\]
By Lemma \eqref{eq:Dirac_mass_space}, these are precisely all genuine constant Dirac masses. Hence they are all forbidden.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Weaker version.}
The full continuous \(U(1)_V\) is stronger than necessary. The discrete remnant
\begin{equation}
S_V:=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
S_V^2=\mathbf 1_4,
\label{eq:Zv_generator}
\end{equation}
already suffices, because
\begin{equation}
S_V(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)S_V^{-1}
=
-(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2),
\qquad
S_V(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2)S_V^{-1}
=
-(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2).
\label{eq:Z2_forbidden_mass}
\end{equation}
So an exact residual \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) also forbids all constant Dirac masses.

\subsubsection{3. Stability under remote-sector elimination}

We now show that the same symmetry protects against radiatively induced constant masses from the remote sector.

Let the full Hamiltonian be decomposed as
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V(p)^\dagger\\
V(p) & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:Hfull_DR}
\end{equation}
where \(H_R\) is the remote sector and \(V\) is the coupling between the doubled shell block and the remote sector.

Assume that the full microscopic theory preserves the residual valley symmetry, meaning that there exists a unitary action \(U_\theta\oplus U_{R,\theta}\) such that
\begin{equation}
(U_\theta\oplus U_{R,\theta})
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)
(U_\theta\oplus U_{R,\theta})^{-1}
=
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p).
\label{eq:full_valley_sym}
\end{equation}
Then the Schur-complement effective shell Hamiltonian
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(p,\omega)
=
H_D(p)
+
V(p)^\dagger
\bigl(\omega-H_R(p)\bigr)^{-1}
V(p)
\label{eq:Heff_Schur}
\end{equation}
inherits the same symmetry:
\begin{equation}
U_\theta H_{\mathrm{eff}}(p,\omega) U_\theta^{-1}
=
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(p,\omega).
\label{eq:Heff_valley_sym}
\end{equation}
In particular, the zero-momentum self-energy
\begin{equation}
\Sigma(0,0):=
V(0)^\dagger \bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}V(0)
\label{eq:Sigma00}
\end{equation}
must commute with \(Q_V\):
\begin{equation}
[Q_V,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
\label{eq:Sigma_comm_Qv}
\end{equation}

If we also impose little-group scalarity at the crossing point, then by the same Schur/representation argument
\begin{equation}
\Sigma(0,0)
=
a_0\,\mathbf 1_4
+
a_3\,\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:Sigma_allowed}
\end{equation}
Hence no radiatively generated term proportional to
\[
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\quad\text{or}\quad
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\]
can appear.

\begin{corollary}[Radiative stability of mass protection]
If the residual valley symmetry is exact in the full microscopic theory and remote-sector elimination preserves that symmetry, then no symmetry-preserving self-energy correction can generate a constant Dirac mass on the isolated doubled shell block.
\end{corollary}

\paragraph{Exact logical status.}
This closes the mass-protection problem at the theorem level, \emph{provided} the residual valley symmetry is exact.
What still remains open is the microscopic identification of that residual symmetry in the full TECT/Class II realization.

So the honest conclusion is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Residual valley symmetry }(\,U(1)_V\text{ or }\mathbb Z_2^V\,)
\Longrightarrow
\text{all constant Dirac masses are forbidden.}
}
\label{eq:mass_protection_closed}
\end{equation}

\[
\mathcal H_D = \mathcal H_+ \oplus \mathcal H_-,
\qquad
H_D(p)=\sum_i v_i p_i\,(\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i).
\]

\[
\mathrm{End}_{G_*}(\mathcal H_D)_{\mathrm{const}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{
\mathbf 1_4,\,
\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\}.
\]

\[
\mathcal M_D
=
\left\{
M:\{M,\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i\}=0\ \forall i
\right\}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\}.
\]

If the residual symmetry generated by
\[
Q_V=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\]
is exact, then
\[
[Q_V,H_{\mathrm eff}(p,\omega)]=0,
\]
hence the symmetry-allowed constant sector reduces to
\[
\mathrm{End}_{G_*\cap U(1)_V}(\mathcal H_D)_{\mathrm{const}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{
\mathbf 1_4,\,
\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\}.
\]
Therefore
\[
\mathcal M_D
\cap
\mathrm{End}_{G_*\cap U(1)_V}(\mathcal H_D)_{\mathrm{const}}
=
\{0\}.
\]

Hence all genuine constant Dirac masses are forbidden:
\[
m_1=m_2=0.
\]

So:
\[
\boxed{
\text{exact residual valley symmetry}
\Longrightarrow
\text{mass protection}
}
\]
with radiative stability under symmetry-preserving remote-sector elimination.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\mathcal H_D = \mathcal H_+ \oplus \mathcal H_-,
\qquad
H_D(p)=\sum_i v_i p_i\,(\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i).
\]

\[
\mathrm{End}_{G_*}(\mathcal H_D)_{\mathrm{const}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{
\mathbf 1_4,\,
\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\}.
\]

\[
\mathcal M_D
=
\left\{
M:\{M,\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i\}=0\ \forall i
\right\}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\}.
\]

If the residual symmetry generated by
\[
Q_V=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\]
is exact, then
\[
[Q_V,H_{\mathrm eff}(p,\omega)]=0,
\]
hence the symmetry-allowed constant sector reduces to
\[
\mathrm{End}_{G_*\cap U(1)_V}(\mathcal H_D)_{\mathrm{const}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{
\mathbf 1_4,\,
\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\}.
\]
Therefore
\[
\mathcal M_D
\cap
\mathrm{End}_{G_*\cap U(1)_V}(\mathcal H_D)_{\mathrm{const}}
=
\{0\}.
\]

Hence all genuine constant Dirac masses are forbidden:
\[
m_1=m_2=0.
\]

So:
\[
\boxed{
\text{exact residual valley symmetry}
\Longrightarrow
\text{mass protection}
}
\]
with radiative stability under symmetry-preserving remote-sector elimination.

\subsection{Little-group mismatch implies \(V(0)=0\)}

\paragraph{Important correction of notation.}
In the spectral-isolation decomposition,
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V(p)\\
V(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:Hfull_block}
\end{equation}
the symbol \(V(p)\) denotes the \emph{off-diagonal inter-sector mixing block}, not a vacuum-energy scalar.
Thus \(V(0)=0\) means \emph{absence of constant hybridization at the crossing}, not vanishing vacuum energy.

\paragraph{Setup.}
Let \(H_\ast\) be the little group at the selected shell crossing \(p=0\).
Assume that the full Hilbert space decomposes as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}=\mathcal H_D\oplus \mathcal H_R,
\label{eq:Hfull_split}
\end{equation}
where

\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathcal H_D\) is the isolated doubled shell block carrying the local Dirac sector,
\item \(\mathcal H_R\) is the orthogonal remote sector.
\end{itemize}

Assume further that \(H_\ast\) acts unitarily and preserves this decomposition:
\begin{equation}
U(h)\mathcal H_D\subset \mathcal H_D,
\qquad
U(h)\mathcal H_R\subset \mathcal H_R,
\qquad h\in H_\ast.
\label{eq:Hstar_invariant_split}
\end{equation}
Thus we obtain restricted representations
\begin{equation}
U_D(h):=U(h)|_{\mathcal H_D},
\qquad
U_R(h):=U(h)|_{\mathcal H_R}.
\label{eq:UD_UR_def}
\end{equation}

At \(p=0\), write the Hamiltonian in block form:
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(0) & V(0)\\
V(0)^\dagger & H_R(0)
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:H0_block}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Equivariance hypothesis.}
Assume that the microscopic Hamiltonian is \(H_\ast\)-equivariant at the crossing:
\begin{equation}
U(h)\,H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)\,U(h)^{-1}=H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)
\qquad
\forall h\in H_\ast.
\label{eq:H0_equivariance}
\end{equation}

\begin{lemma}[The constant mixing block is an intertwiner]
Under \eqref{eq:Hstar_invariant_split} and \eqref{eq:H0_equivariance}, the off-diagonal block satisfies
\begin{equation}
U_D(h)\,V(0)\,U_R(h)^{-1}=V(0)
\qquad
\forall h\in H_\ast,
\label{eq:V0_intertwiner_eq}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_\ast}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
\label{eq:V0_in_Hom}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Since the decomposition \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}=\mathcal H_D\oplus\mathcal H_R\) is \(H_\ast\)-invariant, the symmetry operator has block form
\[
U(h)=
\begin{pmatrix}
U_D(h) & 0\\
0 & U_R(h)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Substituting this and \eqref{eq:H0_block} into \eqref{eq:H0_equivariance}, we obtain
\[
\begin{pmatrix}
U_D(h) & 0\\
0 & U_R(h)
\end{pmatrix}
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(0) & V(0)\\
V(0)^\dagger & H_R(0)
\end{pmatrix}
\begin{pmatrix}
U_D(h)^{-1} & 0\\
0 & U_R(h)^{-1}
\end{pmatrix}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(0) & V(0)\\
V(0)^\dagger & H_R(0)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Comparing the off-diagonal block gives
\[
U_D(h)\,V(0)\,U_R(h)^{-1}=V(0)
\]
for all \(h\in H_\ast\), which is exactly the condition that \(V(0)\) be an \(H_\ast\)-intertwiner.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Irreducible decomposition.}
Let \(\{W_\lambda\}_\lambda\) be a complete set of inequivalent irreducible \(H_\ast\)-modules.
Write the isotypic decompositions
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_D \cong \bigoplus_\lambda m_\lambda^{(D)}\,W_\lambda,
\qquad
\mathcal H_R \cong \bigoplus_\lambda m_\lambda^{(R)}\,W_\lambda,
\label{eq:isotypic_decomp}
\end{equation}
where \(m_\lambda^{(D)},m_\lambda^{(R)}\in \mathbb N_0\) are multiplicities.

Then standard representation theory yields
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_\ast}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)
\cong
\bigoplus_\lambda
\mathrm{Mat}_{\,m_\lambda^{(D)}\times m_\lambda^{(R)}}(\mathbb C).
\label{eq:Hom_decomposition}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_\ast}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
m_\lambda^{(D)}m_\lambda^{(R)}=0
\ \text{for all }\lambda.
\label{eq:Hom_zero_iff}
\end{equation}

This is the precise algebraic meaning of \emph{little-group mismatch}.

\begin{theorem}[Little-group mismatch implies \(V(0)=0\)]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)\) is \(H_\ast\)-equivariant;
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}=\mathcal H_D\oplus\mathcal H_R\) is an \(H_\ast\)-invariant decomposition;
\item \(\mathcal H_D\) and \(\mathcal H_R\) have no common irreducible \(H_\ast\)-component, equivalently
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_\ast}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0.
\label{eq:LG_mismatch_assumption}
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}
Then
\begin{equation}
V(0)=0.
\label{eq:V0_zero_main}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By the intertwiner lemma, \(V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_\ast}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)\).
By assumption \eqref{eq:LG_mismatch_assumption}, this Hom-space is zero.
Hence \(V(0)=0\).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Irreducible special case]
If \(\mathcal H_D\) and \(\mathcal H_R\) are irreducible \(H_\ast\)-modules and
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_D \not\cong \mathcal H_R,
\label{eq:irrep_mismatch}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
V(0)=0.
\label{eq:V0_zero_irred}
\end{equation}
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Schur's lemma,
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_\ast}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\]
for inequivalent irreducible modules. Apply the theorem.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{First nontrivial order in momentum.}
Once \(V(0)=0\), the leading mixing begins at higher order in \(p\).
If the momentum vector transforms in the little-group representation \(R_p\), then the linear coefficient must lie in
\begin{equation}
V_i \in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_\ast}(R_p\otimes \mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
\label{eq:linear_mixing_Hom}
\end{equation}
Therefore:

\begin{itemize}
\item if \(\mathrm{Hom}_{H_\ast}(R_p\otimes \mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0\), then
\begin{equation}
V(p)=O(|p|^2);
\label{eq:Vp_quadratic}
\end{equation}

\item if this Hom-space is nonzero, then generically
\begin{equation}
V(p)=O(|p|).
\label{eq:Vp_linear}
\end{equation}
\end{itemize}

In either case, together with a remote spectral gap \(\Delta>0\), one obtains the Schur-complement estimate
\begin{equation}
\Sigma(E,p)
=
V(p)\bigl(H_R(p)-E\bigr)^{-1}V(p)^\dagger
=
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right)
\label{eq:self_energy_bound}
\end{equation}
whenever \(V(p)=O(|p|)\).

\paragraph{Important honesty clause.}
The statement
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_\ast}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)
=
\mathrm{Hom}(H_{R,\mathrm{shell}},H_{D,\mathrm{shell}})
\otimes
\mathrm{Hom}(H_{R,\mathrm{int}},H_{D,\mathrm{int}})
\label{eq:Hom_factorized_unsafe}
\end{equation}
is \emph{not} a general identity.
It is valid only under an additional product-group/product-representation assumption, e.g. if
\[
H_\ast=G_1\times G_2,
\qquad
\mathcal H_D \cong D_1\boxtimes D_2,
\qquad
\mathcal H_R \cong R_1\boxtimes R_2.
\]
Without such an assumption, the correct and fully general theorem is the intertwiner theorem above.

\paragraph{Conclusion.}
The exact theorem-level closure is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_\ast}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
V(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:V0_closure_box}
\end{equation}
This is the precise content of the little-group mismatch condition.

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(0) & V(0)\\
V(0)^\dagger & H_R(0)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}=\mathcal H_D\oplus \mathcal H_R .
\]

If the little group \(H_\ast\) acts unitarily and
\[
U(h)\,H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)\,U(h)^{-1}=H_{\mathrm{full}}(0),
\qquad
U(h)\mathcal H_D\subset \mathcal H_D,
\quad
U(h)\mathcal H_R\subset \mathcal H_R,
\]
then
\[
U_D(h)V(0)U_R(h)^{-1}=V(0),
\]
so
\[
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_\ast}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
\]

Writing
\[
\mathcal H_D \cong \bigoplus_\lambda m_\lambda^{(D)} W_\lambda,
\qquad
\mathcal H_R \cong \bigoplus_\lambda m_\lambda^{(R)} W_\lambda,
\]
one has
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_\ast}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)
\cong
\bigoplus_\lambda
\mathrm{Mat}_{m_\lambda^{(D)}\times m_\lambda^{(R)}}(\mathbb C).
\]

Hence
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_\ast}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
m_\lambda^{(D)}m_\lambda^{(R)}=0
\ \text{for all }\lambda.
\]

Therefore the little-group mismatch condition
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_\ast}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
}
\]
implies
\[
\boxed{
V(0)=0.
}
\]

Once \(V(0)=0\), the linear mixing coefficient belongs to
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_\ast}(R_p\otimes \mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
\]
Thus generically
\[
V(p)=O(|p|),
\]
and with a remote gap \(\Delta>0\),
\[
\Sigma(E,p)=V(p)(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}V(p)^\dagger
=
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right).
\]

So the theorem-level closure is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{little-group mismatch}
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0
\Longrightarrow
\text{no constant hybridization at the crossing.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Remote-gap positivity as an independent spectral input}

\paragraph{Logical goal.}
We now close the statement
\[
\Delta>0
\]
in the precise theorem-level form that is actually justified by the current TECT framework.

The correct statement is not that the Class II correction \emph{creates} a remote gap automatically.
Rather, the remote gap is an \emph{independent spectral property} of the remote sector, and the Class II correction is compatible with it and preserves it under a small bounded perturbation.

\paragraph{Remote-sector definition.}
Let the full microscopic Hamiltonian be decomposed as
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V(p)\\
V(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:full_block_gap}
\end{equation}
where \(H_D(p)\) is the isolated doubled shell Dirac block and \(H_R(p)\) is the remote sector.

The remote-gap condition is
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap (-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing
\qquad
\text{for all sufficiently small }p.
\label{eq:remote_gap_condition}
\end{equation}

This is the correct spectral statement already isolated in the TECT Dirac program.

\subsubsection{A. Why a positive shell determinant does not by itself prove \(\Delta>0\)}

Let
\begin{equation}
\det M = A(B^2+C^2)
\label{eq:detM_shell}
\end{equation}
be the shell-level Weyl/Dirac determinant of the enriched local block.
This quantity controls the nondegeneracy of the projected shell Dirac symbol, but it does \emph{not} determine the full spectrum of the complementary operator \(H_R\).

Indeed, two distinct operators may have the same shell-level determinant \(\det M\) while having different remote spectra.
Therefore any positivity statement of the form
\[
\delta(\det M)>0
\]
can at most be regarded as a compatibility or heuristic indication, not as a theorem proving
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R)\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing.
\]

Hence the theorem-level route to \(\Delta>0\) must be spectral, not determinant-based.

\subsubsection{B. Unperturbed remote gap}

Assume there exists an unperturbed microscopic realization with block decomposition
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}^{(0)}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D^{(0)}(p) & V^{(0)}(p)\\
V^{(0)}(p)^\dagger & H_R^{(0)}(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:H0_decomp}
\end{equation}
and suppose the remote sector has a uniform positive gap:
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{(0)}(p))\cap (-\Delta_0,\Delta_0)=\varnothing
\qquad
\text{for all sufficiently small }p,
\label{eq:unpert_remote_gap}
\end{equation}
for some \(\Delta_0>0\).

This is the genuine microscopic input.

\subsubsection{C. Class II correction as a bounded perturbation}

Now perturb the theory by a self-adjoint Class II correction:
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)=H_{\mathrm{full}}^{(0)}(p)+\delta H(p),
\label{eq:full_plus_delta}
\end{equation}
and write the remote block as
\begin{equation}
H_R(p)=H_R^{(0)}(p)+\delta H_R(p).
\label{eq:HR_pert}
\end{equation}

Assume that the remote correction is uniformly bounded in operator norm:
\begin{equation}
\sup_{|p|\le p_*}\|\delta H_R(p)\|\le \varepsilon.
\label{eq:deltaHR_bound}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Remote-gap stability under bounded perturbation]
Assume \eqref{eq:unpert_remote_gap} and \eqref{eq:deltaHR_bound}.
If
\begin{equation}
\varepsilon<\Delta_0,
\label{eq:eps_less_gap}
\end{equation}
then the perturbed remote sector still satisfies a positive uniform gap
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta:=\Delta_0-\varepsilon>0,
\label{eq:perturbed_gap_positive}
\end{equation}
for all sufficiently small \(p\).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Fix \(p\) in the allowed small-momentum region and let \(\lambda\in\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\).
By standard spectral stability for self-adjoint bounded perturbations,
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(\lambda,\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{(0)}(p))\bigr)\le \|\delta H_R(p)\|.
\label{eq:spectral_variation}
\end{equation}
Since \(\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{(0)}(p))\) avoids \((-\Delta_0,\Delta_0)\), every point of the unperturbed spectrum has absolute value at least \(\Delta_0\).
Therefore any point of the perturbed spectrum must satisfy
\begin{equation}
|\lambda|
\ge
\Delta_0-\|\delta H_R(p)\|
\ge
\Delta_0-\varepsilon
=
\Delta.
\label{eq:abs_lambda_gap}
\end{equation}
Since \(\Delta>0\), we conclude
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing.
\]
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Immediate corollary (the P6 compatibility form).}
If one imposes the stronger smallness condition
\begin{equation}
\|\delta H_R\|<\frac{\Delta_0}{2},
\label{eq:half_gap_bound}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\Delta\ge \Delta_0-\|\delta H_R\|>\frac{\Delta_0}{2}>0.
\label{eq:half_gap_positive}
\end{equation}
This is the exact theorem-level meaning of the earlier ``Class II is gap-compatible'' statement.

\subsubsection{D. Resolvent bound in the low-energy window}

Let \(E\) satisfy
\begin{equation}
|E|<\frac{\Delta}{2}.
\label{eq:E_window}
\end{equation}
Then by \eqref{eq:perturbed_gap_positive},
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(E,\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\bigr)\ge \frac{\Delta}{2},
\label{eq:dist_to_spec}
\end{equation}
hence the resolvent is well-defined and obeys
\begin{equation}
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|\le \frac{2}{\Delta}.
\label{eq:resolvent_bound}
\end{equation}

This is the exact place where the remote gap enters the Schur-complement control of the low-energy Dirac block.

\subsubsection{E. Independence of the leading Dirac cone}

Assume in addition that
\begin{equation}
V(0)=0,
\qquad
\|V(p)\|\le c|p|
\label{eq:V_small_gap}
\end{equation}
for small \(p\).
Then the Schur complement gives the effective low-energy operator
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
H_D(p)-\Sigma(E,p),
\qquad
\Sigma(E,p):=
V(p)(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}V(p)^\dagger.
\label{eq:Heff_gap}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:resolvent_bound} and \eqref{eq:V_small_gap},
\begin{equation}
\|\Sigma(E,p)\|
\le
\|V(p)\|^2\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|
\le
\frac{2c^2}{\Delta}|p|^2.
\label{eq:sigma_gap_bound}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)=H_D(p)+O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right).
\label{eq:Heff_preserved}
\end{equation}
So the remote sector affects the low-energy Dirac cone only through subleading curvature corrections.
In this precise sense, the positive remote gap is \emph{independent} of the shell-level linear Dirac structure.

\subsubsection{F. Honest TECT conclusion}

The theorem-level status is therefore:

\begin{enumerate}
\item The existence of a remote spectral gap \(\Delta>0\) is an independent microscopic spectral check.
\item The Class II correction does not by itself prove the existence of that gap.
\item If an already-gapped realization exists and the Class II correction is sufficiently small in operator norm, then the positive remote gap persists.
\item Once this gap persists, the remote sector contributes only \(O(|p|^2/\Delta)\) corrections to the isolated Dirac block.
\end{enumerate}

Hence the mathematically honest closure is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_0>0
\ \text{for the unperturbed remote sector}
\quad + \quad
\|\delta H_R\|<\Delta_0
\ \Longrightarrow\
\Delta\ge \Delta_0-\|\delta H_R\|>0.
}
\label{eq:final_remote_gap_box}
\end{equation}

%%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V(p)\\
V(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing .
\]

The remote-gap condition is a spectral property of \(H_R\), not a consequence of the shell-level determinant
\[
\det M=A(B^2+C^2).
\]

Assume an unperturbed realization
\[
H_R^{(0)}(p)
\]
with
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{(0)}(p))\cap(-\Delta_0,\Delta_0)=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta_0>0,
\]
and a bounded Class II correction
\[
H_R(p)=H_R^{(0)}(p)+\delta H_R(p),
\qquad
\sup_{|p|\le p_*}\|\delta H_R(p)\|\le \varepsilon.
\]

Then, if
\[
\varepsilon<\Delta_0,
\]
the perturbed remote sector still has a positive gap
\[
\Delta=\Delta_0-\varepsilon>0,
\qquad
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing.
\]

For \(|E|<\Delta/2\),
\[
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|\le \frac{2}{\Delta}.
\]

If also
\[
V(0)=0,
\qquad
\|V(p)\|\le c|p|,
\]
then the Schur-complement self-energy satisfies
\[
\Sigma(E,p)=V(p)(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}V(p)^\dagger,
\qquad
\|\Sigma(E,p)\|\le \frac{2c^2}{\Delta}|p|^2,
\]
hence
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)=H_D(p)+O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right).
\]

Therefore:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the remote gap is an independent microscopic spectral input,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{Class II preserves it under sufficiently small bounded perturbations,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{and the gapped remote sector modifies the Dirac block only at }O(|p|^2/\Delta).
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Final Spectral Isolation Theorem}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now combine the three independently closed ingredients

\[
V(0)=0,
\qquad
\Delta>0,
\qquad
\text{mass protection},
\]

into a single theorem proving spectral isolation of the local doubled Dirac block and stability of the massless Dirac cone.

\subsubsection{A. Local doubled Dirac block}

Assume that an opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\) exists and that the shell-relevant doubled block has already been reduced to the \(4\times 4\) Dirac form
\begin{equation}
H_D(p)=\Gamma_i (Mp)_i,
\label{eq:HD_local_final}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\{\Gamma_i,\Gamma_j\}=2\delta_{ij},
\qquad
M\in M_{3\times 3}(\mathbb R),
\qquad
\det M\neq 0.
\label{eq:Gamma_M_nondeg}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, in the coefficient language used in the shell-level reduction,
\begin{equation}
M=
\begin{pmatrix}
B & -C & 0\\
C & B & 0\\
0 & 0 & A
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\det M=A(B^2+C^2)\neq 0.
\label{eq:M_ABC_final}
\end{equation}
Hence the isolated shell block is a nondegenerate massless Dirac block.

\subsubsection{B. Full microscopic block decomposition}

Let the full microscopic Hamiltonian near the selected crossing be written as
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V(p)\\
V(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:Hfull_final_block}
\end{equation}
where \(H_D\) acts on the local four-dimensional doubled shell sector \(\mathcal H_D\), and \(H_R\) acts on the remote complement \(\mathcal H_R\).

\subsubsection{C. Three structural inputs, now theorem-level}

We now insert the three conditions in their theorem-level form.

\paragraph{(C1) Zero constant mixing from little-group mismatch.}
Assume the little group \(H_*\) at \(p=0\) preserves the decomposition
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}=\mathcal H_D\oplus \mathcal H_R,
\]
and that
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0.
\label{eq:LG_mismatch_final}
\end{equation}
Then the constant mixing block must vanish:
\begin{equation}
V(0)=0.
\label{eq:V0_final}
\end{equation}
Moreover, the first nontrivial term is at least linear:
\begin{equation}
\|V(p)\|\le c|p|
\qquad
\text{for small }p.
\label{eq:Vp_linear_final}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(C2) Positive remote gap from independent spectral input.}
Assume the unperturbed remote sector \(H_R^{(0)}(p)\) has a positive gap \(\Delta_0>0\):
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{(0)}(p))\cap(-\Delta_0,\Delta_0)=\varnothing
\qquad
\text{for }|p|\le p_*,
\label{eq:gap0_final}
\end{equation}
and the correction satisfies
\begin{equation}
H_R(p)=H_R^{(0)}(p)+\delta H_R(p),
\qquad
\sup_{|p|\le p_*}\|\delta H_R(p)\|\le \varepsilon<\Delta_0.
\label{eq:deltaHR_final}
\end{equation}
Then the corrected remote sector still has a positive gap
\begin{equation}
\Delta:=\Delta_0-\varepsilon>0,
\qquad
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing.
\label{eq:gap_final}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(C3) Mass protection from residual valley symmetry.}
Assume the local doubled shell block carries an exact residual symmetry generated by
\begin{equation}
Q_V=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\label{eq:Qv_final}
\end{equation}
or an equivalent \(\mathbb Z_2\) remnant, such that all constant Dirac masses are forbidden.
Equivalently, for the constant Hermitian mass space
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\},
\label{eq:mass_space_final}
\end{equation}
one has
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M_D\cap \mathcal A_{\mathrm{res}}=\{0\},
\label{eq:mass_forbidden_final}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal A_{\mathrm{res}}\) is the algebra of symmetry-allowed constant operators.
Hence no constant Dirac mass is generated.

\subsubsection{D. Schur-complement reduction}

Fix an energy window
\begin{equation}
|E|<\frac{\Delta}{2}.
\label{eq:Ewindow_final}
\end{equation}
Then the remote resolvent exists and satisfies
\begin{equation}
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|\le \frac{2}{\Delta}.
\label{eq:resolvent_final}
\end{equation}
Therefore the Schur-complement effective Hamiltonian on \(\mathcal H_D\) is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
H_D(p)-\Sigma(E,p),
\qquad
\Sigma(E,p):=
V(p)(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}V(p)^\dagger.
\label{eq:Heff_final_def}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:Vp_linear_final} and \eqref{eq:resolvent_final},
\begin{equation}
\|\Sigma(E,p)\|
\le
\|V(p)\|^2\,\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|
\le
\frac{2c^2}{\Delta}|p|^2.
\label{eq:Sigma_final_bound}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
H_D(p)+O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right).
\label{eq:Heff_quadratic_final}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{E. Exclusion of a generated mass term}

The estimate \eqref{eq:Heff_quadratic_final} alone still allows, in principle, a constant \(O(1)\) contribution if symmetry permits it.
However, by \eqref{eq:mass_forbidden_final}, all symmetry-allowed constant Dirac masses vanish.
Therefore the effective Hamiltonian has no constant mass deformation:
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(0,0)=0
\quad
\text{in the Dirac-mass channel}.
\label{eq:no_mass_final}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{F. Final theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Final Spectral Isolation Theorem]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the local opposite-valley doubled shell block exists and has the nondegenerate Dirac form \eqref{eq:HD_local_final} with \(\det M\neq 0\);
\item the little-group mismatch condition \eqref{eq:LG_mismatch_final} holds, hence \(V(0)=0\) and \(\|V(p)\|\le c|p|\);
\item the remote sector has a positive uniform gap \(\Delta>0\) in the sense of \eqref{eq:gap_final};
\item a residual symmetry excludes all constant Dirac masses as in \eqref{eq:mass_forbidden_final}.
\end{enumerate}
Then, for sufficiently small \(p\) and \(|E|<\Delta/2\), the full microscopic Hamiltonian contains a spectrally isolated four-dimensional low-energy sector whose effective Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
\Gamma_i(Mp)_i
+
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right).
\label{eq:Final_Spectral_Isolation}
\end{equation}
In particular, the full theory contains a stable massless Dirac cone.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Item (1) gives a nondegenerate local massless Dirac block.
Item (2) removes constant inter-sector hybridization and makes the first nontrivial mixing at least linear in \(p\).
Item (3) gives the resolvent bound \eqref{eq:resolvent_final}.
Therefore the Schur-complement correction is quadratic in \(p\), as in \eqref{eq:Sigma_final_bound}, and the effective Hamiltonian differs from the local Dirac block only by \(O(|p|^2/\Delta)\).
Item (4) excludes all symmetry-allowed constant Dirac mass terms, so no \(O(1)\) gap can be generated.
Hence the leading linear Dirac cone survives and remains spectrally isolated from all remote states.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Dirac Emergence Closure Theorem}

We now combine the spectral-isolation theorem with the shell-level nonvanishing conditions.

\begin{theorem}[Dirac Emergence Closure Theorem]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the shell-level witness conditions hold:
\begin{equation}
\widehat U(G_*)=0,
\qquad
v_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
PVT^{(1)}\neq 0,
\qquad
PVT^{(2)}\neq 0;
\label{eq:witness_final}
\end{equation}
\item the hypotheses of the Final Spectral Isolation Theorem hold.
\end{enumerate}
Then the full TECT linearized theory contains a stable low-energy massless Dirac fermion with effective Hamiltonian
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{Dirac}}(p)
=
\Gamma_i(Mp)_i
+
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right),
\qquad
\{\Gamma_i,\Gamma_j\}=2\delta_{ij},
\qquad
\det M\neq 0.
\label{eq:Dirac_Closure_final}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The shell-level witness conditions imply the existence of the nondegenerate local massless Dirac block.
The Final Spectral Isolation Theorem shows that this block remains spectrally isolated and is corrected only at quadratic order by remote states.
Therefore the full low-energy theory contains a stable massless Dirac cone.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Exact logical status.}
What is now genuinely closed is the theorem-level implication
\[
\text{(shell Dirac block)}
+
\text{(little-group mismatch)}
+
\text{(remote-gap positivity)}
+
\text{(mass protection)}
\Longrightarrow
\text{stable massless Dirac cone}.
\]
What may still remain open in an actual microscopic realization is only the direct verification of the input hypotheses from the final TECT linearization.

%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V(p)\\
V(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
H_D(p)=\Gamma_i(Mp)_i,
\qquad
\det M\neq 0.
\]

If
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0,
\]
then
\[
V(0)=0,
\qquad
\|V(p)\|\le c|p|.
\]

If the remote sector satisfies
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing,
\]
then for \(|E|<\Delta/2\),
\[
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|\le \frac{2}{\Delta}.
\]

Hence the Schur-complement self-energy obeys
\[
\Sigma(E,p)=V(p)(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}V(p)^\dagger,
\qquad
\|\Sigma(E,p)\|
\le
\frac{2c^2}{\Delta}|p|^2.
\]

If, in addition, a residual symmetry forbids all constant Dirac masses, then
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
H_D(p)-\Sigma(E,p)
=
\Gamma_i(Mp)_i
+
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right),
\]
with no generated constant mass term.

Therefore:
\[
\boxed{
\text{local nondegenerate Dirac block}
+
\text{little-group mismatch}
+
\text{positive remote gap}
+
\text{mass protection}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\Longrightarrow
\text{spectrally isolated stable massless Dirac cone.}
}
\]

Combining this with the shell-level witness conditions
\[
\widehat U(G_*)=0,
\qquad
v_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
PVT^{(1)}\neq 0,
\qquad
PVT^{(2)}\neq 0,
\]
one obtains the final closure theorem:
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{Dirac}}(p)
=
\Gamma_i(Mp)_i
+
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right),
\qquad
\det M\neq 0.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Witness-to-Weyl theorem for the BCC shell pair}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now turn the remaining local valley-existence problem into a finite-dimensional witness problem.
The objective is to prove that once one constructs

\begin{enumerate}
\item one admissible longitudinal witness, and
\item one admissible transverse witness,
\end{enumerate}

inside the actual symmetry-allowed microscopic tensor space, the local BCC shell crossing is generically Weyl.

\subsubsection{A. Allowed microscopic tensor space and witness functionals}

Fix a selected opposite BCC shell pair \(\pm G_*\), and let
\[
\hat n:=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|}
\]
be the distinguished axis, together with an adapted orthonormal transverse frame
\[
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\}.
\]

Let \(V\) denote the finite-dimensional real vector space of symmetry-allowed microscopic shell tensors contributing to the first-order enriched shell Hamiltonian near \(G_*\).
The shell-projected first-order operator has the form
\begin{equation}
\delta L_{\mathrm{enr}}^{(1)}
=
g_{\parallel} O_{\parallel}
+
g_I O_I
+
g_J O_J,
\label{eq:deltaL_witness}
\end{equation}
where \(O_{\parallel},O_I,O_J\) are the shell-adapted basis operators.

Define the dual witness functionals
\begin{equation}
W_{\parallel}(X):=\langle O_{\parallel},X\rangle,
\qquad
W_I(X):=\frac12\langle O_I,X\rangle,
\qquad
W_J(X):=\frac12\langle O_J,X\rangle.
\label{eq:witness_functionals}
\end{equation}
Then, by construction,
\begin{equation}
W_{\parallel}(\delta L_{\mathrm{enr}}^{(1)})=g_{\parallel},
\qquad
W_I(\delta L_{\mathrm{enr}}^{(1)})=g_I,
\qquad
W_J(\delta L_{\mathrm{enr}}^{(1)})=g_J.
\label{eq:witness_extract_coeffs}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Weyl determinant in witness form}

The local shell Weyl determinant is
\begin{equation}
\det M
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3
\,W_{\parallel}(X)
\bigl(
W_I(X)^2+W_J(X)^2
\bigr).
\label{eq:detM_witness_form}
\end{equation}
Therefore the shell crossing is Weyl exactly when
\begin{equation}
W_{\parallel}(X)\neq 0,
\qquad
\bigl(W_I(X),W_J(X)\bigr)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:weyl_criterion_witness}
\end{equation}

Define the transverse polynomial
\begin{equation}
D_{\perp}(X):=W_I(X)^2+W_J(X)^2.
\label{eq:Dperp_def}
\end{equation}
Then the Weyl condition is equivalently
\begin{equation}
W_{\parallel}(X)\neq 0,
\qquad
D_{\perp}(X)\neq 0.
\label{eq:weyl_criterion_compact}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. Two witness existence theorem}

We now prove the main reduction theorem.

\begin{theorem}[Two-witness generic Weyl theorem]
Let \(V\) be the finite-dimensional real vector space of symmetry-allowed microscopic shell tensors near the selected BCC shell pair.
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item there exists \(N^{(\parallel)}\in V\) such that
\begin{equation}
W_{\parallel}\!\bigl(N^{(\parallel)}\bigr)\neq 0;
\label{eq:longitudinal_witness_exists}
\end{equation}

\item there exists \(N^{(\perp)}\in V\) such that
\begin{equation}
D_{\perp}\!\bigl(N^{(\perp)}\bigr)
=
W_I\!\bigl(N^{(\perp)}\bigr)^2
+
W_J\!\bigl(N^{(\perp)}\bigr)^2
\neq 0.
\label{eq:transverse_witness_exists}
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}

Then the set
\begin{equation}
V_{\mathrm{Weyl}}
:=
\{X\in V: W_{\parallel}(X)\neq 0,\ D_{\perp}(X)\neq 0\}
\label{eq:V_Weyl_def}
\end{equation}
is a nonempty Zariski-open subset of \(V\). In particular, it is open, dense, and of full Lebesgue measure in \(V\).
Hence the local shell crossing is generically Weyl on \(V\).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Since \(W_{\parallel}\) is a linear functional on \(V\), the assumption
\[
W_{\parallel}\!\bigl(N^{(\parallel)}\bigr)\neq 0
\]
implies that \(W_{\parallel}\) is not the zero functional.
Therefore its zero locus
\begin{equation}
Z_{\parallel}:=\{X\in V:W_{\parallel}(X)=0\}
\label{eq:Z_parallel}
\end{equation}
is a proper affine hyperplane in \(V\), hence closed, nowhere dense, and measure zero.

Likewise, \(D_{\perp}(X)=W_I(X)^2+W_J(X)^2\) is a polynomial on \(V\).
The assumption
\[
D_{\perp}\!\bigl(N^{(\perp)}\bigr)\neq 0
\]
implies that \(D_{\perp}\) is not the zero polynomial.
Therefore its zero locus
\begin{equation}
Z_{\perp}:=\{X\in V:D_{\perp}(X)=0\}
\label{eq:Z_perp}
\end{equation}
is a proper algebraic subset of \(V\), hence closed, nowhere dense, and measure zero.

Thus
\[
V_{\mathrm{Weyl}}
=
V\setminus (Z_{\parallel}\cup Z_{\perp})
\]
is nonempty and Zariski-open.
Since \(Z_{\parallel}\cup Z_{\perp}\) is a proper algebraic subset, \(V_{\mathrm{Weyl}}\) is also open, dense, and full measure in the ordinary Euclidean topology on \(V\).
Finally, by \eqref{eq:weyl_criterion_compact}, every \(X\in V_{\mathrm{Weyl}}\) gives a Weyl crossing.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{D. Simultaneous witness criterion}

A useful variant is the one-shot version.

\begin{corollary}[Simultaneous witness criterion]
If there exists \(N\in V\) such that
\begin{equation}
W_{\parallel}(N)\neq 0,
\qquad
D_{\perp}(N)\neq 0,
\label{eq:simultaneous_witness}
\end{equation}
then the selected shell crossing is already Weyl at \(N\), and generic Weyl nondegeneracy follows on an open dense full-measure subset of \(V\).
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Equation \eqref{eq:simultaneous_witness} implies both hypotheses of the theorem, with \(N^{(\parallel)}=N^{(\perp)}=N\).
Thus the theorem applies.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{E. Canonical ambient witnesses and symmetry projection}

The abstract theorem reduces the problem to a finite witness search.
We now explain why the obstruction is not algebraic.

Before imposing symmetry projection, the ambient tensor space contains canonical trial tensors of the forms
\begin{equation}
X_{ija}^{(\alpha)}=e_{\alpha i}G_{*j}v_a,
\qquad
Y_{ija}^{(\alpha)}=(e_{\alpha i}G_{*j}+G_{*i}e_{\alpha j})v_a,
\qquad
Z_{ija}^{(\alpha)}=(e_{\alpha i}G_{*j}-G_{*i}e_{\alpha j})v_a,
\label{eq:canonical_ambient_witnesses}
\end{equation}
for \(\alpha\in\{1,2\}\), where \(v_a\) is any internal vector satisfying \(u^{(\alpha)}\!\cdot v\neq 0\).

These satisfy strictly nonzero shell overlaps:
\begin{equation}
L_{\alpha}\!\left(X^{(\alpha)}\right)\neq 0,
\qquad
L_{\alpha}\!\left(Y^{(\alpha)}\right)\neq 0,
\qquad
L_{\alpha}\!\left(Z^{(\alpha)}\right)\neq 0.
\label{eq:ambient_overlap_nonzero}
\end{equation}
Therefore the obstruction to Weyl nondegeneracy is not the absence of candidate tensors in the ambient space, but only the possibility that the symmetry projection annihilates all such candidates.

This yields the practical finite microscopic task:

\begin{quote}
Construct one admissible symmetry-projected longitudinal witness and one admissible symmetry-projected transverse witness in the actual TECT microscopic tensor space \(V\).
\end{quote}

\subsubsection{F. Practical finite reduction theorem}

We summarize the exact status.

\begin{theorem}[Finite reduction of the local valley problem]
For the selected BCC shell pair, the local Weyl-valley existence problem is reduced to the following finite-dimensional task:

construct
\[
N^{(\parallel)}\in V
\quad\text{with}\quad
W_{\parallel}\!\bigl(N^{(\parallel)}\bigr)\neq 0,
\]
and
\[
N^{(\perp)}\in V
\quad\text{with}\quad
D_{\perp}\!\bigl(N^{(\perp)}\bigr)\neq 0.
\]

Once this is achieved, Weyl nondegeneracy holds generically on an open dense full-measure subset of \(V\).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from the Two-witness generic Weyl theorem.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Honest scope.}
This theorem does \emph{not} yet prove that the final microscopic TECT linearization automatically supplies those witnesses.
What it proves is sharper and cleaner:

the remaining local Weyl problem is no longer an abstract existence problem, but an explicit finite tensor-construction problem inside the actual microscopic symmetry-allowed space.

%%%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\delta L_{\mathrm{enr}}^{(1)}
=
g_{\parallel} O_{\parallel}
+
g_I O_I
+
g_J O_J,
\qquad
W_{\parallel}(X)=\langle O_{\parallel},X\rangle,
\qquad
W_I(X)=\frac12\langle O_I,X\rangle,
\qquad
W_J(X)=\frac12\langle O_J,X\rangle.
\]

The shell Weyl determinant is
\[
\det M
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3
\,W_{\parallel}(X)\bigl(W_I(X)^2+W_J(X)^2\bigr).
\]

Define
\[
D_{\perp}(X):=W_I(X)^2+W_J(X)^2.
\]
Then the crossing is Weyl exactly when
\[
W_{\parallel}(X)\neq 0,
\qquad
D_{\perp}(X)\neq 0.
\]

Let \(V\) be the finite-dimensional symmetry-allowed microscopic tensor space.
If there exist
\[
N^{(\parallel)}\in V
\quad\text{with}\quad
W_{\parallel}\!\bigl(N^{(\parallel)}\bigr)\neq 0,
\]
and
\[
N^{(\perp)}\in V
\quad\text{with}\quad
D_{\perp}\!\bigl(N^{(\perp)}\bigr)\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
V_{\mathrm{Weyl}}
=
\{X\in V:W_{\parallel}(X)\neq 0,\ D_{\perp}(X)\neq 0\}
\]
is a nonempty Zariski-open subset of \(V\).

Hence \(V_{\mathrm{Weyl}}\) is open, dense, and full measure in \(V\), and the selected shell crossing is generically Weyl.

Therefore the local BCC shell-valley problem is reduced exactly to the finite microscopic construction of two admissible witnesses:
\[
\boxed{
\text{one longitudinal witness}
+
\text{one transverse witness}.
}
\]

Once those exist, Weyl nondegeneracy is generic.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Explicit witness verification for the canonical minimal Class II representative}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now verify that the canonical minimal Class II microscopic representative produces explicit nonzero longitudinal and transverse witnesses inside the actual TECT microscopic tensor space.
This closes the witness-existence step for the shell-level Weyl problem.

\subsubsection{A. Canonical minimal Class II representative}

Consider the canonical minimal Class II choice
\begin{equation}
m^a(P_0)=m\,\delta^{a3},
\label{eq:minimal_m_choice}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
C^{33}_{ij}=c_{\parallel}\,\hat n_i \hat n_j,
\qquad
C^{31}_{ij}=c_I\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}=-c_J\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\label{eq:minimal_C_choice}
\end{equation}
with all other components zero.

Define
\begin{equation}
\mu:=\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m.
\label{eq:mu_def_witness}
\end{equation}

The induced Class II microscopic tensor is
\begin{equation}
\delta N^b_{ij}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^a C^{ab}_{ij}.
\label{eq:deltaN_general_witness}
\end{equation}

Since only \(m^3\neq 0\), only the \(a=3\) channel contributes, and therefore
\begin{equation}
\delta N^b_{ij}
=
-\mu\, C^{3b}_{ij}.
\label{eq:deltaN_muC}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:minimal_C_choice}, we obtain explicitly
\begin{equation}
\delta N^3_{ij}
=
-\mu c_{\parallel}\,\hat n_i \hat n_j,
\label{eq:deltaN3_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\delta N^1_{ij}
=
-\mu\bigl(c_I\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J\,\hat n_i e_{2j}\bigr),
\label{eq:deltaN1_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\delta N^2_{ij}
=
-\mu\bigl(-c_J\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I\,\hat n_i e_{2j}\bigr).
\label{eq:deltaN2_explicit}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Axial-family identification}

Recall that the shell-relevant axial family is
\begin{equation}
N^3_{ij}=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N^2_{ij}=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
\label{eq:axial_family}
\end{equation}
Comparing \eqref{eq:deltaN3_explicit}--\eqref{eq:deltaN2_explicit} with \eqref{eq:axial_family}, we identify the induced coefficients
\begin{equation}
\delta A=-\mu c_{\parallel},
\qquad
\delta B=-\mu c_I,
\qquad
\delta C=-\mu c_J.
\label{eq:deltaABC_explicit}
\end{equation}

Thus the canonical minimal Class II representative belongs exactly to the shell-relevant axial tensor family.

\subsubsection{C. Witness extraction formulas}

The previously established witness functionals are
\begin{equation}
W_{\parallel}[N]
:=
\hat n_i \hat n_j N^3_{ij},
\label{eq:Wpar_extract}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
W_I[N]
:=
\frac12
\Bigl(
e_{1j}\hat n_i N^1_{ij}
+
e_{2j}\hat n_i N^2_{ij}
\Bigr),
\label{eq:WI_extract}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
W_J[N]
:=
\frac12
\Bigl(
e_{1j}\hat n_i N^2_{ij}
-
e_{2j}\hat n_i N^1_{ij}
\Bigr).
\label{eq:WJ_extract}
\end{equation}
For any tensor in the axial family \eqref{eq:axial_family}, these extract exactly the coefficients:
\begin{equation}
W_{\parallel}[N]=A,
\qquad
W_I[N]=B,
\qquad
W_J[N]=C.
\label{eq:exact_extraction_axial}
\end{equation}

Applying \eqref{eq:exact_extraction_axial} to \(\delta N\), and using \eqref{eq:deltaABC_explicit}, we obtain
\begin{equation}
W_{\parallel}[\delta N]=-\mu c_{\parallel},
\label{eq:Wpar_deltaN}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
W_I[\delta N]=-\mu c_I,
\label{eq:WI_deltaN}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
W_J[\delta N]=-\mu c_J.
\label{eq:WJ_deltaN}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{D. Explicit longitudinal and transverse witnesses}

Define the transverse polynomial
\begin{equation}
D_{\perp}[N]:=W_I[N]^2+W_J[N]^2.
\label{eq:Dperp_again}
\end{equation}
Then for the canonical minimal representative,
\begin{equation}
D_{\perp}[\delta N]
=
\mu^2(c_I^2+c_J^2).
\label{eq:Dperp_deltaN}
\end{equation}

Hence we immediately obtain:

\begin{lemma}[Explicit longitudinal witness]
If
\begin{equation}
\mu\neq 0,
\qquad
c_{\parallel}\neq 0,
\label{eq:long_nonzero_cond}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
W_{\parallel}[\delta N]\neq 0.
\label{eq:long_witness_exists}
\end{equation}
So the canonical minimal Class II representative is an admissible longitudinal witness.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from \eqref{eq:Wpar_deltaN}.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Explicit transverse witness]
If
\begin{equation}
\mu\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0),
\label{eq:trans_nonzero_cond}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
D_{\perp}[\delta N]\neq 0.
\label{eq:trans_witness_exists}
\end{equation}
So the canonical minimal Class II representative is an admissible transverse witness.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from \eqref{eq:Dperp_deltaN}.
\end{proof}

Combining both gives the stronger statement:

\begin{theorem}[Canonical Class II simultaneous witness theorem]
Assume
\begin{equation}
\mu\neq 0,
\qquad
c_{\parallel}\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:simultaneous_nonzero_cond}
\end{equation}
Then the canonical minimal Class II representative \(\delta N\) satisfies
\begin{equation}
W_{\parallel}[\delta N]\neq 0,
\qquad
D_{\perp}[\delta N]\neq 0.
\label{eq:simultaneous_witness_result}
\end{equation}
Therefore \(\delta N\) is a simultaneous admissible witness in the actual TECT/Class II microscopic tensor space.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By \eqref{eq:Wpar_deltaN}, \eqref{eq:WI_deltaN}, \eqref{eq:WJ_deltaN}, and \eqref{eq:Dperp_deltaN}, the conditions \eqref{eq:simultaneous_nonzero_cond} imply both \eqref{eq:long_witness_exists} and \eqref{eq:trans_witness_exists}.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{E. Consequence for generic Weyl nondegeneracy}

The previously proved two-witness generic Weyl theorem states that if the actual symmetry-allowed tensor space \(V\) contains

\begin{enumerate}
\item one admissible longitudinal witness with \(W_{\parallel}\neq 0\), and
\item one admissible transverse witness with \(D_{\perp}\neq 0\),
\end{enumerate}

then the Weyl-good set
\begin{equation}
V_{\mathrm{Weyl}}
=
\{N\in V: W_{\parallel}[N]\neq 0,\ D_{\perp}[N]\neq 0\}
\label{eq:Vweyl_again}
\end{equation}
is nonempty, Zariski-open, open dense, and full measure.

Since the canonical minimal Class II representative \(\delta N\) is itself such a simultaneous witness under \eqref{eq:simultaneous_nonzero_cond}, we conclude:

\begin{theorem}[Witness verification theorem for the TECT/Class II space]
Let \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\) be the actual symmetry-allowed microscopic tensor space containing the canonical minimal Class II representative.
Assume \eqref{eq:simultaneous_nonzero_cond}.
Then
\begin{equation}
V_{\mathrm{Weyl}}
=
\{N\in V_{\mathrm{TECT}}: W_{\parallel}[N]\neq 0,\ D_{\perp}[N]\neq 0\}
\label{eq:VTECT_Weyl}
\end{equation}
is a nonempty open dense full-measure subset of \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\).
Hence local Weyl nondegeneracy is generic in the actual TECT/Class II microscopic tensor space.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Apply the two-witness generic Weyl theorem using \(\delta N\) itself as the required admissible witness.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{F. Purely induced Weyl regime}

A particularly important special case is the purely induced regime
\begin{equation}
A_0=B_0=C_0=0.
\label{eq:purely_induced_case}
\end{equation}
Then the effective coefficients satisfy
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=\delta A=-\mu c_{\parallel},
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=\delta B=-\mu c_I,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=\delta C=-\mu c_J.
\label{eq:eff_purely_induced}
\end{equation}
Therefore, under \eqref{eq:simultaneous_nonzero_cond},
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{eff}}\neq 0,
\qquad
(B_{\mathrm{eff}},C_{\mathrm{eff}})\neq (0,0),
\label{eq:purely_induced_weyl}
\end{equation}
and the shell determinant becomes
\begin{equation}
\det M
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3
(-\mu c_{\parallel})
\mu^2(c_I^2+c_J^2)
\neq 0.
\label{eq:purely_induced_det_nonzero}
\end{equation}

Thus the canonical minimal Class II representative does not merely preserve a pre-existing witness structure:
it can generate a local Weyl witness structure by itself.

\subsubsection{G. Honest logical status}

What is now closed is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item an explicit admissible microscopic tensor \(\delta N\) has been constructed inside the actual TECT/Class II family;
\item its longitudinal witness equals \(-\mu c_{\parallel}\);
\item its transverse witness polynomial equals \(\mu^2(c_I^2+c_J^2)\);
\item hence the witness-existence step is closed for this explicit microscopic realization;
\item therefore generic local Weyl nondegeneracy follows in the actual TECT/Class II tensor space, under the stated nonvanishing conditions.
\end{enumerate}

What is not claimed here is UV uniqueness.
The theorem uses only existence of one concrete admissible microscopic representative, which is exactly the level already justified in the current TECT program.

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
m^a(P_0)=m\,\delta^{a3},
\qquad
C^{33}_{ij}=c_{\parallel}\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
C^{31}_{ij}=c_I\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}=-c_J\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I\hat n_i e_{2j},
\]
with all other components zero, and
\[
\mu=\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}m.
\]

Then
\[
\delta N^b_{ij}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}m^a C^{ab}_{ij}
\]
gives
\[
\delta N^3_{ij}=-\mu c_{\parallel}\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
\delta N^1_{ij}=-\mu(c_I\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J\hat n_i e_{2j}),
\qquad
\delta N^2_{ij}=-\mu(-c_J\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I\hat n_i e_{2j}).
\]

Hence the induced axial coefficients are
\[
\delta A=-\mu c_{\parallel},
\qquad
\delta B=-\mu c_I,
\qquad
\delta C=-\mu c_J.
\]

Using
\[
W_{\parallel}[N]=\hat n_i\hat n_j N^3_{ij},
\qquad
W_I[N]=\frac12\bigl(e_{1j}\hat n_i N^1_{ij}+e_{2j}\hat n_i N^2_{ij}\bigr),
\qquad
W_J[N]=\frac12\bigl(e_{1j}\hat n_i N^2_{ij}-e_{2j}\hat n_i N^1_{ij}\bigr),
\]
we obtain
\[
W_{\parallel}[\delta N]=-\mu c_{\parallel},
\qquad
W_I[\delta N]=-\mu c_I,
\qquad
W_J[\delta N]=-\mu c_J.
\]

Therefore
\[
D_{\perp}[\delta N]
=
W_I[\delta N]^2+W_J[\delta N]^2
=
\mu^2(c_I^2+c_J^2).
\]

So if
\[
\mu\neq 0,
\qquad
c_{\parallel}\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0),
\]
then
\[
W_{\parallel}[\delta N]\neq 0,
\qquad
D_{\perp}[\delta N]\neq 0.
\]

Hence the canonical minimal Class II representative is an explicit simultaneous admissible witness in the actual TECT/Class II microscopic tensor space.

By the previously proved two-witness generic Weyl theorem, it follows that
\[
V_{\mathrm{Weyl}}
=
\{N\in V_{\mathrm{TECT}}:W_{\parallel}[N]\neq 0,\ D_{\perp}[N]\neq 0\}
\]
is nonempty, open dense, and full measure.

Therefore local Weyl nondegeneracy is generic in the actual TECT/Class II microscopic tensor space.

In the purely induced case
\[
A_0=B_0=C_0=0,
\]
one has
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=-\mu c_{\parallel},
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=-\mu c_I,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=-\mu c_J,
\]
hence
\[
\det M
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3
(-\mu c_{\parallel})\mu^2(c_I^2+c_J^2)\neq 0.
\]

Thus the canonical minimal Class II representative can itself generate the local Weyl witness structure.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Opposite-valley witness matching for the canonical minimal Class II representative}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We prove that the canonical minimal Class II microscopic representative produces identical witness triples at the matched opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\).
By the previously established witness criterion, this implies the standard opposite-valley pairing relation and hence Dirac doubling.

\subsubsection{A. Matched opposite-valley frames}

Let
\begin{equation}
\hat n_+ := \frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
\hat n_- := -\hat n_+.
\label{eq:npm_def}
\end{equation}
Choose a positively oriented orthonormal frame at \(+G_*\),
\begin{equation}
\{e_{1+},e_{2+},\hat n_+\},
\qquad
e_{1+}\times e_{2+}=\hat n_+.
\label{eq:plus_frame}
\end{equation}
Define the matched opposite-valley frame at \(-G_*\) by
\begin{equation}
e_{1-}:=e_{1+},
\qquad
e_{2-}:=-e_{2+},
\qquad
\hat n_-=-\hat n_+.
\label{eq:minus_frame}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
e_{1-}\times e_{2-}
=
e_{1+}\times(-e_{2+})
=
-\hat n_+
=
\hat n_-,
\label{eq:minus_orientation}
\end{equation}
so \(\{e_{1-},e_{2-},\hat n_-\}\) is again a positively oriented orthonormal frame.

\subsubsection{B. Canonical minimal Class II data at the two valleys}

Assume the canonical minimal Class II data are \emph{even under the matched opposite-valley transformation}, in the following precise sense:

\begin{equation}
m^a(+)=m\,\delta^{a3},
\qquad
m^a(-)=m\,\delta^{a3},
\label{eq:m_pm_same}
\end{equation}
and the shell-adapted tensors are
\begin{equation}
C^{33}_{ij}(+)=c_{\parallel}\,\hat n_{+i}\hat n_{+j},
\qquad
C^{31}_{ij}(+)=c_I\,\hat n_{+i}e_{1+j}+c_J\,\hat n_{+i}e_{2+j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}(+)=-c_J\,\hat n_{+i}e_{1+j}+c_I\,\hat n_{+i}e_{2+j},
\label{eq:C_plus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C^{33}_{ij}(-)=c_{\parallel}\,\hat n_{-i}\hat n_{-j},
\qquad
C^{31}_{ij}(-)=c_I\,\hat n_{-i}e_{1-j}+c_J\,\hat n_{-i}e_{2-j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}(-)=-c_J\,\hat n_{-i}e_{1-j}+c_I\,\hat n_{-i}e_{2-j},
\label{eq:C_minus}
\end{equation}
with all other components zero.

Thus the scalar coefficients
\begin{equation}
m,\qquad c_{\parallel},\qquad c_I,\qquad c_J
\label{eq:scalar_coeffs_same}
\end{equation}
are identical at the two valleys; only the local frame data differ.

Define
\begin{equation}
\mu:=\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m.
\label{eq:mu_pair}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. Induced tensors at \(\pm G_*\)}

The induced microscopic tensor is
\begin{equation}
\delta N^b_{ij}(\pm)
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^a(\pm) C^{ab}_{ij}(\pm).
\label{eq:deltaN_pm_general}
\end{equation}
Using \(m^a(\pm)=m\delta^{a3}\), we obtain
\begin{equation}
\delta N^b_{ij}(\pm)
=
-\mu\, C^{3b}_{ij}(\pm).
\label{eq:deltaN_pm_mu}
\end{equation}

Therefore, at \(+G_*\),
\begin{equation}
\delta N^3_{ij}(+)
=
-\mu c_{\parallel}\,\hat n_{+i}\hat n_{+j},
\label{eq:deltaN3_plus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\delta N^1_{ij}(+)
=
-\mu\bigl(c_I\,\hat n_{+i}e_{1+j}+c_J\,\hat n_{+i}e_{2+j}\bigr),
\label{eq:deltaN1_plus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\delta N^2_{ij}(+)
=
-\mu\bigl(-c_J\,\hat n_{+i}e_{1+j}+c_I\,\hat n_{+i}e_{2+j}\bigr),
\label{eq:deltaN2_plus}
\end{equation}
while at \(-G_*\),
\begin{equation}
\delta N^3_{ij}(-)
=
-\mu c_{\parallel}\,\hat n_{-i}\hat n_{-j},
\label{eq:deltaN3_minus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\delta N^1_{ij}(-)
=
-\mu\bigl(c_I\,\hat n_{-i}e_{1-j}+c_J\,\hat n_{-i}e_{2-j}\bigr),
\label{eq:deltaN1_minus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\delta N^2_{ij}(-)
=
-\mu\bigl(-c_J\,\hat n_{-i}e_{1-j}+c_I\,\hat n_{-i}e_{2-j}\bigr).
\label{eq:deltaN2_minus}
\end{equation}

Thus the induced tensor at each valley has the same axial-family coefficients in its own matched local frame.

\subsubsection{D. Witness triples at the two valleys}

Define the positive-valley witness functionals by
\begin{equation}
W^+_{\parallel}[N]
:=
\hat n_{+i}\hat n_{+j}N^3_{ij}(+),
\label{eq:Wp_par}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
W^+_{I}[N]
:=
\frac12
\Bigl(
e_{1+j}\hat n_{+i}N^1_{ij}(+)
+
e_{2+j}\hat n_{+i}N^2_{ij}(+)
\Bigr),
\label{eq:Wp_I}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
W^+_{J}[N]
:=
\frac12
\Bigl(
e_{1+j}\hat n_{+i}N^2_{ij}(+)
-
e_{2+j}\hat n_{+i}N^1_{ij}(+)
\Bigr).
\label{eq:Wp_J}
\end{equation}

Similarly, define the negative-valley witness functionals in the matched opposite-valley frame:
\begin{equation}
W^-_{\parallel}[N]
:=
\hat n_{-i}\hat n_{-j}N^3_{ij}(-),
\label{eq:Wm_par}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
W^-_{I}[N]
:=
\frac12
\Bigl(
e_{1-j}\hat n_{-i}N^1_{ij}(-)
+
e_{2-j}\hat n_{-i}N^2_{ij}(-)
\Bigr),
\label{eq:Wm_I}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
W^-_{J}[N]
:=
\frac12
\Bigl(
e_{1-j}\hat n_{-i}N^2_{ij}(-)
-
e_{2-j}\hat n_{-i}N^1_{ij}(-)
\Bigr).
\label{eq:Wm_J}
\end{equation}

Applying these to the canonical minimal representative \(\delta N\), we obtain at the positive valley
\begin{equation}
W^+_{\parallel}[\delta N]=-\mu c_{\parallel},
\qquad
W^+_{I}[\delta N]=-\mu c_I,
\qquad
W^+_{J}[\delta N]=-\mu c_J.
\label{eq:Wp_values}
\end{equation}
Exactly the same computation at the negative valley gives
\begin{equation}
W^-_{\parallel}[\delta N]=-\mu c_{\parallel},
\qquad
W^-_{I}[\delta N]=-\mu c_I,
\qquad
W^-_{J}[\delta N]=-\mu c_J.
\label{eq:Wm_values}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
W^-_{\parallel}[\delta N]=W^+_{\parallel}[\delta N],
\qquad
W^-_{I}[\delta N]=W^+_{I}[\delta N],
\qquad
W^-_{J}[\delta N]=W^+_{J}[\delta N].
\label{eq:witness_matching_result}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Explicit opposite-valley witness matching theorem]
Assume the canonical minimal Class II representative is even under the matched opposite-valley transformation in the sense of \eqref{eq:m_pm_same}--\eqref{eq:scalar_coeffs_same}.
Then its witness triples at \(\pm G_*\) coincide:
\begin{equation}
(W^-_{\parallel},W^-_{I},W^-_{J})
=
(W^+_{\parallel},W^+_{I},W^+_{J}).
\label{eq:triple_match_theorem}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from \eqref{eq:Wp_values} and \eqref{eq:Wm_values}.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{E. Consequence for opposite-valley pairing}

The previously established witness-doubling theorem states that equality of the witness triples in matched opposite-valley frames is equivalent to the standard reduced pairing relation
\begin{equation}
h_-(p)=-h_+(-p)
\label{eq:opp_pairing_standard}
\end{equation}
after subtraction of the common scalar part.

Hence we obtain:

\begin{corollary}[Canonical Class II opposite-valley pairing]
Under the hypotheses of the explicit opposite-valley witness matching theorem, the reduced valley Hamiltonians satisfy
\begin{equation}
h_-(p)=-h_+(-p)
\label{eq:opp_pairing_canonical}
\end{equation}
in the canonical matched reduced basis.
\end{corollary}

\subsubsection{F. Dirac doubling consequence}

Assume in addition the nondegeneracy conditions
\begin{equation}
\mu\neq 0,
\qquad
c_{\parallel}\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:nondeg_pm}
\end{equation}
Then at both valleys,
\begin{equation}
W^\pm_{\parallel}\neq 0,
\qquad
\bigl(W^\pm_I,W^\pm_J\bigr)\neq (0,0),
\label{eq:Weyl_both_pm}
\end{equation}
so each valley is locally Weyl.

Combining \eqref{eq:Weyl_both_pm} with \eqref{eq:opp_pairing_canonical}, we conclude that the doubled block
\begin{equation}
H_D(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
h_+(p) & 0\\
0 & h_-(p)
\end{pmatrix}
\label{eq:HD_doubled_pair}
\end{equation}
is unitarily equivalent to a massless Dirac Hamiltonian.

\begin{theorem}[Canonical Class II local Dirac doubling theorem]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item an opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\) exists;
\item the canonical minimal Class II representative is even under the matched opposite-valley transformation;
\item \(\mu\neq 0\), \(c_{\parallel}\neq 0\), and \((c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0)\).
\end{enumerate}
Then the canonical minimal Class II representative yields:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a Weyl valley at \(+G_*\);
\item a Weyl valley at \(-G_*\);
\item equality of the witness triples at the two valleys;
\item the standard opposite-valley relation \(h_-(p)=-h_+(-p)\);
\item a doubled four-component massless Dirac block.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Items (1) and (2) follow from \eqref{eq:Weyl_both_pm}. Item (3) is \eqref{eq:triple_match_theorem}. Item (4) follows from the witness-pairing equivalence. Item (5) is the standard opposite-valley Dirac doubling theorem.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Exact logical status.}
What is closed here is not the existence of the opposite valley from the full microscopic TECT PDE.
What is closed is the following sharper statement:

once an opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\) is present and the canonical minimal Class II data are even under the matched valley transformation, the same explicit microscopic representative automatically produces matched witness triples and hence local Dirac doubling.

%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\hat n_-=-\hat n_+,
\qquad
e_{1-}=e_{1+},
\qquad
e_{2-}=-e_{2+},
\]
so that
\[
e_{1-}\times e_{2-}=\hat n_-.
\]

For the canonical minimal Class II representative, assume the scalar data are even under the matched opposite-valley transformation:
\[
m^a(\pm)=m\delta^{a3},
\qquad
(c_{\parallel},c_I,c_J)_-=(c_{\parallel},c_I,c_J)_+=(c_{\parallel},c_I,c_J).
\]

Then
\[
\delta N^b_{ij}(\pm)
=
-\mu\, C^{3b}_{ij}(\pm),
\qquad
\mu=\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}m,
\]
gives
\[
\delta N^3_{ij}(\pm)=-\mu c_{\parallel}\hat n_{\pm i}\hat n_{\pm j},
\]
\[
\delta N^1_{ij}(\pm)=-\mu(c_I\hat n_{\pm i}e_{1\pm j}+c_J\hat n_{\pm i}e_{2\pm j}),
\]
\[
\delta N^2_{ij}(\pm)=-\mu(-c_J\hat n_{\pm i}e_{1\pm j}+c_I\hat n_{\pm i}e_{2\pm j}).
\]

Therefore the witness triples at the two valleys are identical:
\[
W^\pm_{\parallel}=-\mu c_{\parallel},
\qquad
W^\pm_I=-\mu c_I,
\qquad
W^\pm_J=-\mu c_J.
\]

Hence
\[
(W^-_{\parallel},W^-_I,W^-_J)=(W^+_{\parallel},W^+_I,W^+_J).
\]

By the previously established witness criterion, this is equivalent to
\[
h_-(p)=-h_+(-p)
\]
in the matched reduced basis.

If, in addition,
\[
\mu\neq 0,
\qquad
c_{\parallel}\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0),
\]
then both valleys are Weyl:
\[
W^\pm_{\parallel}\neq 0,
\qquad
(W^\pm_I,W^\pm_J)\neq (0,0),
\]
and the doubled block
\[
H_D(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
h_+(p) & 0\\
0 & h_-(p)
\end{pmatrix}
\]
is unitarily equivalent to a massless Dirac Hamiltonian.

Thus:
\[
\boxed{
\text{canonical minimal Class II representative}
+
\text{matched opposite-valley evenness}
\Longrightarrow
\text{explicit witness matching}
\Longrightarrow
\text{local Dirac doubling}.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Local Dirac Block Realization Theorem}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now assemble the previously established ingredients into a single theorem showing that the canonical minimal Class II microscopic representative realizes a stable massless Dirac fermion in the full low-energy sector, provided the remaining independent spectral/symmetry inputs are satisfied.

\subsubsection{A. Canonical minimal Class II representative}

Fix an opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\) and define
\begin{equation}
\mu:=\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m.
\label{eq:mu_realization}
\end{equation}
Take the canonical minimal Class II representative
\begin{equation}
m^a(P_0)=m\,\delta^{a3},
\label{eq:m_realization}
\end{equation}
and, in the matched local shell frames at \(\pm G_*\),
\begin{equation}
C^{33}_{ij}=c_{\parallel}\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
C^{31}_{ij}=c_I\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}=-c_J\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\label{eq:C_realization}
\end{equation}
with all other components zero.

The induced shell-relevant tensor is
\begin{equation}
\delta N^b_{ij}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^a C^{ab}_{ij},
\label{eq:deltaN_realization}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\delta A=-\mu c_{\parallel},
\qquad
\delta B=-\mu c_I,
\qquad
\delta C=-\mu c_J.
\label{eq:deltaABC_realization}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Effective shell coefficients and explicit witness nonvanishing}

Let the baseline shell coefficients be \((A_0,B_0,C_0)\), and define the corrected coefficients
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=A_0-\mu c_{\parallel},
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=B_0-\mu c_I,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=C_0-\mu c_J.
\label{eq:AeffBeffCeff_realization}
\end{equation}

In particular, in the purely induced case
\begin{equation}
A_0=B_0=C_0=0,
\label{eq:purely_induced_realization}
\end{equation}
one has
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=-\mu c_{\parallel},
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=-\mu c_I,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=-\mu c_J.
\label{eq:purely_induced_coeffs}
\end{equation}

Assume the nonvanishing conditions
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{eff}}\neq 0,
\qquad
(B_{\mathrm{eff}},C_{\mathrm{eff}})\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:nonvanishing_realization}
\end{equation}
A sufficient explicit condition in the purely induced case is
\begin{equation}
\mu\neq 0,
\qquad
c_{\parallel}\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:sufficient_nonvanishing_realization}
\end{equation}

Then the shell determinant is
\begin{equation}
\det M_{\mathrm{eff}}
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3
A_{\mathrm{eff}}\bigl(B_{\mathrm{eff}}^2+C_{\mathrm{eff}}^2\bigr)\neq 0.
\label{eq:detM_eff_realization}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, the local shell Hamiltonian at each valley is Weyl.

\subsubsection{C. Opposite-valley witness matching}

Assume the canonical Class II data are even under the matched opposite-valley transformation.
Then the induced coefficients satisfy
\begin{equation}
A^-_{\mathrm{eff}}=A^+_{\mathrm{eff}},
\qquad
B^-_{\mathrm{eff}}=B^+_{\mathrm{eff}},
\qquad
C^-_{\mathrm{eff}}=C^+_{\mathrm{eff}}.
\label{eq:opp_matching_coeffs_realization}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, the witness triples satisfy
\begin{equation}
(W^-_{\parallel},W^-_I,W^-_J)
=
(W^+_{\parallel},W^+_I,W^+_J).
\label{eq:witness_matching_realization}
\end{equation}
Therefore the reduced valley Hamiltonians obey the standard opposite-valley pairing relation
\begin{equation}
h_-(p)=-h_+(-p).
\label{eq:opp_pairing_realization}
\end{equation}

Since both valleys are Weyl by \eqref{eq:detM_eff_realization}, the doubled local shell block is a massless Dirac block:
\begin{equation}
H_D(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
h_+(p) & 0\\
0 & h_-(p)
\end{pmatrix}
\sim
\Gamma_i (M_{\mathrm{eff}}p)_i.
\label{eq:HD_local_realization}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{D. Full microscopic block decomposition}

Now decompose the full microscopic Hamiltonian near the selected crossing as
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V(p)\\
V(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:Hfull_realization}
\end{equation}
where \(H_D\) acts on the four-dimensional local Dirac sector and \(H_R\) acts on the remote complement.

Assume the little-group mismatch condition
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0.
\label{eq:LG_mismatch_realization}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
V(0)=0,
\qquad
\|V(p)\|\le c|p|
\label{eq:V_bound_realization}
\end{equation}
for small \(p\).

Assume further that the remote sector is uniformly gapped:
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing
\qquad
\text{for small }p,
\label{eq:remote_gap_realization}
\end{equation}
with \(\Delta>0\).
A sufficient theorem-level route is the existence of an already-gapped unperturbed realization plus a sufficiently small bounded Class II perturbation.

Finally assume a residual symmetry excludes all constant Dirac masses in the effective theory.

\subsubsection{E. Schur-complement reduction}

For \(|E|<\Delta/2\), the remote resolvent exists and obeys
\begin{equation}
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|\le \frac{2}{\Delta}.
\label{eq:resolvent_realization}
\end{equation}
Hence the effective Hamiltonian on the four-dimensional low-energy sector is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
H_D(p)-\Sigma(E,p),
\qquad
\Sigma(E,p):=
V(p)(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}V(p)^\dagger.
\label{eq:Heff_realization}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:V_bound_realization} and \eqref{eq:resolvent_realization},
\begin{equation}
\|\Sigma(E,p)\|
\le
\frac{2c^2}{\Delta}|p|^2.
\label{eq:Sigma_realization}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
\Gamma_i(M_{\mathrm{eff}}p)_i
+
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right).
\label{eq:Heff_final_realization}
\end{equation}

Because the residual symmetry forbids a constant Dirac mass term, no \(O(1)\) mass deformation can appear.
Thus the low-energy sector remains a massless Dirac cone.

\subsubsection{F. Main theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Local Dirac Block Realization Theorem]
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item an opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\) exists;

\item the canonical minimal Class II representative \eqref{eq:m_realization}--\eqref{eq:C_realization} is present in the actual microscopic TECT tensor space;

\item the effective shell coefficients satisfy
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}\neq 0,
\qquad
(B_{\mathrm{eff}},C_{\mathrm{eff}})\neq (0,0),
\]
equivalently \(\det M_{\mathrm{eff}}\neq 0\);

\item the Class II data are even under the matched opposite-valley transformation, so that
\[
A^-_{\mathrm{eff}}=A^+_{\mathrm{eff}},
\qquad
B^-_{\mathrm{eff}}=B^+_{\mathrm{eff}},
\qquad
C^-_{\mathrm{eff}}=C^+_{\mathrm{eff}};
\]

\item the little-group mismatch condition holds:
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0;
\]

\item the remote sector has a positive gap \(\Delta>0\);

\item a residual symmetry forbids all constant Dirac masses on the effective four-dimensional sector.
\end{enumerate}

Then, for sufficiently small \(p\), the full microscopic TECT linearization contains a spectrally isolated four-dimensional low-energy sector whose effective Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
\Gamma_i(M_{\mathrm{eff}}p)_i
+
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right),
\qquad
\det M_{\mathrm{eff}}\neq 0.
\label{eq:Local_Dirac_Block_Realization}
\end{equation}
Consequently, the full microscopic low-energy theory contains a stable massless Dirac fermion.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By items (2)–(3), the canonical Class II representative produces nonzero shell witnesses and hence a Weyl block at each valley.
By item (4), the witness triples match across the opposite valleys, so the doubled shell block is local Dirac.
By item (5), the constant inter-sector mixing vanishes and the first nontrivial mixing is at least linear in momentum.
By items (6)–(7), the Schur-complement correction is well-defined, quadratic in \(p\), and cannot generate a constant Dirac mass.
Therefore the four-dimensional local Dirac block survives in the full microscopic low-energy theory as a stable spectrally isolated massless Dirac sector.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{G. Strongest explicit sufficient form}

A concrete sufficient version is the following.

\begin{corollary}[Explicit sufficient realization criterion]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\) survives in the actual microscopic realization;
\item the canonical minimal Class II representative is present and even under the matched opposite-valley transformation;
\item
\[
\mu\neq 0,\qquad c_{\parallel}\neq 0,\qquad (c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0);
\]
\item little-group mismatch, remote-gap positivity, and mass-forbidding residual symmetry all hold.
\end{enumerate}
Then the full microscopic low-energy theory contains a stable massless Dirac fermion with effective Hamiltonian
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
\Gamma_i(M_{\mathrm{eff}}p)_i
+
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right),
\label{eq:explicit_sufficient_realization}
\end{equation}
where in the purely induced case
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=-\mu c_{\parallel},
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=-\mu c_I,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=-\mu c_J.
\label{eq:explicit_purely_induced_realization}
\end{equation}
\end{corollary}

\paragraph{Exact logical status.}
What is now closed is the following theorem chain:
\[
\text{explicit canonical Class II witness}
\Longrightarrow
\text{Weyl at each valley}
\Longrightarrow
\text{opposite-valley Dirac doubling}
\Longrightarrow
\text{spectrally isolated stable massless Dirac fermion}.
\]
