What still remains outside the theorem itself is only the final microscopic verification that the actual TECT linearization satisfies the input hypotheses:
survival of the opposite shell pair, little-group mismatch, remote-gap positivity, and the residual mass-forbidding symmetry.

%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
m^a(P_0)=m\delta^{a3},
\qquad
C^{33}_{ij}=c_{\parallel}\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
C^{31}_{ij}=c_I\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}=-c_J\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I\hat n_i e_{2j},
\]
with
\[
\mu=\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}m.
\]

The induced shell coefficients are
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=A_0-\mu c_{\parallel},
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=B_0-\mu c_I,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=C_0-\mu c_J.
\]

If
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}\neq 0,
\qquad
(B_{\mathrm{eff}},C_{\mathrm{eff}})\neq (0,0),
\]
then
\[
\det M_{\mathrm{eff}}
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3
A_{\mathrm{eff}}(B_{\mathrm{eff}}^2+C_{\mathrm{eff}}^2)\neq 0,
\]
so each valley is Weyl.

If the Class II data are even under the matched opposite-valley transformation, then
\[
A^-_{\mathrm{eff}}=A^+_{\mathrm{eff}},
\qquad
B^-_{\mathrm{eff}}=B^+_{\mathrm{eff}},
\qquad
C^-_{\mathrm{eff}}=C^+_{\mathrm{eff}},
\]
hence
\[
h_-(p)=-h_+(-p),
\]
so the doubled shell block is a local Dirac block:
\[
H_D(p)\sim \Gamma_i(M_{\mathrm{eff}}p)_i.
\]

If, in addition,
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0,
\qquad
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing,
\]
and a residual symmetry forbids constant Dirac masses, then
\[
V(0)=0,\qquad \|V(p)\|\le c|p|,
\]
and the Schur-complement effective Hamiltonian satisfies
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
\Gamma_i(M_{\mathrm{eff}}p)_i
+
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right).
\]

Therefore:
\[
\boxed{
\text{canonical minimal Class II representative}
+
\text{opposite-valley evenness}
+
\text{little-group mismatch}
+
\text{remote gap}
+
\text{mass-forbidding symmetry}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\Longrightarrow
\text{full microscopic low-energy TECT sector contains a stable massless Dirac fermion.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Actual little-group mismatch audit for the BCC local Dirac block}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now reformulate the condition
\[
V(0)=0
\]
at the level of the actual BCC representation content of the local Dirac block.
The purpose is to replace the abstract sufficient condition
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\]
by a concrete sectorwise audit in the actual TECT shell construction.

\subsubsection{A. Exact discrete little group versus IR axial remnant}

Fix the selected BCC shell direction
\begin{equation}
\hat n=\frac{1}{\sqrt 2}(1,1,0),
\qquad
G_*=|G_*|\hat n.
\label{eq:selected_axis_audit}
\end{equation}
Then the exact ordinary cubic stabilizers are
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Stab}(+\hat n)\cong C_{2v},
\qquad
\mathrm{Stab}(\{\pm \hat n\})\cong D_{2h}.
\label{eq:little_groups_audit}
\end{equation}
Both groups are abelian, hence all ordinary complex irreducible representations are one-dimensional.
Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\text{ordinary cubic little-group irreducibility does \emph{not} force a 2D local sector.}
\label{eq:no_2D_irrep_audit}
\end{equation}

What remains true kinematically is the canonical splitting
\begin{equation}
\mathbb R^3=\mathbb R\hat n\oplus \hat n^\perp,
\label{eq:kinematic_split_audit}
\end{equation}
i.e. one longitudinal direction plus a two-dimensional transverse plane.
The actual two-dimensional shell structure arises only at the infrared axial-remnant level acting on \(\hat n^\perp\), not from ordinary bare cubic irreps.

\subsubsection{B. Actual representation content of the local Dirac block}

Let
\begin{equation}
W_{\mathrm{mix}}=\mathrm{span}\{W^{(1)},W^{(2)}\}=\hat n^\perp\otimes \hat n
\label{eq:Wmix_audit}
\end{equation}
denote the shell-transverse doublet, where
\begin{equation}
W^{(\alpha)}_{ij}=e_{\alpha i}\hat n_j,\qquad \alpha=1,2.
\label{eq:Walpha_audit}
\end{equation}
Assume the internal channel contains a matching two-dimensional subspace
\begin{equation}
U_D=\mathrm{span}\{u^{(1)},u^{(2)}\}
\label{eq:UD_audit}
\end{equation}
transforming in the same transverse way.
Then the shell-relevant local Dirac carrier is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
\label{eq:HD_content_audit}
\end{equation}
where

\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\) is the opposite-shell pair space \(\mathrm{span}\{\phi_+,\phi_-\}\),
\item \(\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\) is the shell-relevant transverse/internal doublet.
\end{itemize}

Thus the actual local Dirac block is not an ordinary 2D irrep of \(C_{2v}\) or \(D_{2h}\), but a four-dimensional shell-relevant carrier built from:
\begin{equation}
\text{(opposite shell pair)}\ \otimes\ \text{(matching transverse/internal doublet)}.
\label{eq:HD_factor_meaning}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. Sectorwise decomposition of the remote space}

Let the full Hilbert space decompose at the crossing point as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}=\mathcal H_D\oplus \mathcal H_R,
\qquad
\mathcal H_R=\bigoplus_a K_a,
\label{eq:HR_sectorwise}
\end{equation}
where each \(K_a\) is \(H_*\)-invariant.

The practical shell-relevant labels carried by \(\mathcal H_D\) are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the selected shell-pair label \(\pm G_*\),
\item transverse/non-volumetric character,
\item enriched internal doublet label,
\item residual grading/parity/chirality labels, if present,
\item any additional conserved microscopic labels carried by \(\mathcal H_D\).
\end{enumerate}

A remote sector \(K_a\) can mix at \(p=0\) with \(\mathcal H_D\) only if it matches \(\mathcal H_D\) in \emph{all} of these shell-relevant labels.

\subsubsection{D. Three canonical mismatch sectors}

We now audit the three most important remote sectors explicitly.

\paragraph{Sector 1: higher-shell sector.}
Suppose \(K_a\subset \mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}\), i.e. \(K_a\) belongs to a shell orbit different from the selected pair \(\pm G_*\).
Then \(K_a\) carries a different shell label from \(\mathcal H_D\), hence
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0.
\label{eq:high_shell_zero}
\end{equation}
Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\text{different shell orbit}\quad \Longrightarrow \quad V_{K_a\to D}(0)=0.
\label{eq:high_shell_phrase}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Sector 2: same shell but non-enriched sector.}
Suppose \(K_a\) lies on the same shell orbit but does not carry the enriched internal doublet \(\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\) required by \(\mathcal H_D\).
Then the internal matching condition fails, so
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0.
\label{eq:non_enr_zero}
\end{equation}
Hence:
\begin{equation}
\text{same shell but no enriched internal doublet}
\quad \Longrightarrow \quad
V_{K_a\to D}(0)=0.
\label{eq:non_enr_phrase}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Sector 3: wrong internal sector.}
Suppose \(K_a\) has a nontrivial internal structure, but not the one matching the shell-relevant internal doublet.
Examples include:

\begin{itemize}
\item an internal singlet instead of a doublet,
\item a different doublet not identified with the shell-relevant one,
\item a larger representation whose shell-relevant multiplicity does not match.
\end{itemize}

Then the internal representation still mismatches, so
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0.
\label{eq:wrong_int_zero}
\end{equation}
Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\text{wrong internal representation}
\quad \Longrightarrow \quad
V_{K_a\to D}(0)=0.
\label{eq:wrong_int_phrase}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{E. Sectorwise zero-mixing theorem}

We now combine the above into the actual representation-audit theorem.

\begin{theorem}[Actual little-group mismatch audit]
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the full Hamiltonian is \(H_*\)-equivariant at \(p=0\);
\item the local shell-relevant Dirac block has the actual representation content
\[
\mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}};
\]
\item the remote sector admits an \(H_*\)-invariant decomposition
\[
\mathcal H_R=\bigoplus_a K_a;
\]
\item for every sector \(K_a\), at least one shell-relevant label mismatches that of \(\mathcal H_D\).
\end{enumerate}

Then
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0
\qquad
\forall a,
\label{eq:Ka_zero_all}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0,
\label{eq:HR_zero_all}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
V(0)=0.
\label{eq:V0_zero_audit}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Because the decomposition \(\mathcal H_R=\oplus_a K_a\) is \(H_*\)-invariant, one has
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)
\cong
\bigoplus_a \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D).
\label{eq:Hom_sum_audit}
\end{equation}
By assumption, each \(K_a\) fails to match \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one shell-relevant label.
Hence no nonzero \(H_*\)-intertwiner can map \(K_a\) into \(\mathcal H_D\), so
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0
\]
for all \(a\).
Therefore the direct sum \eqref{eq:Hom_sum_audit} vanishes, giving \eqref{eq:HR_zero_all}.

Since the Hamiltonian is \(H_*\)-equivariant at \(p=0\), the constant mixing block must satisfy
\[
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
\]
Because the latter Hom-space is zero, we conclude
\[
V(0)=0.
\]
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{F. Practical audit checklist}

The theorem reduces the microscopic \(V(0)=0\) problem to the following finite checklist.

A remote sector is excluded from constant mixing if it differs from \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one of:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the selected shell-pair label \(\pm G_*\),
\item transverse versus longitudinal/volumetric character,
\item presence of the enriched shell-relevant internal doublet,
\item residual grading / parity / chirality,
\item any extra conserved microscopic label.
\end{enumerate}

Thus the actual microscopic task is no longer abstract:
it is a sectorwise label audit of the remote spectrum.

\paragraph{Exact logical status.}
What is now proved is not that the BCC ordinary little group itself produces a 2D irrep.
Rather, the exact ordinary little-group route is known to fail.
The correct theorem is instead:

\[
\text{actual local carrier } \mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}
\quad + \quad
\text{sectorwise remote-label mismatch}
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
\]

This is the sharpest honest microscopic form of the little-group mismatch argument presently justified in TECT.

%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\mathrm{Stab}(+\hat n)\cong C_{2v},
\qquad
\mathrm{Stab}(\{\pm \hat n\})\cong D_{2h},
\]
and both groups are abelian, so all ordinary complex irreducible representations are one-dimensional.

Hence:
\[
\boxed{
\text{ordinary cubic little-group irreducibility does not force the local 2D/4D Dirac carrier.}
}
\]

The actual shell-relevant local Dirac block is
\[
\mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
\]
where \(\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\) is the opposite-shell pair \(\pm G_*\), and \(\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\) is the matching transverse/internal doublet furnished at the IR axial-remnant level.

Let
\[
\mathcal H_R=\bigoplus_a K_a
\]
be an \(H_*\)-invariant decomposition of the remote sector.
A sector \(K_a\) can mix at \(p=0\) with \(\mathcal H_D\) only if it matches \(\mathcal H_D\) in all shell-relevant labels:

\[
\pm G_*,
\quad
\text{transverse/non-volumetric character},
\quad
\text{enriched internal doublet},
\quad
\text{grading/parity/chirality},
\quad
\text{extra conserved labels}.
\]

In particular:

\[
\text{different shell orbit}
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0,
\]
\[
\text{same shell but no enriched internal doublet}
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0,
\]
\[
\text{wrong internal representation}
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0.
\]

Therefore, if every remote sector \(K_a\) fails to match \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one shell-relevant label, then
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0.
\]
Since equivariance implies
\[
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D),
\]
we obtain
\[
\boxed{
V(0)=0.
}
\]

Thus the actual microscopic little-group mismatch statement is:
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}
\quad+\quad
\text{sectorwise remote-label mismatch}
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Remote-gap sectorwise lower-bound theorem in the minimal truncation}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now close the remote-gap problem at the level of the first nontrivial finite truncation.
The point is to replace the abstract condition
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing
\]
by an explicit finite-dimensional lower-bound criterion.

\subsubsection{A. Minimal truncated Hilbert space}

Consider the shell-relevant minimal truncation
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_D
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}.
\label{eq:Hfull_truncated}
\end{equation}
Here:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathcal H_D\cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{pair}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\) is the local doubled Dirac carrier;
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}\) is the volumetric/longitudinal sector;
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}\) is the higher-shell sector not belonging to the selected shell pair \(\pm G_*\);
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}\) is the same-shell but non-enriched sector;
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}\) contains modes with internal content not matching the selected shell doublet.
\end{itemize}

This is the smallest truncation in which all previously identified dangerous remote channels are explicitly present.

\subsubsection{B. Block decomposition and zero constant Dirac--remote mixing}

Write the truncated Hamiltonian as
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}^{\mathrm{tr}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V_{DR}(p)\\
V_{DR}(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:Hfull_tr_block}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
H_R(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_{\mathrm{vol}}(p) & R_{\mathrm{vol,high}}(p) & \cdots\\
R_{\mathrm{high,vol}}(p) & H_{\mathrm{high}}(p) & \cdots\\
\vdots & \vdots & \ddots
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:HR_block}
\end{equation}

Assume the shell-relevant label mismatch audit has already been verified for the minimal truncation.
Then
\begin{equation}
V_{DR}(0)=0.
\label{eq:VDR0_zero}
\end{equation}
Hence the only remaining spectral question is whether the remote block \(H_R(p)\) can approach zero.

\subsubsection{C. Diagonal sector-center energies and remote mixing norm}

For the four remote sectors define the diagonal or sector-center energies
\begin{equation}
\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p),\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p),\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p),\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}(p).
\label{eq:mu_sector_def}
\end{equation}
Set the pointwise remote diagonal distance from zero
\begin{equation}
\delta_0(p):=
\min\Bigl\{
|\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}(p)|
\Bigr\}.
\label{eq:delta0_def}
\end{equation}

Now split the remote block as
\begin{equation}
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p),
\label{eq:HR_DR_RR}
\end{equation}
where \(D_R(p)\) is the diagonal (or sector-center) part carrying the energies \(\mu_a(p)\), and \(R_R(p)\) is the residual remote--remote mixing.
Define
\begin{equation}
\eta_R(p):=\|R_R(p)\|.
\label{eq:etaR_def}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{D. Pointwise lower bound}

\begin{lemma}[Pointwise operator lower bound]
For every \(\psi\in \mathcal H_R\),
\begin{equation}
\|H_R(p)\psi\|
\ge
\bigl(\delta_0(p)-\eta_R(p)\bigr)\,\|\psi\|.
\label{eq:pointwise_lower_bound}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Using \(H_R=D_R+R_R\), the reverse triangle inequality gives
\[
\|H_R\psi\|
=
\|(D_R+R_R)\psi\|
\ge
\|D_R\psi\|-\|R_R\psi\|.
\]
By construction of \(\delta_0(p)\), every vector in the remote sector satisfies
\[
\|D_R(p)\psi\|\ge \delta_0(p)\|\psi\|.
\]
Also,
\[
\|R_R(p)\psi\|\le \|R_R(p)\|\,\|\psi\|=\eta_R(p)\|\psi\|.
\]
Combining the two inequalities yields \eqref{eq:pointwise_lower_bound}.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Pointwise remote-gap bound]
If
\begin{equation}
\delta_0(p)>\eta_R(p),
\label{eq:pointwise_gap_condition}
\end{equation}
then the remote spectrum has a positive pointwise gap:
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta(p),\Delta(p))=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta(p)\ge \delta_0(p)-\eta_R(p)>0.
\label{eq:pointwise_gap_result}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Since \(H_R(p)\) is Hermitian, \eqref{eq:pointwise_lower_bound} implies that every singular value, hence every absolute eigenvalue, is bounded below by \(\delta_0(p)-\eta_R(p)\).
Therefore no eigenvalue can enter the interval
\[
\bigl(-(\delta_0(p)-\eta_R(p)),\ \delta_0(p)-\eta_R(p)\bigr).
\]
This proves \eqref{eq:pointwise_gap_result}.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{E. Uniform local remote gap}

Fix a neighborhood
\begin{equation}
N_\rho:=\{p:|p|\le \rho\}.
\label{eq:Nrho_def}
\end{equation}
Define
\begin{equation}
\delta_{0,\rho}:=\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\delta_0(p),
\qquad
\eta_{R,\rho}:=\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\eta_R(p).
\label{eq:delta0rho_etaRrho}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Uniform remote-gap sectorwise lower-bound theorem]
If
\begin{equation}
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho},
\label{eq:uniform_gap_condition}
\end{equation}
then for all \(|p|\le \rho\),
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing,
\label{eq:uniform_gap_spectral}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\Delta_\rho:=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
\label{eq:Delta_rho_def}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Apply the pointwise bound \eqref{eq:pointwise_gap_result} for each \(p\in N_\rho\):
\[
\Delta(p)\ge \delta_0(p)-\eta_R(p).
\]
Taking the infimum over \(|p|\le \rho\) gives
\[
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\Delta(p)\ge \delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}=\Delta_\rho>0.
\]
Hence \eqref{eq:uniform_gap_spectral} holds uniformly on \(N_\rho\).
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{F. Gershgorin alternative}

Sometimes a basis-dependent estimate is easier.
Let the remote matrix entries in a fixed basis be \((H_R)_{ab}(p)\), and define the row sums
\begin{equation}
R_a(p):=\sum_{b\neq a}|(H_R)_{ab}(p)|.
\label{eq:row_sums}
\end{equation}
Then Gershgorin's theorem gives the following sufficient condition:

\begin{equation}
\min_a\bigl(|(H_R)_{aa}(p)|-R_a(p)\bigr)>0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_G(p),\Delta_G(p))=\varnothing,
\label{eq:gershgorin_pointwise}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\Delta_G(p):=\min_a\bigl(|(H_R)_{aa}(p)|-R_a(p)\bigr).
\label{eq:DeltaG_def}
\end{equation}

Uniformly on \(N_\rho\), define
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{G,\rho}:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\min_a\bigl(|(H_R)_{aa}(p)|-R_a(p)\bigr).
\label{eq:DeltaG_rho}
\end{equation}
If
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{G,\rho}>0,
\label{eq:DeltaG_rho_positive}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_{G,\rho},\Delta_{G,\rho})=\varnothing
\qquad
(|p|\le \rho).
\label{eq:gershgorin_uniform}
\end{equation}

This is often convenient in sparse truncations.

\subsubsection{G. Sectorwise sufficient conditions}

The theorem becomes especially transparent when each remote sector admits an individual lower bound:
\begin{equation}
|\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p)|\ge \Delta_{\mathrm{vol}},
\qquad
|\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p)|\ge \Delta_{\mathrm{high}},
\qquad
|\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p)|\ge \Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}},
\qquad
|\mu_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}(p)|\ge \Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},
\label{eq:sectorwise_bounds}
\end{equation}
for all \(|p|\le \rho\).

Then
\begin{equation}
\delta_{0,\rho}\ge
\Delta_{\min}:=
\min\{
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol}},
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}},
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}},
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}
\}.
\label{eq:Deltamin_def}
\end{equation}
Therefore, if
\begin{equation}
\eta_{R,\rho}<\Delta_{\min},
\label{eq:sectorwise_small_mixing}
\end{equation}
the remote block has a uniform gap
\begin{equation}
\Delta_\rho\ge \Delta_{\min}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
\label{eq:sectorwise_gap_final}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{H. Heavy volumetric sector as a natural remote contributor}

In the EFT reduction of the heavy volumetric mode \(\sigma\), the effective longitudinal stiffness is shifted by
\begin{equation}
(\lambda+2\mu)\longmapsto (\lambda+2\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2},
\label{eq:long_stiffening}
\end{equation}
while heavy-sector effects are suppressed by powers of \(M_\sigma^{-2}\).
Therefore the volumetric sector is naturally pushed upward relative to the light transverse shell sector and contributes positively to the remote diagonal distance from zero.

This does not by itself prove the full remote gap, but it provides a natural microscopic mechanism making
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol}}>0
\]
plausible and often large compared to the shell-relevant low-energy scale.

\subsubsection{I. Consequence for spectral isolation}

Assume also the already-established zero constant mixing and linear bound
\begin{equation}
V_{DR}(0)=0,
\qquad
\|V_{DR}(p)\|\le c|p|.
\label{eq:VDR_linear}
\end{equation}
Then, for \(|E|<\Delta_\rho/2\),
\begin{equation}
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|\le \frac{2}{\Delta_\rho}.
\label{eq:resolvent_remote_gap}
\end{equation}
Hence the Schur-complement self-energy satisfies
\begin{equation}
\Sigma(E,p)
=
V_{DR}(p)(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}V_{DR}(p)^\dagger
=
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_\rho}\right).
\label{eq:Sigma_remote_gap}
\end{equation}
Thus the remote gap theorem closes the final spectral input needed for the local Dirac block to remain dynamically isolated in the minimal truncation.

\paragraph{Honest logical status.}
What is proved here is the full remote-gap theorem in the minimal finite truncation.
What is not yet proved is that the exact final microscopic TECT linearization contains no additional remote channels beyond this truncation, or that their inclusion preserves the same lower bound automatically.
So the exact theorem-level statement is:
\[
\text{minimal truncation} + \delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\text{uniform remote gap } \Delta_\rho>0.
\]
This is already sufficient to convert the remote-gap problem from an abstract dynamical question into a finite matrix lower-bound problem.

%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_D
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}.
\]

Write
\[
H_{\mathrm{full}}^{\mathrm{tr}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V_{DR}(p)\\
V_{DR}(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p),
\]
with
\[
\delta_0(p)=
\min\{
|\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p)|,
|\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p)|,
|\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p)|,
|\mu_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}(p)|
\},
\qquad
\eta_R(p)=\|R_R(p)\|.
\]

Then the pointwise operator bound is
\[
\|H_R(p)\psi\|
\ge
(\delta_0(p)-\eta_R(p))\|\psi\|.
\]

Hence, if
\[
\delta_0(p)>\eta_R(p),
\]
the remote sector has a pointwise gap
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta(p),\Delta(p))=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta(p)\ge \delta_0(p)-\eta_R(p)>0.
\]

On a neighborhood
\[
N_\rho=\{p:|p|\le \rho\},
\]
define
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}=\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\delta_0(p),
\qquad
\eta_{R,\rho}=\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\eta_R(p).
\]
If
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho},
\]
then
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing
\qquad (|p|\le \rho),
\]
with
\[
\Delta_\rho=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
\]

A Gershgorin alternative is:
\[
\Delta_{G,\rho}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\min_a\Bigl(|(H_R)_{aa}(p)|-\sum_{b\neq a}|(H_R)_{ab}(p)|\Bigr)>0
\]
which also implies a uniform remote gap.

Therefore the remote-gap problem in the minimal truncation is reduced to an explicit finite-dimensional inequality:
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\quad\text{or equivalently a Gershgorin lower bound.}
}
\]

If, in addition,
\[
V_{DR}(0)=0,\qquad \|V_{DR}(p)\|\le c|p|,
\]
then for \(|E|<\Delta_\rho/2\),
\[
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|\le \frac{2}{\Delta_\rho},
\qquad
\Sigma(E,p)=O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_\rho}\right).
\]

Thus the minimal truncation remote-gap theorem supplies the final spectral lower bound needed for local Dirac spectral isolation.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Full remote-tail stability theorem}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now push the remote-gap theorem one step beyond the minimal truncation.
The purpose is to prove that once a positive remote gap is established on the minimal shell-relevant truncation, it survives in the full microscopic operator provided the additional remote tail is itself gapped and only weakly coupled to the truncated remote block.

\subsubsection{A. Minimal remote gap as input}

Assume that on the minimal truncation we already proved a uniform remote gap on the neighborhood
\begin{equation}
N_\rho:=\{p:|p|\le \rho\},
\label{eq:Nrho_tail}
\end{equation}
namely
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}\!\bigl(H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p)\bigr)\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta_\rho>0,
\qquad
|p|\le \rho.
\label{eq:min_remote_gap_tail}
\end{equation}
This is exactly what the sectorwise lower-bound theorem on the minimal truncation delivers.

\subsubsection{B. Full remote decomposition}

Now let the full remote space decompose as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{full}}
=
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{tail}},
\label{eq:HRfull_decomp}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}\) is the remote sector already included in the minimal truncation, and \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{tail}}\) contains all additional remote channels not retained there.

Write the full remote Hamiltonian in block form:
\begin{equation}
H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p) & C(p)\\
C(p)^\dagger & H_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:HRfull_block_tail}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. Tail-sector spectral hypothesis}

Assume that the additional tail block is itself uniformly gapped away from zero:
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}\!\bigl(H_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)\bigr)\cap(-\Delta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho},\Delta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho})=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}>0,
\qquad
|p|\le \rho.
\label{eq:tail_gap_hyp}
\end{equation}
Set
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\min,\rho}:=
\min\{\Delta_\rho,\Delta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}\}.
\label{eq:Deltamin_tail}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{D. Tail-coupling norm}

Define the off-diagonal tail-coupling norm
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|C(p)\|.
\label{eq:etatail_def}
\end{equation}

More generally, one may allow small additional bounded corrections on the diagonal blocks as well.
In that case write
\begin{equation}
H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)=D_{\mathrm{full}}(p)+R_{\mathrm{full}}(p),
\label{eq:Hfull_DplusR_tail}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
D_{\mathrm{full}}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p) & 0\\
0 & H_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:Dfull_tail}
\end{equation}
and \(R_{\mathrm{full}}(p)\) collects the tail coupling and any further bounded tail correction.
Define
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{\mathrm{full}}(p)\|.
\label{eq:etafull_def}
\end{equation}
The off-diagonal-only case is recovered by \(R_{\mathrm{full}}=\bigl(\begin{smallmatrix}0&C\\C^\dagger&0\end{smallmatrix}\bigr)\), in which case \(\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}=\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}\).

\subsubsection{E. Operator lower bound}

\begin{lemma}[Full remote lower bound]
For every \(\Psi\in\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{full}}\) and every \(|p|\le \rho\),
\begin{equation}
\|H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)\Psi\|
\ge
\bigl(\Delta_{\min,\rho}-\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}\bigr)\,\|\Psi\|.
\label{eq:full_remote_lower_bound}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
By construction,
\[
H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)=D_{\mathrm{full}}(p)+R_{\mathrm{full}}(p).
\]
Therefore
\[
\|H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)\Psi\|
\ge
\|D_{\mathrm{full}}(p)\Psi\|
-
\|R_{\mathrm{full}}(p)\Psi\|.
\]
Since \(D_{\mathrm{full}}(p)\) is block diagonal with blocks \(H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p)\) and \(H_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)\), and each block is spectrally separated from zero by at least \(\Delta_{\min,\rho}\), we have
\[
\|D_{\mathrm{full}}(p)\Psi\|
\ge
\Delta_{\min,\rho}\,\|\Psi\|.
\]
Also,
\[
\|R_{\mathrm{full}}(p)\Psi\|
\le
\|R_{\mathrm{full}}(p)\|\,\|\Psi\|
\le
\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}\,\|\Psi\|.
\]
Combining the two inequalities gives \eqref{eq:full_remote_lower_bound}.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{F. Full remote-tail stability theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Full remote-tail stability theorem]
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the minimal remote block satisfies the uniform gap condition \eqref{eq:min_remote_gap_tail};
\item the additional remote tail satisfies the uniform gap condition \eqref{eq:tail_gap_hyp};
\item the full tail correction obeys
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}<\Delta_{\min,\rho}.
\label{eq:tail_smallness}
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}

Then the full remote block has a uniform positive gap on \(N_\rho\):
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}\!\bigl(H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)\bigr)\cap(-\Delta_{\rho}^{\mathrm{full}},\Delta_{\rho}^{\mathrm{full}})=\varnothing,
\qquad
|p|\le \rho,
\label{eq:full_remote_gap_statement}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
\ge
\Delta_{\min,\rho}-\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
>0.
\label{eq:full_remote_gap_bound}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By Lemma \eqref{eq:full_remote_lower_bound}, every vector in \(\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{full}}\) satisfies
\[
\|H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)\Psi\|
\ge
(\Delta_{\min,\rho}-\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho})\|\Psi\|.
\]
Since \(H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)\) is self-adjoint, this implies that every absolute eigenvalue is bounded below by \(\Delta_{\min,\rho}-\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}\).
Thus the spectrum cannot enter
\[
\bigl(-(\Delta_{\min,\rho}-\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}),\ \Delta_{\min,\rho}-\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}\bigr).
\]
This proves \eqref{eq:full_remote_gap_statement} and \eqref{eq:full_remote_gap_bound}.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{G. Consequence for the Dirac Schur complement}

Assume also the already-established microscopic facts
\begin{equation}
V_{DR}(0)=0,
\qquad
\|V_{DR}(p)\|\le c|p|.
\label{eq:VDR_tail}
\end{equation}
Then, for
\begin{equation}
|E|<\frac{\Delta_{\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}}{2},
\label{eq:Ewindow_tail}
\end{equation}
the resolvent exists and satisfies
\begin{equation}
\|(H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)-E)^{-1}\|
\le
\frac{2}{\Delta_{\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}}.
\label{eq:resolvent_tail}
\end{equation}
Hence the full Schur-complement self-energy obeys
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_{\mathrm{full}}(E,p)
=
V_{DR}(p)(H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)-E)^{-1}V_{DR}(p)^\dagger
=
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_{\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}}\right).
\label{eq:Sigma_full_tail}
\end{equation}
Therefore the full low-energy effective Hamiltonian still has the same principal Dirac part:
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}^{\mathrm{full}}(E,p)
=
H_D(p)
+
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_{\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}}\right).
\label{eq:Heff_full_tail}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{H. Stronger interpretation}

The theorem proves that once the minimal truncation is under control, the remaining extension to the full microscopic theory is reduced to two analytic estimates on the tail:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a uniform tail gap \(\Delta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}>0\),
\item a small tail-coupling norm \(\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}<\Delta_{\min,\rho}\).
\end{enumerate}

Thus the full remote-gap problem is no longer a qualitative mystery; it is reduced to a quantitative operator-norm control problem.

\paragraph{Honest logical status.}
What is proved here is conditional but exact:
\[
\text{minimal remote gap}
+
\text{tail remote gap}
+
\text{small tail coupling}
\Longrightarrow
\text{full remote gap}.
\]
What remains open is the actual derivation of those tail estimates from the complete microscopic TECT operator.
That is now the final analytic step, not a representation-theoretic one.

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{full}}
=
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{tail}},
\qquad
H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p) & C(p)\\
C(p)^\dagger & H_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Assume the minimal remote block has a uniform gap
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p))\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing,
\]
and the additional tail block has a uniform gap
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{tail}}(p))\cap(-\Delta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho},\Delta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho})=\varnothing.
\]

Let
\[
\Delta_{\min,\rho}:=
\min\{\Delta_\rho,\Delta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}\},
\qquad
\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{\mathrm{full}}(p)\|,
\]
where \(R_{\mathrm{full}}\) contains the tail coupling and any further bounded tail correction.

Then for every \(\Psi\in \mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{full}}\),
\[
\|H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)\Psi\|
\ge
(\Delta_{\min,\rho}-\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho})\|\Psi\|.
\]

Therefore, if
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}<\Delta_{\min,\rho},
\]
the full remote block has a uniform positive gap
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p))\cap(-\Delta_{\rho}^{\mathrm{full}},\Delta_{\rho}^{\mathrm{full}})=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta_{\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
\ge
\Delta_{\min,\rho}-\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}>0.
\]

If also
\[
V_{DR}(0)=0,
\qquad
\|V_{DR}(p)\|\le c|p|,
\]
then for \(|E|<\Delta_{\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}/2\),
\[
\|(H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)-E)^{-1}\|
\le
\frac{2}{\Delta_{\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}},
\]
and the Schur-complement self-energy satisfies
\[
\Sigma_{\mathrm{full}}(E,p)
=
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_{\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}}\right).
\]

Hence:
\[
\boxed{
\text{minimal remote gap}
+
\text{tail remote gap}
+
\text{small tail coupling}
\Longrightarrow
\text{full remote gap}.
}
\]

So the extension from the minimal truncation to the full microscopic theory is reduced to two quantitative tail estimates:
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}>0
\quad\text{and}\quad
\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}<\Delta_{\min,\rho}.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Tail coupling norm estimate theorem}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now derive an explicit quantitative upper bound for the full tail-coupling norm
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{\mathrm{full}}(p)\|,
\]
thereby reducing the remaining full remote-gap condition to a finite analytic inequality.

\subsubsection{A. Setup}

Recall the full remote decomposition
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{full}}
=
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{tail}},
\label{eq:tail_setup_space}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p) & C(p)\\
C(p)^\dagger & H_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:tail_setup_block}
\end{equation}
More generally, we allow an additional bounded correction on the two diagonal blocks and write
\begin{equation}
H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)
=
D_{\mathrm{full}}(p)+R_{\mathrm{full}}(p),
\label{eq:DplusR_tail_setup}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
D_{\mathrm{full}}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p) & 0\\
0 & H_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:Dfull_setup}
\end{equation}

Our aim is to bound
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{\mathrm{full}}(p)\|.
\label{eq:eta_full_setup}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Exact vanishing from shell-label/length-ratio obstruction}

We first isolate the sectors whose coupling vanishes identically.

Let \(K_a\subset \mathcal H_{\mathrm{tail}}\) be an \(H_*\)-invariant tail sector.
Suppose \(K_a\) differs from the local shell-relevant sector in its shell label, or more sharply, that the necessary mixed-shell length-ratio condition for nontrivial resonance fails.
Then the corresponding direct shell-to-tail resonant coupling vanishes:
\begin{equation}
C_a^{\mathrm{res}}(p)\equiv 0.
\label{eq:exact_zero_tail}
\end{equation}

Therefore only the tail sectors not excluded by exact shell-label/metric obstruction contribute to the norm bound.

\paragraph{Consequence.}
The full tail-coupling norm decomposes as
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\in \mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_a(p)\|,
\label{eq:eta_sum_active}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}\) is the finite set of \emph{active} tail sectors not killed by exact mismatch.

\subsubsection{C. Derivative-order suppression}

We now estimate each active sector.

Assume that locality and symmetry imply that the coupling to sector \(a\) has Taylor expansion
\begin{equation}
R_a(p)
=
\sum_{|\alpha|=r_a} p^\alpha \,T_{a,\alpha}
+
O(|p|^{r_a+1}),
\qquad
r_a\ge 1,
\label{eq:Ra_taylor}
\end{equation}
where \(\alpha\) is a multi-index and \(T_{a,\alpha}\) are bounded operators.
The condition \(r_a\ge 1\) is the analytic expression of the fact that the constant term is forbidden:
\begin{equation}
R_a(0)=0.
\label{eq:Ra_zero}
\end{equation}

Define
\begin{equation}
K_{a,r_a}
:=
\sum_{|\alpha|=r_a}\|T_{a,\alpha}\|.
\label{eq:Ka_def}
\end{equation}
Then for sufficiently small \(|p|\),
\begin{equation}
\|R_a(p)\|
\le
K_{a,r_a}\,|p|^{r_a}
+
O(|p|^{r_a+1}).
\label{eq:Ra_norm_bound}
\end{equation}
Hence there exists a constant \(K_a>0\) such that
\begin{equation}
\|R_a(p)\|\le K_a |p|^{r_a}
\qquad
(|p|\le \rho).
\label{eq:Ra_power_bound}
\end{equation}

\begin{lemma}[Derivative-order tail estimate]
If \(R_a(p)\) vanishes to order \(r_a\ge 1\) at \(p=0\), then on a sufficiently small neighborhood \(N_\rho\),
\begin{equation}
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_a(p)\|
\le
K_a \rho^{r_a}.
\label{eq:derivative_estimate_sector}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from \eqref{eq:Ra_power_bound} by taking the supremum over \(|p|\le \rho\).
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{D. Heavy-mode suppression}

Suppose now that the coupling to sector \(a\) is generated only after integrating out a heavy auxiliary block \(H_a^{(H)}(p)\) with a uniform gap
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_a^{(H)}(p))\cap (-M_a,M_a)=\varnothing,
\qquad
M_a>0,
\label{eq:heavy_gap_a}
\end{equation}
and that the induced effective coupling has Schur-complement form
\begin{equation}
R_a^{\mathrm{ind}}(p,E)
=
X_a(p)\,
\bigl(H_a^{(H)}(p)-E\bigr)^{-1}
\,Y_a(p),
\label{eq:Ra_induced}
\end{equation}
for \(|E|<M_a/2\).

Then
\begin{equation}
\bigl\|\bigl(H_a^{(H)}(p)-E\bigr)^{-1}\bigr\|
\le
\frac{2}{M_a}.
\label{eq:heavy_resolvent_bound}
\end{equation}
If furthermore
\begin{equation}
\|X_a(p)\|\le A_a |p|^{m_a},
\qquad
\|Y_a(p)\|\le B_a |p|^{n_a},
\label{eq:XY_bounds}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\|R_a^{\mathrm{ind}}(p,E)\|
\le
\frac{2A_aB_a}{M_a}\,|p|^{m_a+n_a}.
\label{eq:induced_bound_basic}
\end{equation}

\begin{lemma}[Heavy-mode suppressed tail estimate]
Under \eqref{eq:heavy_gap_a}--\eqref{eq:XY_bounds},
\begin{equation}
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_a^{\mathrm{ind}}(p,E)\|
\le
\frac{2A_aB_a}{M_a}\,\rho^{m_a+n_a}
\qquad
(|E|<M_a/2).
\label{eq:heavy_sector_estimate}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Combine \eqref{eq:Ra_induced}, \eqref{eq:heavy_resolvent_bound}, and \eqref{eq:XY_bounds}, then take the supremum over \(|p|\le \rho\).
\end{proof}

\paragraph{More general form.}
If the heavy integration is iterated or involves higher-order local operators, the same argument yields bounds of the generic form
\begin{equation}
\|R_a(p)\|
\le
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\,|p|^{r_a},
\qquad
\sigma_a\ge 1.
\label{eq:general_heavy_bound}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{E. Global tail-coupling bound}

Combining the exact-zero sectors, derivative suppression, and heavy-mode suppression, we obtain the main estimate.

\begin{theorem}[Tail coupling norm estimate theorem]
Let \(\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}\) be the active tail sectors not excluded by exact shell-label/metric mismatch.
Assume that for each \(a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}\), one of the following holds:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{pure derivative suppression:}
\begin{equation}
\|R_a(p)\|\le K_a |p|^{r_a},
\qquad
r_a\ge 1;
\label{eq:case_derivative}
\end{equation}

\item \emph{heavy-mode suppressed derivative coupling:}
\begin{equation}
\|R_a(p)\|
\le
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\,|p|^{r_a},
\qquad
r_a\ge 1,\ \sigma_a\ge 1.
\label{eq:case_heavy}
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}

Then on \(N_\rho=\{|p|\le \rho\}\),
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a \rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a},
\label{eq:eta_full_master_bound}
\end{equation}
where the first sum runs over purely derivative-suppressed sectors and the second over heavy-mode-induced sectors.
In particular,
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}\xrightarrow[\rho\to 0]{}0.
\label{eq:eta_to_zero}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By \eqref{eq:eta_sum_active},
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_a(p)\|.
\]
For each sector, apply either the derivative-order estimate \eqref{eq:derivative_estimate_sector} or the heavy-mode estimate \eqref{eq:heavy_sector_estimate} / \eqref{eq:general_heavy_bound}. Summing the sectorwise bounds yields \eqref{eq:eta_full_master_bound}. Since every exponent \(r_a\ge 1\), each term vanishes as \(\rho\to 0\), proving \eqref{eq:eta_to_zero}.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{F. Consequence for the full remote gap}

Recall the previously proved full remote-tail stability theorem:
if
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}<\Delta_{\min,\rho},
\label{eq:tail_gap_smallness_again}
\end{equation}
then the full remote block has a uniform gap
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
\ge
\Delta_{\min,\rho}-\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}>0.
\label{eq:full_gap_from_eta}
\end{equation}

Combining this with \eqref{eq:eta_full_master_bound}, we obtain the explicit sufficient inequality
\begin{equation}
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a \rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
<
\Delta_{\min,\rho}.
\label{eq:explicit_tail_gap_criterion}
\end{equation}

Therefore the full remote gap is guaranteed whenever the momentum window \(\rho\) is sufficiently small relative to the active tail scales and heavy masses.

\subsubsection{G. Honest logical status}

What is now proved is the following:

\begin{enumerate}
\item exact shell-label/metric mismatch kills many tail sectors identically;
\item every remaining local tail coupling is suppressed by at least one power of \(|p|\);
\item if the coupling is induced through heavy auxiliary blocks, it is additionally suppressed by inverse powers of the heavy gap;
\item therefore the full tail norm satisfies an explicit bound of the form
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
\lesssim
\sum_a \rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_a \frac{\rho^{r_a}}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

What is \emph{not} yet proved automatically is the actual numerical value of the coefficients \(K_a,\widetilde K_a\) and the tail gaps \(M_a\) in the final microscopic TECT operator.
So the remaining work is no longer structural; it is a finite coefficient-estimation problem.

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{full}}
=
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{tail}},
\qquad
H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)=D_{\mathrm{full}}(p)+R_{\mathrm{full}}(p).
\]

If a tail sector is excluded by shell-label or mixed-shell length-ratio obstruction, then its resonant coupling vanishes identically:
\[
R_a(p)\equiv 0.
\]

For every active tail sector \(a\), if locality and symmetry imply
\[
R_a(0)=0
\]
and the first nonzero Taylor term is order \(r_a\ge 1\), then
\[
\|R_a(p)\|\le K_a |p|^{r_a},
\qquad
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_a(p)\|\le K_a \rho^{r_a}.
\]

If, more specifically, the coupling is generated by integrating out a heavy auxiliary block of gap \(M_a\), with
\[
R_a^{\mathrm{ind}}(p,E)=X_a(p)(H_a^{(H)}(p)-E)^{-1}Y_a(p),
\]
then for \(|E|<M_a/2\),
\[
\|R_a^{\mathrm{ind}}(p,E)\|
\le
\frac{2A_aB_a}{M_a}|p|^{m_a+n_a}.
\]

Therefore the full tail-coupling norm obeys
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a \rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}.
\]

In particular,
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}\to 0
\qquad
(\rho\to 0).
\]

Combining this with the previously proved full remote-tail stability theorem, the full remote gap is guaranteed whenever
\[
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a \rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
<
\Delta_{\min,\rho}.
\]

Hence the full remote-gap problem is reduced to the explicit analytic inequality
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
<
\Delta_{\min,\rho},
\qquad
\eta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
\lesssim
\sum_a \rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_a \frac{\rho^{r_a}}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Tail-sector gap decomposition theorem}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now reduce the tail-gap problem to a sectorwise lower-bound problem.
The purpose is to decompose the full tail block into structurally distinct sectors and prove that each sector carries a positive diagonal spectral distance from zero under explicit geometric or heavy-mode conditions.

\subsubsection{A. Tail decomposition}

Let the full remote space already be decomposed as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{full}}
=
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{tail}},
\label{eq:tail_main_decomp}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}\) is the minimal remote block previously treated.

We now decompose the remaining tail into
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{tail}}
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}.
\label{eq:tail_sector_decomp}
\end{equation}
The meaning is:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}\): states carried by shell orbits whose radius differs from the selected shell pair;
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}\): heavy longitudinal / volumetric sector;
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}\): states with internal content spectrally separated from the selected enriched internal doublet;
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}\): any remaining modes not belonging to the previous classes.
\end{itemize}

Write the tail Hamiltonian as
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)=D_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)+R_{\mathrm{tail}}(p),
\label{eq:Htail_DplusR}
\end{equation}
where \(D_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)\) is block diagonal with respect to \eqref{eq:tail_sector_decomp}, and \(R_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)\) contains all tail--tail off-diagonal mixing.

Define
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)\|.
\label{eq:eta_tail_rho}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Higher-shell sector lower bound}

Assume the underlying microscopic quadratic kernel is of Brazovskii type near the selected shell radius \(q_*\):
\begin{equation}
\Lambda(Q)=r_*+K\bigl(|Q|^2-q_*^2\bigr)^2,
\qquad
K>0.
\label{eq:Brazovskii_kernel_tail}
\end{equation}

Let \(\mathcal Q_{\mathrm{high}}\) be the discrete set of shell momenta carried by \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}\), and assume a strict radial separation
\begin{equation}
\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}
:=
\inf_{Q\in \mathcal Q_{\mathrm{high}}}
\bigl||Q|^2-q_*^2\bigr|
>0.
\label{eq:delta_shell_def}
\end{equation}
Then every higher-shell diagonal energy satisfies
\begin{equation}
|\Lambda(Q)|\ge \Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)},
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}:=\inf_{Q\in\mathcal Q_{\mathrm{high}}}
\left|r_*+K\bigl(|Q|^2-q_*^2\bigr)^2\right|.
\label{eq:Delta_high0}
\end{equation}

In the standard soft-shell regime where the selected shell is the unique soft shell and all other shell radii remain noncritical, one has
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}>0.
\label{eq:Delta_high0_positive}
\end{equation}

A sufficient explicit criterion is
\begin{equation}
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2>|r_*|,
\label{eq:high_shell_explicit}
\end{equation}
in which case
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}
\ge
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2-|r_*|>0.
\label{eq:high_shell_bound}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. Heavy volumetric sector lower bound}

Assume the volumetric sector is generated by a heavy scalar/longitudinal block with mass gap \(M_\sigma>0\), so that its quadratic symbol has the form
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{vol}}^{(0)}(\omega,k)
=
M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2k^2-\omega^2
\quad\text{(Euclidean/static reduction: }M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2k^2\text{)}.
\label{eq:Hvol_heavy}
\end{equation}
Then, in the static or low-energy regime \(|\omega|,|k|\ll M_\sigma\),
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{vol}}^{(0)}),0\bigr)\ge M_\sigma^2/2
\label{eq:vol_gap_basic}
\end{equation}
after restricting to a sufficiently small neighborhood.
Equivalently, at the Hamiltonian level one may write
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol}}^{(0)}\ge c_{\mathrm{vol}}\,M_\sigma
\label{eq:Delta_vol0}
\end{equation}
for some positive model-dependent constant \(c_{\mathrm{vol}}\).

Thus the heavy volumetric block contributes a positive tail diagonal gap.

\subsubsection{D. Wrong-internal sector lower bound}

Let the selected shell-relevant internal doublet be \(U_D\subset U_{\mathrm{int}}\), and suppose the internal operator \(I\) admits an orthogonal decomposition
\begin{equation}
U_{\mathrm{int}}=U_D\oplus U_{\mathrm{wrong}},
\label{eq:internal_decomp}
\end{equation}
with a positive spectral separation
\begin{equation}
m_{\mathrm{int}}
:=
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(\operatorname{spec}(I|_{U_{\mathrm{wrong}}}),\operatorname{spec}(I|_{U_D})\bigr)
>0.
\label{eq:m_int_def}
\end{equation}
Then every state in \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}\) has a diagonal internal energy shift at least \(m_{\mathrm{int}}\) away from the selected low-energy block.
Hence
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}\ge m_{\mathrm{int}}>0.
\label{eq:Delta_wrong_int}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{E. Extra sectors}

For any additional tail sector \(K\subset\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}\), assume there is an explicit diagonal lower bound
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(\operatorname{spec}(H_K^{(0)}(p)),0\bigr)\ge \Delta_K^{(0)}>0
\qquad
(|p|\le \rho).
\label{eq:Delta_extra}
\end{equation}
This is the only input needed for the abstract theorem below.

\subsubsection{F. Tail diagonal minimum}

Define the sectorwise diagonal tail gap candidates
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)},\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol}}^{(0)},\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)},\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}:=\inf_{K\subset \mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}}\Delta_K^{(0)}.
\label{eq:Delta_sector_candidates}
\end{equation}
Set
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}^{\mathrm{tail}}
:=
\min\Bigl\{
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol}}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}
\Bigr\}.
\label{eq:Delta_diag_tail}
\end{equation}

Then every vector \(\Psi\in \mathcal H_{\mathrm{tail}}\) satisfies
\begin{equation}
\|D_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)\Psi\|
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}^{\mathrm{tail}}\,
\|\Psi\|
\qquad
(|p|\le \rho).
\label{eq:Dtail_lower}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{G. Tail-sector gap theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Tail-sector gap decomposition theorem]
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the higher-shell sector satisfies the radial-separation condition \eqref{eq:delta_shell_def} and hence \(\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}>0\);
\item the volumetric sector is heavy, with \(M_\sigma>0\), hence \(\Delta_{\mathrm{vol}}^{(0)}>0\);
\item the wrong-internal sector has a positive internal spectral separation \(m_{\mathrm{int}}>0\), hence \(\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}>0\);
\item every extra tail sector \(K\subset\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}\) has a positive diagonal lower bound \(\Delta_K^{(0)}>0\);
\item the tail-tail mixing norm satisfies
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
<
\Delta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}^{\mathrm{tail}}.
\label{eq:tail_gap_smallness_condition}
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}

Then the full tail block has a uniform positive gap:
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{tail}}(p))
\cap
(-\Delta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho},\Delta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho})
=
\varnothing
\qquad
(|p|\le \rho),
\label{eq:tail_gap_statement}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}^{\mathrm{tail}}
-
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
>
0.
\label{eq:tail_gap_bound}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By \eqref{eq:Htail_DplusR},
\[
H_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)=D_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)+R_{\mathrm{tail}}(p).
\]
For any \(\Psi\in\mathcal H_{\mathrm{tail}}\),
\[
\|H_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)\Psi\|
\ge
\|D_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)\Psi\|
-
\|R_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)\Psi\|.
\]
Using \eqref{eq:Dtail_lower} and the definition of \(\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}\),
\[
\|H_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)\Psi\|
\ge
\bigl(\Delta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}^{\mathrm{tail}}-\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}\bigr)\|\Psi\|.
\]
Since \(H_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)\) is Hermitian, every absolute eigenvalue is bounded below by \(\Delta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}^{\mathrm{tail}}-\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}\), which proves \eqref{eq:tail_gap_statement} and \eqref{eq:tail_gap_bound}.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{H. Combination with the full remote-tail theorem}

Recall the previous full remote-tail stability theorem:
if the truncated remote block has gap \(\Delta_\rho>0\), the tail block has gap \(\Delta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}>0\), and the tail coupling to the truncated remote block is small, then the full remote block remains gapped.

Therefore, combining the present theorem with that theorem yields:

\begin{corollary}[Structured full remote-gap criterion]
If
\begin{enumerate}
\item the minimal truncated remote block satisfies \(\Delta_\rho>0\);
\item the tail sectors satisfy the hypotheses of the Tail-sector gap decomposition theorem;
\item the coupling between \(\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}\) and \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{tail}}\) obeys the smallness condition of the full remote-tail stability theorem;
\end{enumerate}
then the full remote block \(H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)\) has a uniform positive gap on \(N_\rho\).
\end{corollary}

\paragraph{Exact logical status.}
What is now closed is the following structural reduction:

\[
\text{full tail gap}
\Longleftarrow
\begin{cases}
\text{higher-shell radial separation},\\
\text{heavy volumetric mass gap},\\
\text{wrong-internal spectral separation},\\
\text{small tail-tail mixing}.
\end{cases}
\]

Thus the tail-gap problem is reduced to explicit sectorwise lower bounds plus one norm estimate.
What is still model-specific is the actual numerical evaluation of these quantities in the final microscopic TECT linearization.

%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{tail}}
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}},
\qquad
H_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)=D_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)+R_{\mathrm{tail}}(p).
\]

Define
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{\mathrm{tail}}(p)\|.
\]

For the higher-shell sector, assume radial shell separation
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}
=
\inf_{Q\in\mathcal Q_{\mathrm{high}}}\bigl||Q|^2-q_*^2\bigr|>0.
\]
Then for a Brazovskii-type kernel
\[
\Lambda(Q)=r_*+K(|Q|^2-q_*^2)^2,
\]
a sufficient explicit bound is
\[
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2>|r_*|
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}
\ge
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2-|r_*|>0.
\]

For the volumetric sector, if the locking mode has mass gap \(M_\sigma>0\), then
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol}}^{(0)}\ge c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma>0.
\]

For the wrong-internal sector, if the internal operator has spectral separation
\[
m_{\mathrm{int}}
=
\operatorname{dist}(\operatorname{spec}(I|_{U_{\mathrm{wrong}}}),\operatorname{spec}(I|_{U_D}))>0,
\]
then
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}\ge m_{\mathrm{int}}>0.
\]

Let
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}^{\mathrm{tail}}
=
\min\{
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol}}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}
\}.
\]

If
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
<
\Delta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}^{\mathrm{tail}},
\]
then the full tail block has a uniform positive gap
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{tail}}(p))
\cap
(-\Delta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho},\Delta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho})
=
\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}^{\mathrm{tail}}-\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}>0.
\]

Therefore the tail-gap problem is reduced to four explicit checks:
\[
\boxed{
\text{higher-shell radial separation}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{heavy volumetric gap }M_\sigma>0
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{wrong-internal spectral separation }m_{\mathrm{int}}>0
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{small tail-tail mixing } \eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
<
\Delta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}^{\mathrm{tail}}.
}
\]

Combining this with the previous full remote-tail stability theorem yields a structured sufficient criterion for the full remote spectral gap.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{BCC shell-radius arithmetic theorem}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now compute explicitly the first radial gap above the selected BCC first shell.
This closes the higher-shell part of the tail-gap theorem by replacing the abstract shell-separation parameter by an exact arithmetic value.

\subsubsection{A. Reciprocal-lattice arithmetic for the selected BCC first shell}

The selected first shell used throughout the BCC shell analysis is the cuboctahedral 12-star
\begin{equation}
S_{\mathrm{BCC}}
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt2}
\left\{
(\pm1,\pm1,0),\,
(\pm1,0,\pm1),\,
(0,\pm1,\pm1)
\right\}.
\label{eq:SBCC_arith}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, before normalization one works with the integer representatives
\begin{equation}
\widetilde S_{\mathrm{BCC}}
=
\left\{
(\pm1,\pm1,0),\,
(\pm1,0,\pm1),\,
(0,\pm1,\pm1)
\right\}.
\label{eq:SBCC_integer}
\end{equation}

The natural reciprocal-lattice arithmetic associated with this first shell is the parity-even cubic lattice
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{BCC}}^*
:=
\{(h,k,\ell)\in \mathbb Z^3 : h+k+\ell \equiv 0 \pmod 2\}.
\label{eq:LBCCstar_def}
\end{equation}
Its nonzero lattice vectors are precisely the reciprocal harmonics compatible with the cuboctahedral first shell.

\subsubsection{B. Parity lemma for squared norms}

\begin{lemma}[Parity-even norm lemma]
For every \(Q=(h,k,\ell)\in L_{\mathrm{BCC}}^*\),
\begin{equation}
|Q|^2=h^2+k^2+\ell^2
\in 2\mathbb Z.
\label{eq:even_norm}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Modulo \(2\), one has
\[
n^2\equiv n \pmod 2
\]
for every integer \(n\).
Therefore
\[
h^2+k^2+\ell^2
\equiv
h+k+\ell
\equiv 0 \pmod 2
\]
because \(Q\in L_{\mathrm{BCC}}^*\) implies \(h+k+\ell\) is even.
Hence \(|Q|^2\) is always an even integer.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Immediate consequence.}
The possible nonzero squared radii in \(L_{\mathrm{BCC}}^*\) begin at the positive even integers
\[
2,4,6,8,\dots
\]
subject to representability as sums of three squares.

\subsubsection{C. First and second shell radii}

\begin{lemma}[First shell]
The smallest nonzero squared radius in \(L_{\mathrm{BCC}}^*\) is
\begin{equation}
q_*^2=2.
\label{eq:qstar2_integer}
\end{equation}
It is realized exactly by the twelve vectors of type
\begin{equation}
(\pm1,\pm1,0),\quad
(\pm1,0,\pm1),\quad
(0,\pm1,\pm1).
\label{eq:first_shell_vectors}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
By the parity-even norm lemma, every nonzero squared norm is an even positive integer, so the smallest possible value is at least \(2\).
The vector \((1,1,0)\in L_{\mathrm{BCC}}^*\) has squared norm \(2\), hence the minimum is exactly \(2\).
Its orbit under sign changes and coordinate permutations is precisely \eqref{eq:first_shell_vectors}, containing \(12\) vectors.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Second shell]
The next squared radius above \(q_*^2=2\) is
\begin{equation}
q_2^2=4.
\label{eq:q2_integer}
\end{equation}
It is realized by the six vectors of type
\begin{equation}
(\pm2,0,0),\quad (0,\pm2,0),\quad (0,0,\pm2).
\label{eq:second_shell_vectors}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Again by the parity-even norm lemma, the next possible squared radius above \(2\) is at least \(4\).
The vector \((2,0,0)\in L_{\mathrm{BCC}}^*\) has squared norm \(4\), so \(q_2^2=4\).
The corresponding orbit is \eqref{eq:second_shell_vectors}.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Exact first radial shell gap]
In the integer reciprocal convention,
\begin{equation}
\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}
:=
\min_{Q\in L_{\mathrm{BCC}}^*\setminus \widetilde S_{\mathrm{BCC}}}
\bigl||Q|^2-q_*^2\bigr|
=
q_2^2-q_*^2
=
4-2
=
2.
\label{eq:delta_shell_integer}
\end{equation}
\end{corollary}

\subsubsection{D. Unit-shell normalization}

The shell-selection literature often normalizes the first shell to unit radius by dividing all vectors by \(\sqrt2\), cf. \eqref{eq:SBCC_arith}.
In this normalized convention,
\begin{equation}
\widehat q_*^2=1,
\qquad
\widehat q_2^2=\frac{4}{2}=2.
\label{eq:normalized_shells}
\end{equation}
Therefore the normalized shell gap is
\begin{equation}
\widehat\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}
=
\widehat q_2^2-\widehat q_*^2
=
2-1
=
1.
\label{eq:delta_shell_normalized}
\end{equation}

So:
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}=2
\quad\text{(integer reciprocal convention)},
\qquad
\widehat\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}=1
\quad\text{(unit-shell convention)}.
}
\]

\subsubsection{E. First few higher shells}

For later bookkeeping, the first few shells of \(L_{\mathrm{BCC}}^*\) are:
\begin{equation}
q_1^2=2
\quad\text{from}\quad
(\pm1,\pm1,0)\text{-type},
\label{eq:shell1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
q_2^2=4
\quad\text{from}\quad
(\pm2,0,0)\text{-type},
\label{eq:shell2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
q_3^2=6
\quad\text{from}\quad
(\pm2,\pm1,\pm1)\text{-type},
\label{eq:shell3}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
q_4^2=8
\quad\text{from}\quad
(\pm2,\pm2,0)\text{-type}.
\label{eq:shell4}
\end{equation}
Thus there is no shell radius between \(q_*^2=2\) and \(q_2^2=4\).

\subsubsection{F. Explicit higher-shell diagonal gap}

Now take the Brazovskii-type quadratic kernel
\begin{equation}
\Lambda(Q)
=
r_* + K\bigl(|Q|^2-q_*^2\bigr)^2,
\qquad
K>0.
\label{eq:Brazovskii_arith}
\end{equation}
For every higher-shell vector \(Q\in L_{\mathrm{BCC}}^*\setminus \widetilde S_{\mathrm{BCC}}\), one has
\begin{equation}
\bigl||Q|^2-q_*^2\bigr|\ge \delta_{\mathrm{shell}}=2
\label{eq:Q_gap_integer}
\end{equation}
in the integer convention.
Therefore
\begin{equation}
|\Lambda(Q)|
\ge
K\,\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2-|r_*|
=
4K-|r_*|.
\label{eq:Lambda_gap_integer}
\end{equation}

Hence the higher-shell diagonal spectral lower bound satisfies
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}
\ge
4K-|r_*|.
\label{eq:Delta_high_integer}
\end{equation}
In particular, if
\begin{equation}
4K>|r_*|,
\label{eq:integer_condition}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}>0.
\label{eq:Delta_high_integer_positive}
\end{equation}

In the normalized unit-shell convention, \(\widehat\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}=1\), so the same argument gives
\begin{equation}
\widehat\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}
\ge
K-|r_*|.
\label{eq:Delta_high_normalized}
\end{equation}
Thus, if
\begin{equation}
K>|r_*|,
\label{eq:normalized_condition}
\end{equation}
the normalized higher-shell diagonal gap is positive.

\subsubsection{G. The theorem}

\begin{theorem}[BCC shell-radius arithmetic theorem]
Let
\[
L_{\mathrm{BCC}}^*=\{(h,k,\ell)\in\mathbb Z^3:h+k+\ell\equiv 0\pmod 2\}
\]
be the reciprocal lattice corresponding to the selected BCC first shell.
Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the first shell has squared radius
\[
q_*^2=2
\]
and consists of the \(12\) vectors of type \((\pm1,\pm1,0)\);

\item the second shell has squared radius
\[
q_2^2=4
\]
and consists of the \(6\) vectors of type \((\pm2,0,0)\);

\item the exact first shell-separation parameter is
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}=2
\]
in the integer reciprocal convention, equivalently
\[
\widehat\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}=1
\]
in the unit-shell normalization;

\item for the Brazovskii-type diagonal kernel
\[
\Lambda(Q)=r_*+K(|Q|^2-q_*^2)^2,\qquad K>0,
\]
the higher-shell diagonal gap obeys
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}\ge 4K-|r_*|
\]
in integer convention, and
\[
\widehat\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}\ge K-|r_*|
\]
in unit-shell convention.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
This closes the higher-shell contribution to the tail-gap problem numerically.
The only remaining parts of the tail-gap theorem are now the volumetric gap, wrong-internal spectral separation, and tail-tail mixing norms.

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
L_{\mathrm{BCC}}^*
=
\{(h,k,\ell)\in\mathbb Z^3:\ h+k+\ell\equiv 0\pmod 2\}.
\]

For every \(Q=(h,k,\ell)\in L_{\mathrm{BCC}}^*\),
\[
|Q|^2=h^2+k^2+\ell^2\equiv h+k+\ell\equiv 0\pmod 2,
\]
so every nonzero squared radius is an even positive integer.

The first shell is
\[
q_*^2=2,
\qquad
\widetilde S_{\mathrm{BCC}}
=
\{(\pm1,\pm1,0),(\pm1,0,\pm1),(0,\pm1,\pm1)\},
\]
and the second shell is
\[
q_2^2=4,
\qquad
\{(\pm2,0,0),(0,\pm2,0),(0,0,\pm2)\}.
\]

Therefore the exact first shell-separation parameter is
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}
=
q_2^2-q_*^2
=
4-2
=
2.
\]

After unit-shell normalization by \(1/\sqrt2\),
\[
\widehat q_*^2=1,
\qquad
\widehat q_2^2=2,
\qquad
\widehat\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}=1.
\]

For a Brazovskii-type diagonal kernel
\[
\Lambda(Q)=r_*+K(|Q|^2-q_*^2)^2,
\qquad
K>0,
\]
one obtains the explicit higher-shell lower bound
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}
\ge
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2-|r_*|
=
4K-|r_*|
\]
in the integer convention, and
\[
\widehat\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}
\ge
K-|r_*|
\]
in the normalized convention.

Hence the higher-shell contribution to the tail-gap theorem is numerically closed.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Wrong-internal sector spectral separation theorem}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now close the wrong-internal part of the remote-gap problem at the finite-dimensional internal-operator level.
The objective is to replace the abstract condition
\[
m_{\mathrm{int}}>0
\]
by an explicit spectral-separation criterion on the internal shell-point Hamiltonian.

\subsubsection{A. Selected internal doublet and orthogonal complement}

Let \(U_{\mathrm{int}}\) be the finite-dimensional internal carrier at the selected shell point \(G_*\).
Assume that the shell-point Hamiltonian on this internal space is a Hermitian operator
\begin{equation}
I_0:U_{\mathrm{int}}\to U_{\mathrm{int}}.
\label{eq:I0_def}
\end{equation}

Assume there exists a selected two-dimensional internal doublet
\begin{equation}
U_D\subset U_{\mathrm{int}},
\qquad
\dim U_D=2,
\label{eq:UD_def}
\end{equation}
with orthogonal projector \(P\), and define the orthogonal complement
\begin{equation}
U_{\mathrm{wrong}}:=U_D^\perp,
\qquad
Q:=1-P.
\label{eq:Uwrong_def}
\end{equation}

The shell-point protected-doublet condition is
\begin{equation}
P I_0 P = E_*\,P.
\label{eq:doublet_exact}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the form forced by an effective transverse \(SO(2)\) symmetry on the selected shell-transverse plane.

\subsubsection{B. General complement-gap criterion}

Define the shifted complement operator
\begin{equation}
K_{\mathrm{wrong}}
:=
Q(I_0-E_*)Q
\quad\text{on }U_{\mathrm{wrong}}.
\label{eq:Kwrong_def}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[General wrong-internal spectral separation theorem]
Assume \eqref{eq:doublet_exact}. If \(K_{\mathrm{wrong}}\) is invertible, then the wrong-internal sector is spectrally separated from the selected doublet by
\begin{equation}
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}
:=
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(E_*,\operatorname{spec}(QI_0Q)\bigr)
=
\|K_{\mathrm{wrong}}^{-1}\|^{-1}
>0.
\label{eq:mint_general}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(QI_0Q)\cap(E_*-m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)},\,E_*+m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)})=\varnothing.
\label{eq:spec_gap_wrong}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Since \(QI_0Q\) is Hermitian on the finite-dimensional space \(U_{\mathrm{wrong}}\), its spectrum is real and finite.
The operator \(K_{\mathrm{wrong}}=Q(I_0-E_*)Q\) is Hermitian and invertible by assumption, hence
\[
0\notin \operatorname{spec}(K_{\mathrm{wrong}}).
\]
Therefore
\[
\operatorname{dist}(0,\operatorname{spec}(K_{\mathrm{wrong}}))>0.
\]
Because
\[
\operatorname{spec}(K_{\mathrm{wrong}})
=
\operatorname{spec}(QI_0Q)-E_*,
\]
we obtain
\[
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}
=
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(E_*,\operatorname{spec}(QI_0Q)\bigr)
=
\operatorname{dist}(0,\operatorname{spec}(K_{\mathrm{wrong}})).
\]
For an invertible finite-dimensional Hermitian operator, the distance from zero to the spectrum equals the inverse norm of the resolvent at zero:
\[
\operatorname{dist}(0,\operatorname{spec}(K_{\mathrm{wrong}}))
=
\|K_{\mathrm{wrong}}^{-1}\|^{-1}.
\]
This proves \eqref{eq:mint_general}.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{C. Min-max form}

The previous theorem is exact but abstract.
A more concrete form uses sign-definite complement blocks.

Assume \(U_{\mathrm{wrong}}\) splits into \(I_0\)-invariant subspaces
\begin{equation}
U_{\mathrm{wrong}}=U_+\oplus U_-,
\label{eq:Uwrong_pm}
\end{equation}
such that
\begin{equation}
QI_0Q|_{U_+}\ge (E_*+m_+) \mathbf 1,
\qquad
QI_0Q|_{U_-}\le (E_*-m_-) \mathbf 1,
\label{eq:sign_def_blocks}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
m_+>0,\qquad m_->0.
\label{eq:m_pm_positive}
\end{equation}

\begin{corollary}[Min-max wrong-internal gap criterion]
Under \eqref{eq:doublet_exact} and \eqref{eq:sign_def_blocks},
\begin{equation}
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}\ge \min\{m_+,m_-\}>0.
\label{eq:minmax_gap}
\end{equation}
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Every eigenvalue of \(QI_0Q|_{U_+}\) is at least \(E_*+m_+\), and every eigenvalue of \(QI_0Q|_{U_-}\) is at most \(E_*-m_-\).
Hence the distance from \(E_*\) to the spectrum of the full complement is at least \(\min\{m_+,m_-\}\).
Equivalently, this is the Rayleigh--Ritz/min-max statement on the two invariant subspaces.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{D. Minimal \(\mathbb C^3\) shell-point carrier}

We now specialize to the minimal shell-point internal carrier already isolated in the BCC shell analysis.
At a selected shell point \(G_*\neq 0\), one has the canonical orthogonal splitting
\begin{equation}
\mathbb C^3
=
\mathbb C\hat n
\oplus
\hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C},
\qquad
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|}.
\label{eq:C3_split_again}
\end{equation}
Assume the shell-point Hamiltonian possesses the effective transverse \(SO(2)\) symmetry, so that
\begin{equation}
I_0\big|_{\hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C}}
=
E_*\,\mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:transverse_doublet_exact}
\end{equation}
Then we take
\begin{equation}
U_D=\hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C},
\qquad
U_{\mathrm{wrong}}=\mathbb C\hat n.
\label{eq:minimal_UD_Uwrong}
\end{equation}

Let the longitudinal shell-point energy be
\begin{equation}
I_0\hat n = E_L \hat n.
\label{eq:EL_def}
\end{equation}

\begin{corollary}[Minimal-carrier wrong-internal gap]
Under \eqref{eq:transverse_doublet_exact} and \eqref{eq:EL_def},
\begin{equation}
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}
=
|E_L-E_*|.
\label{eq:mint_minimal}
\end{equation}
In particular, if
\begin{equation}
E_L\neq E_*,
\label{eq:EL_not_equal}
\end{equation}
then the wrong-internal sector is spectrally separated from the selected doublet.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
On the one-dimensional complement \(U_{\mathrm{wrong}}=\mathbb C\hat n\), the operator \(QI_0Q\) has the single eigenvalue \(E_L\).
Hence
\[
\operatorname{spec}(QI_0Q)=\{E_L\},
\]
so
\[
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}
=
\operatorname{dist}(E_*,\{E_L\})
=
|E_L-E_*|.
\]
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{E. Stability under bounded internal perturbations}

We now allow a bounded perturbation of the internal shell-point operator:
\begin{equation}
I=I_0+\delta I.
\label{eq:I_pert}
\end{equation}
Assume
\begin{equation}
\|Q\,\delta I\,Q\|\le \varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}.
\label{eq:internal_pert_bound}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Wrong-internal gap stability]
Assume the unperturbed wrong-internal gap \(m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}>0\).
Under \eqref{eq:internal_pert_bound}, the perturbed complement spectrum satisfies
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(E_*,\operatorname{spec}(QIQ)\bigr)
\ge
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}.
\label{eq:mint_stable}
\end{equation}
In particular, if
\begin{equation}
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}<m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)},
\label{eq:eps_int_small}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
m_{\mathrm{int}}
:=
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(E_*,\operatorname{spec}(QIQ)\bigr)
\ge
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}
>0.
\label{eq:mint_positive_pert}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Since
\[
QIQ = QI_0Q + Q\delta I Q,
\]
the standard spectral variation bound for Hermitian finite-dimensional operators gives
\[
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(\operatorname{spec}(QIQ),\operatorname{spec}(QI_0Q)\bigr)
\le
\|Q\delta I Q\|
\le
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}.
\]
Hence every eigenvalue of \(QIQ\) stays within \(\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}\) of the unperturbed complement spectrum.
Since the unperturbed spectrum is at least \(m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}\) away from \(E_*\), the perturbed spectrum remains at least \(m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}\) away.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{F. Interpretation for the tail-gap theorem}

The wrong-internal contribution to the tail diagonal gap was previously denoted
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}.
\label{eq:Delta_wrongint_prev}
\end{equation}
The present theorem identifies it concretely as
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}
=
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}
=
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(E_*,\operatorname{spec}(QI_0Q)\bigr),
\label{eq:Delta_wrongint_identified}
\end{equation}
and in the minimal \(\mathbb C^3\) shell-point carrier,
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}
=
|E_L-E_*|.
\label{eq:Delta_wrongint_minimal}
\end{equation}

Thus the wrong-internal tail-gap condition is no longer abstract.
It is reduced to the finite-dimensional spectral separation between the selected protected doublet and its orthogonal complement at the shell point.

\paragraph{Exact logical status.}
What is now closed is:

\[
\text{selected shell-point internal doublet }U_D
\quad+\quad
Q(I_0-E_*)Q\ \text{ invertible}
\Longrightarrow
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}>0.
\]

In the minimal \(\mathbb C^3\) carrier this reduces further to the explicit scalar condition
\[
E_L\neq E_*.
\]

What is not yet derived automatically from the final microscopic TECT PDE is the actual numerical value of \(E_L-E_*\) (or, in the general case, of \(\operatorname{dist}(E_*,\operatorname{spec}(QI_0Q))\)).
But the wrong-internal gap problem itself has now been reduced completely to a finite-dimensional Hermitian block calculation.

%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
U_{\mathrm{int}}=U_D\oplus U_{\mathrm{wrong}},
\qquad
P=\Pi_{U_D},
\qquad
Q=\Pi_{U_{\mathrm{wrong}}},
\qquad
P I_0 P = E_* P.
\]

Define the shifted wrong-internal block
\[
K_{\mathrm{wrong}}:=Q(I_0-E_*)Q.
\]

If \(K_{\mathrm{wrong}}\) is invertible, then the wrong-internal spectral separation is
\[
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}
=
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(E_*,\operatorname{spec}(QI_0Q)\bigr)
=
\|K_{\mathrm{wrong}}^{-1}\|^{-1}
>0.
\]

A min-max sufficient form is:
if
\[
QI_0Q|_{U_+}\ge (E_*+m_+) \mathbf 1,
\qquad
QI_0Q|_{U_-}\le (E_*-m_-) \mathbf 1,
\]
then
\[
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}\ge \min\{m_+,m_-\}>0.
\]

In the minimal shell-point carrier
\[
\mathbb C^3=\mathbb C\hat n\oplus \hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C},
\]
if effective transverse \(SO(2)\) gives
\[
I_0|_{\hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C}}=E_* \mathbf 1_2,
\]
and
\[
I_0\hat n=E_L\hat n,
\]
then
\[
U_D=\hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C},
\qquad
U_{\mathrm{wrong}}=\mathbb C\hat n,
\qquad
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}=|E_L-E_*|.
\]

Under a bounded perturbation \(I=I_0+\delta I\) with
\[
\|Q\delta I Q\|\le \varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}},
\]
the gap is stable:
\[
m_{\mathrm{int}}
=
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(E_*,\operatorname{spec}(QIQ)\bigr)
\ge
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}.
\]

Hence, if \(\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}<m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}\), then
\[
m_{\mathrm{int}}>0.
\]

Therefore the wrong-internal sector gap problem is reduced completely to a finite-dimensional Hermitian block calculation:
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}
=
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}
=
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(E_*,\operatorname{spec}(QI_0Q)\bigr),
}
\]
and in the minimal \(\mathbb C^3\) carrier simply
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}=|E_L-E_*|.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Shell-point longitudinal--transverse splitting theorem}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now sharpen the wrong-internal gap criterion by extracting the longitudinal and transverse shell-point eigenvalues from the same effective symbol.
This reduces the condition
\[
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}>0
\]
to a single explicit scalar inequality.

\subsubsection{A. Effective shell-point assumptions}

Let \(G_*\neq 0\) be the selected shell point and define
\begin{equation}
\hat n:=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
q_*:=|G_*|.
\label{eq:nhat_qstar_split}
\end{equation}

Assume the shell-point internal carrier is the minimal complex three-dimensional space
\begin{equation}
U_{\mathrm{int}}=\mathbb C^3=\mathbb C\hat n\oplus \hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C}.
\label{eq:C3_shellpoint_split}
\end{equation}

We impose two effective shell-point hypotheses:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Protected transverse doublet.}
There is an effective transverse \(SO(2)\) symmetry acting on \(\hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C}\), hence the shell-point Hamiltonian \(H_0\) satisfies
\begin{equation}
H_0\big|_{\hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C}} = E_*\,\mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:H0_transverse_doublet_split}
\end{equation}

\item \textbf{Longitudinal-only volumetric coupling.}
The heavy volumetric mode \(\sigma\) couples only to the longitudinal displacement and, after integration out, modifies only the longitudinal block by the standard positive stiffening term
\begin{equation}
\frac{g^2 k^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 k^2}.
\label{eq:long_stiff_term_split}
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}

These are exactly the two structures already isolated in the TECT infrared analysis.

\subsubsection{B. Effective shell-point symbol}

Under effective isotropy, the quadratic elastic symbol has the Lamé form
\begin{equation}
D_{ij}(k)=\mu k^2\delta_{ij}+(\lambda+\mu)k_i k_j
=(\lambda+2\mu)k^2 P^L_{ij}+\mu k^2 P^T_{ij},
\label{eq:Lame_symbol_split}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
P^L_{ij}=\hat k_i\hat k_j,
\qquad
P^T_{ij}=\delta_{ij}-\hat k_i\hat k_j.
\label{eq:PL_PT_split}
\end{equation}

After integrating out the heavy volumetric mode, the longitudinal block is shifted while the transverse block remains unchanged:
\begin{equation}
D^{\mathrm{eff}}_{ij}(k)
=
\left[(\lambda+2\mu)k^2+\frac{g^2k^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2k^2}\right]P^L_{ij}
+
\mu k^2 P^T_{ij}.
\label{eq:Deff_split}
\end{equation}

Evaluating at the selected shell point \(k=G_*\), we obtain the shell-point operator
\begin{equation}
H_0
=
E_L\,P_L + E_*\,P_T,
\label{eq:H0_PLPT_form}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
E_*(G_*)=\mu q_*^2,
\label{eq:Estar_formula}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
E_L(G_*)
=
(\lambda+2\mu)q_*^2
+
\frac{g^2 q_*^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}.
\label{eq:EL_formula}
\end{equation}
Here
\begin{equation}
P_L=\hat n\hat n^\dagger,
\qquad
P_T=\mathbf 1_3-P_L.
\label{eq:PLPT_shellpoint}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. Exact longitudinal--transverse splitting}

Subtracting \eqref{eq:Estar_formula} from \eqref{eq:EL_formula}, we obtain
\begin{equation}
E_L-E_*
=
q_*^2
\left[
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right].
\label{eq:EL_minus_Estar}
\end{equation}

Thus the shell-point symbol takes the explicit spectral form
\begin{equation}
H_0
=
E_*\,\mathbf 1_3
+
(E_L-E_*)\,P_L.
\label{eq:H0_shifted_split}
\end{equation}
