Hence the transverse plane \(\hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C}\) is a protected exact doublet of energy \(E_*\), while the longitudinal line \(\mathbb C\hat n\) has energy \(E_L\).

\begin{theorem}[Shell-point longitudinal--transverse splitting theorem]
Under the effective shell-point assumptions above, the shell-point operator on \(\mathbb C^3=\mathbb C\hat n\oplus \hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C}\) has the exact spectral decomposition
\begin{equation}
H_0 = E_L P_L + E_* P_T,
\label{eq:H0_splitting_thm}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
E_*(G_*)=\mu q_*^2,
\qquad
E_L(G_*)=(\lambda+2\mu)q_*^2+\frac{g^2 q_*^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2},
\label{eq:EL_Estar_thm}
\end{equation}
and splitting
\begin{equation}
E_L-E_*
=
q_*^2
\left[
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right].
\label{eq:splitting_thm}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Equation \eqref{eq:Lame_symbol_split} gives the isotropic elastic decomposition into one longitudinal and two transverse sectors.
Equation \eqref{eq:Deff_split} shows that the heavy volumetric mode contributes only to the longitudinal block.
Evaluating at \(k=G_*\) yields \eqref{eq:H0_PLPT_form}, with eigenvalues \eqref{eq:Estar_formula} and \eqref{eq:EL_formula}. Subtracting them gives \eqref{eq:splitting_thm}.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{D. Wrong-internal gap in the minimal shell-point carrier}

Take the selected protected doublet to be
\begin{equation}
U_D=\hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C},
\qquad
U_{\mathrm{wrong}}=\mathbb C\hat n.
\label{eq:UD_Uwrong_minimal_split}
\end{equation}
Then the wrong-internal spectral gap is precisely
\begin{equation}
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}
=
|E_L-E_*|.
\label{eq:mint_split_formula}
\end{equation}

Therefore:

\begin{corollary}[Explicit wrong-internal gap formula]
In the minimal shell-point carrier,
\begin{equation}
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}
=
q_*^2
\left|
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|.
\label{eq:mint_explicit_final}
\end{equation}
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Since \(U_{\mathrm{wrong}}=\mathbb C\hat n\) is one-dimensional and \(H_0\hat n=E_L\hat n\), the complement spectrum is \(\{E_L\}\), while the selected doublet energy is \(E_*\). Hence
\[
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}=|E_L-E_*|.
\]
Substituting \eqref{eq:splitting_thm} gives \eqref{eq:mint_explicit_final}.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{E. Sufficient conditions for nonvanishing}

The exact condition for wrong-internal separation is simply
\begin{equation}
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\neq 0.
\label{eq:nonzero_condition_exact}
\end{equation}
This is already enough to guarantee
\[
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}>0.
\]

A stronger sufficient condition is positivity:
\begin{equation}
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
>0.
\label{eq:positive_condition}
\end{equation}
Under \eqref{eq:positive_condition},
\begin{equation}
E_L>E_*,
\qquad
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}
=
q_*^2
\left[
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right]
>0.
\label{eq:positive_gap_formula}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Genericity remark.}
If \(g\neq 0\), then the cancellation condition
\[
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
=0
\]
defines a codimension-one locus in the parameter space.
Hence nonzero splitting is generic.

\subsubsection{F. Stability under bounded shell-point perturbations}

Let the shell-point operator be perturbed:
\begin{equation}
H = H_0 + \delta H.
\label{eq:H_shell_pert}
\end{equation}
Assume the perturbation respects the selected decomposition to leading order and satisfies
\begin{equation}
\|Q\,\delta H\,Q\|\le \varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}},
\qquad
Q=P_L.
\label{eq:QdHQ_bound}
\end{equation}
Then by the finite-dimensional spectral stability theorem already proved for the wrong-internal block,
\begin{equation}
m_{\mathrm{int}}
\ge
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}.
\label{eq:mint_pert_stable_again}
\end{equation}
In particular, if
\begin{equation}
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}<m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)},
\label{eq:eps_small_split}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
m_{\mathrm{int}}>0.
\label{eq:mint_positive_perturb}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{G. Honest logical status}

What is now genuinely closed is the following conditional theorem chain:
\[
\text{effective transverse }SO(2)
\quad+\quad
\text{longitudinal-only volumetric locking}
\Longrightarrow
H_0 = E_L P_L + E_* P_T
\Longrightarrow
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}=|E_L-E_*|.
\]

In the minimal shell-point carrier this becomes the explicit scalar formula
\[
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}
=
q_*^2
\left|
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|.
\]

What remains open is not the structure of the gap, but only the actual microscopic verification that the shell-point problem of the full TECT linearization indeed falls into this effective shell-point class.

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\mathbb C^3=\mathbb C\hat n\oplus \hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C},
\qquad
P_L=\hat n\hat n^\dagger,
\qquad
P_T=\mathbf 1_3-P_L,
\qquad
q_*=|G_*|.
\]

If the shell-point Hamiltonian has an effective transverse \(SO(2)\), then
\[
H_0\big|_{\hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C}}=E_*\,\mathbf 1_2.
\]

If, moreover, the heavy volumetric mode couples only to the longitudinal sector and has gap \(M_\sigma>0\), then the effective shell-point symbol is
\[
H_0
=
E_L P_L + E_* P_T,
\]
with
\[
E_*(G_*)=\mu q_*^2,
\qquad
E_L(G_*)
=
(\lambda+2\mu)q_*^2
+
\frac{g^2 q_*^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}.
\]

Therefore the longitudinal--transverse splitting is
\[
E_L-E_*
=
q_*^2
\left[
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right].
\]

In the minimal shell-point carrier
\[
U_D=\hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C},
\qquad
U_{\mathrm{wrong}}=\mathbb C\hat n,
\]
the wrong-internal gap is exactly
\[
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}=|E_L-E_*|
=
q_*^2
\left|
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|.
\]

Hence the exact sufficient condition for wrong-internal separation is
\[
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\neq 0.
\]

A stronger sufficient condition is
\[
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
>0,
\]
which implies
\[
E_L>E_*,
\qquad
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}>0.
\]

Under a bounded perturbation \(H=H_0+\delta H\) with
\[
\|Q\,\delta H\,Q\|\le \varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}},
\qquad Q=P_L,
\]
the gap is stable:
\[
m_{\mathrm{int}}\ge m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}.
\]

Thus the wrong-internal gap is reduced to an explicit shell-point scalar splitting formula.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Master explicit spectral inequality theorem}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now combine all previously established explicit lower bounds and norm estimates into one master inequality guaranteeing full microscopic Dirac isolation.

\subsubsection{A. Structural inputs already reduced to explicit quantities}

Fix the selected shell pair \(\pm G_*\) and write
\begin{equation}
q_*:=|G_*|.
\label{eq:qstar_master}
\end{equation}

Assume the local shell-level Dirac block has already been realized, i.e.
\begin{equation}
H_D(p)=\Gamma_i(M_{\mathrm{eff}}p)_i,
\qquad
\det M_{\mathrm{eff}}\neq 0,
\label{eq:HD_master}
\end{equation}
with opposite-valley matching and no constant Dirac mass allowed by the residual low-energy symmetry.

We now collect the explicit remote-sector lower bounds.

\paragraph{(1) Higher-shell diagonal bound.}
For the BCC reciprocal arithmetic, the first shell-separation parameter is
\begin{equation}
\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}=2
\label{eq:delta_shell_master}
\end{equation}
in the integer reciprocal convention, so the Brazovskii-type diagonal kernel
\begin{equation}
\Lambda(Q)=r_*+K(|Q|^2-q_*^2)^2
\label{eq:Lambda_master}
\end{equation}
gives
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}
\ge
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2-|r_*|
=
4K-|r_*|.
\label{eq:Delta_high_master}
\end{equation}
(Equivalently, in the unit-shell normalization one has \(\widehat\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}\ge K-|r_*|\).)

\paragraph{(2) Heavy volumetric diagonal bound.}
From longitudinal-only volumetric locking, the heavy scalar \(\sigma\) yields a positive longitudinal heavy scale.
We write its induced remote lower bound as
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol}}^{(0)}\ge c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma,
\qquad
c_{\mathrm{vol}}>0,
\quad
M_\sigma>0.
\label{eq:Delta_vol_master}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(3) Wrong-internal diagonal bound.}
At the selected shell point, effective transverse \(SO(2)\) gives an exact protected transverse doublet
\[
H_0|_{\hat n^\perp_{\mathbb C}}=E_*\,\mathbf 1_2,
\]
while longitudinal-only volumetric locking gives
\[
E_L-E_*
=
q_*^2
\left[
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right].
\]
Hence the wrong-internal gap is
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}
=
q_*^2
\left|
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|.
\label{eq:Delta_wrong_master}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(4) Extra remote sectors.}
Let
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}>0
\label{eq:Delta_extra_master}
\end{equation}
be any explicit lower bound for all additional remote channels not covered by the three classes above.

\subsubsection{B. Explicit diagonal benchmark}

Define the global explicit diagonal remote benchmark
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,\;
c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma,\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}
\Biggr\}.
\label{eq:Delta_bench}
\end{equation}
(If one works in the normalized unit-shell convention, replace \(4K-|r_*|\) by \(K-|r_*|\).)

By construction, every remote diagonal channel lies at least \(\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}\) away from zero.

\subsubsection{C. Total remote mixing budget}

Let \(D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\) be the corresponding block-diagonal benchmark operator on the full remote sector, and let
\begin{equation}
H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)=D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)+R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p).
\label{eq:HR_Drem_Rrem}
\end{equation}
Define the total remote mixing budget
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\|.
\label{eq:eta_rem_master}
\end{equation}
This includes:

\begin{itemize}
\item all remote--remote off-diagonal mixing,
\item all tail couplings,
\item all bounded residual corrections to the diagonal benchmark.
\end{itemize}

By the previously proved tail-coupling estimate theorem, one may bound this norm explicitly by
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}} K_a \rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}} \frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a},
\qquad
r_a\ge 1.
\label{eq:eta_rem_bound_master}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{D. Explicit remote-gap theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Master explicit spectral inequality theorem]
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the local shell-level Dirac block \eqref{eq:HD_master} exists and is nondegenerate;
\item little-group mismatch gives
\begin{equation}
V(0)=0,
\qquad
\|V(p)\|\le c|p|;
\label{eq:V_bound_master}
\end{equation}
\item a residual symmetry forbids all constant Dirac mass terms;
\item the explicit diagonal benchmark \(\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}\) is positive:
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}>0;
\label{eq:Delta_bench_positive}
\end{equation}
\item the total remote mixing budget satisfies the master inequality
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}
>
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\label{eq:master_ineq}
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}

Then the full remote block has a uniform positive spectral gap on \(N_\rho=\{|p|\le \rho\}\):
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p))
\cap
(-\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho},\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho})
=
\varnothing,
\qquad
|p|\le \rho,
\label{eq:full_remote_gap_master}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
>0.
\label{eq:Delta_full_master}
\end{equation}
Consequently, for \(|E|<\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}/2\),
\begin{equation}
\|(H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)-E)^{-1}\|
\le
\frac{2}{\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}},
\label{eq:resolvent_master}
\end{equation}
and the Schur-complement effective Hamiltonian satisfies
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
\Gamma_i(M_{\mathrm{eff}}p)_i
+
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}}\right).
\label{eq:Heff_master}
\end{equation}
Hence the full microscopic low-energy sector contains a stable massless Dirac cone.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By construction of the diagonal benchmark, every eigenvalue of \(D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\) has absolute value at least \(\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}\) for \(|p|\le \rho\).
Hence for every \(\Psi\) in the full remote sector,
\[
\|D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\Psi\|
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}\|\Psi\|.
\]
Using \(H_R^{\mathrm{full}}=D_{\mathrm{rem}}+R_{\mathrm{rem}}\), the reverse triangle inequality gives
\[
\|H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)\Psi\|
\ge
\|D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\Psi\|
-
\|R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\Psi\|
\ge
(\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho})\|\Psi\|.
\]
By \eqref{eq:master_ineq}, the right-hand side is positive, so
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p))
\cap
(-\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho},\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho})
=
\varnothing
\]
with \(\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}\ge \Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}\).

For \(|E|<\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}/2\), the resolvent bound \eqref{eq:resolvent_master} follows immediately.
Then, together with \(V(0)=0\) and \(\|V(p)\|\le c|p|\),
\[
\Sigma(E,p)
=
V(p)(H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)-E)^{-1}V(p)^\dagger
=
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}}\right).
\]
Therefore the effective Hamiltonian equals the local Dirac block plus a quadratic correction.
Finally, the residual symmetry excludes any constant Dirac mass term, so the leading linear massless Dirac cone persists.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{E. Strong explicit sufficient form}

Using \eqref{eq:eta_rem_bound_master}, a concrete sufficient inequality is
\begin{equation}
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}} K_a \rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}} \frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
<
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,\;
c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma,\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}
\Biggr\}.
\label{eq:strong_master_ineq}
\end{equation}
Under this inequality, the full microscopic Dirac isolation follows immediately.

\paragraph{Normalized-shell version.}
If all shell radii are normalized so that \(q_*^2=1\), replace the first benchmark entry \(4K-|r_*|\) by \(K-|r_*|\).

\subsubsection{F. Exact logical status}

What is now mathematically closed is:

\[
\text{higher-shell arithmetic}
+
\text{heavy volumetric gap}
+
\text{wrong-internal splitting}
+
\text{tail-coupling norm estimate}
\Longrightarrow
\text{one explicit master inequality}.
\]

The remaining open work is no longer conceptual:
it is the actual coefficient estimation of
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)},
\qquad
K_a,\widetilde K_a,M_a,
\]
inside the final microscopic TECT operator.

Thus the full low-energy Dirac-isolation problem has been reduced to a finite explicit spectral inequality problem.

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{high}}^{(0)}\ge 4K-|r_*|,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol}}^{(0)}\ge c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}^{(0)}
=
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\]
together with
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}>0.
\]

Define the explicit remote diagonal benchmark
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,\;
c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma,\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}
\Biggr\}.
\]

Let
\[
H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)=D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)+R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p),
\qquad
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\|.
\]
By the tail-coupling estimate theorem,
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}} K_a \rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}} \frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}.
\]

If
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho},
\]
then the full remote block has a uniform positive gap
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p))
\cap
(-\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho},\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho})
=
\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}>0.
\]

If also
\[
V(0)=0,\qquad \|V(p)\|\le c|p|,
\]
and a residual symmetry forbids constant Dirac masses, then
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
\Gamma_i(M_{\mathrm{eff}}p)_i
+
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}}\right),
\]
so the full microscopic low-energy sector contains a stable massless Dirac cone.

Therefore the entire spectral-isolation problem is reduced to the single explicit inequality
\[
\boxed{
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,\;
c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma,\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}
\Biggr\}
>
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Extra-sector coercivity theorem}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now eliminate the last abstract slot in the master spectral inequality, namely the quantity
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)},
\]
by deriving it from coercivity of the quadratic form on the remaining extra remote sector.

\subsubsection{A. Extra remote sector and quadratic form}

Let the full tail sector be decomposed as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{tail}}
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}},
\label{eq:tail_extra_decomp}
\end{equation}
and let
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p)
\end{equation}
denote the unperturbed block acting on \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}\).

Assume \(H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p)\) is self-adjoint for all \(|p|\le \rho\), and define the corresponding quadratic form
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{extra},p}[\psi]
:=
\langle \psi, H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p)\psi\rangle,
\qquad
\psi\in \mathcal D_{\mathrm{extra}},
\label{eq:qextra_def}
\end{equation}
on a common dense form domain \(\mathcal D_{\mathrm{extra}}\).

\subsubsection{B. Uniform coercivity hypothesis}

We assume the extra sector is uniformly coercive on the low-momentum neighborhood
\begin{equation}
N_\rho:=\{p:|p|\le \rho\},
\label{eq:Nrho_extra}
\end{equation}
in the sense that there exists \(c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}>0\) such that
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{extra},p}[\psi]
\ge
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\,\|\psi\|^2
\qquad
\forall \psi\in\mathcal D_{\mathrm{extra}},
\quad
\forall |p|\le \rho.
\label{eq:coercivity_hyp}
\end{equation}

This is the natural positivity statement for all additional remote channels not covered by the higher-shell, volumetric, or wrong-internal classifications.

\subsubsection{C. Coercivity implies spectral gap}

\begin{theorem}[Extra-sector coercivity theorem]
Assume \eqref{eq:coercivity_hyp}. Then the unperturbed extra block has a uniform positive spectral lower bound:
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}\!\bigl(H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p)\bigr)
\subset
[c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},\infty)
\qquad
(|p|\le \rho).
\label{eq:spec_extra_positive}
\end{equation}
In particular,
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p))\bigr)
\ge
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
>
0.
\label{eq:Delta_extra_from_coercivity}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Fix \(|p|\le \rho\).
By the spectral theorem (or min-max principle), a self-adjoint operator satisfies
\[
\inf\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p))
=
\inf_{\psi\neq 0}
\frac{\langle \psi,H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p)\psi\rangle}{\|\psi\|^2}.
\]
By \eqref{eq:coercivity_hyp}, the Rayleigh quotient is bounded below by \(c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\).
Hence
\[
\inf\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p))\ge c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
\]
This proves \eqref{eq:spec_extra_positive}. Taking the infimum over \(|p|\le \rho\) yields \eqref{eq:Delta_extra_from_coercivity}.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{D. Two-sided coercivity variant}

In some models the extra block may not be strictly positive but only bounded away from zero on both sides.
Then one assumes the stronger absolute coercivity condition
\begin{equation}
\|H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p)\psi\|
\ge
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\,\|\psi\|
\qquad
\forall \psi\in \mathcal D(H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p)),
\quad
|p|\le \rho.
\label{eq:absolute_coercivity}
\end{equation}
This implies
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p))
\cap
(-c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho})
=
\varnothing.
\label{eq:absolute_gap_extra}
\end{equation}

In the present TECT application, however, the extra sector is naturally treated as part of the remote positive-energy complement, so the one-sided coercivity form \eqref{eq:coercivity_hyp} is the relevant one.

\subsubsection{E. Stability under bounded extra-sector corrections}

Let the actual extra block be
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{extra}}(p)
=
H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p)+\delta H_{\mathrm{extra}}(p),
\label{eq:Hextra_pert}
\end{equation}
with bounded correction satisfying
\begin{equation}
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|\delta H_{\mathrm{extra}}(p)\|
<
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
\label{eq:extra_pert_small}
\end{equation}

\begin{corollary}[Extra-sector gap stability]
Under \eqref{eq:coercivity_hyp} and \eqref{eq:extra_pert_small},
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{extra}}(p))
\subset
[c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},\infty)
\qquad
(|p|\le \rho),
\label{eq:extra_gap_stable_spec}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\ge
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
>
0.
\label{eq:extra_gap_stable}
\end{equation}
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
For every \(\psi\),
\[
\langle \psi,H_{\mathrm{extra}}(p)\psi\rangle
=
\langle \psi,H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p)\psi\rangle
+
\langle \psi,\delta H_{\mathrm{extra}}(p)\psi\rangle.
\]
By coercivity,
\[
\langle \psi,H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p)\psi\rangle
\ge
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\|\psi\|^2.
\]
By boundedness of the perturbation,
\[
|\langle \psi,\delta H_{\mathrm{extra}}(p)\psi\rangle|
\le
\|\delta H_{\mathrm{extra}}(p)\|\,\|\psi\|^2
\le
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\|\psi\|^2.
\]
Therefore
\[
\langle \psi,H_{\mathrm{extra}}(p)\psi\rangle
\ge
(c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho})\|\psi\|^2.
\]
Applying the min-max principle again proves \eqref{eq:extra_gap_stable_spec} and \eqref{eq:extra_gap_stable}.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{F. Replacement of the last unknown slot in the master inequality}

The previous master explicit spectral inequality theorem contained the benchmark quantity
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}.
\label{eq:Delta_extra_slot}
\end{equation}
The present theorem identifies a concrete sufficient realization:
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}
\ge
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},
\label{eq:Delta_extra_replace}
\end{equation}
and, after bounded extra-sector perturbation,
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\ge
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
\label{eq:Delta_extra_replace_pert}
\end{equation}

Therefore the master benchmark may be replaced by
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{coer}}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,\;
c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma,\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,\;
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\Biggr\}.
\label{eq:Delta_bench_coer}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{G. Coercive master inequality}

\begin{theorem}[Coercive master explicit spectral inequality]
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the local shell Dirac block exists and is nondegenerate;
\item little-group mismatch gives \(V(0)=0\) and \(\|V(p)\|\le c|p|\);
\item residual symmetry forbids constant Dirac masses;
\item the extra remote sector is coercive with constant \(c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}>0\);
\item the bounded extra-sector correction satisfies \(\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}<c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\);
\item the total remote mixing budget satisfies
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
<
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{coer}}.
\label{eq:coercive_master_ineq}
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}

Then the full remote block has a uniform positive gap
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{coer}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
>0,
\label{eq:coercive_master_gap}
\end{equation}
and consequently
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
\Gamma_i(M_{\mathrm{eff}}p)_i
+
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}}\right).
\label{eq:coercive_master_Heff}
\end{equation}
Hence the full microscopic low-energy sector contains a stable massless Dirac cone.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The previous theorem replaces the extra-sector slot by a positive explicit lower bound \(c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\).
Substituting this into the master benchmark and applying the previously proved master explicit spectral inequality theorem yields the result.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Exact logical status.}
What is now closed is:
\[
\text{extra-sector gap}
\Longleftarrow
\text{coercivity of the extra quadratic form}
\]
and therefore the master inequality no longer needs a separate abstract \(\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}\) input.
The remaining open work is the actual extraction of the coercivity constant \(c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\) from the final microscopic TECT quadratic form.

%%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{tail}}
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}},
\qquad
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{extra},p}[\psi]
=
\langle \psi,H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p)\psi\rangle .
\]

If the extra-sector quadratic form is uniformly coercive on \(N_\rho=\{|p|\le \rho\}\),
\[
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{extra},p}[\psi]
\ge
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\|\psi\|^2,
\qquad
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}>0,
\]
then
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p))
\subset
[c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},\infty),
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}\ge c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}>0.
\]

If
\[
H_{\mathrm{extra}}(p)=H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p)+\delta H_{\mathrm{extra}}(p),
\qquad
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|\delta H_{\mathrm{extra}}(p)\|
<
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},
\]
then the extra-sector gap is stable:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\ge
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
>0.
\]

Hence the abstract benchmark slot \(\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}\) in the master spectral inequality can be replaced by
\[
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
\]

The fully explicit benchmark becomes
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{coer}}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,\;
c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma,\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,\;
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\Biggr\}.
\]

If
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}<\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{coer}},
\]
then the full remote block has a uniform positive gap
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{coer}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}>0,
\]
and therefore
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
\Gamma_i(M_{\mathrm{eff}}p)_i
+
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}}\right).
\]

Thus the extra-sector slot in the master inequality is reduced to coercivity of the extra quadratic form.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Principal-symbol coercivity theorem}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now derive the extra-sector coercivity constant \(c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\) directly from the principal symbol of the extra-sector operator, together with a quantitative lower-order perturbation bound.

\subsubsection{A. Extra-sector operator and quadratic form}

Let
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p)
=
P_{\mathrm{pr}}(p,D)+B_{\mathrm{lo}}(p)
\label{eq:Hextra_pr_lo}
\end{equation}
be the unperturbed extra-sector operator on the low-momentum neighborhood
\begin{equation}
N_\rho:=\{p:|p|\le \rho\}.
\label{eq:Nrho_principal}
\end{equation}
Assume \(P_{\mathrm{pr}}(p,D)\) is a formally self-adjoint principal differential/pseudodifferential operator of order \(m\ge 1\), and \(B_{\mathrm{lo}}(p)\) is a lower-order symmetric remainder.

Let the associated quadratic form be
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{extra},p}[\psi]
=
\langle \psi,H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p)\psi\rangle
=
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{pr},p}[\psi]+\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{lo},p}[\psi].
\label{eq:qextra_split}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Uniform principal-symbol positivity}

Let \(s_{\mathrm{pr}}(p,\xi)\) denote the Hermitian principal symbol of \(P_{\mathrm{pr}}(p,D)\) on the extra-sector fiber.
Assume there exists \(\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}>0\) such that
\begin{equation}
\langle u,s_{\mathrm{pr}}(p,\xi)u\rangle
\ge
\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\,\langle \xi\rangle^m\,\|u\|^2
\qquad
\forall u,\ \forall |p|\le \rho,\ \forall \xi.
\label{eq:principal_symbol_positive}
\end{equation}
This is the uniform elliptic/coercive positivity of the principal part on the extra sector.

\subsubsection{C. Spectral exclusion of the low shell inside the extra sector}

Because the extra sector is, by definition, orthogonal to the selected low-energy shell carrier, one has a sectorwise Poincaré/Fourier lower bound.
Assume there exists \(\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}>0\) such that
\begin{equation}
\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2
\ge
\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\,\|\psi\|^2
\qquad
\forall \psi\in \mathcal D_{\mathrm{extra}},
\quad
|p|\le \rho.
\label{eq:Poincare_extra}
\end{equation}
This constant encodes the fact that the extra sector does not contain the selected soft shell modes.

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
In concrete TECT truncations, \(\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\) can arise from:

\begin{itemize}
\item shell-radius separation (higher-shell exclusion),
\item heavy longitudinal/volumetric frequency exclusion,
\item internal-sector orthogonality constraints,
\item or a direct finite-dimensional spectral exclusion in the Bloch basis.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection{D. Lower-order relative bound}

Assume the lower-order remainder is form-bounded relative to the \(H^{m/2}\)-norm:
\begin{equation}
|\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{lo},p}[\psi]|
\le
\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}}\,\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2
+
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\,\|\psi\|^2,
\label{eq:lower_order_bound}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
0\le \alpha_{\mathrm{extra}}<1,
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\ge 0,
\qquad
|p|\le \rho.
\label{eq:alpha_beta_conditions}
\end{equation}

This is the standard small relative-boundedness condition needed to preserve coercivity.

\subsubsection{E. Principal-form lower bound}

\begin{lemma}[Principal coercive form bound]
Under \eqref{eq:principal_symbol_positive}, there exists a constant \(c_{\mathrm{pr}}>0\) (which may be taken as \(\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\) after normalization) such that
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{pr},p}[\psi]
\ge
\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2
\qquad
\forall \psi\in \mathcal D_{\mathrm{extra}},
\quad
|p|\le \rho.
\label{eq:qpr_lower}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
This is the standard Gårding/elliptic lower-bound consequence of the uniform positivity of the principal symbol \eqref{eq:principal_symbol_positive}.
Because the symbol is Hermitian and uniformly positive, the quadratic form of the principal operator dominates the \(H^{m/2}\)-norm up to normalization.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{F. Coercivity constant from principal positivity}

\begin{theorem}[Principal-symbol coercivity theorem]
Assume \eqref{eq:principal_symbol_positive}, \eqref{eq:Poincare_extra}, and \eqref{eq:lower_order_bound}.
Then the extra-sector quadratic form satisfies
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{extra},p}[\psi]
\ge
\Bigl(
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\Bigr)\|\psi\|^2
\qquad
\forall \psi\in \mathcal D_{\mathrm{extra}},
\quad
|p|\le \rho.
\label{eq:principal_coercive_bound}
\end{equation}
In particular, if
\begin{equation}
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
>
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},
\label{eq:principal_gap_condition}
\end{equation}
then the extra sector is uniformly coercive with explicit constant
\begin{equation}
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
>0.
\label{eq:cextra_explicit}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
From \eqref{eq:qextra_split},
\[
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{extra},p}[\psi]
=
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{pr},p}[\psi]+\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{lo},p}[\psi].
\]
Using \eqref{eq:qpr_lower} and \eqref{eq:lower_order_bound},
\[
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{extra},p}[\psi]
\ge
\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2
-
\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}}\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\|\psi\|^2.
\]
Hence
\[
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{extra},p}[\psi]
\ge
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\|\psi\|^2.
\]
Now apply the sectorwise Poincaré/Fourier exclusion bound \eqref{eq:Poincare_extra}:
\[
\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2
\ge
\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\|\psi\|^2.
\]
Therefore
\[
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{extra},p}[\psi]
\ge
\Bigl((1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\Bigr)\|\psi\|^2.
\]
This proves \eqref{eq:principal_coercive_bound}, and under \eqref{eq:principal_gap_condition} the explicit coercivity constant is \eqref{eq:cextra_explicit}.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{G. Spectral consequence}

By the extra-sector coercivity theorem already proved, \eqref{eq:cextra_explicit} implies
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}
\ge
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
>0.
\label{eq:Delta_extra_principal}
\end{equation}

Thus the abstract extra-sector slot in the master inequality is replaced by a completely explicit principal-symbol expression.

\subsubsection{H. TECT specialization}

In the TECT setting, the motivation for the decomposition
\[
H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}=P_{\mathrm{pr}}+B_{\mathrm{lo}}
\]
is as follows.

\begin{enumerate}
\item The exact BCC linearized Hessian \(D_{ij}(k)\) exists and decomposes exactly into an isotropic Lamé-type part plus a cubic anisotropy remainder \(\Delta D_{ij}(k)\). Thus the natural principal part is the isotropic positive sector, while \(\Delta D_{ij}(k)\) is a lower-order anisotropic remainder in the infrared analysis.

\item Integrating out the heavy volumetric mode yields a controlled local \(1/M_\sigma^2\) expansion with explicit remainder bounds. Therefore the heavy-induced corrections naturally enter the lower-order perturbation budget \(\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\).

\item The extra sector is by definition orthogonal to the selected soft shell carrier, so its Fourier support or Bloch labels exclude the selected low shell, which is exactly the source of the constant \(\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}>0\).
\end{enumerate}

Hence the theorem fits the actual TECT analytic architecture.

\subsubsection{I. Master replacement}

The master benchmark from the previous step was
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{coer}}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,\;
c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma,\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,\;
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\Biggr\}.
\label{eq:bench_old_pr}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:cextra_explicit}, this becomes the fully analytic benchmark
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{pr}}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,\;
c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma,\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\Biggr\}.
\label{eq:bench_new_pr}
\end{equation}

Hence the entire full remote-gap problem reduces to the explicit inequality
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
<
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{pr}}.
\label{eq:final_principal_master}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Exact logical status.}
What is now proved is:
\[
\text{principal-symbol positivity}
+
\text{sectorwise Fourier/Bloch exclusion}
+
\text{small lower-order remainder}
\Longrightarrow
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}>0.
\]
So the extra-sector slot is no longer abstract.
The only remaining open work is the actual extraction of the numerical constants
\[
\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}},
\qquad
\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},
\qquad
\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}},
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\]
from the final microscopic TECT operator.

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p)=P_{\mathrm{pr}}(p,D)+B_{\mathrm{lo}}(p),
\qquad
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{extra},p}[\psi]
=
\langle \psi,H_{\mathrm{extra}}^{(0)}(p)\psi\rangle.
\]

Assume:

\[
\langle u,s_{\mathrm{pr}}(p,\xi)u\rangle
\ge
\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\langle \xi\rangle^m\|u\|^2,
\]
\[
\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2
\ge
\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\|\psi\|^2,
\]
\[
|\mathfrak b_{\mathrm{lo},p}[\psi]|
\le
\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}}\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\|\psi\|_{H^{m/2}}^2
+
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\|\psi\|^2,
\qquad
0\le \alpha_{\mathrm{extra}}<1.
\]

Then
\[
\mathfrak q_{\mathrm{extra},p}[\psi]
\ge
\Bigl(
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\Bigr)\|\psi\|^2.
\]

Therefore, if
\[
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
>
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},
\]
the extra sector is uniformly coercive with explicit constant
\[
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
>0,
\]
hence
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{(0)}
\ge
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}>0.
\]

Substituting into the master benchmark gives
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{pr}}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,\;
c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma,\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\Biggr\}.
\]

Hence the full remote-gap condition is reduced to the explicit analytic inequality
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
<
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{pr}}.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Bloch-exclusion constant theorem}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now identify the abstract exclusion constant \(\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\) appearing in the principal-symbol coercivity theorem with an explicit Bloch/Fourier shell-exclusion constant.

\subsubsection{A. Bloch harmonic representation near the selected shell point}

Let the periodic BCC background define a reciprocal lattice \(\mathcal G\), and let the Bloch fiber at quasi-momentum \(k\) act on periodic functions
\begin{equation}
u_k(x)=\sum_{G\in \mathcal G} c_G e^{iG\cdot x},
\qquad
\delta\phi_k(x)=\sum_{G\in\mathcal G} c_G e^{i(k+G)\cdot x}.
\label{eq:Bloch_harmonics_excl}
\end{equation}
Fix a selected shell point \(G_*\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}\) and set
\begin{equation}
k=G_*+p,
\qquad
|p|\le \rho.
\label{eq:k_Gstar_p}
\end{equation}

The exact Bloch operator is diagonal in the bare part:
\begin{equation}
\bigl(H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\bigr)_{G,G'}
=
h_0(k+G)\delta_{G,G'}
+
\widehat V(G-G'),
\label{eq:Hbloch_diag_excl}
\end{equation}
with bare dispersion
\begin{equation}
h_0(q)=r+\kappa |q|^2+\lambda |q|^4,
\qquad
q_*^2=-\frac{\kappa}{2\lambda}
\quad
(\kappa<0,\ \lambda>0).
\label{eq:h0_Brazovskii_excl}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Selected shell carrier and extra sector}

Let \(S_*\subset \mathcal G\) denote the finite set of reciprocal harmonics retained in the local shell carrier, chosen so that
\[
h_0(G_*+p+G)
\]
is near the shell minimum for \(G\in S_*\).
This is exactly the shell-projected Bloch truncation used in the local valley theorem.

Define the extra Bloch sector as the orthogonal complement of the selected shell carrier:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}(p)
:=
\left\{
u=\sum_{G\in\mathcal G} c_G e^{iG\cdot x}
:
c_G=0\ \text{for all }G\in S_*
\right\}.
\label{eq:Hextra_Bloch_def}
\end{equation}

Thus every extra-sector state is supported only on excluded harmonics \(G\notin S_*\).

\subsubsection{C. Shell-distance exclusion constant}

Define the shell-distance exclusion constant
\begin{equation}
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}
:=
\inf_{\substack{|p|\le \rho\\ G\notin S_*}}
\left|
\,|G_*+p+G|^2-q_*^2
\right|.
\label{eq:delta_Bloch_def}
\end{equation}

\begin{lemma}[Positivity of the Bloch exclusion constant]
Assume \(S_*\) contains all reciprocal harmonics whose bare radius lies on the selected soft shell
\[
|G_*+G|^2=q_*^2
\]
inside the chosen local truncation.
Then, for sufficiently small \(\rho\),
\begin{equation}
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}>0.
\label{eq:delta_Bloch_positive}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
At \(p=0\), the excluded set \(G\notin S_*\) contains no harmonic with shell radius \(q_*^2\) by construction, so
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},0}
=
\inf_{G\notin S_*}
\left|
\,|G_*+G|^2-q_*^2
\right|
>0
\]
because the reciprocal lattice is discrete and \(S_*\) is finite.
The map
\[
(p,G)\mapsto \left||G_*+p+G|^2-q_*^2\right|
\]
is continuous in \(p\) and the excluded harmonic set is discrete, so the positive minimum persists for sufficiently small \(|p|\le \rho\).
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{D. Explicit Bloch lower bound}

For any \(u\in \mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}(p)\),
\begin{equation}
u(x)=\sum_{G\notin S_*} c_G e^{iG\cdot x}.
\label{eq:u_extra_expand}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\sum_{G\notin S_*}
\bigl(|G_*+p+G|^2-q_*^2\bigr)^2 |c_G|^2
\ge
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
\sum_{G\notin S_*}|c_G|^2.
\label{eq:Bloch_distance_bound}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\left\|
\bigl(|D+G_*+p|^2-q_*^2\bigr)u
\right\|_{L^2}^2
\ge
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2 \|u\|_{L^2}^2.
\label{eq:operator_Bloch_bound}
\end{equation}

Thus the natural extra-sector exclusion constant in the Brazovskii shell geometry is
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}^{\mathrm{Bloch}}
=
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2.
\label{eq:Lambdaextra_Bloch}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{E. Principal-symbol coercivity from shell exclusion}

Consider the extra-sector principal part
\begin{equation}
P_{\mathrm{pr}}(p)
=
K\bigl(|D+G_*+p|^2-q_*^2\bigr)^2,
\qquad
K>0.
\label{eq:Ppr_Brazovskii}
\end{equation}
Then for every \(u\in \mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}(p)\),
\begin{equation}
\langle u,P_{\mathrm{pr}}(p)u\rangle
=
K
\sum_{G\notin S_*}
\bigl(|G_*+p+G|^2-q_*^2\bigr)^2 |c_G|^2
\ge
K\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2\|u\|_{L^2}^2.
\label{eq:Ppr_Bloch_coercive}
\end{equation}

Hence the principal-symbol positivity constant and exclusion constant may be identified as
\begin{equation}
\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}=K,
\qquad
\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}=\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2.
\label{eq:kappa_Lambda_identify}
\end{equation}

Substituting into the previously proved principal-symbol coercivity theorem yields
\begin{equation}
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,
K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho},
\label{eq:cextra_Bloch}
\end{equation}
provided
\begin{equation}
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,
K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
>
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
\label{eq:Bloch_gap_condition}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{F. Explicit BCC first-shell estimate}

We now specialize to the normalized BCC first-shell convention
\begin{equation}
q_*^2=1,
\label{eq:qstar_norm_BCC}
\end{equation}
and assume \(S_*\) contains all first-shell harmonics.
Then every excluded harmonic \(Q:=G_*+G\) satisfies either
\begin{equation}
|Q|^2=0
\label{eq:Q_zero_case}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
|Q|^2\ge 2,
\label{eq:Q_high_case}
\end{equation}
because the next BCC shell has normalized squared radius \(2\).

\paragraph{Case 1: \(Q=0\).}
Then
\begin{equation}
\left||Q+p|^2-1\right|
=
\left||p|^2-1\right|
\ge
1-\rho^2.
\label{eq:Q0_bound}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Case 2: \(|Q|^2\ge 2\).}
Then \(|Q|\ge \sqrt2\), so
\begin{align}
\left||Q+p|^2-1\right|
&=
\left||Q|^2-1 + 2Q\cdot p + |p|^2\right| \nonumber\\
&\ge
(|Q|^2-1)-2|Q|\rho-\rho^2 \nonumber\\
&\ge
1-2\sqrt2\,\rho-\rho^2.
\label{eq:Qhigh_bound}
\end{align}

Therefore, for all excluded harmonics,
\begin{equation}
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}
\ge
\min\{1-\rho^2,\ 1-2\sqrt2\,\rho-\rho^2\}
=
1-2\sqrt2\,\rho-\rho^2.
\label{eq:delta_Bloch_explicit}
\end{equation}
In particular, if
\begin{equation}
0<\rho<\sqrt3-\sqrt2,
\label{eq:rho_condition_explicit}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}>0.
\label{eq:delta_Bloch_explicit_positive}
\end{equation}

\begin{corollary}[Explicit BCC Bloch-exclusion coercivity]
Under \eqref{eq:rho_condition_explicit},
\begin{equation}
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\ge
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,
K\,
\bigl(1-2\sqrt2\,\rho-\rho^2\bigr)^2
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
\label{eq:cextra_explicit_BCC}
\end{equation}
Hence a sufficient explicit positivity condition is
\begin{equation}
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,
K\,
\bigl(1-2\sqrt2\,\rho-\rho^2\bigr)^2
>
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
\label{eq:explicit_BCC_condition}
\end{equation}
\end{corollary}

\subsubsection{G. Master inequality replacement}

The master explicit benchmark from the previous step contained the extra-sector slot
\[
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
-\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
\]
Using \eqref{eq:kappa_Lambda_identify}, this becomes
\begin{equation}
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})K\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
-\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
\label{eq:master_slot_Bloch}
\end{equation}
Thus the fully analytic benchmark is
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{Bloch}}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,\;
c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma,\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})K\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2-\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\Biggr\}.
\label{eq:bench_Bloch}
\end{equation}

Hence the full remote-gap condition is reduced to the explicit inequality
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
<
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{Bloch}}.
\label{eq:final_Bloch_master}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Exact logical status.}
What is now proved is:
\[
\text{Bloch harmonic exclusion from the selected shell carrier}
\Longrightarrow
\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2.
\]
So the extra-sector coercivity constant is no longer abstract.
In the normalized BCC first-shell setting, it admits the explicit lower bound
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}\ge 1-2\sqrt2\,\rho-\rho^2.
\]
The remaining work is purely coefficient-level: estimate \(\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}}\), \(\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}\), and \(\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}\) in the final microscopic TECT operator.

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
u_k(x)=\sum_{G\in\mathcal G} c_G e^{iG\cdot x},
\qquad
\delta\phi_k(x)=\sum_{G\in\mathcal G} c_G e^{i(k+G)\cdot x},
\qquad
k=G_*+p.
\]

Let \(S_*\subset \mathcal G\) be the selected finite shell carrier, and define the extra Bloch sector by
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}(p)
=
\left\{
u=\sum c_G e^{iG\cdot x}: c_G=0 \text{ for } G\in S_*
\right\}.
\]

Define the shell-distance exclusion constant
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}
:=
\inf_{\substack{|p|\le \rho\\ G\notin S_*}}
\left|
\,|G_*+p+G|^2-q_*^2
\right|.
\]
If \(S_*\) contains all selected soft-shell harmonics, then
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}>0
\]
for sufficiently small \(\rho\).

For every \(u\in\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}(p)\),
\[
\sum_{G\notin S_*}
\bigl(|G_*+p+G|^2-q_*^2\bigr)^2 |c_G|^2
\ge
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
\sum_{G\notin S_*}|c_G|^2.
\]

Hence for the Brazovskii principal part
\[
P_{\mathrm{pr}}(p)=K\bigl(|D+G_*+p|^2-q_*^2\bigr)^2,
\]
one has
\[
\langle u,P_{\mathrm{pr}}(p)u\rangle
\ge
K\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2\|u\|_{L^2}^2.
\]

Therefore
\[
\kappa_{\mathrm{extra}}=K,
\qquad
\Lambda_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}=\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2,
\]
and the extra-sector coercivity constant becomes
\[
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
=
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,
K\,\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
\]

In the normalized BCC first-shell convention \(q_*^2=1\), if \(S_*\) contains all first-shell harmonics, then every excluded harmonic satisfies either \(|Q|^2=0\) or \(|Q|^2\ge 2\), so
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}
\ge
1-2\sqrt2\,\rho-\rho^2.
\]
Thus for
\[
0<\rho<\sqrt3-\sqrt2,
\]
one obtains the explicit bound
\[
c_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\ge
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})\,
K\,
\bigl(1-2\sqrt2\,\rho-\rho^2\bigr)^2
-
\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}.
\]

So the master explicit benchmark becomes
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{Bloch}}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,\;
c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma,\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
(1-\alpha_{\mathrm{extra}})K\delta_{\mathrm{Bloch},\rho}^2-\beta_{\mathrm{extra},\rho}
\Biggr\},
\]
and the full remote-gap condition is
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}<\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{Bloch}}.
}

\subsection{Class II microscopic PDE: coupled UV system and effective reduced equation}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now write the actual PDE system generated by the Class II mediated completion.
The logic is:

\[
\text{minimal triplet Brazovskii PDE}
\quad+\quad
\text{Class II auxiliary mediator}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{coupled UV PDE}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{effective shell-enriched PDE after eliminating the heavy field}.
\]

\subsubsection{A. Minimal microscopic condensate PDE already fixed}

The minimal microscopic TECT field is a complex triplet
\begin{equation}
\Psi(x,t)\in \mathbb C^3.
\label{eq:ClassII_Psi_field}
\end{equation}
Within the minimal local, isotropic, \(U(3)\)-invariant, second-order-in-time, fourth-order-in-space truncation, the microscopic action is
\begin{equation}
S_0[\Psi]
=
\int dt\,d^3x\,
\left[
\frac12 \partial_t\Psi^\dagger\partial_t\Psi
-\frac{\mu^2}{2}\Psi^\dagger\Psi
+\frac Z2 \partial_i\Psi^\dagger\partial_i\Psi
-\frac Y2 (\nabla^2\Psi)^\dagger(\nabla^2\Psi)
-\frac g4 (\Psi^\dagger\Psi)^2
\right].
\label{eq:ClassII_S0}
\end{equation}
Its Euler--Lagrange equation is
\begin{equation}
\partial_t^2\Psi
=
-\mu^2\Psi
+
Z\nabla^2\Psi
-
Y\nabla^4\Psi
-
g(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)\Psi.
\label{eq:ClassII_minimal_PDE}
\end{equation}

This is the already-established minimal microscopic TECT PDE.

\subsubsection{B. Why Class II must be added}

The shell-level Dirac reduction requires enriched microscopic tensors \(N_{ij}^a\) entering a first-order shell operator of the form
\begin{equation}
\delta L_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
N_{ij}^a\,(\partial_i\phi_0)\,(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a.
\label{eq:ClassII_target_tensor}
\end{equation}
The minimal triplet Brazovskii PDE \eqref{eq:ClassII_minimal_PDE} fixes the shell instability and the internal \(CP^2\) geometry, but does not by itself yet produce a fully explicit microscopic source for \eqref{eq:ClassII_target_tensor}. This is precisely why the Class II mediated completion was introduced.

\subsubsection{C. Class II UV completion: mediator field}

Introduce a heavy auxiliary internal vector mediator
\begin{equation}
X_i^a(x),
\qquad
i=1,2,3,
\qquad
a=1,2,3,
\label{eq:ClassII_X_field}
\end{equation}
and consider the UV-completed action
\begin{equation}
S_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(II)}[\Psi,P,\psi,X]
=
S_0[\Psi]
+
\int dt\,d^3x\,
\left[
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+\alpha X_i^a J_i^a[\Psi]
+\beta X_i^a K_i^a[P,\psi]
\right].
\label{eq:ClassII_UV_action}
\end{equation}
Here:

\begin{equation}
J_i^a[\Psi]
:=
(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger)T^a\Psi+\Psi^\dagger T^a(\partial_i\Psi),
\label{eq:ClassII_J}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
K_i^a[P,\psi]
\sim
(T^a\partial_iP)\,\mathcal O[\psi].
\label{eq:ClassII_K}
\end{equation}
At the linearized shell-relevant level, one may take
\begin{equation}
K_i^a[P,\psi]\sim \partial_i\delta P^a\,\psi.
\label{eq:ClassII_K_linearized}
\end{equation}

The exact choice of \(\mathcal O[\psi]\) depends on the reduced test-mode sector, but this does not affect the basic Euler--Lagrange structure below.

\subsubsection{D. Euler--Lagrange equations of the coupled Class II system}

We now vary \eqref{eq:ClassII_UV_action}.

\paragraph{(1) Equation for the heavy mediator \(X_i^a\).}
Since \(X_i^a\) is auxiliary (no derivatives on \(X\)), its equation is algebraic:
\begin{equation}
\frac{\delta S_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(II)}}{\delta X_i^a}
=
M_X^2 X_i^a+\alpha J_i^a[\Psi]+\beta K_i^a[P,\psi]
=
0.
\label{eq:ClassII_X_EOM}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
X_i^a
=
-\frac{\alpha}{M_X^2}J_i^a[\Psi]
-\frac{\beta}{M_X^2}K_i^a[P,\psi].
\label{eq:ClassII_X_solution}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(2) Equation for \(\Psi\).}
Varying with respect to \(\Psi^\dagger\) gives
\begin{equation}
\partial_t^2\Psi
=
-\mu^2\Psi
+
Z\nabla^2\Psi
-
Y\nabla^4\Psi
-
g(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)\Psi
+
\mathcal S_{\Psi}^{(II)}[X,\Psi,P,\psi],
\label{eq:ClassII_Psi_EOM_raw}
\end{equation}
where the Class II source is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal S_{\Psi}^{(II)}
=
-\alpha\,\partial_i\!\bigl(X_i^a T^a\Psi\bigr)
+\alpha\,X_i^a T^a\partial_i\Psi
+\cdots .
\label{eq:ClassII_Psi_source_raw}
\end{equation}
The omitted terms come from the precise symmetrization convention of \(J_i^a[\Psi]\); they are all bilinear in \(X\) and \(\Psi\), with one spatial derivative.

\paragraph{(3) Equation for the projector/tangent fluctuation.}
If \(P\) (or equivalently its tangent fluctuation \(\delta P^a\sim \xi^a\)) is treated as an explicit dynamical variable, then varying with respect to \(P\) gives
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_P[\delta P]
+
\beta\,\mathcal J_P[X,\psi]
=
0,
\label{eq:ClassII_P_EOM_raw}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal L_P\) is the intrinsic projector/tangent-sector operator and \(\mathcal J_P\) is the Class II source induced by \(X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi]\).

Thus the actual microscopic Class II PDE is a coupled system:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
\partial_t^2\Psi
&=
-\mu^2\Psi
+
Z\nabla^2\Psi
-
Y\nabla^4\Psi
-
g(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)\Psi
+
\mathcal S_{\Psi}^{(II)}[X,\Psi,P,\psi],\\
M_X^2 X_i^a
&=
-\alpha J_i^a[\Psi]-\beta K_i^a[P,\psi],\\
\mathcal L_P[\delta P]
&=
-\beta\,\mathcal J_P[X,\psi].
\end{aligned}
}
\label{eq:ClassII_full_coupled_PDE}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{E. Effective PDE after eliminating the heavy mediator}

Substitute \eqref{eq:ClassII_X_solution} back into the action.
Completing the square in \(X_i^a\) gives
\begin{equation}
S_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(II)}
=
S_0[\Psi]
-
\frac{1}{2M_X^2}
\int dt\,d^3x\,
\bigl(
\alpha J_i^a[\Psi]+\beta K_i^a[P,\psi]
\bigr)^2.
\label{eq:ClassII_Seff_exact}
\end{equation}
Expanding the square,
\begin{equation}
S_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(II)}
=
S_0[\Psi]
-
\frac{\alpha^2}{2M_X^2}\int J_i^aJ_i^a
-
\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}\int J_i^aK_i^a
-
\frac{\beta^2}{2M_X^2}\int K_i^aK_i^a.
\label{eq:ClassII_Seff_expand}
\end{equation}
The load-bearing mixed term is
\begin{equation}
S_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(II)}
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}
\int dt\,d^3x\, J_i^a[\Psi]K_i^a[P,\psi].
\label{eq:ClassII_Smix}
\end{equation}

Therefore the effective \(\Psi\)-equation becomes
\begin{equation}
\partial_t^2\Psi
=
-\mu^2\Psi
+
Z\nabla^2\Psi
-
Y\nabla^4\Psi
-
g(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)\Psi
+
\mathcal S_{\Psi,\mathrm{eff}}^{(II)}[\Psi,P,\psi],
\label{eq:ClassII_Psi_EOM_eff}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\mathcal S_{\Psi,\mathrm{eff}}^{(II)}
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}
\frac{\delta}{\delta\Psi^\dagger}
\Bigl(J_i^a[\Psi]K_i^a[P,\psi]\Bigr)
+\cdots .
\label{eq:ClassII_Psi_eff_source}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{F. Locked-background reduction to the shell-enriched tensor PDE}

Now expand around the locked BCC background
\begin{equation}
\Psi_0=\phi_0 z_0,
\qquad
P_0=z_0 z_0^\dagger,
\label{eq:ClassII_locked_background}
\end{equation}
and write
\begin{equation}
\Psi=\Psi_0+\sigma z_0+\psi,
\qquad
\delta P\sim \xi^a.
\label{eq:ClassII_fluct_decomp}
\end{equation}
Then the shell current contains the key piece
\begin{equation}
J_i^a[\Psi]
=
(\partial_i\phi_0)\,C^a[\psi]
+\cdots,
\label{eq:ClassII_shell_current_piece}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
K_i^a[P,\psi]\sim \partial_i\xi^a\,\psi.
\label{eq:ClassII_shell_K_piece}
\end{equation}
Therefore the mixed term gives
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(2)}
\sim
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}
(\partial_i\phi_0)\,C^a[\psi]\,
\partial_i\xi^a.
\label{eq:ClassII_mix_quadratic}
\end{equation}
After integration by parts / shell reduction / projection onto the shell-relevant internal doublet,
this becomes precisely
\begin{equation}
\delta L_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
N_{ij}^a(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a,
\label{eq:ClassII_target_recovered}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
N_{ij}^a
\sim
\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}
\times
(\text{projected shell/tangent tensor coefficient}).
\label{eq:ClassII_Nij_scaling}
\end{equation}

Thus the honest effective PDE produced by Class II is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_t^2\Psi
=
-\mu^2\Psi
+
Z\nabla^2\Psi
-
Y\nabla^4\Psi
-
g(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)\Psi
+
N_{ij}^a(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)\,s^a\Psi
+\cdots
}
\label{eq:ClassII_effective_enriched_PDE}
\end{equation}
where the dots denote higher-order shell-irrelevant, heavy-suppressed, or nonleading fluctuation terms.

\subsubsection{G. Canonical minimal Class II representative}

For the canonical minimal Class II representative, one fixes
\begin{equation}
m^a(P_0)=m\,\delta^{a3},
\qquad
C_{ij}^{33}=c_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
C_{ij}^{31}=c_I \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J \hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C_{ij}^{32}=-c_J \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I \hat n_i e_{2j},
\label{eq:ClassII_canonical_rep}
\end{equation}
with all other components zero.
Then the induced shell tensor lies in the axial family
\begin{equation}
N_{ij}^3=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N_{ij}^1=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N_{ij}^2=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\label{eq:ClassII_axial_family}
\end{equation}
and produces the explicit corrected coefficients
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=A_0-\mu c_\parallel,
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=B_0-\mu c_I,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=C_0-\mu c_J,
\qquad
\mu=\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}m.
\label{eq:ClassII_Aeff_Beff_Ceff}
\end{equation}

So the PDE \eqref{eq:ClassII_effective_enriched_PDE} is not vague anymore: in the canonical Class II realization, its shell-relevant enriched tensor is exactly the one already used in the Weyl test.

\subsubsection{H. Exact logical status}

What is now genuinely closed is:

\[
\text{minimal microscopic PDE}
\quad+\quad
\text{Class II auxiliary mediator}
\Longrightarrow
\text{coupled UV PDE}
\Longrightarrow
\text{effective shell-enriched PDE}
\]
with shell-relevant term
\[
N_{ij}^a(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a.
\]

What is \emph{not} yet closed is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item that this Class II completion is the unique UV realization;
\item that the resulting full corrected PDE automatically satisfies
\[
V(0)=0,\qquad \Delta>0,\qquad \text{mass protection};
\]
\item that the full microscopic TECT chooses exactly this representative rather than a shell-equivalent alternative.
\end{enumerate}

But the PDE itself is now explicit.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\Psi(x,t)\in\mathbb C^3,
\qquad
S_0[\Psi]
=
\int dt\,d^3x\,
\left[
\frac12 \partial_t\Psi^\dagger\partial_t\Psi
-\frac{\mu^2}{2}\Psi^\dagger\Psi
+\frac Z2 \partial_i\Psi^\dagger\partial_i\Psi
-\frac Y2 (\nabla^2\Psi)^\dagger(\nabla^2\Psi)
-\frac g4 (\Psi^\dagger\Psi)^2
\right].
\]

Its Euler--Lagrange equation is
\[
\partial_t^2\Psi
=
-\mu^2\Psi+Z\nabla^2\Psi-Y\nabla^4\Psi-g(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)\Psi.
\]

Class II adds a heavy auxiliary internal vector mediator
\[
X_i^a(x)
\]
through
\[
S_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(II)}
=
S_0[\Psi]
+
\int dt\,d^3x
\left[
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+\alpha X_i^a J_i^a[\Psi]
+\beta X_i^a K_i^a[P,\psi]
\right].
\]

The Euler--Lagrange equations are
\[
\partial_t^2\Psi
=
-\mu^2\Psi+Z\nabla^2Psi-Y\nabla^4\Psi-g(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)\Psi
+\mathcal S_{\Psi}^{(II)}[X,\Psi,P,\psi],
\]
\[
M_X^2 X_i^a+\alpha J_i^a[\Psi]+\beta K_i^a[P,\psi]=0,
\]
\[
\mathcal L_P[\delta P]=-\beta\,\mathcal J_P[X,\psi].
\]

Eliminating the auxiliary field gives
\[
X_i^a
=
-\frac{\alpha}{M_X^2}J_i^a[\Psi]
-\frac{\beta}{M_X^2}K_i^a[P,\psi],
\]
hence the effective action contains the mixed term
\[
S_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(II)}
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}\int J_i^a[\Psi]K_i^a[P,\psi].
\]

Around the locked BCC background
\[
\Psi_0=\phi_0 z_0,
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger,
\]
this reduces after shell projection to
\[
\delta L_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
N_{ij}^a(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a,
\qquad
N_{ij}^a
\sim
\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}\times(\text{projected tensor coefficient}).
\]

Therefore the effective Class II-enriched microscopic PDE is
\[
\boxed{
\partial_t^2\Psi
=
-\mu^2\Psi
+
Z\nabla^2\Psi
-
Y\nabla^4\Psi
-
g(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)\Psi
+
N_{ij}^a(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)\,s^a\Psi
+\cdots
}
\]

For the canonical minimal Class II representative,
\[
N_{ij}^3=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,\qquad
N_{ij}^1=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},\qquad
N_{ij}^2=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\]
so the shell-relevant corrected coefficients are
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=A_0-\mu c_\parallel,\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=B_0-\mu c_I,\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=C_0-\mu c_J.
\]

Thus the PDE is now explicit at the Class II level:
\[
\text{minimal triplet Brazovskii wave equation}
+
\text{Class II mediator}
\Longrightarrow
\text{shell-enriched effective PDE}.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Linearization of the Class II-enriched PDE and shell-projected coefficient extraction}

\paragraph{Honest scope.}
The full infinite-dimensional Bloch Hessian of the periodic BCC condensate is still an open microscopic calculation.
What we now close is the shell-projected linearization of the Class II-enriched effective PDE, i.e. the exact level at which the already-established Weyl/Dirac matching theorem operates.

\subsubsection{A. Class II-enriched effective PDE}

Start from the effective Class II-enriched PDE
\begin{equation}
\partial_t^2\Psi
=
-\mu_0^2\Psi
+
Z\nabla^2\Psi
-
Y\nabla^4\Psi
-
g(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)\Psi
+
N_{ij}^a(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)\,s^a\Psi
+\cdots,
\label{eq:ClassII_enriched_PDE_start}
\end{equation}
where \(\phi_0(x)\) is the locked BCC amplitude background and \(N_{ij}^a\) is the shell-relevant enriched tensor produced by the Class II mediator.
The dots denote shell-irrelevant, higher-order, or heavy-suppressed terms.

Let the locked background be
\begin{equation}
\Psi_0(x)=\phi_0(x)z_0,
\qquad
\phi_0(x)=2A\sum_{m=1}^6 \cos(Q_m\cdot x),
\label{eq:Psi0_phi0_BCC}
\end{equation}
with \(Q_m\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}\).

Linearize around \(\Psi_0\):
\begin{equation}
\Psi=\Psi_0+\delta\Psi.
\label{eq:Psi_linearize}
\end{equation}
At the shell-effective level used in the existing matching theorem, all background-induced linear terms are collected into a periodic linear operator \(\mathcal U_{\mathrm{per}}(x)\), so the linearized equation takes the form
\begin{equation}
\partial_t^2\delta\Psi
=
\mathcal L_0\,\delta\Psi
+
\mathcal U_{\mathrm{per}}(x)\,\delta\Psi
+
N_{ij}^a(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)\,s^a\delta\Psi
+
\cdots,
\label{eq:linearized_ClassII_PDE}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_0:=-\mu_0^2+Z\nabla^2-Y\nabla^4.
\label{eq:L0_def}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Bloch ansatz near a selected shell vector}

Fix one selected shell vector \(G_*\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}\), and write
\begin{equation}
k=G_*+p,
\qquad
p=p_\parallel \hat n + p_1 e_1 + p_2 e_2,
\qquad
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|}.
\label{eq:k_Gstar_plus_p}
\end{equation}
Use the Bloch ansatz
\begin{equation}
\delta\Psi_{k}(x,t)
=
e^{-i\omega t}\,e^{ik\cdot x}\,u_p(x),
\qquad
u_p(x+R)=u_p(x),
\label{eq:Bloch_ansatz}
\end{equation}
and expand the periodic part in reciprocal harmonics:
\begin{equation}
u_p(x)=\sum_{G\in\mathcal G} c_G\,e^{iG\cdot x}.
\label{eq:periodic_part_expansion}
\end{equation}
Then the linearized Bloch problem becomes
\begin{equation}
\omega^2 u_p
=
H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}^{(II)}(G_*+p)\,u_p,
\label{eq:Bloch_eigenproblem}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}^{(II)}(k)
=
H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}^{(0)}(k)
+
\delta H_{\mathrm{enr}}(k),
\label{eq:Hbloch_split}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\left(H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}^{(0)}(k)\right)_{G,G'}
=
h_0(k+G)\delta_{G,G'}
+
\widehat{\mathcal U}_{G-G'},
\label{eq:Hbloch_0_matrix}
\end{equation}
while the enriched term comes from the shell-current operator
\begin{equation}
\delta H_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
N_{ij}^a(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)\,s^a.
\label{eq:deltaHenr_def}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. Shell projection}

Let \(S_*\subset \mathcal G\) be the selected finite shell carrier, and denote by \(\Pi_{S_*}\) the corresponding projector.
The shell-projected Bloch operator is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(II)}(p)
=
\Pi_{S_*}\,H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}^{(II)}(G_*+p)\,\Pi_{S_*}.
\label{eq:Hshell_def}
\end{equation}
Assume, as in the already-established matching theorem, that inside \(H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(II)}(p)\) there is a spectrally isolated complex two-dimensional valley subspace \(H_*\).
Let \(P_*\) be the orthogonal projector onto \(H_*\).

Then the linearized reduced operator is
\begin{equation}
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
P_*
\Bigl(
p_i K_i^{(II)}
\Bigr)
P_*
\Big|_{H_*},
\qquad
K_i^{(II)}:=\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}^{(II)}(k)\big|_{k=G_*}.
\label{eq:hlin_projected}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{D. Pauli decomposition and coefficient extraction}

Since \(h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)\) is Hermitian on \(H_*\cong \mathbb C^2\), it decomposes as
\begin{equation}
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)=a_0(p)\mathbf 1 + a_\mu(p)\sigma^\mu,
\qquad
\mu=1,2,3.
\label{eq:Pauli_decomp}
\end{equation}
The coefficient matrix is
\begin{equation}
M_{\mu i}
=
\frac12 \operatorname{Tr}_{H_*}\!\left(\sigma^\mu P_* K_i^{(II)} P_*\right),
\label{eq:Mui_def}
\end{equation}
so that
\begin{equation}
a_\mu(p)=M_{\mu i}p_i.
\label{eq:amu_Mui}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the already-established projector extraction theorem for the local Weyl data.

\subsubsection{E. Shell-adapted axial family and contraction formulas}

Now impose the shell-adapted axial tensor family
\begin{equation}
N_{ij}^3 = A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N_{ij}^1 = B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N_{ij}^2 = -C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
\label{eq:axial_family_again}
\end{equation}
Then the shell-level matching formulas are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\kappa_*|G_*|\,\hat n_i\hat n_j N_{ij}^3,
\label{eq:lambda_parallel_extract}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
\frac{\kappa_*|G_*|}{2}
\left(
e_{1j}\hat n_i N_{ij}^1
+
e_{2j}\hat n_i N_{ij}^2
\right),
\label{eq:alpha_extract}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\beta
=
\frac{\kappa_*|G_*|}{2}
\left(
e_{2j}\hat n_i N_{ij}^1
-
e_{1j}\hat n_i N_{ij}^2
\right).
\label{eq:beta_extract}
\end{equation}
For the axial family \eqref{eq:axial_family_again}, these reduce to
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\kappa_*|G_*|A,
\qquad
\alpha=\kappa_*|G_*|B,
\qquad
\beta=\kappa_*|G_*|C.
\label{eq:ABC_to_lambdabeta}
\end{equation}

Therefore the projected positive-valley Hamiltonian becomes
\begin{equation}
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:hplus_final}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{F. Weyl coefficient matrix and determinant}

The corresponding Weyl coefficient matrix is
\begin{equation}
M=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha & -\beta & 0\\
\beta & \alpha & 0\\
0 & 0 & \lambda_\parallel
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:M_matrix_final}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\det M
=
\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2).
\label{eq:detM_lambda_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, in the axial tensor coefficients,
\begin{equation}
\det M
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3 A(B^2+C^2).
\label{eq:detM_ABC}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{G. Canonical Class II representative}

For the canonical minimal Class II representative, the induced tensor lies in the same axial family and simply renormalizes the coefficients:
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=A_0-\mu c_\parallel,
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=B_0-\mu c_I,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=C_0-\mu c_J,
\qquad
\mu=\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}m.
\label{eq:Aeff_Beff_Ceff_again}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{eff}}
=
\kappa_*|G_*|A_{\mathrm{eff}},
\qquad
\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}
=
\kappa_*|G_*|B_{\mathrm{eff}},
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{eff}}
=
\kappa_*|G_*|C_{\mathrm{eff}},
\label{eq:eff_lambda_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}
and the corrected determinant is
\begin{equation}
\det M_{\mathrm{eff}}
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3
A_{\mathrm{eff}}
\left(
B_{\mathrm{eff}}^2+C_{\mathrm{eff}}^2
\right).
\label{eq:detM_eff_final}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{H. Exact logical status}

What is closed here is:

\[
\text{Class II-enriched effective PDE}
\Longrightarrow
\text{shell-projected first-order Bloch block}
\Longrightarrow
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
\Longrightarrow
\det M.
\]

What is still not closed is the full infinite-dimensional Bloch-Hessian derivation proving that the actual microscopic TECT operator admits exactly this isolated shell block.
But at the shell-projected level used by the existing Weyl/Dirac matching theorem, the coefficient extraction is now explicit and complete.

%%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\partial_t^2\Psi
=
-\mu_0^2\Psi
+
Z\nabla^2\Psi
-
Y\nabla^4\Psi
-
g(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)\Psi
+
N_{ij}^a(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)s^a\Psi
+\cdots
\]

Linearizing around the locked BCC background
\[
\Psi_0=\phi_0 z_0,
\qquad
\phi_0(x)=2A\sum_{m=1}^6 \cos(Q_m\cdot x),
\]
and using the Bloch ansatz
\[
\delta\Psi_k(x,t)=e^{-i\omega t}e^{i(G_*+p)\cdot x}u_p(x),
\qquad
u_p(x)=\sum_{G\in\mathcal G} c_G e^{iG\cdot x},
\]
one obtains the shell-projected Bloch operator
\[
H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(II)}(p)
=
\Pi_{S_*}H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}^{(II)}(G_*+p)\Pi_{S_*}.
\]

Projecting to the isolated two-dimensional valley space \(H_*\), the reduced linear operator is
\[
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
P_*(p_iK_i^{(II)})P_*\big|_{H_*}.
\]

For the shell-adapted axial tensor family
\[
N_{ij}^3=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N_{ij}^1=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N_{ij}^2=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\]
the matching formulas are
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\kappa_*|G_*|A,
\qquad
\alpha=\kappa_*|G_*|B,
\qquad
\beta=\kappa_*|G_*|C.
\]

Hence the positive-valley Hamiltonian is
\[
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]

The Weyl coefficient matrix is
\[
M=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha & -\beta & 0\\
\beta & \alpha & 0\\
0 & 0 & \lambda_\parallel
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\det M=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2).
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\det M=(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3A(B^2+C^2).
\]

For the canonical Class II representative,
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=A_0-\mu c_\parallel,\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=B_0-\mu c_I,\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=C_0-\mu c_J,
\]
so
\[
\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{eff}}=\kappa_*|G_*|A_{\mathrm{eff}},
\qquad
\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}=\kappa_*|G_*|B_{\mathrm{eff}},
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{eff}}=\kappa_*|G_*|C_{\mathrm{eff}},
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\det M_{\mathrm{eff}}
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3
A_{\mathrm{eff}}
\left(B_{\mathrm{eff}}^2+C_{\mathrm{eff}}^2\right).
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Negative-valley shell projection of the Class II-enriched PDE}

\paragraph{Honest scope.}
What we close here is the shell-projected opposite-valley pairing implied by the Class II-enriched effective PDE.
We do \emph{not} claim that the full infinite-dimensional periodic Bloch Hessian has been explicitly diagonalized in the final microscopic TECT model.
Rather, we show that once the shell-projected valley reduction exists, the Class II-enriched PDE reproduces the standard opposite-valley pairing formula at that level.

\subsubsection{A. Positive-valley reduced operator}

From the previous step, the shell-projected positive-valley linearized operator takes the form
\begin{equation}
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha (p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta (-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\label{eq:hplus_again}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\kappa_*|G_*|A,
\qquad
\alpha=\kappa_*|G_*|B,
\qquad
\beta=\kappa_*|G_*|C,
\label{eq:lambda_alpha_beta_again}
\end{equation}
where the shell-adapted axial tensor family is
\begin{equation}
N_{ij}^3 = A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N_{ij}^1 = B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N_{ij}^2 = -C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
\label{eq:axial_family_positive}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Matched opposite-valley frame}

At the opposite shell point \(-G_*\), define the matched frame
\begin{equation}
\hat n_-=-\hat n_+ = -\hat n,
\qquad
e_{1-}=e_1,
\qquad
e_{2-}=-e_2.
\label{eq:matched_frame_minus}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
e_{1-}\times e_{2-}
=
e_1\times(-e_2)
=
-\hat n
=
\hat n_-,
\label{eq:matched_orientation_minus}
\end{equation}
so the frame remains right-handed at the negative valley.

The local momentum decomposition near \(-G_*\) is
\begin{equation}
k=-G_*+p,
\qquad
p=p_\parallel \hat n_- + p_1 e_{1-}+p_2 e_{2-}.
\label{eq:momentum_decomp_minus}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, expressed in the original \(+\)-frame,
\begin{equation}
p
=
-p_\parallel \hat n
+
p_1 e_1
-
p_2 e_2.
\label{eq:momentum_minus_in_plus_frame}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. Negative-valley tensor coefficients}

Let the shell-relevant microscopic tensor near \(-G_*\) be denoted \(N_{ij}^a(-)\).
Define the reduced coefficients in the matched opposite-valley frame by
\begin{equation}
A^-=\kappa_*|G_*|\,\hat n_{-i}\hat n_{-j}N_{ij}^3(-),
\label{eq:Aminus_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
B^-=
\frac{\kappa_*|G_*|}{2}
\Bigl(
e_{1-j}\hat n_{-i}N_{ij}^1(-)
+
e_{2-j}\hat n_{-i}N_{ij}^2(-)
\Bigr),
\label{eq:Bminus_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C^-=
\frac{\kappa_*|G_*|}{2}
\Bigl(
e_{2-j}\hat n_{-i}N_{ij}^1(-)
-
e_{1-j}\hat n_{-i}N_{ij}^2(-)
\Bigr).
\label{eq:Cminus_def}
\end{equation}

The standard microscopic sufficient condition for opposite-valley pairing is exactly
\begin{equation}
A^- = A^+,\qquad B^- = B^+,\qquad C^- = C^+,
\label{eq:ABC_match_criterion}
\end{equation}
in the matched opposite-valley frame.
This is already the known finite tensor criterion for
\[
h_-(p)=-h_+(-p).
\]

\subsubsection{D. Class II evenness condition}

For the canonical Class II completion, the induced tensor is linear in the background vector \(m^a(P_0)\) and the mediator kernel \(C_{ij}^{ab}\).
If these are even under the matched opposite-valley transformation, then the induced shell-relevant corrections satisfy
\begin{equation}
\delta A^-=\delta A^+,\qquad
\delta B^-=\delta B^+,\qquad
\delta C^-=\delta C^+.
\label{eq:deltaABC_match}
\end{equation}
Therefore, if the baseline shell construction already has
\[
A_0^- = A_0^+,\qquad B_0^- = B_0^+,\qquad C_0^- = C_0^+,
\]
then the Class II corrected coefficients still satisfy
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{eff}}^- = A_{\mathrm{eff}}^+,\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}^- = B_{\mathrm{eff}}^+,\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}^- = C_{\mathrm{eff}}^+.
\label{eq:Aeff_match}
\end{equation}

In particular, for the canonical minimal representative,
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=A_0-\mu c_\parallel,\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=B_0-\mu c_I,\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=C_0-\mu c_J,
\label{eq:Aeff_formula_minus_plus}
\end{equation}
and the same formula holds at both valleys under the evenness hypothesis.

\subsubsection{E. Negative-valley reduced Hamiltonian}

Define
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel^-=\kappa_*|G_*|A^-,
\qquad
\alpha^-=\kappa_*|G_*|B^-,
\qquad
\beta^-=\kappa_*|G_*|C^-.
\label{eq:minus_lambda_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}
Then the negative-valley reduced operator in its own matched frame is
\begin{equation}
h_-^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel^- p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha^- (p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta^- (-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:hminus_local_frame}
\end{equation}

Now use the matching condition
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel^-=\lambda_\parallel^+,\qquad
\alpha^-=\alpha^+,\qquad
\beta^-=\beta^+.
\label{eq:coeff_match}
\end{equation}
Because the valley label is reversed, the standard canonical reduced basis uses the same coefficient triple but opposite shell point.
Evaluating \(h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(-p)\) gives
\begin{equation}
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(-p)
=
-\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
-
\alpha (p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
-
\beta (-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:hplus_minus_p}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
-h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(-p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha (p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta (-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\label{eq:minus_hplus_minus_p}
\end{equation}
which coincides with \eqref{eq:hminus_local_frame} under \eqref{eq:coeff_match}. Hence
\begin{equation}
h_-^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)=-h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(-p).
\label{eq:opposite_pairing_final}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{F. Dirac doubling}

Once both valleys are Weyl and satisfy \eqref{eq:opposite_pairing_final}, the doubled Hamiltonian
\begin{equation}
H_D^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p) & 0\\
0 & h_-^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
\end{pmatrix}
\label{eq:doubled_H}
\end{equation}
takes the canonical opposite-valley form
\begin{equation}
H_D^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
d_i(p)\sigma_i & 0\\
0 & -d_i(-p)\sigma_i
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:doubled_canonical}
\end{equation}
and therefore is unitarily equivalent to a massless Dirac Hamiltonian.

\subsubsection{G. Exact logical status}

What is closed here is:
\[
\text{Class II-enriched shell-projected PDE}
\Longrightarrow
A^-_{\mathrm{eff}}=A^+_{\mathrm{eff}},\;
B^-_{\mathrm{eff}}=B^+_{\mathrm{eff}},\;
C^-_{\mathrm{eff}}=C^+_{\mathrm{eff}}
\Longrightarrow
h_-^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)=-h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(-p).
\]

What is still not closed is the full infinite-dimensional proof that the exact microscopic periodic Bloch Hessian admits no additional symmetry-breaking corrections beyond this shell-projected sector.

%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha (p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta (-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel=\kappa_*|G_*|A,\quad
\alpha=\kappa_*|G_*|B,\quad
\beta=\kappa_*|G_*|C.
\]

At the opposite valley use the matched frame
\[
\hat n_-=-\hat n,\qquad e_{1-}=e_1,\qquad e_{2-}=-e_2.
\]

Define
\[
A^-=\kappa_*|G_*|\,\hat n_{-i}\hat n_{-j}N_{ij}^3(-),
\]
\[
B^-=
\frac{\kappa_*|G_*|}{2}
\Bigl(
e_{1-j}\hat n_{-i}N_{ij}^1(-)
+
e_{2-j}\hat n_{-i}N_{ij}^2(-)
\Bigr),
\]
\[
C^-=
\frac{\kappa_*|G_*|}{2}
\Bigl(
e_{2-j}\hat n_{-i}N_{ij}^1(-)
-
e_{1-j}\hat n_{-i}N_{ij}^2(-)
\Bigr).
\]

If the Class II data are even under the matched opposite-valley transformation, then
\[
\delta A^-=\delta A^+,\qquad
\delta B^-=\delta B^+,\qquad
\delta C^-=\delta C^+,
\]
hence
\[
A^-_{\mathrm{eff}}=A^+_{\mathrm{eff}},\qquad
B^-_{\mathrm{eff}}=B^+_{\mathrm{eff}},\qquad
C^-_{\mathrm{eff}}=C^+_{\mathrm{eff}}.
\]

Therefore
\[
\lambda_\parallel^-=\lambda_\parallel^+,\qquad
\alpha^-=\alpha^+,\qquad
\beta^-=\beta^+,
\]
and the negative-valley reduced Hamiltonian is
\[
h_-^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha (p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta (-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
=
-h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(-p).
\]

Hence the doubled Hamiltonian
\[
H_D^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p) & 0\\
0 & h_-^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
\end{pmatrix}
\]
