is of standard opposite-valley form and is unitarily equivalent to a massless Dirac Hamiltonian.

So at the shell-projected PDE level:
\[
\boxed{
\text{matched opposite-valley evenness}
\Longrightarrow
A^-_{\mathrm{eff}}=A^+_{\mathrm{eff}},\ 
B^-_{\mathrm{eff}}=B^+_{\mathrm{eff}},\ 
C^-_{\mathrm{eff}}=C^+_{\mathrm{eff}}
\Longrightarrow
h_-^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)=-h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(-p).
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Minimal \(2\)-state valley truncation from the Class II-enriched PDE}

\paragraph{Honest scope.}
The full periodic Bloch-Hessian calculation proving the existence of an isolated \(2\)-dimensional valley subspace is still open.
What we do here is the exact finite calculation \emph{once} the shell-projected \(2\)-state valley carrier has been selected.

\subsubsection{A. Minimal per-valley shell basis}

Fix a selected shell vector \(G_*\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}\), and write
\begin{equation}
k=G_*+p,
\qquad
p=p_\parallel \hat n+p_1e_1+p_2e_2,
\qquad
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|}.
\label{eq:min2_k}
\end{equation}
Choose two orthonormal shell-envelope states spanning the valley carrier:
\begin{equation}
\Psi_{+,a}(x)=e^{iG_*\cdot x}u_a(x),
\qquad
a=1,2,
\label{eq:min2_basis}
\end{equation}
where \(u_a(x)\) span the internal periodic shell envelopes.
This is exactly the minimal \(2\)-state truncation at one valley.

Projecting the Bloch Hamiltonian onto this carrier gives a \(2\times 2\) Hermitian matrix
\begin{equation}
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
P_*
\bigl(p_iK_i\bigr)
P_*
\Big|_{H_*},
\label{eq:min2_projected}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
K_i=\partial_{k_i}L(k)\big|_{k=G_*},
\qquad
H_*= \mathrm{span}_{\mathbb C}\{\Psi_{+,1},\Psi_{+,2}\}.
\label{eq:min2_Ki}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Pauli decomposition}

Since \(h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)\) is Hermitian on \(H_*\cong \mathbb C^2\), it has the unique Pauli decomposition
\begin{equation}
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)=a_0(p)\mathbf 1_2+a_\mu(p)\sigma^\mu,
\qquad
\mu=1,2,3.
\label{eq:min2_pauli}
\end{equation}
The coefficients are extracted by
\begin{equation}
a_\mu(p)
=
\frac12\mathrm{Tr}_{H_*}\!\left(\sigma^\mu h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)\right),
\qquad
a_0(p)=\frac12\mathrm{Tr}_{H_*}\!\left(h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)\right).
\label{eq:min2_trace}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
a_\mu(p)=M_{\mu i}p_i,
\qquad
M_{\mu i}:=\frac12\mathrm{Tr}_{H_*}\!\left(\sigma^\mu P_*K_iP_*\right).
\label{eq:min2_Mui}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. Class II-enriched first-order operator}

The shell-relevant Class II-enriched term is
\begin{equation}
\delta L_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
N_{ij}^a(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a.
\label{eq:min2_deltaLenr}
\end{equation}
At the shell-projected level, its first-order contribution is completely encoded by the three contractions
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\kappa_*|G_*|\,\hat n_i\hat n_jN_{ij}^3,
\label{eq:min2_lam}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
\frac{\kappa_*|G_*|}{2}
\left(
e_{1j}\hat n_iN_{ij}^1
+
e_{2j}\hat n_iN_{ij}^2
\right),
\label{eq:min2_alpha}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\beta
=
\frac{\kappa_*|G_*|}{2}
\left(
e_{2j}\hat n_iN_{ij}^1
-
e_{1j}\hat n_iN_{ij}^2
\right).
\label{eq:min2_beta}
\end{equation}
Therefore the minimal per-valley \(2\times2\) Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha (p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta (-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
+
O(|p|^2).
\label{eq:min2_hplus_final}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{D. Axial tensor family}

Now impose the shell-adapted axial family
\begin{equation}
N_{ij}^3=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\label{eq:min2_N3}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
N_{ij}^1=B\,\hat n_ie_{1j}+C\,\hat n_ie_{2j},
\label{eq:min2_N1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
N_{ij}^2=-C\,\hat n_ie_{1j}+B\,\hat n_ie_{2j}.
\label{eq:min2_N2}
\end{equation}
Substituting \eqref{eq:min2_N3}--\eqref{eq:min2_N2} into \eqref{eq:min2_lam}--\eqref{eq:min2_beta} yields
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\kappa_*|G_*|A,
\qquad
\alpha=\kappa_*|G_*|B,
\qquad
\beta=\kappa_*|G_*|C.
\label{eq:min2_ABC}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
\kappa_*|G_*|
\Bigl[
A\,p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
B\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
C\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
\Bigr]
+
O(|p|^2).
\label{eq:min2_hplus_ABC}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{E. Weyl determinant of the minimal \(2\)-state truncation}

The corresponding Weyl coefficient matrix is
\begin{equation}
M=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha & -\beta & 0\\
\beta & \alpha & 0\\
0 & 0 & \lambda_\parallel
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:min2_M}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\det M=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2).
\label{eq:min2_det1}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:min2_ABC},
\begin{equation}
\det M
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3A(B^2+C^2).
\label{eq:min2_det2}
\end{equation}
Therefore the minimal \(2\)-state valley truncation is Weyl iff
\begin{equation}
A\neq 0,
\qquad
(B,C)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:min2_weylcrit}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{F. Canonical Class II representative}

For the canonical minimal Class II representative,
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=A_0-\mu c_\parallel,
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=B_0-\mu c_I,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=C_0-\mu c_J,
\qquad
\mu=\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}m.
\label{eq:min2_Aeff}
\end{equation}
Hence the actual shell-projected \(2\times2\) Hamiltonian becomes
\begin{equation}
h_{+,\mathrm{eff}}^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
\kappa_*|G_*|
\Bigl[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}\,p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
B_{\mathrm{eff}}(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
C_{\mathrm{eff}}(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
\Bigr]
+
O(|p|^2),
\label{eq:min2_heff}
\end{equation}
with determinant
\begin{equation}
\det M_{\mathrm{eff}}
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3
A_{\mathrm{eff}}
\left(B_{\mathrm{eff}}^2+C_{\mathrm{eff}}^2\right).
\label{eq:min2_deteff}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{G. Doubling to the \(4\times4\) Dirac block}

At the opposite valley \(-G_*\), assume the matched opposite-valley condition
\begin{equation}
h_-^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)=-h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(-p).
\label{eq:min2_opp}
\end{equation}
Then the doubled four-state block
\begin{equation}
H_D^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p) & 0\\
0 & h_-^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
\end{pmatrix}
\label{eq:min2_HD}
\end{equation}
is unitarily equivalent to a massless Dirac Hamiltonian.

Thus the exact role of the minimal \(2\)-state truncation is:
\[
\text{one valley } \Rightarrow 2\times2\ \text{Weyl block},
\qquad
\text{two opposite valleys } \Rightarrow 4\times4\ \text{Dirac block}.
\]

\subsubsection{H. Exact logical status}

What is closed here is the explicit finite matrix calculation:
\[
\text{Class II-enriched shell tensor }N_{ij}^a
\Longrightarrow
\text{minimal }2\times2\text{ valley Hamiltonian}
\Longrightarrow
\det M.
\]
What remains open is not this calculation, but the prior spectral step:
that the true microscopic periodic Bloch operator actually contains this isolated \(2\)-state valley carrier.

%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\Psi_{+,a}(x)=e^{iG_*\cdot x}u_a(x),
\qquad
a=1,2,
\qquad
H_*=\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb C}\{\Psi_{+,1},\Psi_{+,2}\}.
\]

Projecting the Bloch operator to \(H_*\) gives the minimal per-valley \(2\times2\) Hamiltonian
\[
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
P_*(p_iK_i)P_*\big|_{H_*}.
\]

For the Class II shell-enriched tensor
\[
\delta L_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
N_{ij}^a(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a,
\]
the extracted coefficients are
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\kappa_*|G_*|\,\hat n_i\hat n_jN_{ij}^3,
\]
\[
\alpha=
\frac{\kappa_*|G_*|}{2}
\left(
e_{1j}\hat n_iN_{ij}^1+e_{2j}\hat n_iN_{ij}^2
\right),
\]
\[
\beta=
\frac{\kappa_*|G_*|}{2}
\left(
e_{2j}\hat n_iN_{ij}^1-e_{1j}\hat n_iN_{ij}^2
\right).
\]

Hence
\[
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha (p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta (-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
+
O(|p|^2).
\]

For the axial family
\[
N_{ij}^3=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,\qquad
N_{ij}^1=B\,\hat n_ie_{1j}+C\,\hat n_ie_{2j},\qquad
N_{ij}^2=-C\,\hat n_ie_{1j}+B\,\hat n_ie_{2j},
\]
one gets
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\kappa_*|G_*|A,\qquad
\alpha=\kappa_*|G_*|B,\qquad
\beta=\kappa_*|G_*|C.
\]

Thus
\[
M=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha & -\beta & 0\\
\beta & \alpha & 0\\
0 & 0 & \lambda_\parallel
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\det M=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2)
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3A(B^2+C^2).
\]

For the canonical Class II representative,
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=A_0-\mu c_\parallel,\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=B_0-\mu c_I,\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=C_0-\mu c_J,
\]
so
\[
\det M_{\mathrm{eff}}
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3
A_{\mathrm{eff}}
\left(B_{\mathrm{eff}}^2+C_{\mathrm{eff}}^2\right).
\]

Hence the minimal \(2\)-state truncation is Weyl iff
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}\neq 0,\qquad (B_{\mathrm{eff}},C_{\mathrm{eff}})\neq (0,0).
\]

If the opposite valley satisfies
\[
h_-^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)=-h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(-p),
\]
then the doubled \(4\times4\) block is Dirac.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Minimal enriched \(4\times 4\) shell-pair matrix at the Bragg point}

\paragraph{Correction of the minimal truncation.}
The genuine minimal Bloch-pair truncation is centered not at \(k=G_*\), but at the Brillouin-zone boundary point
\begin{equation}
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2}.
\label{eq:kstar_bragg}
\end{equation}
For the plain scalar periodic problem, the two-harmonic Bragg truncation gives
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{pair}}(p)
=
E_0(p)\mathbf 1
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel \tau_3
+
m\tau_1
+
O(|p|^2),
\qquad
k=k_*+p,
\label{eq:scalar_pair_bragg}
\end{equation}
which is not yet Weyl because its linear traceless part is only one-dimensional.

Therefore the genuine minimal shell-Dirac candidate is the enriched shell space
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{shell}}
=
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{pair}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
\label{eq:enriched_shell_space}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{1. Shell basis and projected matrix}

Choose shell basis states
\begin{equation}
\Psi_{+,a}(x)=e^{ik_*\cdot x}u_a(x),
\qquad
\Psi_{-,a}(x)=e^{-ik_*\cdot x}u_a(x),
\qquad
a=1,2,
\label{eq:enriched_shell_basis}
\end{equation}
where \(u_a(x)\) span the internal periodic shell envelopes.
Projecting the Bloch Hamiltonian to this enriched shell space gives
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(p) & B(p)\\
B(p)^\dagger & E_-(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:Hproj_blocks}
\end{equation}
where \(E_\pm(p)\) and \(B(p)\) are \(2\times 2\) internal matrices.

\subsubsection{2. Principal-order shell-Dirac conditions}

The shell-level Dirac theorem requires the following principal-order conditions:
\begin{equation}
B_0:=B(0)=0,
\label{eq:S1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
E_+(p)-E_-(p)=2v_\parallel p_\parallel \mathbf 1_2 + O(|p|^2),
\qquad
v_\parallel\neq 0,
\label{eq:S2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
B(p)=p_1W^1+p_2W^2+O(|p|^2),
\label{eq:S3}
\end{equation}
where \(W^1,W^2\) are traceless Hermitian, nonzero, and anticommuting after internal basis reduction.
Under these conditions,
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p)
\sim
v_\parallel p_\parallel \tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1
+
\nu_1 p_1 \tau_1\otimes s_1
+
\nu_2 p_2 \tau_1\otimes s_2,
\label{eq:Dirac_principal_4x4}
\end{equation}
which is the massless Dirac principal operator on \(\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{pair}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\).

\subsubsection{3. Constant-envelope reduction}

For the simplest constant-envelope ansatz
\begin{equation}
u_a(x)=\frac{1}{\sqrt{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}}\xi_a,
\qquad
\xi_a^\dagger\xi_b=\delta_{ab},
\label{eq:constant_envelope}
\end{equation}
the shell-level quantities reduce to primitive-cell Fourier coefficients:
\begin{equation}
B_0=\widehat U(G_*)\,\mathbf 1_2,
\label{eq:B0_Uhat}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
W^\alpha=\widehat T^\alpha(G_*)\,s_\alpha.
\label{eq:Walpha_That}
\end{equation}

If the scalar periodic potential is generated quadratically from the first-shell BCC condensate,
\begin{equation}
U_{\mathrm{per}}(x)\propto \phi_0(x)^2,
\label{eq:Uper_quad}
\end{equation}
then the quadratic first-shell selection rule gives
\begin{equation}
\widehat U(G_*)=0,
\label{eq:Uhat_zero}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
B_0=0.
\label{eq:B0_zero}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{4. Minimal allowed enriched coupling}

The most natural minimal enriched coefficient fields are linear derivative couplings
\begin{equation}
T^\alpha(x)=C_{\alpha j}\,\partial_j\phi_0(x)\otimes s_\alpha,
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
\label{eq:Talpha_minimal}
\end{equation}
Their first-shell Fourier coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\widehat T^\alpha(G_*)
=
i(C_\alpha\cdot G_*)A_{G_*}\,s_\alpha.
\label{eq:That_explicit}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
W^\alpha\neq 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
(C_\alpha\cdot G_*)A_{G_*}\neq 0.
\label{eq:Walpha_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{5. Explicit minimal \(4\times4\) matrix}

Choose the internal basis so that
\begin{equation}
W^1=\nu_1 s_1,
\qquad
W^2=\nu_2 s_2,
\label{eq:W_basis_choice}
\end{equation}
with \(\nu_1,\nu_2\in\mathbb R\), \(\nu_1\nu_2\neq 0\).
Then the projected shell Hamiltonian takes the explicit form
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p)
=
E_0(p)\,\mathbf 1_4
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel \tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
p_1\tau_1\otimes W^1
+
p_2\tau_1\otimes W^2
+
O(|p|^2),
\label{eq:Hproj_explicit_4x4}
\end{equation}
that is,
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p)
=
E_0(p)\,\mathbf 1_4
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel \tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\nu_1 p_1\tau_1\otimes s_1
+
\nu_2 p_2\tau_1\otimes s_2
+
O(|p|^2).
\label{eq:Hproj_4x4_canonical}
\end{equation}

In block-matrix form,
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_0(p)+v_\parallel p_\parallel & \nu_1 p_1 s_1+\nu_2 p_2 s_2\\
\nu_1 p_1 s_1+\nu_2 p_2 s_2 & E_0(p)-v_\parallel p_\parallel
\end{pmatrix}
+
O(|p|^2).
\label{eq:Hproj_block_explicit}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{6. Dirac form}

Define
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_1=\tau_1\otimes s_1,
\qquad
\Gamma_2=\tau_1\otimes s_2,
\qquad
\Gamma_3=\tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:Gamma_triplet}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\{\Gamma_i,\Gamma_j\}=2\delta_{ij}\mathbf 1_4,
\label{eq:Clifford_rel}
\end{equation}
and the principal operator becomes
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{Dirac}}^{\mathrm{pr}}(p)
=
\nu_1 p_1\Gamma_1+\nu_2 p_2\Gamma_2+v_\parallel p_\parallel \Gamma_3.
\label{eq:Dirac_principal_final}
\end{equation}
Thus the enriched shell-pair truncation is exactly Dirac at principal order.

\subsubsection{7. Honest status}

What is explicitly computed here is the finite projected shell matrix once the enriched shell carrier
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{shell}}=\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{pair}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
is selected.

What remains open is the prior microscopic spectral step:
to derive from the full periodic BCC Bloch Hessian that this enriched shell block is indeed spectrally isolated and that the coefficients \(v_\parallel,\nu_1,\nu_2\) are nonzero in the actual TECT linearization.

%%%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{shell}}=\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{pair}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
\]

Choose basis states
\[
\Psi_{+,a}(x)=e^{ik_*\cdot x}u_a(x),\qquad
\Psi_{-,a}(x)=e^{-ik_*\cdot x}u_a(x),\qquad a=1,2.
\]

Then the projected shell Hamiltonian is
\[
H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(p) & B(p)\\
B(p)^\dagger & E_-(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
with \(2\times2\) internal blocks.

A shell-level Dirac operator emerges if
\[
B_0=B(0)=0,
\]
\[
E_+(p)-E_-(p)=2v_\parallel p_\parallel \mathbf 1_2+O(|p|^2),
\qquad
v_\parallel\neq 0,
\]
\[
B(p)=p_1W^1+p_2W^2+O(|p|^2),
\]
where \(W^1,W^2\) are traceless Hermitian, nonzero, and anticommuting.

For the constant-envelope reduction,
\[
B_0=\widehat U(G_*)\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
W^\alpha=\widehat T^\alpha(G_*)\,s_\alpha.
\]
If \(U_{\mathrm{per}}(x)\propto \phi_0(x)^2\), then
\[
\widehat U(G_*)=0
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
B_0=0.
\]

For the minimal derivative-enriched class
\[
T^\alpha(x)=C_{\alpha j}\partial_j\phi_0(x)\otimes s_\alpha,
\]
one has
\[
\widehat T^\alpha(G_*)
=
i(C_\alpha\cdot G_*)A_{G_*}\,s_\alpha.
\]
Hence
\[
(C_1\cdot G_*)A_{G_*}\neq 0,\qquad
(C_2\cdot G_*)A_{G_*}\neq 0
\]
imply two nonzero transverse matrices.

Choosing internal basis so that
\[
W^1=\nu_1 s_1,\qquad W^2=\nu_2 s_2,
\]
the projected \(4\times4\) shell Hamiltonian is
\[
H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p)
=
E_0(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel \tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\nu_1 p_1\tau_1\otimes s_1
+
\nu_2 p_2\tau_1\otimes s_2
+
O(|p|^2).
\]

Defining
\[
\Gamma_1=\tau_1\otimes s_1,\qquad
\Gamma_2=\tau_1\otimes s_2,\qquad
\Gamma_3=\tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\]
one gets
\[
\{\Gamma_i,\Gamma_j\}=2\delta_{ij}\mathbf 1_4,
\]
so the principal part is exactly
\[
H_{\mathrm{Dirac}}^{\mathrm{pr}}(p)
=
\nu_1 p_1\Gamma_1+\nu_2 p_2\Gamma_2+v_\parallel p_\parallel \Gamma_3.
\]

Thus the genuine minimal finite-dimensional shell Dirac candidate is not the plain \(2\times2\) scalar pair, but the enriched \(4\times4\) shell-pair matrix
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{pair}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Primitive-cell overlap integrals in the constant-envelope shell ansatz}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We compute explicitly the shell-pair overlap integrals
\[
B_0,\qquad W^1,\qquad W^2
\]
for the constant-envelope enriched shell basis, and derive the exact Fourier formulas from the primitive-cell integrals.

\subsubsection{A. Constant-envelope shell basis}

Fix a selected reciprocal-shell vector \(G_*\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}\), and set the Bragg quasimomentum
\begin{equation}
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2}.
\label{eq:kstar_overlap}
\end{equation}
Choose a constant orthonormal internal basis
\begin{equation}
\xi_1,\xi_2\in \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
\qquad
\xi_a^\dagger\xi_b=\delta_{ab},
\label{eq:xi_basis}
\end{equation}
and define the periodic envelopes
\begin{equation}
u_a(x)=\frac{1}{\sqrt{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}}\xi_a,
\qquad
a=1,2.
\label{eq:constant_envelopes}
\end{equation}
The enriched shell-pair basis states are
\begin{equation}
\Psi_{+,a}(x)=e^{ik_*\cdot x}u_a(x),
\qquad
\Psi_{-,a}(x)=e^{-ik_*\cdot x}u_a(x).
\label{eq:shell_pair_basis_overlap}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Minimal enriched periodic operator}

Consider the minimal enriched periodic operator
\begin{equation}
H
=
h_0(-i\nabla)\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
U_{\mathrm{per}}(x)\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\sum_{\alpha=1}^2 T^\alpha(x)(-i\partial_\alpha)\otimes s_\alpha,
\label{eq:minimal_enriched_operator_overlap}
\end{equation}
where:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(h_0(q)\) is the scalar bare kernel;
\item \(U_{\mathrm{per}}(x)\) is a real periodic scalar coefficient;
\item \(T^\alpha(x)\) are real periodic enriched coefficient fields;
\item \(s_\alpha\) are Pauli matrices acting on the internal doublet.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection{C. Bragg mass \(B_0\)}

By definition,
\begin{equation}
(B_0)_{ab}
=
\langle \Psi_{+,a},H(k_*)\Psi_{-,b}\rangle.
\label{eq:B0_def_overlap}
\end{equation}
The translation-invariant bare part \(h_0(-i\nabla)\otimes \mathbf 1_2\) does not contribute to pair mixing between \(\Psi_+\) and \(\Psi_-\), so the leading scalar contribution comes from \(U_{\mathrm{per}}\):
\begin{equation}
(B_0)_{ab}
=
\frac{1}{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\,
\xi_a^\dagger
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}
U_{\mathrm{per}}(x)
\xi_b.
\label{eq:B0_integral_1}
\end{equation}
Since \(U_{\mathrm{per}}\) acts trivially on the internal doublet,
\begin{equation}
(B_0)_{ab}
=
\left(
\frac{1}{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\,
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}U_{\mathrm{per}}(x)
\right)\delta_{ab}.
\label{eq:B0_integral_2}
\end{equation}
Define the primitive-cell Fourier coefficient
\begin{equation}
\widehat U(G)
:=
\frac{1}{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\,e^{-iG\cdot x}U_{\mathrm{per}}(x).
\label{eq:Uhat_def_overlap}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
(B_0)_{ab}=\widehat U(G_*)\,\delta_{ab},
\qquad
B_0=\widehat U(G_*)\,\mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:B0_final_overlap}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{D. Transverse mixing matrices \(W^\alpha\)}

Now consider the enriched term
\[
T^\alpha(x)(-i\partial_\alpha)\otimes s_\alpha.
\]
At the shell-projected first-order level, the corresponding matrix elements are
\begin{equation}
(W^\alpha)_{ab}
=
\langle \Psi_{+,a},
T^\alpha(x)(-i\partial_\alpha)\otimes s_\alpha
\Psi_{-,b}\rangle_{\mathrm{cell}}
\Big|_{\text{shell-projected first order}}.
\label{eq:Walpha_def_raw}
\end{equation}
In the constant-envelope ansatz, the shell-overlap reduction gives directly
\begin{equation}
(W^\alpha)_{ab}
=
\frac{1}{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\,
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}
T^\alpha(x)\,
\xi_a^\dagger s_\alpha \xi_b.
\label{eq:Walpha_integral_1}
\end{equation}
Since the internal matrix is constant over the cell,
\begin{equation}
(W^\alpha)_{ab}
=
\left(
\frac{1}{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\,
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}T^\alpha(x)
\right)
(s_\alpha)_{ab}.
\label{eq:Walpha_integral_2}
\end{equation}
Define
\begin{equation}
\widehat T^\alpha(G)
:=
\frac{1}{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\,e^{-iG\cdot x}T^\alpha(x).
\label{eq:That_def_overlap}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
W^\alpha=\widehat T^\alpha(G_*)\,s_\alpha.
\label{eq:Walpha_final_overlap}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{E. Explicit derivative coupling computation}

Now specialize to the minimal derivative-enriched class
\begin{equation}
T^\alpha(x)=C_{\alpha j}\,\partial_j\phi_0(x),
\qquad
\alpha=1,2,
\label{eq:Talpha_derivative_class}
\end{equation}
where \(C_{\alpha j}\) are constant coefficients and
\begin{equation}
\phi_0(x)=\sum_{Q\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}} A_Q e^{iQ\cdot x},
\qquad
A_{-Q}=A_Q.
\label{eq:phi0_fourier}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\partial_j\phi_0(x)
=
\sum_{Q\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}} iQ_j A_Q e^{iQ\cdot x}.
\label{eq:dphi0_fourier}
\end{equation}
Substituting into \eqref{eq:Talpha_derivative_class},
\begin{equation}
T^\alpha(x)
=
\sum_{Q\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}}
i(C_\alpha\cdot Q)\,A_Q\,e^{iQ\cdot x}.
\label{eq:Talpha_fourier}
\end{equation}
Therefore its \(G_*\)-Fourier coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\widehat T^\alpha(G_*)
=
i(C_\alpha\cdot G_*)A_{G_*}.
\label{eq:That_explicit_overlap}
\end{equation}
Hence the projected shell matrices are
\begin{equation}
W^\alpha
=
i(C_\alpha\cdot G_*)A_{G_*}\,s_\alpha.
\label{eq:Walpha_explicit_overlap}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{F. Exact nonvanishing criterion}

Equation \eqref{eq:Walpha_explicit_overlap} immediately implies:
\begin{equation}
W^\alpha\neq 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
(C_\alpha\cdot G_*)A_{G_*}\neq 0.
\label{eq:W_nonzero_iff}
\end{equation}
Thus a sufficient explicit shell-level criterion is
\begin{equation}
A_{G_*}\neq 0,
\qquad
C_1\cdot G_*\neq 0,
\qquad
C_2\cdot G_*\neq 0.
\label{eq:explicit_nonzero_criterion}
\end{equation}
Under \eqref{eq:explicit_nonzero_criterion},
\begin{equation}
W^1\neq 0,\qquad W^2\neq 0.
\label{eq:W12_nonzero}
\end{equation}
Since \(s_1\) and \(s_2\) anticommute,
\begin{equation}
\{W^1,W^2\}=0
\label{eq:W_anticommute}
\end{equation}
up to the nonzero scalar coefficients.

\subsubsection{G. About the Bragg-mass cancellation}

For the scalar Bragg mass,
\[
B_0=\widehat U(G_*)\mathbf 1_2
\]
is exact from \eqref{eq:B0_final_overlap}.
To go further and prove
\begin{equation}
\widehat U(G_*)=0,
\label{eq:Uhat_zero_claim}
\end{equation}
one must specify the precise microscopic form of \(U_{\mathrm{per}}(x)\), not merely that it is ``quadratic'' in the first-shell condensate.
At the present level, the exact direct calculation is
\begin{equation}
\widehat U(G_*)
=
\frac{1}{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\,e^{-iG_*\cdot x}U_{\mathrm{per}}(x).
\label{eq:Uhat_exact_only}
\end{equation}
If one inserts a specific quadratic Hessian form for \(U_{\mathrm{per}}\), then the first-shell quadratic selection rule established in the existing shell-Dirac analysis gives
\[
\widehat U(G_*)=0.
\]
So the new calculation here fully establishes the overlap formula itself; the vanishing of \(\widehat U(G_*)\) remains a further Fourier-selection computation tied to the detailed microscopic scalar potential.

\subsubsection{H. Resulting projected \(4\times4\) matrix}

Combining the overlap formulas with the enriched shell-pair basis, the principal projected Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p)
=
E_0(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel \tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
p_1\tau_1\otimes W^1
+
p_2\tau_1\otimes W^2
+
O(|p|^2),
\label{eq:Hproj_from_overlaps}
\end{equation}
and for the derivative-enriched class this becomes
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p)
=
E_0(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel \tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
i(C_1\cdot G_*)A_{G_*}\,p_1\tau_1\otimes s_1
+
i(C_2\cdot G_*)A_{G_*}\,p_2\tau_1\otimes s_2
+
O(|p|^2).
\label{eq:Hproj_derivative_explicit}
\end{equation}
After a harmless basis rephasing to make the coefficients real, this is the canonical enriched shell Dirac principal operator whenever \eqref{eq:explicit_nonzero_criterion} holds and \(B_0=0\).

\paragraph{Exact logical status.}
What is fully computed here is the primitive-cell overlap reduction:
\[
B_0=\widehat U(G_*)\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
W^\alpha=\widehat T^\alpha(G_*)s_\alpha,
\qquad
\widehat T^\alpha(G_*)=i(C_\alpha\cdot G_*)A_{G_*}.
\]
What is not fully recomputed here is the separate first-shell quadratic cancellation proving \(\widehat U(G_*)=0\) for the exact microscopic scalar Hessian.

%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
u_a(x)=\frac{1}{\sqrt{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}}\xi_a,
\qquad
\Psi_{+,a}(x)=e^{ik_*\cdot x}u_a(x),
\qquad
\Psi_{-,a}(x)=e^{-ik_*\cdot x}u_a(x),
\qquad
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2}.
\]

For the scalar periodic potential,
\[
(B_0)_{ab}
=
\frac{1}{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\,
\xi_a^\dagger e^{-iG_*\cdot x}U_{\mathrm{per}}(x)\xi_b
=
\widehat U(G_*)\delta_{ab},
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
B_0=\widehat U(G_*)\,\mathbf 1_2.
}
\]

For the enriched coefficient field \(T^\alpha(x)\),
\[
(W^\alpha)_{ab}
=
\frac{1}{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\,
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}T^\alpha(x)\,
\xi_a^\dagger s_\alpha \xi_b
=
\widehat T^\alpha(G_*)(s_\alpha)_{ab},
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
W^\alpha=\widehat T^\alpha(G_*)\,s_\alpha.
}
\]

For the derivative-enriched class
\[
T^\alpha(x)=C_{\alpha j}\partial_j\phi_0(x),
\qquad
\phi_0(x)=\sum_{Q\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}}A_Q e^{iQ\cdot x},
\]
one finds
\[
\partial_j\phi_0(x)=\sum_{Q\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}} iQ_j A_Q e^{iQ\cdot x},
\]
so
\[
\widehat T^\alpha(G_*)
=
i(C_\alpha\cdot G_*)A_{G_*}.
\]
Therefore
\[
\boxed{
W^\alpha=i(C_\alpha\cdot G_*)A_{G_*}\,s_\alpha.
}
\]

Hence the explicit shell-level nonvanishing criterion is
\[
\boxed{
A_{G_*}\neq 0,\qquad
C_1\cdot G_*\neq 0,\qquad
C_2\cdot G_*\neq 0.
}
\]

Under this condition,
\[
W^1\neq 0,\qquad W^2\neq 0,
\]
and because \(s_1,s_2\) anticommute, the transverse shell-Dirac matrices anticommute.

The resulting projected \(4\times4\) shell Hamiltonian is
\[
H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p)
=
E_0(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel \tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
p_1\tau_1\otimes W^1
+
p_2\tau_1\otimes W^2
+
O(|p|^2),
\]
i.e.
\[
H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p)
=
E_0(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel \tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
i(C_1\cdot G_*)A_{G_*}\,p_1\tau_1\otimes s_1
+
i(C_2\cdot G_*)A_{G_*}\,p_2\tau_1\otimes s_2
+
O(|p|^2).
\]

So the primitive-cell overlap calculation is now explicit.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Direct computation of \texorpdfstring{$\widehat U(G_*)$}{Uhat(G*)} for a quadratic scalar periodic potential}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We compute explicitly the first-shell Fourier coefficient of a literal quadratic scalar periodic potential
\[
U_{\mathrm{per}}(x)=c\,\phi_0(x)^2
\]
for the BCC first-shell condensate, and determine whether
\[
\widehat U(G_*)=0
\]
actually holds.

\subsubsection{A. BCC first-shell condensate}

Let the normalized BCC first shell be
\begin{equation}
S_{\mathrm{BCC}}
=
\frac1{\sqrt2}
\left\{
(\pm1,\pm1,0),(\pm1,0,\pm1),(0,\pm1,\pm1)
\right\}.
\label{eq:BCC_shell_square}
\end{equation}
Write the equal-amplitude real condensate as
\begin{equation}
\phi_0(x)
=
2A\sum_{a=1}^6 \cos(Q_a\cdot x)
=
A\sum_{Q\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}} e^{iQ\cdot x}.
\label{eq:phi0_equal_amp}
\end{equation}
Hence the Fourier coefficient of \(\phi_0\) is
\begin{equation}
\widehat{\phi_0}(Q)=
\begin{cases}
A,& Q\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}},\\[3pt]
0,& Q\notin S_{\mathrm{BCC}}.
\end{cases}
\label{eq:phi0_fourier_coeff}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Quadratic scalar periodic potential}

Now take the literal quadratic scalar periodic potential
\begin{equation}
U_{\mathrm{per}}(x)=c\,\phi_0(x)^2.
\label{eq:Uper_literal_square}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\phi_0(x)^2
=
A^2
\sum_{Q_1,Q_2\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}}
e^{i(Q_1+Q_2)\cdot x}.
\label{eq:phi0_square_expand}
\end{equation}
Therefore the Fourier coefficient at \(G_*\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}\) is
\begin{equation}
\widehat{\phi_0^2}(G_*)
=
A^2\,N(G_*),
\qquad
N(G_*):=
\#\left\{
(Q_1,Q_2)\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}^2:\ Q_1+Q_2=G_*
\right\}.
\label{eq:phi0_square_coeff_general}
\end{equation}

So the problem reduces to counting ordered first-shell pairs summing to a first-shell vector.

\subsubsection{C. Explicit pair counting}

Choose for concreteness
\begin{equation}
G_*=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}(1,1,0).
\label{eq:Gstar_choice}
\end{equation}
The first-shell vectors satisfying \(Q_1+Q_2=G_*\) are:
\begin{equation}
\frac{1}{\sqrt2}(1,0,1)
+
\frac{1}{\sqrt2}(0,1,-1)
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt2}(1,1,0),
\label{eq:pair1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\frac{1}{\sqrt2}(1,0,-1)
+
\frac{1}{\sqrt2}(0,1,1)
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt2}(1,1,0).
\label{eq:pair2}
\end{equation}
Since ordered pairs are counted in \eqref{eq:phi0_square_expand}, the reversed pairs also contribute:
\begin{equation}
(Q_1,Q_2),\quad (Q_2,Q_1).
\label{eq:ordered_pairs}
\end{equation}
Thus
\begin{equation}
N(G_*)=4.
\label{eq:NGstar_4}
\end{equation}

By cubic symmetry, the same count holds for every \(G_*\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}\).

\begin{lemma}[First-shell square coefficient]
For the equal-amplitude BCC first-shell condensate,
\begin{equation}
\widehat{\phi_0^2}(G_*)=4A^2
\qquad
\forall G_*\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}.
\label{eq:phi0square_final}
\end{equation}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Equation \eqref{eq:NGstar_4} proves the result for one representative \(G_*\), and cubic symmetry propagates it to the full shell.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{D. Consequence for the Bragg mass}

From \eqref{eq:Uper_literal_square},
\begin{equation}
\widehat U(G_*)
=
c\,\widehat{\phi_0^2}(G_*)
=
4cA^2.
\label{eq:Uhat_direct}
\end{equation}
Hence the projected constant Bragg mass is
\begin{equation}
B_0=\widehat U(G_*)\,\mathbf 1_2
=
4cA^2\,\mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:B0_direct}
\end{equation}
Therefore,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\mathrm{per}}(x)=c\,\phi_0(x)^2
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\widehat U(G_*)\neq 0
\ \text{ generically}.
}
\label{eq:Uhat_nonzero_box}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{E. Implication}

Thus the statement
\[
\widehat U(G_*)=0
\]
is \emph{not} true for a literal pure square \(U_{\mathrm{per}}\propto \phi_0^2\).
To make \(B_0=0\), one needs one of the following:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a more complicated microscopic scalar Hessian in which distinct contributions cancel at first-shell momentum;
\item a non-scalar enriched mechanism so that the relevant shell Dirac structure comes from \(W^1,W^2\), not from vanishing scalar Bragg mass;
\item a modified choice of \(U_{\mathrm{per}}\) with an explicit first-shell subtraction.
\end{enumerate}

\subsubsection{F. Example: scalar \(\phi^4\) Hessian}

For a standard scalar quartic model
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L
=
\frac12 \phi\,\mathcal K(-i\nabla)\phi
+\frac{g}{4}\phi^4,
\label{eq:scalar_phi4_model}
\end{equation}
linearization around \(\phi_0\) gives a scalar Hessian
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{lin}}
=
\mathcal K(-i\nabla)+3g\,\phi_0(x)^2.
\label{eq:scalar_hessian_phi4}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\widehat U(G_*)
=
3g\,\widehat{\phi_0^2}(G_*)
=
12gA^2,
\label{eq:scalar_hessian_firstshell}
\end{equation}
which is again nonzero generically.

So the direct computation confirms:
a plain scalar quartic Hessian does \emph{not} automatically eliminate the constant Bragg mass at the first shell.

\subsubsection{G. Honest conclusion}

What is proved here is stronger than a restatement:

\[
\text{for the literal quadratic scalar example }U_{\mathrm{per}}\propto \phi_0^2,
\quad
\widehat U(G_*)=4cA^2\neq 0.
\]

Therefore any previous claim that a bare quadratic first-shell scalar potential automatically gives
\[
\widehat U(G_*)=0
\]
must be interpreted as requiring an additional cancellation mechanism beyond the literal square.

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\phi_0(x)=2A\sum_{a=1}^6\cos(Q_a\cdot x)
=
A\sum_{Q\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}} e^{iQ\cdot x},
\qquad
\widehat{\phi_0}(Q)=A\ \text{for }Q\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}.
\]

For the literal quadratic scalar periodic potential
\[
U_{\mathrm{per}}(x)=c\,\phi_0(x)^2,
\]
one has
\[
\phi_0(x)^2
=
A^2\sum_{Q_1,Q_2\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}} e^{i(Q_1+Q_2)\cdot x}.
\]

Hence
\[
\widehat{\phi_0^2}(G_*)
=
A^2\,N(G_*),
\qquad
N(G_*):=
\#\{(Q_1,Q_2)\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}^2:\ Q_1+Q_2=G_*\}.
\]

For every \(G_*\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}\),
\[
N(G_*)=4.
\]
Therefore
\[
\widehat{\phi_0^2}(G_*)=4A^2,
\qquad
\widehat U(G_*)=4cA^2.
\]

So the constant Bragg mass is
\[
B_0=\widehat U(G_*)\,\mathbf 1_2
=
4cA^2\,\mathbf 1_2,
\]
which is generically nonzero.

Thus:
\[
\boxed{
U_{\mathrm{per}}(x)=c\,\phi_0(x)^2
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\widehat U(G_*)\neq 0.
}
\]

In particular, the statement
\[
\widehat U(G_*)=0
\]
does not hold for the literal pure-square scalar example.

For a standard scalar \(\phi^4\) Hessian,
\[
H_{\mathrm{lin}}=\mathcal K(-i\nabla)+3g\,\phi_0(x)^2,
\]
one gets
\[
\widehat U(G_*)=12gA^2\neq 0
\]
generically, again confirming that the constant Bragg mass is not automatically removed in a plain scalar model.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{\(B_0\neq 0\) in the enriched \(4\times4\) shell matrix: exact spectrum and obstruction theorem}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now accept the direct primitive-cell computation
\[
B_0=\widehat U(G_*)\,\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
\widehat U(G_*)=4cA^2\neq 0
\]
for the literal quadratic scalar example \(U_{\mathrm{per}}=c\phi_0^2\), and determine the exact spectral effect of this term in the minimal enriched shell-pair Hamiltonian.

\subsubsection{A. Minimal enriched shell Hamiltonian with nonzero scalar Bragg mass}

The shell-level Dirac theorem requires \(B_0=0\). 
Without imposing that condition, the minimal enriched \(4\times4\) projected shell Hamiltonian has the form
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p)
=
E_0(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel \tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\tau_1\otimes
\Bigl(
B_0\mathbf 1_2
+
\nu_1 p_1 s_1
+
\nu_2 p_2 s_2
\Bigr)
+
O(|p|^2).
\label{eq:Hproj_B0_nonzero}
\end{equation}
Here:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(\tau_i\) act on the shell-pair sector,
\item \(s_i\) act on the internal doublet,
\item \(B_0=\widehat U(G_*)\) is the constant scalar Bragg mass,
\item \(\nu_1,\nu_2\neq 0\) are the transverse enriched shell couplings.
\end{itemize}

Define
\begin{equation}
r_\perp(p):=\sqrt{\nu_1^2p_1^2+\nu_2^2p_2^2}.
\label{eq:rperp_def}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Exact diagonalization}

Subtract the scalar part \(E_0(p)\mathbf 1_4\) and define
\begin{equation}
\widetilde H(p)
:=
H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p)-E_0(p)\mathbf 1_4
=
v_\parallel p_\parallel \tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\tau_1\otimes
\Bigl(
B_0\mathbf 1_2+\nu_1 p_1 s_1+\nu_2 p_2 s_2
\Bigr).
\label{eq:Htilde_def}
\end{equation}
Because \(\tau_3\) anticommutes with \(\tau_1\),
\begin{equation}
\widetilde H(p)^2
=
v_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2\,\mathbf 1_4
+
\mathbf 1_2\otimes
\Bigl(
B_0\mathbf 1_2+\nu_1 p_1 s_1+\nu_2 p_2 s_2
\Bigr)^2.
\label{eq:Htilde_square}
\end{equation}

Now set
\begin{equation}
M_\perp(p):=B_0\mathbf 1_2+\nu_1 p_1 s_1+\nu_2 p_2 s_2.
\label{eq:Mperp_def}
\end{equation}
Since \(s_1,s_2\) anticommute and square to \(\mathbf 1_2\), the internal \(2\times2\) matrix
\[
\nu_1 p_1 s_1+\nu_2 p_2 s_2
\]
has eigenvalues \(\pm r_\perp(p)\).
Therefore \(M_\perp(p)\) has eigenvalues
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\pm(p)=B_0\pm r_\perp(p).
\label{eq:Mperp_evalues}
\end{equation}
Hence the eigenvalues of \(\widetilde H(p)^2\) are
\begin{equation}
v_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2+\bigl(B_0\pm r_\perp(p)\bigr)^2.
\label{eq:Htilde_square_evalues}
\end{equation}
Taking square roots, the full spectrum of \(H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p)\) is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}\bigl(H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p)\bigr)
=
E_0(p)
\pm
\sqrt{v_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2+\bigl(B_0+r_\perp(p)\bigr)^2}
,
\quad
E_0(p)
\pm
\sqrt{v_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2+\bigl(B_0-r_\perp(p)\bigr)^2}
.
}
\label{eq:full_spectrum_B0}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. Consequences at the expansion point}

At \(p=0\), one has \(r_\perp(0)=0\), so
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}\bigl(H_{\mathrm{proj}}(0)\bigr)
=
E_0(0)\pm |B_0|,
\qquad
\text{each doubly degenerate}.
\label{eq:spectrum_at_zero}
\end{equation}
Thus the gap at the nominal shell expansion point is
\begin{equation}
\Delta_0=2|B_0|.
\label{eq:gap_at_zero}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Scalar Bragg mass obstruction theorem]
If \(B_0\neq 0\), then the minimal enriched shell Hamiltonian \eqref{eq:Hproj_B0_nonzero} does \emph{not} have a massless Dirac point at \(p=0\).
In fact, the crossing is gapped by \(2|B_0|\).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from \eqref{eq:spectrum_at_zero} and \eqref{eq:gap_at_zero}.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{D. Why a scalar energy shift cannot remove \(B_0\)}

A scalar redefinition of the reference energy changes only the term
\[
E_0(p)\mathbf 1_4.
\]
But the constant Bragg term is
\[
B_0\,\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\]
which is traceless in the shell-pair sector and therefore cannot be removed by adding or subtracting a multiple of the identity.

Hence:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{a scalar energy subtraction cannot eliminate } B_0\,\tau_1\otimes\mathbf 1_2.
}
\label{eq:no_scalar_shift_removal}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{E. Zero set of the principal symbol}

The zero-energy condition for the traceless principal symbol \(\widetilde H(p)\) is
\[
0\in \operatorname{spec}(\widetilde H(p)).
\]
By \eqref{eq:Htilde_square_evalues}, this requires
\begin{equation}
p_\parallel=0,
\qquad
B_0\pm r_\perp(p)=0.
\label{eq:zero_condition}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
p_\parallel=0,
\qquad
r_\perp(p)=|B_0|.
\label{eq:ring_condition}
\end{equation}
Thus the zero set is the ellipse
\begin{equation}
\nu_1^2p_1^2+\nu_2^2p_2^2=B_0^2,
\qquad
p_\parallel=0.
\label{eq:ellipse_zero}
\end{equation}

\begin{corollary}[No isolated Dirac point for \(B_0\neq 0\)]
If \(B_0\neq 0\), the zero set of the principal symbol is not an isolated point but an elliptic ring in the transverse plane.
Hence the minimal enriched shell matrix does not produce a Dirac cone.
\end{corollary}

\subsubsection{F. General classification of constant pair-mixing terms}

We now go one step further.
Replace the scalar constant Bragg mass \(B_0\mathbf 1_2\) by the most general constant Hermitian internal matrix
\begin{equation}
M_0
=
m_0\mathbf 1_2+m_1 s_1+m_2 s_2+m_3 s_3.
\label{eq:M0_general}
\end{equation}
Then the principal shell Hamiltonian becomes
\begin{equation}
\widetilde H_{M_0}(p)
=
v_\parallel p_\parallel \tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\tau_1\otimes
\Bigl(
M_0+\nu_1 p_1 s_1+\nu_2 p_2 s_2
\Bigr).
\label{eq:H_M0_general}
\end{equation}
A zero of the principal symbol requires
\begin{equation}
p_\parallel=0,
\qquad
M_0+\nu_1 p_1 s_1+\nu_2 p_2 s_2
\ \text{has a zero eigenvalue}.
\label{eq:M0_zero_condition}
\end{equation}

Now observe:

\begin{itemize}
\item the identity component \(m_0\mathbf 1_2\) cannot be canceled by momentum-dependent \(s_1,s_2\) terms;
\item the \(s_3\) component \(m_3 s_3\) cannot be canceled either, because the available momentum-dependent matrices lie only in the \(s_1,s_2\) plane;
\item the planar components \(m_1 s_1+m_2 s_2\) \emph{can} be absorbed by shifting the transverse momentum origin:
\begin{equation}
p_1\mapsto p_1+\frac{m_1}{\nu_1},
\qquad
p_2\mapsto p_2+\frac{m_2}{\nu_2}.
\label{eq:momentum_shift}
\end{equation}
\end{itemize}

Therefore:

\begin{theorem}[Classification of constant pair-mixing terms]
For the minimal enriched shell Hamiltonian:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(m_1 s_1+m_2 s_2\) is not a genuine mass; it merely shifts the transverse valley center.
\item \(m_3 s_3\) is a genuine internal mass term.
\item \(m_0\mathbf 1_2\) is a genuine scalar Bragg mass term.
\end{enumerate}

Hence a massless Dirac point requires
\begin{equation}
m_0=0,\qquad m_3=0,
\label{eq:massless_conditions_general}
\end{equation}
while \(m_1,m_2\) may be removed by redefining the transverse momentum origin.
\end{theorem}

\subsubsection{G. Application to the literal quadratic scalar example}

For the literal quadratic scalar example
\begin{equation}
U_{\mathrm{per}}(x)=c\,\phi_0(x)^2,
\label{eq:literal_square_again}
\end{equation}
the primitive-cell calculation gave
\begin{equation}
B_0=\widehat U(G_*)\mathbf 1_2=4cA^2\,\mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:B0_literal_square}
\end{equation}
So this corresponds precisely to the \(m_0\mathbf 1_2\) case with
\[
m_0=4cA^2,\qquad m_1=m_2=m_3=0.
\]
Therefore the constant term is a genuine scalar Bragg mass and cannot be removed by:

\begin{enumerate}
\item subtracting a scalar reference energy,
\item shifting the valley momentum origin,
\item or using only the transverse enriched linear couplings.
\end{enumerate}

Hence:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the literal scalar quadratic example does not produce a massless shell Dirac point.}
}
\label{eq:literal_square_no_dirac}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{H. Honest conclusion}

This computation sharpens the previous correction.
Not only is it false that
\[
U_{\mathrm{per}}\propto \phi_0^2 \Longrightarrow \widehat U(G_*)=0,
\]
but in fact the resulting nonzero \(\widehat U(G_*)\) is a \emph{genuine scalar Bragg mass obstruction} to shell Dirac emergence in the minimal enriched \(4\times4\) truncation.

Therefore a consistent microscopic Dirac construction must do one of the following:

\begin{enumerate}
\item produce an exact cancellation so that the total scalar pair-mixing coefficient satisfies
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}=0;
\]
\item derive a different microscopic operator in which the constant pair-mixing block is not proportional to the identity and its removable part can be shifted away;
\item or realize a grading/odd-coupling mechanism in which the relevant projected principal operator is block-off-diagonal from the outset, bypassing the literal scalar Bragg mass channel.
\end{enumerate}

%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p)
=
E_0(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel \tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\tau_1\otimes
\Bigl(
B_0\mathbf 1_2+\nu_1 p_1 s_1+\nu_2 p_2 s_2
\Bigr)
+
O(|p|^2).
\]

Let
\[
r_\perp(p)=\sqrt{\nu_1^2p_1^2+\nu_2^2p_2^2}.
\]
Then the exact spectrum is
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p))
=
E_0(p)\pm\sqrt{v_\parallel^2p_\parallel^2+\bigl(B_0+r_\perp(p)\bigr)^2},
\qquad
E_0(p)\pm\sqrt{v_\parallel^2p_\parallel^2+\bigl(B_0-r_\perp(p)\bigr)^2}.
\]

At \(p=0\),
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{proj}}(0))=E_0(0)\pm |B_0|,
\]
so the gap is
\[
\Delta_0=2|B_0|.
\]

Therefore:
\[
\boxed{
B_0\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\text{no massless Dirac point at }p=0.
}
\]

A scalar energy subtraction cannot remove \(B_0\), because it changes only
\[
E_0(p)\mathbf 1_4,
\]
whereas the constant Bragg term is
\[
B_0\,\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]

The zero set of the principal symbol is
\[
p_\parallel=0,
\qquad
\nu_1^2p_1^2+\nu_2^2p_2^2=B_0^2,
\]
which is an elliptic ring, not an isolated Dirac point.

More generally, for a constant pair-mixing block
\[
M_0=m_0\mathbf 1_2+m_1 s_1+m_2 s_2+m_3 s_3,
\]
one has:

\[
m_1 s_1+m_2 s_2
\quad\text{can be removed by shifting }(p_1,p_2),
\]
\[
m_3 s_3
\quad\text{is a genuine internal mass},
\]
\[
m_0\mathbf 1_2
\quad\text{is a genuine scalar Bragg mass}.
\]

Hence a massless Dirac point requires
\[
\boxed{
m_0=0,\qquad m_3=0,
}
\]
while \(m_1,m_2\) are removable by redefining the transverse momentum origin.

For the literal scalar quadratic example
\[
U_{\mathrm{per}}(x)=c\,\phi_0(x)^2,
\qquad
B_0=4cA^2\,\mathbf 1_2,
\]
so the constant term is precisely a genuine scalar Bragg mass obstruction.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Actual microscopic scalar Hessian and the impossibility of scalar Bragg-mass cancellation}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now compute the \emph{actual} microscopic scalar Hessian seen by the internal doublet sector, and determine whether the constant shell-pair Bragg mass
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}
\]
can cancel inside the scalar Hessian itself.

\subsubsection{A. Exact microscopic linearization}

Consider the canonical complex condensate model
\begin{equation}
N(\Phi)
=
r\Phi-\kappa \nabla^2\Phi+\lambda \nabla^4\Phi+u(\Phi^\dagger\Phi)\Phi.
\label{eq:N_Phi_actual}
\end{equation}
Its exact first variation around a background \(\Phi_0\) is
\begin{equation}
\delta N_{\Phi_0}[\eta]
=
r\eta-\kappa\nabla^2\eta+\lambda\nabla^4\eta
+
u\Big[
(\Phi_0^\dagger\Phi_0)\eta
+
(\Phi_0^\dagger\eta)\Phi_0
+
(\eta^\dagger\Phi_0)\Phi_0
\Big].
\label{eq:exact_first_variation_actual}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in BdG/conservative form one may write
\begin{equation}
i\partial_t\eta=L_{\Phi_0}\eta+M_{\Phi_0}\bar\eta,
\label{eq:BdG_form_actual}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
L_{\Phi_0}\eta
=
r\eta-\kappa\nabla^2\eta+\lambda\nabla^4\eta
+
u\Big[
(\Phi_0^\dagger\Phi_0)\eta+(\Phi_0^\dagger\eta)\Phi_0
\Big],
\label{eq:L_Phi0_actual}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
M_{\Phi_0}\bar\eta
=
u(\eta^\dagger\Phi_0)\Phi_0.
\label{eq:M_Phi0_actual}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Canonical symmetric BCC background}

Take the canonical locked BCC background
\begin{equation}
\Phi_0(x)=\phi_0(x)\,\zeta,
\qquad
\zeta^\dagger\zeta=1,
\label{eq:Phi0_locked_actual}
\end{equation}
with equal-amplitude first-shell condensate
\begin{equation}
\phi_0(x)
=
A\sum_{Q\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}} e^{iQ\cdot x}
=
2A\sum_{a=1}^6 \cos(Q_a\cdot x).
\label{eq:phi0_BCC_actual}
\end{equation}
Here
\begin{equation}
S_{\mathrm{BCC}}
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt2}
\left\{
(\pm1,\pm1,0),(\pm1,0,\pm1),(0,\pm1,\pm1)
\right\}.
\label{eq:S_BCC_actual}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. Restriction to the internal doublet sector}

Let
\begin{equation}
L=\mathbb C\zeta,
\qquad
Q=(\mathbb C\zeta)^\perp,
\qquad
\mathbb C^3=L\oplus Q.
\label{eq:LQ_split_actual}
\end{equation}
We now restrict the fluctuation \(\eta\) to the internal doublet sector:
\begin{equation}
\eta(x)\in \Gamma(Q),
\qquad
\zeta^\dagger \eta(x)=0.
\label{eq:eta_in_Q}
\end{equation}

Since \(\Phi_0=\phi_0\zeta\), we have
\begin{equation}
\Phi_0^\dagger\eta
=
\phi_0^*\,\zeta^\dagger\eta
=
0,
\label{eq:Phi0eta_zero}
\end{equation}
and similarly
\begin{equation}
\eta^\dagger\Phi_0
=
\phi_0\,\eta^\dagger\zeta
=
0.
\label{eq:etaPhi0_zero}
\end{equation}
Therefore the two rank-one Hessian terms vanish identically on the \(Q\)-sector:
\begin{equation}
(\Phi_0^\dagger\eta)\Phi_0=0,
\qquad
(\eta^\dagger\Phi_0)\Phi_0=0.
\label{eq:rank_one_terms_zero}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact linearized operator on \(Q\) reduces to
\begin{equation}
H_Q
=
r-\kappa\nabla^2+\lambda\nabla^4+u|\phi_0(x)|^2.
\label{eq:HQ_final_actual}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, the actual scalar periodic Hessian seen by the internal doublet sector is
\begin{equation}
U_{\mathrm{per}}^{\mathrm{tot}}(x)=u|\phi_0(x)|^2.
\label{eq:Uper_tot_actual}
\end{equation}

Moreover, the anomalous BdG block vanishes on \(Q\):
\begin{equation}
M_{\Phi_0}\bar\eta
=
u(\eta^\dagger\Phi_0)\Phi_0
=
0.
\label{eq:BdG_anomalous_zero}
\end{equation}
So the \(Q\)-sector sees a purely scalar periodic Hessian.

\subsubsection{D. First-shell Fourier coefficient of \texorpdfstring{$|\phi_0|^2$}{|phi0|^2}}

Because the canonical symmetric condensate is real,
\begin{equation}
|\phi_0(x)|^2=\phi_0(x)^2.
\label{eq:real_condensate_square}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:phi0_BCC_actual},
\begin{equation}
\phi_0(x)^2
=
A^2
\sum_{Q_1,Q_2\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}}
e^{i(Q_1+Q_2)\cdot x}.
\label{eq:phi0_square_expand_actual}
\end{equation}
Therefore the first-shell Fourier coefficient at \(G_*\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}\) is
\begin{equation}
\widehat{\phi_0^2}(G_*)
=
A^2\,N(G_*),
\qquad
N(G_*):=
\#\Bigl\{
(Q_1,Q_2)\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}^2:\ Q_1+Q_2=G_*
\Bigr\}.
\label{eq:phi0_square_coeff_count}
\end{equation}

Choose the representative
\begin{equation}
G_*=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}(1,1,0).
\label{eq:Gstar_representative_actual}
\end{equation}
Then the allowed first-shell decompositions are
\begin{equation}
\frac{1}{\sqrt2}(1,0,1)+\frac{1}{\sqrt2}(0,1,-1)=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}(1,1,0),
\label{eq:pair_decomp_1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\frac{1}{\sqrt2}(1,0,-1)+\frac{1}{\sqrt2}(0,1,1)=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}(1,1,0).
\label{eq:pair_decomp_2}
\end{equation}
Since ordered pairs are counted in \eqref{eq:phi0_square_expand_actual}, the reversed pairs also contribute.
Hence
\begin{equation}
N(G_*)=4.
\label{eq:NGstar_four}
\end{equation}
By cubic symmetry, this holds for every \(G_*\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}\). Therefore
\begin{equation}
\widehat{\phi_0^2}(G_*)=4A^2.
\label{eq:phi0_square_coeff_final}
\end{equation}

Substituting into \eqref{eq:Uper_tot_actual}, we obtain
\begin{equation}
\widehat U_{\mathrm{per}}^{\mathrm{tot}}(G_*)
=
u\,\widehat{|\phi_0|^2}(G_*)
=
4uA^2.
\label{eq:Uhat_tot_final}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{E. Primitive-cell shell overlap and Bragg mass}

In the constant-envelope shell-pair reduction,
\begin{equation}
B_0=\widehat U(G_*)\,\mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:B0_overlap_actual}
\end{equation}
Therefore the \emph{actual} constant pair-mixing Bragg mass generated by the microscopic scalar Hessian is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}=4uA^2\,\mathbf 1_2.
}
\label{eq:B0tot_box}
\end{equation}
In particular, if
\begin{equation}
uA^2\neq 0,
\label{eq:nonzero_uA}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\neq 0.
\label{eq:B0tot_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{F. No scalar-Hessian cancellation}

The key point is now immediate:
inside the \(Q\)-sector scalar Hessian, the only periodic scalar contribution is
\[
u|\phi_0|^2.
\]
The two additional Hessian terms in \eqref{eq:exact_first_variation_actual} vanish identically on \(Q\) by \eqref{eq:rank_one_terms_zero}.
Therefore there are no remaining scalar terms available to cancel \(\widehat U_{\mathrm{per}}^{\mathrm{tot}}(G_*)\).

Hence:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{for the canonical symmetric BCC background, scalar-Hessian cancellation of }B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\text{ is impossible.}
}
\label{eq:no_cancellation_box}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{G. Consequence}

Thus, within the actual microscopic scalar Hessian channel, the shell-pair constant mass does not cancel:
\begin{equation}
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}=4uA^2\,\mathbf 1_2\neq 0.
\label{eq:final_scalar_obstruction}
\end{equation}
So the plain scalar channel does not produce a massless shell Dirac point.
Any consistent microscopic Dirac mechanism must therefore come from a different structure, e.g.
\begin{enumerate}
\item an exact cancellation involving additional non-scalar sectors not present in \(H_Q\),
\item a graded/projection mechanism in which the dangerous scalar pair-mixing block is absent from the relevant reduced operator,
\item or a genuinely different microscopic completion beyond the plain scalar Hessian channel.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Exact logical status.}
What is proved here is exact:
\[
\text{actual scalar Hessian on }Q
\Longrightarrow
U_{\mathrm{per}}^{\mathrm{tot}}(x)=u|\phi_0(x)|^2
\Longrightarrow
\widehat U_{\mathrm{per}}^{\mathrm{tot}}(G_*)=4uA^2
\Longrightarrow
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}=4uA^2\,\mathbf 1_2\neq 0.
\]
So, for the canonical symmetric background, no cancellation is available inside the scalar Hessian itself.

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\delta N_{\Phi_0}[\eta]
=
r\eta-\kappa\nabla^2\eta+\lambda\nabla^4\eta
+
u\Big[
(\Phi_0^\dagger\Phi_0)\eta
+
(\Phi_0^\dagger\eta)\Phi_0
+
(\eta^\dagger\Phi_0)\Phi_0
\Big].
\]

Let
\[
\Phi_0(x)=\phi_0(x)\zeta,
\qquad
\phi_0(x)=A\sum_{Q\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}}e^{iQ\cdot x},
\qquad
Q=(\mathbb C\zeta)^\perp.
\]
For \(\eta\in \Gamma(Q)\), one has
\[
\Phi_0^\dagger\eta=0,
\qquad
\eta^\dagger\Phi_0=0,
\]
so the rank-one Hessian terms vanish identically on \(Q\).

Therefore the actual scalar periodic Hessian on the internal doublet sector is
\[
H_Q
=
r-\kappa\nabla^2+\lambda\nabla^4+u|\phi_0(x)|^2,
\qquad
U_{\mathrm{per}}^{\mathrm{tot}}(x)=u|\phi_0(x)|^2.
\]

For the canonical symmetric BCC first-shell condensate,
\[
\widehat{\phi_0^2}(G_*)=4A^2,
\]
hence
\[
\widehat U_{\mathrm{per}}^{\mathrm{tot}}(G_*)=4uA^2.
\]

Using the shell-pair overlap formula
\[
B_0=\widehat U(G_*)\,\mathbf 1_2,
\]
we obtain
\[
\boxed{
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}=4uA^2\,\mathbf 1_2.
}
\]

Thus, if \(uA^2\neq 0\),
\[
\boxed{
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\neq 0.
}
\]

Since the other Hessian contributions vanish exactly on \(Q\), there is no available scalar-Hessian cancellation mechanism inside the canonical symmetric background.

Therefore:
\[
\boxed{
\text{plain scalar Hessian channel fails to eliminate the Bragg mass.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Graded projector-Hessian calculation: why the current refined model has \(J=0\)}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We test whether the projector/\(Q\)-sector can remove or grade away the scalar Bragg mass
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\,\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\]
at quadratic order in the current refined microscopic model.

\subsubsection{A. Refined microscopic free energy}

The refined model is
\begin{equation}
F_{\mathrm{ref}}
=
F_{\mathrm{triplet}}+F_{\mathrm{align}},
\label{eq:Fref_def}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
F_{\mathrm{triplet}}
=
\int d^3x\,
\left[
\frac r2 \Psi^\dagger\Psi
+
\frac Z2 \partial_i\Psi^\dagger\partial_i\Psi
+
\frac Y2 (\nabla^2\Psi)^\dagger(\nabla^2\Psi)
+
\frac g4 (\Psi^\dagger\Psi)^2
\right],
\label{eq:Ftriplet_def}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
F_{\mathrm{align}}
=
\frac{\chi}{4}\int d^3x\,\rho^2\,\mathrm{Tr}(\partial_iP\,\partial_iP)
=
\frac{\chi}{2}\int d^3x\,\rho^2\,(D_iz)^\dagger(D_iz).
\label{eq:Falign_def}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Locked constant-projector background}

Take the polarization-locked background
\begin{equation}
\Psi_0(x)=\rho_0(x)z_0,
\qquad
z_0^\dagger z_0=1,
\qquad
z_0=\mathrm{const},
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger=\mathrm{const}.
\label{eq:locked_background_ref}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\partial_iP_0=0,
\qquad
D_iz_0=0.
\label{eq:P0_const}
\end{equation}

Now decompose fluctuations as
\begin{equation}
\Psi=(\rho_0+\sigma)z_0+\xi,
\qquad
z_0^\dagger\xi=0.
\label{eq:Psi_decomp_sigma_xi}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, in projector language,
\begin{equation}
z=z_0+\pi+O(\pi^2),
\qquad
z_0^\dagger\pi=0,
\label{eq:z_decomp_pi}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
P=P_0+\delta P+O((\delta P)^2),
\qquad
\delta P=z_0\pi^\dagger+\pi z_0^\dagger.
\label{eq:P_decomp_deltaP}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. Quadratic expansion of the projector stiffness term}

Since \(\partial_iP_0=0\), one has
\begin{equation}
\partial_iP=\partial_i\delta P+O(\pi\,\partial\pi,\pi^2).
\label{eq:dP_expand}
\end{equation}
Therefore, to quadratic order,
\begin{equation}
F_{\mathrm{align}}^{(2)}
=
\frac{\chi}{4}\int d^3x\,\rho_0(x)^2\,\mathrm{Tr}(\partial_i\delta P\,\partial_i\delta P).
\label{eq:Falign_quad_1}
\end{equation}
In the constant-amplitude approximation \(\rho_0\simeq \bar\rho\),
\begin{equation}
F_{\mathrm{align}}^{(2)}
\approx
\frac{\chi\bar\rho^2}{2}\int d^3x\,\partial_i\pi^\dagger\partial_i\pi.
\label{eq:Falign_quad_2}
\end{equation}

This is crucial: \(F_{\mathrm{align}}^{(2)}\) contains only projector-tangent quadratic terms, with no piece linear in \(\pi\), and no bilinear term involving \(\sigma\) or \(\xi\) from the shell sector.

\subsubsection{D. Absence of shell--projector bilinear mixing}

The shell-enriched tensor \(N_{ij}^a\) would have to come from a quadratic mixing source of schematic form
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(2)}
\sim
J[\sigma,\psi]\cdot \xi
\label{eq:Lmix_required}
\end{equation}
or, in projector variables,
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(2)}
\sim
J[\sigma,\psi]\cdot \pi.
\label{eq:Lmix_required_pi}
\end{equation}
But from \eqref{eq:Falign_quad_2} we see that \(F_{\mathrm{align}}\) begins at order \(\pi^2\), not at order \(\pi\).
Moreover, because \(P_0\) is constant, there is no term of the schematic form
\[
(\partial_i\rho_0)\,(\partial_j\psi)\,\pi^a
\]
or
\[
(\partial_i\phi_0)\,(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a
\]
generated at tree level from \(F_{\mathrm{align}}\).

Thus the quadratic source vanishes:
\begin{equation}
J=0.
\label{eq:J_zero}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the quadratic Hessian is block diagonal:
\begin{equation}
\delta^2F_{\mathrm{ref}}
=
\delta^2F_\sigma+\delta^2F_\xi,
\label{eq:block_diag_hessian}
\end{equation}
with no bilinear \(\sigma\)-\(\xi\) term.

\begin{theorem}[Block-diagonal projector Hessian theorem]
For the current refined model \(F_{\mathrm{ref}}=F_{\mathrm{triplet}}+F_{\mathrm{align}}\), expanded around a locked constant-projector background \(P_0=\mathrm{const}\), the quadratic Hessian is block diagonal between the shell sector and the tangent-projector sector:
\begin{equation}
\delta^2F_{\mathrm{ref}}
=
\delta^2F_\sigma+\delta^2F_\xi.
\label{eq:block_diag_theorem}
\end{equation}
In particular,
\begin{equation}
J=0.
\label{eq:J_zero_theorem}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The triplet part respects the locked decomposition \(\Psi=(\rho_0+\sigma)z_0+\xi\) with \(z_0\) constant, while the projector stiffness term begins at quadratic order in \(\delta P\sim \pi\) because \(\partial_iP_0=0\). Therefore no term linear in \(\pi\) and bilinear with the shell sector appears at quadratic order. This gives \eqref{eq:block_diag_theorem} and \eqref{eq:J_zero_theorem}.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{E. Consequence for induced shell-enriched tensors}

The previously discussed mechanism for producing a correction \(\delta N_{ij}^a\) from the projector sector is Gaussian elimination of a heavy projector mode:
\begin{equation}
\delta L_{\mathrm{eff}}
=
-\frac12 J\,G_\pi\,J.
\label{eq:deltaLeff_from_J}
\end{equation}
But if \(J=0\), then
\begin{equation}
\delta L_{\mathrm{eff}}=0,
\qquad
\delta N_{ij}^a=0
\label{eq:deltaN_zero}
\end{equation}
at quadratic order in the current refined model.

Thus the projector sector does not modify the leading witness triple:
\begin{equation}
\delta W_\parallel=\delta W_I=\delta W_J=0
\qquad
\text{(at this order)}.
\label{eq:deltaW_zero}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{F. Implication for the scalar Bragg mass}

We previously proved that in the actual scalar Hessian channel on the internal doublet sector,
\begin{equation}
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}=4uA^2\,\mathbf 1_2\neq 0.
\label{eq:B0tot_again}
\end{equation}
The natural hope was that the projector/\(Q\)-sector might generate a compensating graded or off-diagonal contribution.
However, by \eqref{eq:J_zero_theorem}--\eqref{eq:deltaN_zero}, the current projector stiffness sector does not couple linearly to the shell block at quadratic order.

Therefore the projector sector does \emph{not} cancel or grade away the scalar Bragg mass:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{in the current refined model, }
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}
\text{ survives unchanged at quadratic order.}
}
\label{eq:B0_survives}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{G. What the projector sector actually does}

Although it does not cure the scalar Bragg mass problem, the projector stiffness term has two direct effects:

\begin{enumerate}
\item it gives the tangent projector mode a positive inverse propagator of order
\begin{equation}
G_\pi^{-1}(q_*)\sim \chi\bar\rho^2 q_*^2,
\label{eq:Gpi_inverse}
\end{equation}
so projector modes are pushed upward into the remote sector;

\item because the stiffness term is even under \(G_*\leftrightarrow -G_*\), it tends to preserve opposite-valley matching rather than spoil it.
\end{enumerate}

Thus its role is stabilizing, not mass-canceling.

\subsubsection{H. Final conclusion}

The graded projector-Hessian calculation gives a sharp negative result:

\[
\text{current refined projector sector}
\Longrightarrow
J=0
\Longrightarrow
\delta N_{ij}^a=0
\Longrightarrow
\text{no cancellation of }B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}.
\]

So if one wants a genuine microscopic Dirac mechanism, one must introduce an additional UV coupling whose quadratic expansion contains a nonzero shell--projector mixing source
\[
L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(2)}\sim J[\sigma,\psi]\cdot \xi.
\]
Only then can the projector sector induce a nontrivial \(\delta N_{ij}^a\) and potentially alter the constant shell-pair block.

\paragraph{Exact logical status.}
What is now closed is not merely that the current model fails heuristically, but the stronger statement:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{for the current refined }U(3)\text{-invariant triplet + projector-stiffness model,}
\quad
J=0
\ \text{at quadratic order.}
}
\end{equation}
Hence this model cannot remove the scalar Bragg mass through the projector sector.

%%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
F_{\mathrm{ref}}=F_{\mathrm{triplet}}+F_{\mathrm{align}},
\qquad
F_{\mathrm{align}}=
\frac{\chi}{4}\int d^3x\,\rho^2\,\mathrm{Tr}(\partial_iP\,\partial_iP).
\]

Expand around the locked constant-projector background
\[
\Psi_0(x)=\rho_0(x)z_0,
\qquad
z_0=\mathrm{const},
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger=\mathrm{const},
\qquad
\partial_iP_0=0.
\]

Write fluctuations as
\[
\Psi=(\rho_0+\sigma)z_0+\xi,
\qquad
z_0^\dagger\xi=0,
\]
or equivalently
\[
P=P_0+\delta P+O((\delta P)^2),
\qquad
\delta P=z_0\pi^\dagger+\pi z_0^\dagger.
\]

Then
\[
\partial_iP=\partial_i\delta P+O(\pi\partial\pi,\pi^2),
\]
so to quadratic order
\[
F_{\mathrm{align}}^{(2)}
=
\frac{\chi}{4}\int d^3x\,\rho_0(x)^2\,\mathrm{Tr}(\partial_i\delta P\,\partial_i\delta P)
\approx
\frac{\chi\bar\rho^2}{2}\int d^3x\,\partial_i\pi^\dagger\partial_i\pi.
\]

Therefore the projector stiffness sector begins at order \(\pi^2\), with no term linear in \(\pi\), and hence no quadratic shell--projector mixing source
\[
L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(2)}\sim J[\sigma,\psi]\cdot \pi.
\]

Thus
\[
\boxed{
J=0,
}
\]
and the quadratic Hessian is block diagonal:
\[
\boxed{
\delta^2F_{\mathrm{ref}}=\delta^2F_\sigma+\delta^2F_\xi.
}
\]

Consequently,
\[
\delta L_{\mathrm{eff}}=-\frac12 JG_\pi J=0,
\qquad
\delta N_{ij}^a=0,
\qquad
\delta W_\parallel=\delta W_I=\delta W_J=0
\]
at quadratic order in the current refined model.

Since the actual scalar Hessian channel already gave
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}=4uA^2\,\mathbf 1_2\neq 0,
\]
the projector/\(Q\)-sector does not cancel or grade away this scalar Bragg mass.

Hence:
\[
\boxed{
\text{in the current refined }U(3)\text{-invariant triplet + projector-stiffness model,}
\quad
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\text{ survives unchanged at quadratic order.}
}
\]

The projector sector improves remote-gap stability but does not solve the scalar Bragg-mass obstruction.
A genuine induced correction requires an additional UV coupling producing
\[
L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(2)}\sim J[\sigma,\psi]\cdot \xi
\]
with \(J\neq 0\).

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Class II mediator in projector language: explicit quadratic source with \(J\neq 0\)}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now revisit the quadratic shell--projector mixing problem in projector language and show that, although the current refined projector-stiffness model gives \(J=0\), the minimal Class II auxiliary mediator generates a genuine nonzero quadratic source
\[
L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(2)}\sim J[\psi]\cdot \xi
\]
and hence a nonzero induced shell-enriched tensor correction \(\delta N_{ij}^a\).

\subsubsection{A. What failed before}

For the refined microscopic model
\[
F_{\mathrm{ref}}=F_{\mathrm{triplet}}+F_{\mathrm{align}},
\qquad
F_{\mathrm{align}}=\frac{\chi}{4}\int d^3x\,\rho^2\,\mathrm{Tr}(\partial_iP\,\partial_iP),
\]
expanded around a locked constant-projector background
\[
\Psi_0=\phi_0 z_0,
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger=\mathrm{const},
\qquad
\partial_iP_0=0,
\]
the quadratic projector piece begins at order \((\delta P)^2\sim \xi^2\), so the shell--projector bilinear source vanishes:
\[
J=0.
\]
Hence the current refined model alone cannot induce a nonzero \(\delta N_{ij}^a\) at quadratic order.

\subsubsection{B. Minimal Class II UV extension}

Introduce a heavy auxiliary internal vector mediator
\begin{equation}
X_i^a,
\qquad
i=1,2,3,
\qquad
a=1,2,3.
\label{eq:ClassII_X_again}
\end{equation}
The minimal mediated quadratic extension is
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(II)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha X_i^a\bigl(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger T^a\Psi+\mathrm{h.c.}\bigr)
+
\beta X_i^a\,\partial_i\delta P^a\,\psi.
\label{eq:ClassII_UV_projector_form}
\end{equation}

This is exactly the lowest-order local UV term carrying both:

\begin{enumerate}
\item one spatial derivative index \(i\),
\item one internal shell-reduced index \(a\).
\end{enumerate}

So it is precisely of the type required by the shell-enriched target structure.

\subsubsection{C. Expansion around the locked background}

Expand around
\begin{equation}
\Psi_0=\phi_0 z_0,
\qquad
\delta P^a\sim \xi^a.
\label{eq:locked_bg_ClassII}
\end{equation}
The shell current contains
\begin{equation}
\partial_i\Psi^\dagger T^a\Psi
=
(\partial_i\phi_0)\,z_0^\dagger T^a z_0\,\phi_0
+
(\partial_i\phi_0)\,C^a[\psi]
+\cdots ,
\label{eq:shell_current_expand}
\end{equation}
where the first term is a pure background contribution and the second term is the shell/test-mode contribution linear in the test fluctuation \(\psi\).

Also,
\begin{equation}
\partial_i\delta P^a\sim \partial_i\xi^a.
\label{eq:dP_xi_relation}
\end{equation}

Therefore the part of \(L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(II)}\) relevant for quadratic shell--projector mixing is
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(2)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha X_i^a(\partial_i\phi_0)\,C^a[\psi]
+
\beta X_i^a\partial_i\xi^a.
\label{eq:ClassII_UV_quad_reduced}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{D. Eliminating the heavy mediator}

Since \(X_i^a\) is auxiliary, its Euler--Lagrange equation is algebraic:
\begin{equation}
\frac{\partial L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(2)}}{\partial X_i^a}
=
M_X^2X_i^a
+
\alpha(\partial_i\phi_0)\,C^a[\psi]
+
\beta\partial_i\xi^a
=
0.
\label{eq:X_eom_projector}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
X_i^a
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\Bigl[
\alpha(\partial_i\phi_0)\,C^a[\psi]
+
\beta\partial_i\xi^a
\Bigr].
\label{eq:X_solution_projector}
\end{equation}

Substituting back into \eqref{eq:ClassII_UV_quad_reduced} yields
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(2)}
=
-\frac{1}{2M_X^2}
\Bigl[
\alpha(\partial_i\phi_0)\,C^a[\psi]
+
\beta\partial_i\xi^a
\Bigr]^2.
\label{eq:Leff_after_X}
\end{equation}
The cross term is
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(2)}
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}
(\partial_i\phi_0)\,C^a[\psi]\,
\partial_i\xi^a.
\label{eq:Lmix_explicit}
\end{equation}

Thus the quadratic source is
\begin{equation}
J_i^a[\psi]
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}
(\partial_i\phi_0)\,C^a[\psi].
\label{eq:J_explicit}
\end{equation}
In particular,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J\neq 0
}
\label{eq:J_nonzero_box}
\end{equation}
whenever \(C^a[\psi]\) is nontrivial.

\subsubsection{E. Target shell-enriched structure}

The source \eqref{eq:Lmix_explicit} is already of the schematic target form
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(2)}
\sim
(\partial_i\phi_0)\,(\partial_j\psi)\,\xi^a,
\label{eq:target_schematic_again}
\end{equation}
after unpacking the derivative structure in \(C^a[\psi]\) and integrating by parts when needed.
Therefore integrating out \(\xi^a\) can now generate a genuine shell-enriched tensor correction
\begin{equation}
\delta N_{ij}^a\neq 0.
\label{eq:deltaN_nonzero_box}
\end{equation}

If the tangent projector mode has inverse propagator
\begin{equation}
G_\xi^{-1}(k)\sim \chi_{\mathrm{eff}}k^2+m_\xi^2,
\label{eq:Gxi_inv}
\end{equation}
then eliminating \(\xi\) yields schematically
\begin{equation}
\delta N_{ij}^a
\sim
\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}
\frac{1}{\chi_{\mathrm{eff}}q_*^2+m_\xi^2}
\times
(\text{projected tensor coefficient}).
\label{eq:deltaN_scale_projector}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{F. Equivalent shell-reduced Class II form}

The same mechanism can be written more directly at shell-reduced quadratic order.
Take
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(2)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\lambda X_i^a m^a \partial_i\phi_0
+
g_X X_i^a C_{ij}^{ab}(-i\partial_j)s^b\psi.
\label{eq:ClassII_shell_reduced}
\end{equation}
Then the algebraic equation is
\begin{equation}
M_X^2X_i^a+\lambda m^a\partial_i\phi_0+g_X C_{ij}^{ab}(-i\partial_j)s^b\psi=0,
\label{eq:ClassII_shell_eom}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
X_i^a
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\Bigl[
\lambda m^a\partial_i\phi_0
+
g_X C_{ij}^{ab}(-i\partial_j)s^b\psi
\Bigr].
\label{eq:ClassII_shell_solution}
\end{equation}
Substituting back gives the cross term
\begin{equation}
\delta L_{\mathrm{cross}}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}
m^a C_{ij}^{ab}
(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)s^b\psi.
\label{eq:deltaLcross_shell}
\end{equation}
Comparing with the target enriched operator
\begin{equation}
\delta L_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
\delta N_{ij}^b(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)s^b\psi,
\label{eq:deltaLenr_target}
\end{equation}
we read off
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta N_{ij}^b
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^a C_{ij}^{ab}.
}
\label{eq:deltaN_main_formula_again}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{G. Consequence for the current program}

The current refined projector-stiffness model failed because
\[
J=0.
\]
The Class II mediator succeeds because
\[
J\neq 0
\]
already at quadratic order around the same locked constant-projector background.
Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Class II is the first mathematically consistent route from projector-sector physics to } \delta N_{ij}^a\neq 0.
}
\]

This is precisely the missing ingredient that the bare projector stiffness sector could not provide.

\paragraph{Exact logical status.}
What is now closed is:
\[
\text{locked constant-projector background}
+
\text{Class II mediator}
\Longrightarrow
L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(2)}\sim (\partial_i\phi_0)C^a[\psi]\partial_i\xi^a
\Longrightarrow
J\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\delta N_{ij}^a\neq 0.
\]
What remains open is the full microscopic uniqueness question, not the existence of a nonzero quadratic source.

%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(II)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+\alpha X_i^a(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger T^a\Psi+\mathrm{h.c.})
+\beta X_i^a\,\partial_i\delta P^a\,\psi.
\]

Around the locked background
\[
\Psi_0=\phi_0 z_0,
\qquad
\delta P^a\sim \xi^a,
\]
the shell current contains
\[
\partial_i\Psi^\dagger T^a\Psi
=
(\partial_i\phi_0)\,z_0^\dagger T^a z_0\,\phi_0
+
(\partial_i\phi_0)\,C^a[\psi]
+\cdots,
\]
and
\[
\partial_i\delta P^a\sim \partial_i\xi^a.
\]

Thus the quadratic shell--projector mixing sector is
\[
L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(2)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha X_i^a(\partial_i\phi_0)\,C^a[\psi]
+
\beta X_i^a\partial_i\xi^a.
\]

Eliminating the auxiliary field \(X_i^a\) gives
\[
X_i^a
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\Bigl[
\alpha(\partial_i\phi_0)\,C^a[\psi]
+
\beta\partial_i\xi^a
\Bigr],
\]
hence
\[
L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(2)}
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}
(\partial_i\phi_0)\,C^a[\psi]\,
\partial_i\xi^a.
\]

Therefore the quadratic source is
\[
J_i^a[\psi]
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}
(\partial_i\phi_0)\,C^a[\psi],
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
J\neq 0.
}
\]

Equivalently, in shell-reduced form,
\[
L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(2)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\lambda X_i^a m^a \partial_i\phi_0
+
g_X X_i^a C_{ij}^{ab}(-i\partial_j)s^b\psi,
\]
and integrating out \(X_i^a\) gives
\[
\delta L_{\mathrm{cross}}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}
m^a C_{ij}^{ab}
(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)s^b\psi.
\]

Hence the induced shell-enriched tensor is
\[
\boxed{
\delta N_{ij}^b
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^a C_{ij}^{ab}.
}
\]

So, unlike the bare projector-stiffness model where \(J=0\), the Class II mediator yields a genuine quadratic shell--projector source and therefore a nonzero induced tensor correction
\[
\delta N_{ij}^a\neq 0.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Constant pair-mixing selection theorem for the Class II correction}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We determine whether the nonzero Class II-induced shell tensor
\[
\delta N_{ij}^a
\]
can directly modify or cancel the scalar Bragg mass obstruction
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\,\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\]
found in the actual scalar Hessian channel.

\subsubsection{A. Scalar Bragg mass channel}

For the enriched shell-pair basis
\[
\Psi_{\pm,a}(x)=e^{\pm ik_*\cdot x}u_a(x),
\qquad
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\]
the constant pair-mixing block is
\begin{equation}
(B_0)_{ab}
=
\langle \Psi_{+,a},H(k_*)\Psi_{-,b}\rangle.
\label{eq:B0_def_selection}
\end{equation}
For a scalar periodic potential \(U_{\mathrm{per}}(x)\), the projected Bragg-mass formula is
\begin{equation}
(B_0)_{ab}
=
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\,u_a^\dagger(x)e^{-iG_*\cdot x}U_{\mathrm{per}}(x)u_b(x)
\label{eq:B0_scalar_formula_selection}
\end{equation}
up to possible gradient-sector contributions. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

Under the constant-envelope ansatz,
\begin{equation}
B_0=\widehat U(G_*)\,\mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:B0_identity_selection}
\end{equation}
Thus the actual scalar obstruction found earlier is of the operator form
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{Bragg}}^{\mathrm{scalar}}
=
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\,\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:scalar_bragg_channel}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Class II shell-reduced operator}

The shell-reduced Class II quadratic extension is
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(2)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\lambda X_i^a m^a\partial_i\phi_0
+
g_X X_i^a C_{ij}^{ab}(-i\partial_j)s^b\psi.
\label{eq:ClassII_shell_reduced_selection}
\end{equation}
Eliminating the auxiliary field \(X_i^a\) gives the cross term
\begin{equation}
\delta L_{\mathrm{cross}}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}
m^a C_{ij}^{ab}
(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)s^b\psi,
\label{eq:deltaLcross_selection}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\delta N_{ij}^b
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^a C_{ij}^{ab}.
\label{eq:deltaN_selection}
\end{equation}
This is a gradient-linear enriched correction, exactly of the shell-witness type. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

Therefore the induced shell operator has the form
\begin{equation}
\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}
=
\delta N_{ij}^b(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^b.
\label{eq:deltaH_ClassII_selection}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. Constant pair-mixing from a gradient-enriched operator}

To test whether \eqref{eq:deltaH_ClassII_selection} can affect the scalar Bragg mass, compute its pair-block matrix element at \(p=0\):
\begin{equation}
(\delta B_0^{\mathrm{Class\,II}})_{ab}
=
\langle \Psi_{+,a},\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}(k_*)\Psi_{-,b}\rangle.
\label{eq:deltaB0_def_selection}
\end{equation}

Using the shell-pair basis and applying \((-i\partial_j)\) to \(\Psi_{-,b}=e^{-ik_*\cdot x}u_b(x)\),
\begin{equation}
(-i\partial_j)\Psi_{-,b}
=
(-k_{*,j}-i\partial_j)\,e^{-ik_*\cdot x}u_b(x).
\label{eq:derivative_on_minus_state}
\end{equation}
Thus, at principal order,
\begin{equation}
(\delta B_0^{\mathrm{Class\,II}})_{ab}
=
-\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\,
u_a^\dagger(x)e^{-iG_*\cdot x}
\Bigl[
\delta N_{ij}^b(\partial_i\phi_0)k_{*,j}
\Bigr]
u_b(x)\,(s^b)_{ab}
+\cdots
\label{eq:deltaB0_raw_selection}
\end{equation}
where the omitted terms come from derivatives of the periodic envelopes \(u_b(x)\).

Under the constant-envelope ansatz, those derivative-of-envelope terms vanish at principal order, so
\begin{equation}
\delta B_0^{\mathrm{Class\,II}}
=
-\widehat{\mathcal T}^b(G_*)\,s^b,
\label{eq:deltaB0_Pauli_selection}
\end{equation}
for some shell Fourier coefficients \(\widehat{\mathcal T}^b(G_*)\) determined by \(\delta N_{ij}^b(\partial_i\phi_0)k_{*,j}\).

Therefore any constant pair-mixing produced by Class II lies in the traceless internal sector:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta B_0^{\mathrm{Class\,II}}\in \mathrm{span}\{s_1,s_2,s_3\}.
}
\label{eq:deltaB0_traceless}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{D. Identity-sector selection rule}

The scalar Bragg obstruction lies in the identity channel:
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\,\mathbf 1_2.
\]
The Class II correction lies in the traceless channel:
\[
\delta B_0^{\mathrm{Class\,II}}\in \mathfrak{su}(2).
\]
These two sectors are orthogonal under the Hilbert--Schmidt pairing:
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Tr}(\mathbf 1_2\,s_a)=0.
\label{eq:HS_orthogonality}
\end{equation}

Hence:

\begin{theorem}[Identity-sector selection theorem]
The Class II induced tensor \(\delta N_{ij}^a\) cannot directly cancel the scalar Bragg mass obstruction
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\,\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]
Any constant pair-mixing generated by the Class II derivative operator belongs to the traceless internal sector
\[
\tau_1\otimes s_a
\quad\text{or}\quad
\tau_2\otimes s_a,
\]
not to the identity sector
\[
\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Equation \eqref{eq:deltaH_ClassII_selection} shows that the Class II correction always carries an explicit internal generator \(s^b\).
Therefore its projected pair block, constant or linear, remains in the traceless internal matrix algebra generated by the Pauli matrices.
By contrast, the scalar Bragg mass is proportional to the internal identity.
Orthogonality \eqref{eq:HS_orthogonality} forbids direct cancellation between the two channels.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{E. Natural shell-Dirac parity and vanishing of the constant gradient block}

The shell-level Dirac literature in the uploaded manuscript already states a sharper condition:
the gradient-sector contribution to \(B_0\) vanishes if the first-order mixing is odd and momentum-linear. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}
Also, the transverse mixing matrices are principal-order derivatives,
\begin{equation}
W^\alpha
=
\widehat G_\alpha(G_*)\,s^\alpha,
\label{eq:Walpha_again_selection}
\end{equation}
and the shell-Dirac criterion is formulated precisely in terms of vanishing \(B_0\) together with nonzero \(W^1,W^2\). 

Thus, under the natural shell-exchange/reflection parity used for shell Dirac,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta B_0^{\mathrm{Class\,II}}=0
}
\label{eq:deltaB0_zero_natural}
\end{equation}
at principal order.

So the stronger conclusion is:

\begin{itemize}
\item generically, Class II cannot cancel the scalar identity mass because it lives in the wrong internal channel;
\item under the natural shell-Dirac odd-parity choice, Class II does not even generate a constant pair-mixing block at all.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection{F. Consequence for the role of Class II}

The uploaded manuscript states explicitly that the canonical minimal Class II correction changes the first-order shell tensor coefficients \(A,B,C\), and does not by construction insert an independent constant shell-level Dirac mass term. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

Therefore the actual role of Class II is
\begin{equation}
(A,B,C)\longmapsto (A_{\mathrm{eff}},B_{\mathrm{eff}},C_{\mathrm{eff}}),
\label{eq:ABC_renorm_selection}
\end{equation}
not
\begin{equation}
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\longmapsto 0.
\label{eq:B0_not_touched_selection}
\end{equation}

\begin{corollary}[Constant pair-mixing selection theorem for Class II]
The canonical Class II mediator renormalizes the derivative shell witness sector \((A,B,C)\), but does not remove the scalar Bragg-mass obstruction \(B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2\).
Under the natural odd shell-parity realization, the Class II constant pair-mixing contribution vanishes altogether.
\end{corollary}

\subsubsection{G. Honest conclusion}

The current chain is now sharp:

\[
\text{actual scalar Hessian}
\Longrightarrow
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\,\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2\neq 0,
\]
while
\[
\text{Class II}
\Longrightarrow
\delta N_{ij}^a\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\text{renormalization of }(A,B,C),
\]
but
\[
\text{Class II}\not\Longrightarrow
\text{cancellation of }B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]

So the scalar Bragg-mass obstruction and the Class II derivative witness mechanism live in different operator channels.

%%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}=\widehat U_{\mathrm{per}}^{\mathrm{tot}}(G_*)\,\mathbf 1_2
\]
is the scalar Bragg-mass channel, hence in the enriched shell-pair block it appears as
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\,\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]

By contrast, the shell-reduced Class II correction is
\[
