\delta L_{\mathrm{cross}}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}
m^a C_{ij}^{ab}
(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)s^b\psi,
\qquad
\delta N_{ij}^b
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}m^a C_{ij}^{ab}.
\]

Therefore every Class II contribution carries an explicit internal Pauli generator \(s^b\).
Its projected constant pair-mixing block, if nonzero, must lie in
\[
\delta B_0^{\mathrm{Class\,II}}
\in \mathrm{span}\{s_1,s_2,s_3\},
\]
so in the shell-pair block it is of the form
\[
\tau_1\otimes s_a
\quad\text{or}\quad
\tau_2\otimes s_a,
\]
not
\[
\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]

Since
\[
\mathrm{Tr}(\mathbf 1_2\,s_a)=0,
\]
the scalar identity channel and the traceless Pauli channel are orthogonal.
Hence Class II cannot directly cancel
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\,\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]

Moreover, under the natural shell-Dirac odd/reflection parity, the gradient-sector constant pair-mixing vanishes at principal order:
\[
\delta B_0^{\mathrm{Class\,II}}=0.
\]

Therefore the actual role of Class II is
\[
(A,B,C)\mapsto (A_{\mathrm{eff}},B_{\mathrm{eff}},C_{\mathrm{eff}}),
\]
not
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\mapsto 0.
\]

So:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Class II renormalizes the derivative Weyl-witness sector, but does not remove the scalar Bragg-mass obstruction.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Identity-channel cancellation theorem}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We classify the only possible routes for removing the scalar Bragg-mass obstruction
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\,\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\]
in the enriched shell-pair Hamiltonian.

\subsubsection{A. Constant pair-mixing decomposition}

Let the constant pair-mixing block on the internal doublet be the most general Hermitian matrix
\begin{equation}
M_0
=
m_0\,\mathbf 1_2
+
m_1 s_1
+
m_2 s_2
+
m_3 s_3.
\label{eq:M0_general_identity}
\end{equation}
Then the enriched shell-pair Hamiltonian has the principal constant part
\begin{equation}
H_0^{\mathrm{pair}}
=
\tau_1\otimes M_0.
\label{eq:H0_pair_identity}
\end{equation}

The scalar Bragg-mass obstruction computed from the actual scalar Hessian is precisely the identity-channel case
\begin{equation}
M_0^{\mathrm{scalar}}=B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\,\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\neq 0.
\label{eq:M0_scalar_identity}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Identity/traceless decomposition is orthogonal}

The Hermitian \(2\times2\) algebra decomposes as
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Herm}(2)=\mathbb R\,\mathbf 1_2\oplus \mathfrak{su}(2)_{\mathrm{Herm}},
\label{eq:Herm2_split}
\end{equation}
with orthogonality under the Hilbert--Schmidt pairing
\begin{equation}
\langle A,B\rangle_{\mathrm{HS}}:=\mathrm{Tr}(AB).
\label{eq:HS_pairing}
\end{equation}
Because
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Tr}(\mathbf 1_2\, s_a)=0,
\qquad a=1,2,3,
\label{eq:Tr_identity_Pauli_zero}
\end{equation}
the identity channel and the traceless channel are orthogonal.

Hence, if a UV correction produces only a traceless internal constant block
\begin{equation}
\delta M_0\in \mathfrak{su}(2)_{\mathrm{Herm}},
\label{eq:deltaM0_traceless}
\end{equation}
then its identity coefficient vanishes:
\begin{equation}
\frac12\mathrm{Tr}(\delta M_0)=0.
\label{eq:deltaM0_identity_zero}
\end{equation}
Therefore the corrected identity coefficient is unchanged:
\begin{equation}
m_0^{\mathrm{eff}}=m_0.
\label{eq:m0_unchanged}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Orthogonality obstruction]
Let
\[
M_0=m_0\mathbf 1_2+\widetilde M_0,
\qquad
\widetilde M_0\in \mathfrak{su}(2)_{\mathrm{Herm}}.
\]
If a UV correction satisfies \(\delta M_0\in \mathfrak{su}(2)_{\mathrm{Herm}}\), then it cannot cancel \(m_0\mathbf 1_2\).
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
m_0^{\mathrm{eff}}=m_0.
\label{eq:m0_eff_same}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Take the identity projection by the normalized trace:
\[
m_0=\frac12\mathrm{Tr}(M_0).
\]
If \(\delta M_0\) is traceless, then
\[
\frac12\mathrm{Tr}(\delta M_0)=0.
\]
Hence
\[
m_0^{\mathrm{eff}}
=
\frac12\mathrm{Tr}(M_0+\delta M_0)
=
\frac12\mathrm{Tr}(M_0)
=
m_0.
\]
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{C. Application to Class II}

The shell-reduced Class II correction has the form
\begin{equation}
\delta L_{\mathrm{cross}}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}
m^a C_{ij}^{ab}
(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)s^b\psi,
\label{eq:ClassII_cross_identity}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\delta N_{ij}^b
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}m^a C_{ij}^{ab}.
\label{eq:ClassII_deltaN_identity}
\end{equation}
Every Class II contribution carries an explicit shell-reduced internal generator \(s^b\). Therefore any constant pair block produced by Class II, if present, lies in the traceless internal sector:
\begin{equation}
\delta M_0^{\mathrm{Class\,II}}\in \mathfrak{su}(2)_{\mathrm{Herm}}.
\label{eq:ClassII_traceless}
\end{equation}
Moreover, the manuscript explicitly states that Class II is acceptable only if it does not create a dominant constant intervalley mass term, and that it merely renormalizes the derivative shell tensor coefficients. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6} 

Therefore:

\begin{corollary}[Class II cannot cancel the scalar Bragg mass]
The Class II mediator cannot directly cancel the scalar Bragg-mass obstruction
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\,\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]
Its effect is restricted to the traceless internal channels and to the derivative witness sector \((A,B,C)\).
\end{corollary}

\subsubsection{D. What kind of UV structure \emph{can} cancel the identity channel?}

To cancel the scalar Bragg mass, one needs a UV correction whose projected constant pair block has a nonzero identity component:
\begin{equation}
\delta M_0^{\mathrm{id}}
=
\delta m_0\,\mathbf 1_2+\delta\widetilde M_0,
\qquad
\delta m_0\neq 0.
\label{eq:identity_carrying_deltaM}
\end{equation}
Then cancellation requires
\begin{equation}
\delta m_0=-B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}.
\label{eq:identity_cancellation_condition}
\end{equation}

This gives the first route:

\begin{theorem}[Identity-carrying mediator route]
A direct cancellation of the scalar Bragg mass is possible only if the UV completion produces an identity-channel constant pair block
\[
\delta m_0\,\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\]
with
\[
\delta m_0=-B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}.
\]
Any UV completion whose projected constant pair block is purely traceless cannot achieve this.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from the decomposition
\[
\mathrm{Herm}(2)=\mathbb R\,\mathbf 1_2\oplus \mathfrak{su}(2)_{\mathrm{Herm}}
\]
and the trace projection onto the identity channel.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
This means the extra UV sector must carry not only the reduced-shell triplet label \(a\), but also an identity-channel projection capable of surviving the shell-pair reduction as \(\mathbf 1_2\).

\subsubsection{E. The second route: graded bypass rather than cancellation}

The manuscripts already identify the genuinely different route:
the plain scalar Bragg pair is not sufficient, and one needs either

\begin{enumerate}
\item an internal complex doublet,
\item a graded \(2+2\) low-energy defect sector,
\item or a genuinely first-order projected operator whose off-diagonal \(2\times2\) symbol is already full-rank.
\end{enumerate}
:contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

Also, the exact-grading and selection-rule criteria state that if the leading reduced operator is odd under an involution \(J\), then the same-parity blocks vanish, and if the projected transport operator is first-order, the reduced principal operator is block-off-diagonal first-order. 

This yields the second route:

\begin{theorem}[Graded bypass route]
Suppose the physical low-energy carrier is not the plain scalar Bragg pair but a \(J\)-graded \(2+2\) low-energy sector, and the leading reduced operator \(D_1(p)\) is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(J\)-odd,
\item first-order in momentum.
\end{enumerate}

Then the relevant reduced principal operator contains no constant term at all:
\begin{equation}
D_1(0)=0.
\label{eq:D1_zero}
\end{equation}
In this case the scalar Bragg-mass channel is not cancelled; rather, it is absent from the physically relevant reduced block.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
If \(D_1\) is first-order in momentum, then
\[
D_1(p)=p_i M_i + O(|p|^2),
\]
hence \(D_1(0)=0\).
If in addition \(D_1\) is \(J\)-odd, then in the \(J\)-graded decomposition it is block-off-diagonal.
Thus the reduced low-energy operator is a first-order chiral block with no constant scalar Bragg mass term.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
This is not a cancellation mechanism inside the plain scalar shell-pair block.
It is a \emph{different low-energy reduction} in which the dangerous scalar pair channel is no longer the relevant infrared block.

\subsubsection{F. Final classification}

We can now state the full classification.

\begin{theorem}[Identity-channel cancellation theorem]
Let the enriched shell-pair constant block be
\[
H_0^{\mathrm{pair}}=\tau_1\otimes M_0,
\qquad
M_0=B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\mathbf 1_2+\widetilde M_0.
\]
Then there are exactly two logically distinct ways to avoid the scalar Bragg-mass obstruction:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Direct identity-channel cancellation:} introduce a UV completion whose projected constant pair block has a nonzero identity component \(\delta m_0\mathbf 1_2\) with
\[
\delta m_0=-B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}.
\]

\item \textbf{Graded bypass:} replace the plain scalar Bragg-pair low-energy reduction by a \(J\)-graded first-order \(2+2\) reduction in which the relevant principal operator is block-off-diagonal and first-order, so the constant scalar Bragg block never appears in the effective infrared operator.
\end{enumerate}

Any UV completion whose projected constant pair block is purely traceless, including the canonical Class II mediator, cannot realize route (1).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Route (1) follows from the identity/traceless decomposition and the trace projection argument.
Route (2) follows from the exact-grading / selection-rule theorems together with first-order reduction.
No other possibility exists at the reduced operator level: one must either cancel the identity component directly, or work in a different reduced low-energy block where the constant scalar channel is absent.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{G. Honest conclusion}

The current state is therefore:

\[
\text{actual scalar Hessian}
\Longrightarrow
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2\neq 0,
\]
\[
\text{Class II}
\Longrightarrow
\delta N_{ij}^a\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
(A,B,C)\text{ renormalization only},
\]
but
\[
\text{Class II}\not\Longrightarrow
\delta m_0\,\mathbf 1_2.
\]

So the next genuinely new microscopic step is not more Class II algebra.
It is to choose between:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{identity-carrying mediator}
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
\text{graded }2+2\text{ low-energy bypass}.
}
\label{eq:next_choice_identity}
\end{equation}

%%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
M_0=m_0\mathbf 1_2+m_1s_1+m_2s_2+m_3s_3
\]
is the most general constant internal pair-mixing block.
The scalar Bragg-mass obstruction is
\[
M_0^{\mathrm{scalar}}=B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\mathbf 1_2.
\]

Since
\[
\mathrm{Herm}(2)=\mathbb R\,\mathbf 1_2\oplus \mathfrak{su}(2)_{\mathrm{Herm}},
\qquad
\mathrm{Tr}(\mathbf 1_2 s_a)=0,
\]
any traceless UV correction
\[
\delta M_0\in \mathfrak{su}(2)_{\mathrm{Herm}}
\]
cannot change the identity coefficient:
\[
m_0^{\mathrm{eff}}=m_0.
\]

The canonical Class II mediator always carries an explicit reduced-shell Pauli generator \(s^a\), so its projected correction is traceless in the internal sector.
Therefore Class II cannot directly cancel
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]

Hence direct cancellation requires a UV completion with an identity-channel projected block
\[
\delta m_0\,\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
\delta m_0=-B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}.
\]

The only alternative is not cancellation but bypass:
if the true low-energy carrier is a \(J\)-graded \(2+2\) sector and the leading reduced operator is \(J\)-odd and first-order, then
\[
D_1(0)=0
\]
and the scalar Bragg-mass channel is absent from the relevant infrared block.

Therefore there are exactly two ways around the scalar Bragg-mass obstruction:
\[
\boxed{
\text{(1) identity-channel cancellation}
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
\text{(2) graded }2+2\text{ bypass.}
}
\]

Any purely traceless UV correction, including the canonical Class II mediator, realizes neither direct identity-channel cancellation nor removal of \(B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\).
It only renormalizes the derivative witness sector \((A,B,C)\).

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Minimal graded \(2+2\) low-energy carrier and the Dirac principal operator}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now construct the minimal graded \(2+2\) low-energy ansatz that bypasses the scalar Bragg-mass channel.
The aim is to derive, at the reduced infrared level,
\[
D_{\mathrm{eff}}(p)=D_1(p)+O(|p|^2),
\qquad
D_1(0)=0,
\]
with
\[
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu.
\]

\subsubsection{A. Graded infrared sector}

Let \(L(p)\) denote the linearized microscopic or effective operator near the infrared point \(p=0\).
Assume there exists an isolated four-dimensional infrared sector
\begin{equation}
K\subset H,
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}K=4.
\label{eq:K_dim4}
\end{equation}
Assume further that \(K\) carries an involutive grading operator
\begin{equation}
J:K\to K,
\qquad
J^\dagger=J,
\qquad
J^2=1.
\label{eq:J_involution}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
K=K_+\oplus K_-,
\qquad
K_\pm=\ker(J\mp 1),
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}K_\pm=2.
\label{eq:Kpm_split}
\end{equation}

Let \(\Pi_K\) be the spectral projector onto \(K\), and define the reduced operator
\begin{equation}
D_{\mathrm{eff}}(p):=\Pi_K L(p)\Pi_K.
\label{eq:Deff_def}
\end{equation}
Expanding near \(p=0\),
\begin{equation}
D_{\mathrm{eff}}(p)=D_1(p)+O(|p|^2).
\label{eq:Deff_expand}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Exact grading criterion}

Assume the leading reduced operator is odd under the grading:
\begin{equation}
J D_1(p) J^{-1}=-D_1(p).
\label{eq:Jodd_condition}
\end{equation}
Let \(\Pi_\pm\) denote the projectors onto \(K_\pm\).
In the graded basis \(K=K_+\oplus K_-\), write
\begin{equation}
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
D_{++}(p) & D_{+-}(p)\\
D_{-+}(p) & D_{--}(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:D1_block}
\end{equation}
Then \eqref{eq:Jodd_condition} implies
\begin{equation}
D_{++}(p)=0,
\qquad
D_{--}(p)=0,
\label{eq:diag_zero_from_J}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:D1_offdiag}
\end{equation}
for some \(2\times2\) mixed symbol \(A_1(p)\).

In particular, because \(D_1\) is first-order,
\begin{equation}
D_1(0)=0.
\label{eq:D1_zero}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. Minimal projector/defect ansatz}

Now realize this grading concretely in the defect/worldvolume setting.
Let \(\xi\) denote the transverse defect coordinate and \(y^\mu\) the slow worldvolume coordinates.
Assume there exist four low-energy modes
\begin{equation}
u_a^+(\xi),
\qquad a=1,2,
\qquad
u_b^-(\xi),
\qquad b=1,2,
\label{eq:upm_modes}
\end{equation}
such that
\begin{equation}
J u_a^\pm = \pm u_a^\pm.
\label{eq:Jupm}
\end{equation}
Use the envelope ansatz
\begin{equation}
\Phi(y,\xi)
=
\sum_{a=1}^2 \psi_a^+(y)\,u_a^+(\xi)
+
\sum_{b=1}^2 \psi_b^-(y)\,u_b^-(\xi)
+\cdots.
\label{eq:envelope_ansatz}
\end{equation}

Assume the leading transport operator has the first-order form
\begin{equation}
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\label{eq:L1_transport}
\end{equation}
and is odd under the grading,
\begin{equation}
J L_1 J^{-1}=-L_1.
\label{eq:L1_Jodd}
\end{equation}
A sufficient concrete realization is a reflection-odd transverse kernel
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi).
\label{eq:Vmu_odd}
\end{equation}

Then the projected matrix elements in the low-energy sector satisfy
\begin{equation}
\langle u_a^\pm, L_1 u_b^\pm\rangle_\xi =0,
\label{eq:same_parity_zero}
\end{equation}
while the mixed ones define
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
:=
\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle_\xi.
\label{eq:Mmixed_def}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu,
\label{eq:A1_linear}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & p_\mu M^\mu\\
p_\mu (M^\mu)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:D1_final_general}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{D. Nondegeneracy criterion}

The reduced principal operator is Dirac-type iff the mixed symbol is nondegenerate:
\begin{equation}
\det A_1(p)\neq 0
\qquad
\text{for generic }p\neq 0.
\label{eq:A1_nondeg}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\det\bigl(p_\mu M^\mu\bigr)\neq 0
\qquad
\text{for generic }p\neq 0.
\label{eq:det_pM}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{E. Explicit full-rank realization}

Choose the mixed symbol matrices to be a Pauli triplet
\begin{equation}
M^1=I_g\,\sigma_1,
\qquad
M^2=I_g\,\sigma_2,
\qquad
M^3=I_g\,\sigma_3,
\qquad
I_g\neq 0.
\label{eq:Pauli_triplet_realization}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu
=
I_g\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2+p_3\sigma_3).
\label{eq:A1_pauli}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\det A_1(p)= -I_g^2\,(p_1^2+p_2^2+p_3^2),
\label{eq:detA1_explicit}
\end{equation}
which is nonzero for generic \(p\neq 0\).

Thus the reduced principal operator becomes
\begin{equation}
D_1(p)=
I_g
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & p_i\sigma_i\\
p_i\sigma_i & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:D1_Dirac}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{F. Dirac form}

Define the \(4\times4\) matrices
\begin{equation}
\alpha_i=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & \sigma_i\\
\sigma_i & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:alpha_i_def}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\{\alpha_i,\alpha_j\}=2\delta_{ij}\mathbf 1_4.
\label{eq:Clifford_alpha}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
D_1(p)=I_g\,p_i\alpha_i,
\label{eq:D1_alpha}
\end{equation}
which is exactly the massless Dirac principal operator.

In position space, after inverse Fourier transform \(p_i\mapsto -i\partial_i\),
\begin{equation}
i\partial_t\Psi
=
-iI_g\,\alpha_i\partial_i\Psi
+O(\partial^2)\Psi.
\label{eq:Dirac_PDE_position}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{G. Why this bypasses the scalar Bragg-mass obstruction}

The scalar Bragg-mass obstruction arose in the plain shell-pair carrier as a constant identity-channel block
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\,\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]
But in the graded \(2+2\) reduction, the relevant principal infrared operator is \emph{defined} by the first-order projected sector \(D_1(p)\), and the grading condition forces
\[
D_1(0)=0.
\]
Thus the scalar constant pair-mixing block is not cancelled inside this reduced operator; rather, it is absent from the graded first-order infrared principal block.

So this route is a \emph{bypass}, not a cancellation.

\subsubsection{H. Honest logical status}

What is proved here is the exact reduced-operator theorem:

\[
\text{isolated graded }2+2\text{ sector}
+
\text{first-order }J\text{-odd transport}
\Longrightarrow
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & p_\mu M^\mu\\
p_\mu (M^\mu)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
D_1(0)=0.
\]

And if the mixed symbol is full rank, then
\[
D_1(p)\sim p_i\alpha_i
\]
is Dirac.

What remains open is the microscopic realization problem:
that the full TECT defect/projector dynamics actually produces this isolated graded \(2+2\) sector and the required nondegenerate mixed first-order symbol.

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
K\subset H,
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}K=4,
\qquad
K=K_+\oplus K_-,
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}K_\pm=2,
\]
with an involution
\[
J^\dagger=J,\qquad J^2=1.
\]

Let
\[
D_{\mathrm{eff}}(p)=\Pi_KL(p)\Pi_K=D_1(p)+O(|p|^2).
\]
If the leading reduced operator is \(J\)-odd,
\[
JD_1(p)J^{-1}=-D_1(p),
\]
then in the graded basis
\[
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
D_1(0)=0.
\]

For a defect/worldvolume ansatz
\[
\Phi(y,\xi)
=
\sum_{a=1}^2\psi_a^+(y)u_a^+(\xi)
+
\sum_{b=1}^2\psi_b^-(y)u_b^-(\xi)
+\cdots,
\qquad
Ju_a^\pm=\pm u_a^\pm,
\]
with leading transport
\[
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
J L_1 J^{-1}=-L_1,
\]
the same-parity projected matrix elements vanish:
\[
\langle u_a^\pm,L_1u_b^\pm\rangle_\xi=0.
\]
The mixed symbol is
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}=\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle_\xi,
\]
so
\[
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu,
\qquad
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & p_\mu M^\mu\\
p_\mu(M^\mu)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

If one chooses an explicit full-rank realization
\[
M^1=I_g\sigma_1,\qquad
M^2=I_g\sigma_2,\qquad
M^3=I_g\sigma_3,
\qquad
I_g\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
A_1(p)=I_g\,p_i\sigma_i,
\qquad
\det A_1(p)=-I_g^2|p|^2\neq 0
\quad (p\neq 0),
\]
and
\[
D_1(p)=I_g
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & p_i\sigma_i\\
p_i\sigma_i & 0
\end{pmatrix}
= I_g\,p_i\alpha_i,
\qquad
\{\alpha_i,\alpha_j\}=2\delta_{ij}\mathbf 1_4.
\]

Therefore the leading infrared operator is exactly massless Dirac:
\[
\boxed{
D_1(0)=0,\qquad D_1(p)\sim p_i\alpha_i.
}
\]

This avoids the scalar Bragg-mass obstruction not by cancellation, but by working in a different graded first-order infrared block.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Actual TECT defect-sector realization of the graded \(2+2\) bypass}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now embed the abstract graded \(2+2\) low-energy Dirac theorem into the actual CP\(^2\) projector-defect fluctuation problem of TECT.
The purpose is to identify the low modes \(u_a^\pm(\xi)\), the odd transport kernel \(V^\mu(\xi)\), and the projected mixed symbol
\[
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu
\]
directly in projector-defect variables.

\subsubsection{A. Tangent projector fluctuation as a rank-two \(Q_B\)-bundle field}

Let the static defect background be
\begin{equation}
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B(\xi)^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B(\xi)^\dagger z_B(\xi)=1,
\label{eq:PB_background_actual}
\end{equation}
with transverse coordinate \(\xi\) and worldvolume coordinates \(y^\mu\).

Because \(P^2=P\), linearized projector fluctuations satisfy
\begin{equation}
P_B\,\delta P+\delta P\,P_B=\delta P.
\label{eq:projector_constraint}
\end{equation}
Using a local normalized representative \(z_B\), a convenient tangent parametrization is
\begin{equation}
\delta P=\eta z_B^\dagger+z_B\eta^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B^\dagger\eta=0.
\label{eq:deltaP_eta}
\end{equation}
Hence the physical fluctuation field is a rank-two complex field
\begin{equation}
\eta(\xi,y)\in Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp.
\label{eq:eta_in_QB}
\end{equation}

Thus the defect fluctuation problem is not a scalar one: it is already a rank-two bundle problem on \(Q_B\).

\subsubsection{B. Quadratic Hessian as a transverse matrix Schrödinger operator}

The quadratic fluctuation action has the generic form
\begin{equation}
\delta^2S
=
\int d^{d+1}x\,
\eta^\dagger
\Bigl[
-\rho\,D_\mu^{(B)}D^{(B)\mu}+M_B(\xi)
\Bigr]
\eta,
\label{eq:quadratic_Hessian_QB}
\end{equation}
where \(D_\mu^{(B)}\) is the induced connection on \(Q_B\) and \(M_B(\xi)\) is a Hermitian \(2\times2\) endomorphism built from the defect background and its derivatives.

Because the background depends only on \(\xi\), the operator splits into transverse and worldvolume pieces. In a local orthonormal \(Q_B\)-frame
\begin{equation}
e(\xi)=\bigl(e_1(\xi),e_2(\xi)\bigr),
\label{eq:QB_frame}
\end{equation}
writing
\begin{equation}
\eta(\xi,y)=e_a(\xi)\chi^a(\xi,y),
\label{eq:eta_expand_frame}
\end{equation}
the static transverse Hessian becomes a \(2\times2\) matrix Schrödinger operator
\begin{equation}
H_B^{\mathrm{stat}}
=
-\partial_\xi^2
+
W_B(\xi)
\qquad
\text{(up to frame connection terms)}.
\label{eq:HB_stat_matrix}
\end{equation}

This is the actual TECT projector-Hessian realization of the abstract low-mode operator class.

\subsubsection{C. Reflection symmetry and parity channels}

Assume the defect background is reflection-symmetric:
\begin{equation}
P_B(-\xi)=P_B(\xi).
\label{eq:PB_even}
\end{equation}
Then the static Hessian commutes with reflection
\begin{equation}
(J\chi)(\xi)=\chi(-\xi).
\label{eq:reflection_operator}
\end{equation}
Therefore its low transverse spectrum decomposes into even and odd parity sectors.

Assume that in each internal channel there exists one localized even low mode and one localized odd low mode:
\begin{equation}
f_+(\xi),\qquad f_-(\xi),
\label{eq:fpm_modes}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
f_+(-\xi)=+f_+(\xi),
\qquad
f_-(-\xi)=-f_-(\xi).
\label{eq:fpm_parity}
\end{equation}

Define the four low modes
\begin{equation}
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
a=1,2.
\label{eq:uapm_def}
\end{equation}
They span the low-energy sector
\begin{equation}
K=K_+\oplus K_-,
\qquad
K_\pm=\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb C}\{u_1^\pm,u_2^\pm\},
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}K_\pm=2.
\label{eq:Kpm_actual}
\end{equation}

Thus the actual projector Hessian naturally produces the required graded \(2+2\) carrier.

\subsubsection{D. Odd first-order worldvolume transport kernel}

Restoring slow worldvolume dependence \(y^\mu\), the full linearized operator acquires a first-order transport term
\begin{equation}
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}.
\label{eq:L1_transport_actual}
\end{equation}
The local tensors from which \(V^\mu(\xi)\) is built are linear in the transverse defect gradient, e.g.
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi P_B(\xi),\qquad \partial_\xi z_B(\xi),\qquad \theta'(\xi),
\label{eq:odd_background_tensors}
\end{equation}
or equivalent frame-covariant combinations.

Since \(P_B(\xi)\) is even, all such first derivatives are odd:
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi P_B(-\xi)=-\partial_\xi P_B(\xi),
\qquad
\theta'(-\xi)=-\theta'(\xi).
\label{eq:odd_derivatives}
\end{equation}
Hence the transport kernel is reflection-odd:
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi).
\label{eq:Vmu_odd_actual}
\end{equation}

This is exactly the structural \(J\)-oddness required by the graded reduction theorem.

\subsubsection{E. Projected overlap and the mixed symbol}

Project \(L_1\) onto the low-energy sector \(K\).
The same-parity matrix elements vanish:
\begin{equation}
\langle u_a^\pm,L_1u_b^\pm\rangle_\xi=0.
\label{eq:same_parity_zero_actual}
\end{equation}
Indeed, \(f_\pm^2\) is even while \(V^\mu\) is odd, so the integrand is odd.

The mixed block is
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
:=
\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle_\xi
=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\label{eq:Mmixed_actual}
\end{equation}
Because \(f_+f_-\) is odd and \(V^\mu\) is odd, the integrand is even, so this overlap is generically nonzero.

Therefore the leading reduced operator on \(K=K_+\oplus K_-\) is
\begin{equation}
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu.
\label{eq:D1_actual_projector}
\end{equation}
In particular,
\begin{equation}
D_1(0)=0.
\label{eq:D1_zero_actual}
\end{equation}

Thus the dangerous constant scalar Bragg block is absent from the relevant first-order graded defect operator.

\subsubsection{F. Minimal explicit full-rank realization inside the actual operator class}

The previous step is structural and exact. To get an explicit Dirac symbol, choose a local \(Q_B\)-frame in which the projected mixed matrices form a Pauli triplet:
\begin{equation}
M^1=I_g\sigma_1,
\qquad
M^2=I_g\sigma_2,
\qquad
M^3=I_g\sigma_3,
\qquad
I_g\neq 0.
\label{eq:Pauli_triplet_actual_class}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)=I_g\,p_i\sigma_i,
\label{eq:A1_Ig_sigma}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
D_1(p)
=
I_g
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & p_i\sigma_i\\
p_i\sigma_i & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:D1_Dirac_actual_class}
\end{equation}
This is the massless Dirac principal operator.

Equivalently, with
\begin{equation}
\alpha_i=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & \sigma_i\\
\sigma_i & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\{\alpha_i,\alpha_j\}=2\delta_{ij}\mathbf 1_4,
\label{eq:alpha_i_actual}
\end{equation}
one has
\begin{equation}
D_1(p)=I_g\,p_i\alpha_i.
\label{eq:D1_alpha_actual}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{G. What is actual and what is still open}

What is rigorously matched to the actual TECT defect projector Hessian is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the rank-two \(Q_B\)-bundle fluctuation field,
\item the matrix Schrödinger transverse Hessian,
\item the even/odd parity channel decomposition,
\item the odd first-order transport kernel,
\item the off-diagonal projected overlap formula.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the graded \(2+2\) Dirac bypass is not ad hoc; it belongs to the actual local CP\(^2\) projector-Hessian operator class.

What is still open for the full microscopic TECT dynamics is stronger:

\begin{enumerate}
\item proving that the actual defect background \(P_B(\xi)\) indeed has the required isolated even/odd low modes,
\item proving that the projected mixed symbol \(M^\mu\) is full rank for the actual \(V^\mu(\xi)\),
\item deriving the explicit Pauli-triplet form \eqref{eq:Pauli_triplet_actual_class} directly from the full microscopic transport kernel rather than from an explicit representative in the same operator class.
\end{enumerate}

So the strongest honest statement is:

\[
\text{actual projector Hessian}
\Longrightarrow
\text{graded }2+2\text{ operator class},
\]
and
\[
\text{full-rank Pauli-triplet realization}
\Longrightarrow
\text{explicit Dirac principal symbol}.
\]

%%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\delta P=\eta z_B^\dagger+z_B\eta^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B^\dagger\eta=0,
\qquad
\eta(\xi,y)\in Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb Cz_B(\xi))^\perp.
\]

Thus the actual CP^2 defect fluctuation problem is a rank-two bundle problem on \(Q_B\).
Its quadratic Hessian is a transverse matrix Schrödinger operator on \(Q_B\).

For a reflection-symmetric defect background
\[
P_B(-\xi)=P_B(\xi),
\]
the static transverse spectrum decomposes into even/odd low channels
\[
f_+(\xi),\qquad f_-(\xi),
\qquad
f_+(-\xi)=f_+(\xi),\quad f_-(-\xi)=-f_-(\xi).
\]

Using a local \(Q_B\)-frame \(e_a(\xi)\), define
\[
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
a=1,2.
\]
These span a graded low-energy sector
\[
K=K_+\oplus K_-,
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}K_\pm=2.
\]

The leading worldvolume transport operator has the form
\[
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\]
and because it is built linearly from \(\partial_\xi P_B,\partial_\xi z_B,\theta'(\xi)\), it is reflection-odd:
\[
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi).
\]

Hence same-parity overlaps vanish,
\[
\langle u_a^\pm,L_1u_b^\pm\rangle_\xi=0,
\]
while the mixed projected symbol is
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\]

Therefore the reduced principal operator on \(K\) is
\[
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu,
\qquad
D_1(0)=0.
\]

So the graded \(2+2\) bypass is structurally realized by the actual CP^2 projector-defect Hessian.

If, in addition, one chooses an explicit full-rank representative in this operator class
\[
M^1=I_g\sigma_1,\qquad
M^2=I_g\sigma_2,\qquad
M^3=I_g\sigma_3,
\qquad
I_g\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
A_1(p)=I_g\,p_i\sigma_i,
\]
and
\[
D_1(p)=
I_g
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & p_i\sigma_i\\
p_i\sigma_i & 0
\end{pmatrix}
= I_g\,p_i\alpha_i,
\qquad
\{\alpha_i,\alpha_j\}=2\delta_{ij}\mathbf 1_4.
\]

Thus the actual TECT defect-sector realization reaches:

\[
\boxed{
\text{projector Hessian}
\Rightarrow
\text{graded }2+2\text{ carrier}
\Rightarrow
\text{off-diagonal first-order symbol}
}
\]
and, with full-rank mixed overlap,
\[
\boxed{
D_1(p)\sim p_i\alpha_i
\quad\text{(Dirac principal operator).}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%


\subsection{Explicit evaluation of the graded mixed overlap integral in the CP\(^2\) defect sector}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now evaluate explicitly the graded mixed overlap integral
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty} d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi)
\]
for a concrete reflection-symmetric CP\(^2\) defect representative in the actual TECT projector-Hessian operator class.

\subsubsection{A. Explicit reflection-symmetric defect background}

Take the explicit CP\(^2\)-type defect representative
\begin{equation}
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi),
\qquad
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi).
\label{eq:zB_explicit}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B(\xi)^\dagger
\label{eq:PB_explicit}
\end{equation}
is reflection-even:
\begin{equation}
P_B(-\xi)=P_B(\xi).
\label{eq:PB_even_explicit}
\end{equation}

An explicit even orthonormal frame of
\begin{equation}
Q_B(\xi)=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp
\label{eq:QB_explicit}
\end{equation}
is
\begin{equation}
e_1(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_2(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\
1\\
0
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:frame_explicit}
\end{equation}
Because \(\theta(\xi)\) is even, both \(e_1(\xi)\) and \(e_2(\xi)\) are even under \(\xi\mapsto -\xi\).

\subsubsection{B. Explicit even/odd low modes}

Take the standard normalized localized even/odd pair
\begin{equation}
f_+(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{\kappa}{2}}\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\label{eq:fplus_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
f_-(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{3\kappa}{2}}\,\tanh(\kappa\xi)\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi).
\label{eq:fminus_explicit}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
f_+(-\xi)=f_+(\xi),
\qquad
f_-(-\xi)=-f_-(\xi).
\label{eq:parity_fpm_explicit}
\end{equation}
Define the graded low modes
\begin{equation}
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
a=1,2.
\label{eq:uapm_explicit}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. Odd transport kernel}

From the linearized defect operator class, the first-order transport term has the form
\begin{equation}
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\label{eq:L1_explicit}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi),
\label{eq:Vodd_explicit}
\end{equation}
because \(V^\mu\) is built linearly from \(\partial_\xi P_B\), \(\partial_\xi z_B\), or \(\theta'(\xi)\), and
\[
\theta'(-\xi)=-\theta'(\xi).
\]

To obtain an explicit solvable representative in the same operator class, choose a factorized odd kernel
\begin{equation}
V^i(\xi)=g(\xi)\,\Sigma^i,
\qquad
g(\xi)=3g_0\,\tanh(\kappa\xi),
\label{eq:Vi_factorized}
\end{equation}
where the \(\Sigma^i\) are constant Hermitian endomorphisms acting on the \(Q_B\)-frame.
Choose them as
\begin{equation}
\Sigma^i=v_i\,\sigma_i,
\qquad
v_i\in\mathbb R.
\label{eq:Sigmai_choice}
\end{equation}
In the frame \((e_1,e_2)\), this means
\begin{equation}
e_a^\dagger(\xi)\Sigma^i e_b(\xi)=v_i(\sigma_i)_{ab}.
\label{eq:frame_matrix_Sigma}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{D. Same-parity overlaps vanish}

The same-parity projected overlap is
\begin{equation}
\langle u_a^\pm,V^i u_b^\pm\rangle
=
\int d\xi\, f_\pm(\xi)^2\,e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^i(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\label{eq:same_parity_overlap}
\end{equation}
Since \(f_\pm^2\) is even, \(e_a^\dagger\Sigma^i e_b\) is even, and \(g(\xi)\) is odd, the integrand is odd.
Hence
\begin{equation}
\langle u_a^\pm,V^i u_b^\pm\rangle=0.
\label{eq:same_parity_zero_explicit}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{E. Mixed overlap integral}

Now compute the mixed block:
\begin{equation}
(M^i)_{ab}
=
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty} d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^i(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\label{eq:Mi_def_explicit}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:Vi_factorized} and \eqref{eq:frame_matrix_Sigma},
\begin{equation}
(M^i)_{ab}
=
v_i(\sigma_i)_{ab}
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty} d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,g(\xi).
\label{eq:Mi_factorized}
\end{equation}
Thus
\begin{equation}
M^i=I_g\,v_i\sigma_i,
\label{eq:Mi_Ig_form}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
I_g
:=
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty} d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,g(\xi).
\label{eq:Ig_def}
\end{equation}

Substitute \eqref{eq:fplus_explicit}, \eqref{eq:fminus_explicit}, and \(g(\xi)=3g_0\tanh(\kappa\xi)\):
\begin{equation}
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)
=
\sqrt{\frac{\kappa}{2}}\sqrt{\frac{3\kappa}{2}}
\,\tanh(\kappa\xi)\,\mathrm{sech}^2(\kappa\xi)
=
\frac{\sqrt3\,\kappa}{2}\,
\tanh(\kappa\xi)\,\mathrm{sech}^2(\kappa\xi).
\label{eq:fpfm_product}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
I_g
=
\frac{3g_0\sqrt3\,\kappa}{2}
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}
d\xi\,
\tanh^2(\kappa\xi)\,\mathrm{sech}^2(\kappa\xi).
\label{eq:Ig_integral_1}
\end{equation}
Set
\begin{equation}
t=\tanh(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
dt=\kappa\,\mathrm{sech}^2(\kappa\xi)\,d\xi.
\label{eq:t_subst}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
I_g
=
\frac{3g_0\sqrt3}{2}
\int_{-1}^{1} t^2\,dt
=
\frac{3g_0\sqrt3}{2}\cdot \frac{2}{3}
=
g_0\sqrt3.
\label{eq:Ig_final}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^i=g_0\sqrt3\,v_i\sigma_i.
}
\label{eq:Mi_final}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{F. Reduced symbol and nondegeneracy}

The graded mixed symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)=p_iM^i
=
g_0\sqrt3\,
\bigl(v_1p_1\sigma_1+v_2p_2\sigma_2+v_3p_3\sigma_3\bigr).
\label{eq:A1_final_explicit}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\det A_1(p)
=
-3g_0^2
\bigl(v_1^2p_1^2+v_2^2p_2^2+v_3^2p_3^2\bigr).
\label{eq:detA1_final_explicit}
\end{equation}
In particular, if
\begin{equation}
v_1v_2v_3\neq 0,
\label{eq:vi_nonzero}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\det A_1(p)\neq 0
\qquad
\text{for generic }p\neq 0.
\label{eq:det_nonzero_generic}
\end{equation}

Thus the reduced principal operator on the graded \(2+2\) carrier is
\begin{equation}
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:D1_explicit}
\end{equation}
and since \(A_1(p)\) is Hermitian here,
\begin{equation}
D_1(p)=
g_0\sqrt3
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & v_ip_i\sigma_i\\
v_ip_i\sigma_i & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:D1_hermitian_explicit}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{G. Dirac form}

Define
\begin{equation}
\alpha_i=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & \sigma_i\\
\sigma_i & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\{\alpha_i,\alpha_j\}=2\delta_{ij}\mathbf 1_4.
\label{eq:alpha_explicit}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
D_1(p)=g_0\sqrt3\,v_ip_i\,\alpha_i.
\label{eq:D1_Dirac_explicit}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the massless Dirac principal operator on the graded \(2+2\) low-energy sector.

\subsubsection{H. Honest status}

What is explicit here is a concrete representative inside the actual TECT projector-defect operator class:
\begin{enumerate}
\item explicit reflection-symmetric \(CP^2\) defect profile \(z_B(\xi)\),
\item explicit even \(Q_B\)-frame \(e_a(\xi)\),
\item explicit even/odd low modes \(f_\pm(\xi)\),
\item explicit odd transport kernel \(V^i(\xi)=3g_0\tanh(\kappa\xi)\Sigma^i\),
\item explicit overlap integral \(I_g=g_0\sqrt3\),
\item explicit full-rank mixed symbol \(A_1(p)\).
\end{enumerate}

What remains open is stronger:
deriving this very same \(V^\mu(\xi)\) and the same full-rank Pauli-triplet form directly from the complete microscopic TECT transport kernel without choosing an explicit representative in the same operator class.


%%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\]
with even \(Q_B\)-frame
\[
e_1(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_2(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\
1\\
0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Take the explicit even/odd low modes
\[
f_+(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{\kappa}{2}}\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
f_-(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{3\kappa}{2}}\,\tanh(\kappa\xi)\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\]
and define
\[
u_a^\pm(\xi)=f_\pm(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad a=1,2.
\]

Choose the odd transport representative
\[
V^i(\xi)=g(\xi)\Sigma^i,
\qquad
g(\xi)=3g_0\tanh(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
\Sigma^i=v_i\sigma_i.
\]

Then same-parity overlaps vanish,
\[
\langle u_a^\pm,V^i u_b^\pm\rangle=0,
\]
while the mixed overlap is
\[
(M^i)_{ab}
=
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^i(\xi)e_b(\xi)
=
I_g\,v_i(\sigma_i)_{ab},
\]
with
\[
I_g
=
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)g(\xi).
\]

Using the explicit profiles,
\[
I_g
=
\frac{3g_0\sqrt3\,\kappa}{2}
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}d\xi\,
\tanh^2(\kappa\xi)\mathrm{sech}^2(\kappa\xi).
\]
With \(t=\tanh(\kappa\xi)\), \(dt=\kappa\,\mathrm{sech}^2(\kappa\xi)d\xi\),
\[
I_g
=
\frac{3g_0\sqrt3}{2}\int_{-1}^{1}t^2dt
=
g_0\sqrt3.
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
M^i=g_0\sqrt3\,v_i\sigma_i.
}
\]

Hence
\[
A_1(p)=p_iM^i
=
g_0\sqrt3\,
(v_1p_1\sigma_1+v_2p_2\sigma_2+v_3p_3\sigma_3),
\]
so
\[
\det A_1(p)
=
-3g_0^2\left(v_1^2p_1^2+v_2^2p_2^2+v_3^2p_3^2\right).
\]
If \(v_1v_2v_3\neq 0\), then \(\det A_1(p)\neq 0\) for generic \(p\neq 0\).

Thus the graded \(2+2\) reduced principal operator is
\[
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix}
=
g_0\sqrt3\,v_ip_i\alpha_i,
\qquad
\{\alpha_i,\alpha_j\}=2\delta_{ij}\mathbf 1_4.
\]

So, for this explicit representative inside the actual projector-defect operator class, the graded \(2+2\) bypass yields an explicit massless Dirac principal symbol.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Actual local transport kernel profile: the leading odd scalar is \texorpdfstring{$\theta'(\xi)$}{theta'(xi)}}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now determine the leading scalar profile \(g(\xi)\) in the actual local transport kernel
\[
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
\]
for the CP\(^2\) projector defect, and evaluate the resulting mixed overlap integral explicitly.

\subsubsection{A. Explicit local defect background and frame}

Take the explicit reflection-symmetric defect representative
\begin{equation}
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi),
\qquad
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi).
\label{eq:zB_theta_profile}
\end{equation}
An orthonormal local frame of
\[
Q_B(\xi)=(\mathbb Cz_B(\xi))^\perp
\]
is
\begin{equation}
e_1(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_2(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\
1\\
0
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:e1e2_theta_frame}
\end{equation}

Differentiate:
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi z_B(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix}
=
\theta'(\xi)e_1(\xi).
\label{eq:dzB_exact}
\end{equation}
Also,
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi e_1(\xi)
=
-\theta'(\xi)z_B(\xi),
\qquad
\partial_\xi e_2(\xi)=0.
\label{eq:de_frame_exact}
\end{equation}

Therefore the frame connection along \(\xi\) vanishes:
\begin{equation}
A_\xi=-ie^\dagger\partial_\xi e=0.
\label{eq:Axi_zero_again}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Local gradient structure of the transport kernel}

The actual local defect-Hessian analysis states that the leading transport kernel is built linearly from the transverse defect gradient, i.e. from quantities such as
\[
\partial_\xi P_B(\xi),\qquad \partial_\xi z_B(\xi),\qquad \theta'(\xi),
\]
and is therefore reflection-odd.
Using \eqref{eq:dzB_exact}, every such local first-order building block is proportional to \(\theta'(\xi)\) times an \(\xi\)-even matrix determined by \(\theta(\xi)\).

Indeed,
\begin{equation}
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B(\xi)^\dagger,
\label{eq:PB_theta}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi P_B
=
(\partial_\xi z_B)z_B^\dagger+z_B(\partial_\xi z_B)^\dagger
=
\theta'(\xi)\bigl(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger\bigr).
\label{eq:dPB_exact}
\end{equation}
Thus any local transport endomorphism built linearly from the background gradient has the schematic form
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:Vmu_thetaM}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\) is an even \(2\times2\) Hermitian matrix in the \(Q_B\)-frame.

Expanding in the Pauli basis,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)
=
a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2+a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i.
\label{eq:Mmupm}
\end{equation}
Since \(\theta(\xi)\) is even, all coefficients \(a_0^\mu(\theta(\xi)),a_i^\mu(\theta(\xi))\) are even functions of \(\xi\).
Hence the leading odd scalar profile is exactly
\begin{equation}
g_{\mathrm{lead}}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi).
\label{eq:g_lead_theta}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. Explicit low modes}

Use the explicit even/odd low modes
\begin{equation}
f_+(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{\kappa}{2}}\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\label{eq:fplus_theta}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
f_-(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{3\kappa}{2}}\,\tanh(\kappa\xi)\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\label{eq:fminus_theta}
\end{equation}
and define
\begin{equation}
u_a^\pm(\xi)=f_\pm(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
a=1,2.
\label{eq:uapm_theta}
\end{equation}

The mixed projected symbol is
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\label{eq:Mmu_theta_general}
\end{equation}
At leading order in the local gradient expansion, using \eqref{eq:Vmu_thetaM},
\begin{equation}
M^\mu
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\label{eq:Mmu_theta_expand}
\end{equation}

If one freezes the even matrix coefficient at leading order to a constant traceless Hermitian matrix
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\approx \Sigma^\mu=v_\mu\sigma_\mu,
\label{eq:Sigma_mu_freeze}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
M^\mu
=
I_\theta\,\Sigma^\mu,
\qquad
I_\theta:=\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi).
\label{eq:Mmu_Itheta}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{D. Exact evaluation of \texorpdfstring{$I_\theta$}{Itheta}}

First compute
\begin{equation}
\theta'(\xi)
=
\theta_0\frac{d}{d\xi}\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi)
=
-\theta_0\kappa\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi)\tanh(\kappa\xi).
\label{eq:theta_prime_exact}
\end{equation}
Next,
\begin{equation}
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)
=
\sqrt{\frac{\kappa}{2}}\sqrt{\frac{3\kappa}{2}}
\,\tanh(\kappa\xi)\,\mathrm{sech}^2(\kappa\xi)
=
\frac{\sqrt3\,\kappa}{2}\,
\tanh(\kappa\xi)\,\mathrm{sech}^2(\kappa\xi).
\label{eq:fpfm_theta}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{align}
I_\theta
&=
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty} d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi) \nonumber\\
&=
-\frac{\sqrt3\,\theta_0\kappa^2}{2}
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty} d\xi\,
\tanh^2(\kappa\xi)\,\mathrm{sech}^3(\kappa\xi).
\label{eq:Itheta_step1}
\end{align}

Now set
\begin{equation}
t=\tanh(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
dt=\kappa\,\mathrm{sech}^2(\kappa\xi)\,d\xi,
\qquad
\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi)=\sqrt{1-t^2}.
\label{eq:t_substitution_theta}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{align}
I_\theta
&=
-\frac{\sqrt3\,\theta_0\kappa}{2}
\int_{-1}^{1} t^2\sqrt{1-t^2}\,dt.
\label{eq:Itheta_step2}
\end{align}
Using
\begin{equation}
\int_{-1}^{1} t^2\sqrt{1-t^2}\,dt=\frac{\pi}{8},
\label{eq:t_integral_value}
\end{equation}
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\,\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:Itheta_final}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
I_\theta\neq 0
\qquad
\text{whenever }\theta_0\kappa\neq 0.
\label{eq:Itheta_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{E. Consequence for the mixed symbol}

Substituting \eqref{eq:Itheta_final} into \eqref{eq:Mmu_Itheta},
\begin{equation}
M^\mu
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\,\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,\Sigma^\mu.
\label{eq:Mmu_theta_final}
\end{equation}
If the three frozen matrices \(\Sigma^\mu\) form a full-rank Pauli triple, e.g.
\begin{equation}
\Sigma^1=v_1\sigma_1,\qquad
\Sigma^2=v_2\sigma_2,\qquad
\Sigma^3=v_3\sigma_3,
\qquad
v_1v_2v_3\neq 0,
\label{eq:Sigma_triplet_theta}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\,\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa
\bigl(v_1p_1\sigma_1+v_2p_2\sigma_2+v_3p_3\sigma_3\bigr),
\label{eq:A1_theta_final}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\det A_1(p)
=
-\frac{3\pi^2}{256}\,\theta_0^2\kappa^2
\bigl(v_1^2p_1^2+v_2^2p_2^2+v_3^2p_3^2\bigr).
\label{eq:detA1_theta_final}
\end{equation}
Thus the mixed symbol is nonzero and full rank for generic \(p\neq 0\).

\subsubsection{F. Honest conclusion}

What is now directly computed from the actual local CP\(^2\) defect geometry is the leading odd scalar profile:
\[
g(\xi)\propto \theta'(\xi).
\]
For the explicit profile \(\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi)\), the mixed overlap integral is
\[
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\neq 0.
\]
Therefore the actual local defect-gradient transport mechanism produces a nonzero graded mixed symbol already at the level of the explicit local projector representative.

What remains open is stronger:
deriving the full matrix coefficient \(\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi))\) from the complete microscopic TECT linearization, rather than freezing it to a constant representative \(\Sigma^\mu\).


%%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
e_1(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_2(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\
1\\
0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Then
\[
\partial_\xi z_B=\theta'(\xi)e_1,
\qquad
\partial_\xi P_B=\theta'(\xi)(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger).
\]
Therefore every leading local transport kernel built linearly from the defect gradient has the form
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\]
with \(\mathcal M^\mu\) even in \(\xi\).

So the actual leading odd scalar profile is
\[
\boxed{
g_{\mathrm{lead}}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi).
}
\]

Using
\[
f_+(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{\kappa}{2}}\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
f_-(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{3\kappa}{2}}\,\tanh(\kappa\xi)\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\]
the mixed overlap integral
\[
I_\theta=\int_{-\infty}^{\infty} d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)
\]
is exactly
\[
\boxed{
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\]

Hence \(I_\theta\neq 0\) whenever \(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0\).

If one freezes the even matrix coefficient to a Pauli-triplet representative
\[
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\approx \Sigma^\mu=v_\mu\sigma_\mu,
\]
then
\[
M^\mu=I_\theta\,\Sigma^\mu,
\]
so
\[
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa
\bigl(v_1p_1\sigma_1+v_2p_2\sigma_2+v_3p_3\sigma_3\bigr),
\]
and
\[
\det A_1(p)
=
-\frac{3\pi^2}{256}\,\theta_0^2\kappa^2
\bigl(v_1^2p_1^2+v_2^2p_2^2+v_3^2p_3^2\bigr).
\]

So, in the actual local CP\(^2\) projector-defect geometry, the natural transport scalar profile is \(\theta'(\xi)\), and its graded overlap is explicitly nonzero.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%


\subsection{Unfreezing \texorpdfstring{$\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)$}{M^mu(theta)}: identity part, traceless part, and the full-rank criterion}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now unfreeze the matrix coefficient in the actual local transport kernel
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\]
and determine:

\begin{enumerate}
\item whether the identity component of \(\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\) must vanish,
\item whether the traceless Pauli components can span three independent directions.
\end{enumerate}

\subsubsection{A. General Hermitian decomposition on the rank-two \texorpdfstring{$Q_B$}{QB} bundle}

In the local orthonormal \(Q_B\)-frame \((e_1(\xi),e_2(\xi))\), every Hermitian endomorphism of the rank-two fiber \(Q_B(\xi)\) decomposes uniquely as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)
=
a_0^\mu(\theta)\,\mathbf 1_2
+
a_i^\mu(\theta)\,\sigma_i,
\qquad i=1,2,3,
\label{eq:Mmu_general_decomp}
\end{equation}
with real coefficient functions \(a_0^\mu(\theta),a_i^\mu(\theta)\).

Thus the actual local transport kernel has the general form
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl(
a_0^\mu(\theta(\xi))\,\mathbf 1_2
+
a_i^\mu(\theta(\xi))\,\sigma_i
\Bigr).
\label{eq:Vmu_general_decomp}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Parity of the coefficient functions}

The defect profile satisfies
\[
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi),
\qquad
\theta'(-\xi)=-\theta'(\xi).
\]
Since \(a_0^\mu(\theta),a_i^\mu(\theta)\) are functions of the even variable \(\theta(\xi)\), they are even in \(\xi\):
\begin{equation}
a_0^\mu(\theta(-\xi))=a_0^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\qquad
a_i^\mu(\theta(-\xi))=a_i^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\label{eq:a_even}
\end{equation}
Therefore the transport kernel is odd:
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi),
\label{eq:Vmu_odd_general}
\end{equation}
exactly as required by the local matching theorem for the projector Hessian operator class. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

Importantly, parity alone does \emph{not} force
\[
a_0^\mu(\theta)\equiv 0.
\]
So the identity component is not forbidden by reflection symmetry.

\subsubsection{C. Projected mixed symbol with the unfrozen coefficient}

The mixed overlap matrix is
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty} d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\label{eq:Mmu_overlap_general}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:Vmu_general_decomp},
\begin{equation}
M^\mu
=
\int d\xi\, f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl(
a_0^\mu(\theta(\xi))\,\mathbf 1_2
+
a_i^\mu(\theta(\xi))\,\sigma_i
\Bigr).
\label{eq:Mmu_integral_general}
\end{equation}
Define the coefficient integrals
\begin{equation}
C_0^\mu
:=
\int d\xi\, f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,a_0^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:C0_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C_i^\mu
:=
\int d\xi\, f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,a_i^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\label{eq:Ci_def}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
M^\mu=C_0^\mu\,\mathbf 1_2+C_i^\mu\,\sigma_i.
\label{eq:Mmu_C_decomp}
\end{equation}

Because \(f_+\) is even, \(f_-\) is odd, and \(\theta'\) is odd, the product
\[
f_+f_-\theta'
\]
is even. Hence both \(C_0^\mu\) and \(C_i^\mu\) are generically allowed by parity. There is no parity reason forcing \(C_0^\mu=0\).

\subsubsection{D. Why the identity part is not a mass obstruction}

The reduced first-order mixed symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu
=
p_\mu C_0^\mu\,\mathbf 1_2
+
p_\mu C_i^\mu\,\sigma_i.
\label{eq:A1_general_C}
\end{equation}
Thus the full graded principal operator is
\begin{equation}
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:D1_general_C}
\end{equation}
Since \(A_1(p)\) is linear in momentum,
\begin{equation}
A_1(0)=0,
\qquad
D_1(0)=0.
\label{eq:D1_zero_general}
\end{equation}

Therefore the identity component \(C_0^\mu\mathbf 1_2\) contributes only a \emph{first-order} term
\[
p_\mu C_0^\mu\,\mathbf 1_2,
\]
not a constant mass term.
This is completely different from the scalar Bragg-mass obstruction
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\]
which is momentum-independent.

Hence:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the identity part }C_0^\mu\mathbf 1_2\text{ is not a mass obstruction in the graded }2+2\text{ bypass.}
}
\label{eq:C0_not_mass}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{E. Canonical reduction and irrelevance of the identity part}

The graded infrared theorem already established in the manuscript states that any nondegenerate mixed symbol
\[
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu
\]
with \(M^\mu\) arbitrary \(2\times2\) complex matrices can, after unitary basis changes in \(K_\pm\) and an invertible linear transformation of momentum coordinates, be brought to the canonical form
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)=p_i\sigma_i.
\label{eq:A1_canonical_reduction}
\end{equation}
This means that the identity component is not load-bearing at the principal level; it can be absorbed into the canonical reduction once the full symbol is nondegenerate. 

So the correct statement is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_0^\mu\ \text{need not vanish, but it is principal-level irrelevant once }A_1(p)\text{ is nondegenerate.}
}
\label{eq:C0_irrelevant}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{F. The actual load-bearing data: the traceless coefficient vectors}

Write
\begin{equation}
b^\mu:=(C_1^\mu,C_2^\mu,C_3^\mu)\in \mathbb R^3.
\label{eq:bmu_def}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
M^\mu=C_0^\mu\,\mathbf 1_2+b_i^\mu\sigma_i.
\label{eq:Mmu_bmu}
\end{equation}
The manuscript states explicitly that the mixed symbol is nondegenerate iff the vectors \(b^\mu\in\mathbb R^3\) span \(\mathbb R^3\). :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{span}\{b^1,b^2,b^3\}=\mathbb R^3
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
A_1(p)\ \text{is full rank for generic }p\neq 0.
\label{eq:span_criterion}
\end{equation}

Thus the actual load-bearing condition is not \(C_0^\mu=0\), but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det\bigl[b_i^\mu\bigr]\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:det_b_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{G. Structural realization in the actual local projector-Hessian class}

The honest local matching theorem states that the actual CP\(^2\) projector Hessian around a reflection-symmetric defect background belongs to the same operator class as the minimal graded defect operator: rank-two matrix Schrödinger static part, even/odd parity channels, and odd first-order transport kernel. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

Moreover, the same operator class admits an explicit full-rank realization
\begin{equation}
M^1=I_g\sigma_1,\qquad
M^2=I_g\sigma_2,\qquad
M^3=I_g\sigma_3,
\qquad
I_g\neq 0,
\label{eq:explicit_full_rank_again}
\end{equation}
which is exactly the case
\[
C_0^\mu=0,\qquad
b^\mu=I_g\,\hat e_\mu.
\]
This proves that there is \emph{no structural obstruction} inside the actual local operator class to having three independent traceless directions. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

Therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{in the actual local projector-Hessian operator class, }b^\mu\text{ can span }\mathbb R^3.
}
\label{eq:no_structural_obstruction}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{H. What is still open}

What is not yet proved microscopically is stronger:
that the \emph{actual full TECT transport kernel} produces coefficient functions \(a_i^\mu(\theta(\xi))\) whose projected integrals \(b^\mu\) satisfy
\[
\det[b_i^\mu]\neq 0
\]
for the physically realized defect background.

So the honest status is:

\[
\text{actual local operator class}
\Longrightarrow
\text{no obstruction to full rank},
\]
but
\[
\text{full microscopic TECT dynamics}
\Longrightarrow ?
\]

\paragraph{Exact logical status.}
What is now closed is:
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\qquad
\mathcal M^\mu=a_0^\mu\mathbf 1_2+a_i^\mu\sigma_i,
\]
\[
M^\mu=C_0^\mu\mathbf 1_2+C_i^\mu\sigma_i,
\]
\[
C_0^\mu\ \text{is allowed but not a mass term},
\qquad
\mathrm{span}\{b^\mu\}=\mathbb R^3
\text{ is the real nondegeneracy criterion.}
\]
And the actual local projector-Hessian operator class already contains explicit full-rank representatives.


%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\qquad
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)=a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2+a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i.
\]

Because \(\theta(\xi)\) is even and \(\theta'(\xi)\) is odd, parity does not force \(a_0^\mu(\theta)\) to vanish.
The projected mixed matrices are
\[
M^\mu
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi))
=
C_0^\mu\mathbf 1_2+C_i^\mu\sigma_i,
\]
with
\[
C_0^\mu=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\theta' a_0^\mu(\theta),
\qquad
C_i^\mu=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\theta' a_i^\mu(\theta).
\]

Thus the mixed symbol is
\[
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu
=
p_\mu C_0^\mu\,\mathbf 1_2
+
p_\mu C_i^\mu\,\sigma_i.
\]

Since this is first-order in \(p\),
\[
A_1(0)=0,
\qquad
D_1(0)=0.
\]
Therefore the identity part \(C_0^\mu\mathbf 1_2\) is not a constant mass term.
It is principal-level irrelevant once the full mixed symbol is nondegenerate.

The actual load-bearing data are the traceless coefficient vectors
\[
b^\mu:=(C_1^\mu,C_2^\mu,C_3^\mu)\in\mathbb R^3.
\]
The exact nondegeneracy criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{span}\{b^1,b^2,b^3\}=\mathbb R^3.
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\det[b_i^\mu]\neq 0.
\]

The actual local CP\(^2\) projector-Hessian operator class already contains an explicit full-rank realization
\[
M^1=I_g\sigma_1,\qquad
M^2=I_g\sigma_2,\qquad
M^3=I_g\sigma_3,
\qquad
I_g\neq 0,
\]
so there is no structural obstruction to obtaining three independent traceless directions.

Hence:
\[
\boxed{
a_0^\mu\text{ need not vanish, but it is not the load-bearing issue.}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{The real Dirac criterion is whether the traceless vectors }b^\mu\text{ span }\mathbb R^3.
}
\]


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Three independent traceless transport channels from the actual local \(Q_B\)-geometry}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now derive, directly from the actual local CP\(^2\) projector-defect geometry, why there are naturally three independent traceless transport channels available in the graded \(2+2\) reduction.

\subsubsection{A. Local rank-two bundle and its endomorphism algebra}

For the reflection-symmetric defect background
\begin{equation}
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi),
\label{eq:zB_local_again}
\end{equation}
the physical tangent fluctuation lives in the rank-two complex bundle
\begin{equation}
Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp.
\label{eq:QB_rank2_again}
\end{equation}
An explicit orthonormal local frame is
\begin{equation}
e_1(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_2(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\
1\\
0
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:e1e2_again_local}
\end{equation}
In this frame the transverse \(Q_B\)-connection vanishes:
\begin{equation}
A_\xi=-ie^\dagger\partial_\xi e=0.
\label{eq:Axi_zero_local}
\end{equation}
Therefore the local fiber geometry is completely standard:
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Herm}(Q_B)\cong \mathrm{Herm}(2)=\mathbb R\,\mathbf 1_2\oplus \mathfrak{su}(2)_{\mathrm{Herm}}.
\label{eq:HermQB_split}
\end{equation}
A canonical traceless Hermitian basis is given by
\begin{equation}
\Sigma^{(1)}:=e_1e_2^\dagger+e_2e_1^\dagger,
\label{eq:Sigma1_geom}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\Sigma^{(2)}:=-i e_1e_2^\dagger+i e_2e_1^\dagger,
\label{eq:Sigma2_geom}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\Sigma^{(3)}:=e_1e_1^\dagger-e_2e_2^\dagger.
\label{eq:Sigma3_geom}
\end{equation}
In the local frame \((e_1,e_2)\), these are exactly the Pauli matrices:
\begin{equation}
\Sigma^{(1)}\leftrightarrow \sigma_1,\qquad
\Sigma^{(2)}\leftrightarrow \sigma_2,\qquad
\Sigma^{(3)}\leftrightarrow \sigma_3.
\label{eq:Sigma_Pauli_identification}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Actual local transport kernel}

The local projector-Hessian analysis gives the first-order transport operator
\begin{equation}
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\label{eq:L1_local_again}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)\sim (\partial_\xi P_B(\xi))\,T^\mu
\label{eq:Vmu_dPB}
\end{equation}
for constant matrices \(T^\mu\) determined by the elastic/worldvolume couplings. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}
Because \(P_B(-\xi)=P_B(\xi)\), one has
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi P_B(-\xi)=-\partial_\xi P_B(\xi),
\label{eq:dPB_odd}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi).
\label{eq:Vmu_odd_local}
\end{equation}

Using
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi z_B=\theta'(\xi)e_1,
\qquad
\partial_\xi P_B=\theta'(\xi)\bigl(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger\bigr),
\label{eq:dPB_theta_form}
\end{equation}
every leading local transport kernel built linearly from the background gradient has the form
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:Vmu_theta_general_again}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\) is an even Hermitian endomorphism of \(Q_B\).

Expanding in the canonical basis \(\{\mathbf 1_2,\Sigma^{(1)},\Sigma^{(2)},\Sigma^{(3)}\}\),
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)
=
a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2
+
h_1^\mu(\theta)\Sigma^{(1)}
+
h_2^\mu(\theta)\Sigma^{(2)}
+
h_3^\mu(\theta)\Sigma^{(3)}.
\label{eq:Mmu_expand_Sigma}
\end{equation}
So the traceless local transport channels are exactly
\[
\Sigma^{(1)},\Sigma^{(2)},\Sigma^{(3)}.
\]

\subsubsection{C. Projected mixed symbol}

Let the even/odd low modes be
\begin{equation}
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
a=1,2.
\label{eq:uapm_geom}
\end{equation}
Then the mixed projected matrices are
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\label{eq:Mmu_projected_geom}
\end{equation}
Substituting \eqref{eq:Vmu_theta_general_again} and \eqref{eq:Mmu_expand_Sigma},
\begin{equation}
M^\mu
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl[
a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2
+
h_i^\mu(\theta)\Sigma^{(i)}
\Bigr].
\label{eq:Mmu_integral_geom}
\end{equation}
Define
\begin{equation}
C_0^\mu:=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,a_0^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:C0_geom}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C_i^\mu:=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,h_i^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\label{eq:Ci_geom}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
M^\mu=C_0^\mu\,\mathbf 1_2+C_i^\mu\,\Sigma^{(i)}.
\label{eq:Mmu_geom_final}
\end{equation}

The load-bearing traceless coefficient vectors are therefore
\begin{equation}
b^\mu:=(C_1^\mu,C_2^\mu,C_3^\mu)\in \mathbb R^3.
\label{eq:bmu_geom}
\end{equation}
By the exact mixed-symbol criterion of the graded effective model, the reduced symbol is nondegenerate iff
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{span}\{b^1,b^2,b^3\}=\mathbb R^3.
\label{eq:span_bmu_geom}
\end{equation}


\subsubsection{D. Why three independent channels are structurally natural}

There is no local geometric obstruction to having three independent traceless channels because:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the fiber \(Q_B(\xi)\) is complex rank \(2\), so \(\mathfrak{su}(2)\) is the full traceless Hermitian algebra;
\item the chosen frame is smooth and \(A_\xi=0\), so no covariant-derivative obstruction mixes away the three basis elements;
\item the actual local transport kernel already takes values in \(\mathrm{End}(Q_B)\), so all three traceless basis directions are admissible.
\end{enumerate}

Hence the strongest structural statement is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the actual local projector-defect operator class naturally contains three independent traceless transport channels.}
}
\label{eq:three_channels_exist}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{E. Generic spanning argument}

Suppose the coefficient matrix
\begin{equation}
H(\theta):=\bigl(h_i^\mu(\theta)\bigr)_{\mu,i}
\label{eq:Htheta_matrix}
\end{equation}
has full rank at some range of \(\theta\) values visited by the defect profile.
Then the integrated coefficients
\[
C_i^\mu=\int d\xi\,w(\xi)\,h_i^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\qquad
w(\xi):=f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi),
\]
are generically full rank unless a nontrivial cancellation occurs.
Since \(w(\xi)\) is even and not identically zero, such cancellation requires nongeneric fine tuning of the functions \(h_i^\mu(\theta)\).

Thus, in the absence of special symmetry or tuning,
\begin{equation}
\det[C_i^\mu]\neq 0
\label{eq:generic_full_rank}
\end{equation}
is the generic expectation.

\paragraph{Important honesty.}
This is a genericity statement, not yet a theorem for the full microscopic TECT transport kernel.

\subsubsection{F. Explicit realizable point inside the same operator class}

The same actual local operator class already admits an explicit full-rank realization:
\begin{equation}
M^1=I_g\sigma_1,\qquad
M^2=I_g\sigma_2,\qquad
M^3=I_g\sigma_3,
\qquad
I_g\neq 0,
\label{eq:explicit_full_rank_localclass}
\end{equation}
which corresponds to
\begin{equation}
C_0^\mu=0,
\qquad
b^1=I_g(1,0,0),\quad
b^2=I_g(0,1,0),\quad
b^3=I_g(0,0,1).
\label{eq:bmus_explicit}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{span}\{b^1,b^2,b^3\}=\mathbb R^3.
\label{eq:span_explicit}
\end{equation}

So, while the full microscopic coefficient functions \(h_i^\mu(\theta)\) are still open, the actual local projector-Hessian operator class does contain explicit full-rank points.

\subsubsection{G. Final conclusion}

What is now closed is:
\[
Q_B\text{ rank-2 geometry}
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{Herm}(Q_B)=\mathbb R\mathbf 1_2\oplus \mathrm{span}\{\Sigma^{(1)},\Sigma^{(2)},\Sigma^{(3)}\},
\]
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\Bigl(a_0^\mu\mathbf 1_2+h_i^\mu\Sigma^{(i)}\Bigr),
\]
\[
M^\mu=C_0^\mu\mathbf 1_2+C_i^\mu\Sigma^{(i)},
\qquad
b^\mu=(C_1^\mu,C_2^\mu,C_3^\mu).
\]
The actual nondegeneracy criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{span}\{b^1,b^2,b^3\}=\mathbb R^3.
}
\]
And the local operator class already contains explicit points where this is realized.

What remains open is the final microscopic computation of the actual coefficient functions \(h_i^\mu(\theta)\) from the full TECT transport kernel.


%%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
Q_B(\xi)=(\mathbb Cz_B(\xi))^\perp
\]
is a complex rank-two bundle, so in a local orthonormal frame \((e_1,e_2)\),
\[
\mathrm{Herm}(Q_B)\cong \mathbb R\,\mathbf 1_2\oplus \mathrm{span}\{\Sigma^{(1)},\Sigma^{(2)},\Sigma^{(3)}\},
\]
with canonical traceless basis
\[
\Sigma^{(1)}=e_1e_2^\dagger+e_2e_1^\dagger,\qquad
\Sigma^{(2)}=-ie_1e_2^\dagger+ie_2e_1^\dagger,\qquad
\Sigma^{(3)}=e_1e_1^\dagger-e_2e_2^\dagger.
\]
In the local frame these are exactly
\[
\Sigma^{(1)}\leftrightarrow \sigma_1,\qquad
\Sigma^{(2)}\leftrightarrow \sigma_2,\qquad
\Sigma^{(3)}\leftrightarrow \sigma_3.
\]

The actual local transport kernel has the form
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\]
and therefore can be expanded as
\[
V^\mu(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl(
a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2+h_i^\mu(\theta)\Sigma^{(i)}
\Bigr).
\]

Projecting onto the graded low modes \(u_a^\pm=f_\pm e_a\) gives
\[
M^\mu
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl(
a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2+h_i^\mu(\theta)\Sigma^{(i)}
\Bigr)
=
C_0^\mu\mathbf 1_2+C_i^\mu\Sigma^{(i)}.
\]

The load-bearing traceless coefficient vectors are
\[
b^\mu=(C_1^\mu,C_2^\mu,C_3^\mu)\in\mathbb R^3.
\]
The exact nondegeneracy criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{span}\{b^1,b^2,b^3\}=\mathbb R^3.
}
\]

Therefore the actual local \(Q_B\)-geometry naturally provides exactly three independent traceless transport channels.

Moreover, the same local operator class already contains an explicit full-rank point
\[
M^1=I_g\sigma_1,\qquad
M^2=I_g\sigma_2,\qquad
M^3=I_g\sigma_3,
\qquad
I_g\neq 0,
\]
so there is no structural obstruction to full rank inside the actual projector-defect operator class.


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Minimal actual parametrization of the microscopic transport tensor \(T^\mu\) in the local projector-defect sector}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now write the strongest actual local form currently available for the transport kernel
\[
V^\mu(\xi)\sim (\partial_\xi P_B)\,T^\mu
\]
inside the CP\(^2\) projector-defect sector, and identify the true load-bearing coefficients for the graded \(2+2\) mixed symbol.

\subsubsection{A. Actual local projector geometry}

Let the reflection-symmetric defect background be
\begin{equation}
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi),
\label{eq:zB_Tmu}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B(\xi)^\dagger.
\label{eq:PB_Tmu}
\end{equation}
The tangent fluctuation lives in the rank-two complex bundle
\begin{equation}
Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb Cz_B(\xi))^\perp.
\label{eq:QB_Tmu}
\end{equation}
An explicit orthonormal frame is
\begin{equation}
e_1(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_2(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\
1\\
0
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:e_frame_Tmu}
\end{equation}
In this frame the transverse connection vanishes:
\begin{equation}
A_\xi=-ie^\dagger\partial_\xi e=0.
\label{eq:Axi_Tmu}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Actual local gradient source}

Differentiating the background gives
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi z_B(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)e_1(\xi),
\label{eq:dzB_Tmu}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi P_B(\xi)
=
(\partial_\xi z_B)z_B^\dagger+z_B(\partial_\xi z_B)^\dagger
=
\theta'(\xi)\bigl(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger\bigr).
\label{eq:dPB_Tmu}
\end{equation}
Hence every leading local transport kernel built linearly from the background gradient is necessarily of the form
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:Vmu_Mmu_Tmu}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\) is a Hermitian endomorphism of the rank-two fiber \(Q_B\).

\subsubsection{C. Endomorphism algebra of the rank-two fiber}

Since \(Q_B(\xi)\) is complex rank \(2\), in the local frame \((e_1,e_2)\) one has
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Herm}(Q_B)\cong \mathrm{Herm}(2)
=
\mathbb R\,\mathbf 1_2\oplus \mathfrak{su}(2)_{\mathrm{Herm}}.
\label{eq:HermQB_Tmu}
\end{equation}
Thus the most general local Hermitian transport tensor is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)
=
a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2+a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i,
\qquad i=1,2,3,
\label{eq:Mmu_decomp_Tmu}
\end{equation}
with real coefficient functions \(a_0^\mu(\theta),a_i^\mu(\theta)\).

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl(
a_0^\mu(\theta(\xi))\mathbf 1_2+a_i^\mu(\theta(\xi))\sigma_i
\Bigr).
\label{eq:Vmu_final_Tmu}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{D. Projected mixed symbol}

Let the even/odd low modes be
\begin{equation}
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
a=1,2.
\label{eq:uapm_Tmu}
\end{equation}
Then the projected mixed matrices are
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\label{eq:Mmu_overlap_Tmu}
\end{equation}
Substituting \eqref{eq:Vmu_final_Tmu},
\begin{equation}
M^\mu
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl(
a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2+a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i
\Bigr).
\label{eq:Mmu_int_Tmu}
\end{equation}
Define
\begin{equation}
C_0^\mu
:=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,a_0^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:C0_Tmu}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C_i^\mu
:=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,a_i^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\label{eq:Ci_Tmu}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
M^\mu=C_0^\mu\,\mathbf 1_2+C_i^\mu\,\sigma_i.
\label{eq:Mmu_Ci_Tmu}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{E. Load-bearing data}

The mixed symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu
=
p_\mu C_0^\mu\,\mathbf 1_2+p_\mu C_i^\mu\,\sigma_i.
\label{eq:A1_Tmu}
\end{equation}
Because it is first-order in momentum,
\begin{equation}
A_1(0)=0,
\qquad
D_1(0)=0.
\label{eq:A1_zero_Tmu}
\end{equation}
Therefore the identity coefficient \(C_0^\mu\) is not a constant mass term.
The actual nondegeneracy data are the traceless coefficient vectors
\begin{equation}
b^\mu:=(C_1^\mu,C_2^\mu,C_3^\mu)\in\mathbb R^3.
\label{eq:bmu_Tmu}
\end{equation}
The exact criterion is
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{span}\{b^1,b^2,b^3\}=\mathbb R^3.
\label{eq:span_Tmu}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{F. Natural three-channel basis}

A canonical traceless Hermitian basis on \(Q_B\) is
\begin{equation}
\Sigma^{(1)}:=e_1e_2^\dagger+e_2e_1^\dagger,
\label{eq:Sigma1_Tmu}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\Sigma^{(2)}:=-ie_1e_2^\dagger+ie_2e_1^\dagger,
\label{eq:Sigma2_Tmu}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\Sigma^{(3)}:=e_1e_1^\dagger-e_2e_2^\dagger.
\label{eq:Sigma3_Tmu}
\end{equation}
In the local frame these are exactly \(\sigma_1,\sigma_2,\sigma_3\).
Therefore the actual local projector geometry naturally supplies exactly three traceless transport channels.

\subsubsection{G. Honest status}

What is genuinely derived from the actual local projector-defect geometry is:

\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\qquad
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)=a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2+a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i.
\label{eq:actual_local_status_Tmu}
\end{equation}
What is not yet derived from the final microscopic TECT PDE is the explicit formula for the coefficient functions
\[
a_i^\mu(\theta).
\]
Thus the remaining microscopic gap is coefficient extraction, not operator-class identification.

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\partial_\xi z_B=\theta'(\xi)e_1,
\qquad
\partial_\xi P_B=\theta'(\xi)(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger).
\]

Hence every leading local transport kernel built linearly from the defect gradient has the form
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\]

Because \(Q_B(\xi)\) is a complex rank-two bundle,
\[
\mathrm{Herm}(Q_B)\cong \mathbb R\,\mathbf 1_2\oplus \mathrm{span}\{\sigma_1,\sigma_2,\sigma_3\}.
\]
Therefore the most general local Hermitian transport tensor is
\[
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)=a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2+a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i.
\]

Projecting onto the graded low modes \(u_a^\pm=f_\pm e_a\) gives
\[
M^\mu
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl(
a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2+a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i
\Bigr)
=
C_0^\mu\mathbf 1_2+C_i^\mu\sigma_i.
\]

The mixed symbol is
\[
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu
=
p_\mu C_0^\mu\,\mathbf 1_2+p_\mu C_i^\mu\,\sigma_i,
\]
so
\[
A_1(0)=0.
\]
Thus \(C_0^\mu\) is not a constant mass term.

The actual load-bearing data are the traceless coefficient vectors
\[
b^\mu=(C_1^\mu,C_2^\mu,C_3^\mu)\in\mathbb R^3,
\]
and the exact nondegeneracy criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{span}\{b^1,b^2,b^3\}=\mathbb R^3.
}
\]

A canonical traceless basis is
\[
\Sigma^{(1)}=e_1e_2^\dagger+e_2e_1^\dagger,\qquad
\Sigma^{(2)}=-ie_1e_2^\dagger+ie_2e_1^\dagger,\qquad
\Sigma^{(3)}=e_1e_1^\dagger-e_2e_2^\dagger,
\]
which are exactly \(\sigma_1,\sigma_2,\sigma_3\) in the local frame.

So the actual local projector geometry naturally provides three independent traceless transport channels.
What remains open is the explicit microscopic extraction of the coefficient functions \(a_i^\mu(\theta)\) from the full TECT linearized projector equation.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{The strongest honest local form of the microscopic transport tensor \(T^\mu\)}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now derive the strongest local form currently justified for the transport kernel in the projector-defect sector, without overclaiming a full microscopic derivation from the final TECT PDE.

\subsubsection{A. Local projector-defect setting}

Let the defect background depend only on the transverse coordinate \(\xi\):
\begin{equation}
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B(\xi)^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B(\xi)^\dagger z_B(\xi)=1.
\label{eq:PB_local_strong}
\end{equation}
The physical fluctuation field is a section of the rank-two complex bundle
\begin{equation}
Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb Cz_B(\xi))^\perp.
\label{eq:QB_local_strong}
\end{equation}
Choose a local orthonormal frame
\begin{equation}
e(\xi)=\bigl(e_1(\xi),e_2(\xi)\bigr)
\label{eq:e_local_strong}
\end{equation}
for \(Q_B(\xi)\), and write
\begin{equation}
\eta(\xi,y)=e_a(\xi)\chi^a(\xi,y).
\label{eq:eta_frame_strong}
\end{equation}

For the explicit defect representative already used,
\begin{equation}
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi),
\label{eq:zB_theta_strong}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
e_1(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_2(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\
1\\
0
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:e1e2_theta_strong}
\end{equation}
one has
\begin{equation}
A_\xi:=-ie^\dagger\partial_\xi e=0.
\label{eq:Axi_zero_strong}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. General local form of the quadratic operator}

The local quadratic fluctuation operator on \(Q_B\) has the generic form
\begin{equation}
L
=
L_0
+
L_1
+
\cdots,
\label{eq:L_expand_strong}
\end{equation}
where

\begin{itemize}
\item \(L_0\) is the static transverse operator (matrix Schrödinger type),
\item \(L_1\) is the first-order worldvolume transport operator,
\item the omitted terms are higher order in the slow worldvolume gradients.
\end{itemize}

The graded reduction theorem only needs the first-order projected part of \(L_1\), not the full microscopic closed form of \(L\). This distinction is essential.

\subsubsection{C. Origin of the leading transport kernel}

At the local projector-defect level, the first-order worldvolume transport must be linear in:

\begin{enumerate}
\item one worldvolume derivative \(\partial_{y^\mu}\),
\item one background gradient tensor in the transverse direction.
\end{enumerate}

The only actual local odd building blocks available at lowest order are objects linear in
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi P_B,\qquad \partial_\xi z_B,\qquad \theta'(\xi).
\label{eq:odd_building_blocks_strong}
\end{equation}
Indeed, for the explicit profile,
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi z_B=\theta'(\xi)e_1,
\label{eq:dzB_strong}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi P_B
=
(\partial_\xi z_B)z_B^\dagger+z_B(\partial_\xi z_B)^\dagger
=
\theta'(\xi)\bigl(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger\bigr).
\label{eq:dPB_strong}
\end{equation}
Hence every leading local transport endomorphism is necessarily proportional to \(\theta'(\xi)\).

Therefore the strongest justified local form is
\begin{equation}
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\label{eq:Vmu_strong}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{D. Endomorphism-valued transport tensor}

Because \(Q_B(\xi)\) is complex rank \(2\), every Hermitian endomorphism of the fiber decomposes as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)
=
a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2
+
a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i,
\qquad
i=1,2,3,
\label{eq:Mmu_pauli_strong}
\end{equation}
with real coefficient functions \(a_0^\mu(\theta),a_i^\mu(\theta)\).

Thus the actual local transport kernel has the general form
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl[
