a_0^\mu(\theta(\xi))\mathbf 1_2
+
a_i^\mu(\theta(\xi))\sigma_i
\Bigr].
\label{eq:Vmu_final_strong}
\end{equation}

This is the strongest honest local parametrization of the microscopic transport tensor presently available.

\subsubsection{E. Projection to the graded \(2+2\) carrier}

Let the even/odd low modes be
\begin{equation}
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
a=1,2.
\label{eq:uapm_strong}
\end{equation}
Then the mixed symbol is
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\label{eq:Mmu_overlap_strong}
\end{equation}
Substituting \eqref{eq:Vmu_final_strong},
\begin{equation}
M^\mu
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl[
a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2+a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i
\Bigr].
\label{eq:Mmu_int_strong}
\end{equation}

Define
\begin{equation}
C_0^\mu
:=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,a_0^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:C0mu_strong}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C_i^\mu
:=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,a_i^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\label{eq:Cimu_strong}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
M^\mu=C_0^\mu\,\mathbf 1_2+C_i^\mu\,\sigma_i.
\label{eq:Mmu_C_strong}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{F. Why the identity part is not the load-bearing issue}

The reduced mixed symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu
=
p_\mu C_0^\mu\,\mathbf 1_2+p_\mu C_i^\mu\,\sigma_i.
\label{eq:A1_mixed_strong}
\end{equation}
Because this is first-order in momentum,
\begin{equation}
A_1(0)=0.
\label{eq:A1_zero_strong}
\end{equation}
So the identity contribution \(C_0^\mu\mathbf 1_2\) is not a constant mass term.
It belongs to the same first-order graded mixed symbol as the traceless part.

Hence the genuine nondegeneracy data are the traceless vectors
\begin{equation}
b^\mu:=(C_1^\mu,C_2^\mu,C_3^\mu)\in \mathbb R^3.
\label{eq:bmu_strong}
\end{equation}
The exact criterion is
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{span}\{b^1,b^2,b^3\}=\mathbb R^3.
\label{eq:span_bmu_strong}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{G. What is actually proved and what remains open}

What is actually proved at this point is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the actual local defect geometry forces the transport kernel to be of the form
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi));
\]

\item the transport tensor \(\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\) must be a \(Q_B\)-endomorphism-valued Hermitian matrix, hence admits the Pauli decomposition
\[
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)=a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2+a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i;
\]

\item the reduced Dirac criterion depends only on the projected traceless coefficient vectors \(b^\mu\).
\end{enumerate}

What remains open is the full microscopic coefficient extraction problem:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{derive the actual functions }a_i^\mu(\theta)\text{ from the final TECT linearized projector equation.}
}
\label{eq:open_coeff_problem}
\end{equation}

So the remaining frontier is no longer operator-class identification, parity, or graded reduction.
It is the actual coefficient computation.

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\partial_\xi z_B=\theta'(\xi)e_1,
\qquad
\partial_\xi P_B=\theta'(\xi)(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger).
\]

Therefore every leading local transport kernel built linearly from the defect gradient has the form
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\]

Because \(Q_B(\xi)\) is complex rank \(2\),
\[
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)=a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2+a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i.
\]

Projecting onto the graded low modes \(u_a^\pm=f_\pm e_a\) gives
\[
M^\mu
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl[a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2+a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i\Bigr]
=
C_0^\mu\mathbf 1_2+C_i^\mu\sigma_i.
\]

The mixed symbol is
\[
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu
=
p_\mu C_0^\mu\,\mathbf 1_2+p_\mu C_i^\mu\,\sigma_i,
\qquad
A_1(0)=0.
\]

Thus \(C_0^\mu\) is not a constant mass term.
The actual load-bearing data are the traceless coefficient vectors
\[
b^\mu=(C_1^\mu,C_2^\mu,C_3^\mu)\in\mathbb R^3,
\]
and the exact nondegeneracy criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{span}\{b^1,b^2,b^3\}=\mathbb R^3.
}
\]

So the strongest honest local result is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the actual local projector geometry fixes the transport kernel to be }Q_B\text{-endomorphism valued,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{and the remaining open problem is the explicit microscopic computation of }a_i^\mu(\theta).
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{A minimal microscopic ansatz for the projector transport equation}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now formulate a minimal microscopic ansatz for the full projector transport equation that is consistent with all previously established local structural results and reduces the remaining open problem to a finite coefficient test.

\subsubsection{A. Structural input already fixed}

The actual local CP\(^2\) projector-defect analysis establishes the following operator class:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the physical fluctuation field is a section
\begin{equation}
\eta(\xi,y)\in Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp,
\label{eq:eta_QB_ansatz}
\end{equation}

\item the static transverse Hessian is a matrix Schrödinger operator on the rank-two bundle \(Q_B\),

\item the leading worldvolume transport is first-order and odd under reflection,
\begin{equation}
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi),
\label{eq:L1_odd_ansatz}
\end{equation}

\item for the explicit defect representative
\begin{equation}
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi),
\label{eq:zB_def_ansatz}
\end{equation}
one has
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi z_B=\theta'(\xi)e_1,
\qquad
\partial_\xi P_B=\theta'(\xi)(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger),
\label{eq:dPB_theta_ansatz}
\end{equation}
so every leading local transport kernel linear in the defect gradient must factor through \(\theta'(\xi)\).
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the strongest local form already justified is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:Vmu_theta_Mmu_ansatz}
\end{equation}
with \(\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\in \mathrm{Herm}(Q_B)\).

\subsubsection{B. Minimal microscopic projector transport equation}

The minimal microscopic transport ansatz consistent with the above structure is
\begin{equation}
i\partial_t\eta
=
\Bigl[
-\rho\,\partial_\xi^2
+
U_B(\xi)
-
i\,\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi))\,\partial_{y^\mu}
\Bigr]\eta
+
O(\partial_y^2)\eta,
\label{eq:min_transport_equation}
\end{equation}
where \(U_B(\xi)\) is the static Hermitian \(2\times2\) transverse potential already fixed by the local projector Hessian.

This is not yet a derivation from the final full TECT PDE; it is the minimal microscopic ansatz compatible with all local structural theorems already proved.

\subsubsection{C. Pauli decomposition of the transport tensor}

In a local orthonormal \(Q_B\)-frame,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)
=
a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2
+
a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i,
\qquad
i=1,2,3.
\label{eq:Mmu_pauli_ansatz}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl[
a_0^\mu(\theta(\xi))\mathbf 1_2
+
a_i^\mu(\theta(\xi))\sigma_i
\Bigr].
\label{eq:Vmu_pauli_ansatz}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{D. Minimal even-\texorpdfstring{$\theta$}{theta} expansion}

Because the physical projector \(P_B\) is invariant under the local sign reversal \(\theta\mapsto -\theta\) up to equivalent background relabeling, the minimal scalar coefficient functions are naturally taken to be even in \(\theta\):
\begin{equation}
a_0^\mu(\theta)=\Lambda_0^{\ \mu}+O(\theta^2),
\label{eq:a0_expansion}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
a_i^\mu(\theta)=\Lambda_i^{\ \mu}+O(\theta^2).
\label{eq:ai_expansion}
\end{equation}
Thus, to leading order,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)=\Lambda_0^{\ \mu}\mathbf 1_2+\Lambda_i^{\ \mu}\sigma_i+O(\theta^2),
\label{eq:Mmu_Lambda}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl[
\Lambda_0^{\ \mu}\mathbf 1_2+\Lambda_i^{\ \mu}\sigma_i
\Bigr]
+
O(\theta^2\theta').
\label{eq:Vmu_Lambda}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{E. Projection to the graded \(2+2\) carrier}

Let the even/odd low modes be
\begin{equation}
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
a=1,2.
\label{eq:uapm_Lambda}
\end{equation}
Then the mixed overlap matrices are
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\label{eq:Mmu_overlap_Lambda}
\end{equation}
Substituting \eqref{eq:Vmu_Lambda},
\begin{equation}
M^\mu
=
I_\theta
\Bigl[
\Lambda_0^{\ \mu}\mathbf 1_2+\Lambda_i^{\ \mu}\sigma_i
\Bigr]
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
\label{eq:Mmu_Lambda_projected}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
I_\theta:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi).
\label{eq:Itheta_def_again}
\end{equation}
From the previous explicit computation,
\begin{equation}
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa.
\label{eq:Itheta_explicit_again}
\end{equation}
Hence \(I_\theta\neq 0\) whenever \(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0\).

\subsubsection{F. Reduced mixed symbol}

The projected first-order mixed symbol is therefore
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu
=
I_\theta\,p_\mu
\Bigl[
\Lambda_0^{\ \mu}\mathbf 1_2+\Lambda_i^{\ \mu}\sigma_i
\Bigr]
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa|p|).
\label{eq:A1_Lambda}
\end{equation}
The load-bearing traceless coefficient vectors are
\begin{equation}
b^\mu=
I_\theta\,
(\Lambda_1^{\ \mu},\Lambda_2^{\ \mu},\Lambda_3^{\ \mu})
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa).
\label{eq:bmu_Lambda}
\end{equation}

Thus, to leading order,
\begin{equation}
\det[b_i^{\ \mu}]
=
I_\theta^3\det[\Lambda_i^{\ \mu}]
+
O(\theta_0^5\kappa^3).
\label{eq:detb_Lambda}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Finite-dimensional reduction of the coefficient problem]
Assume the minimal transport ansatz \eqref{eq:min_transport_equation} and the even-\(\theta\) expansion \eqref{eq:ai_expansion}.
If
\begin{equation}
\det[\Lambda_i^{\ \mu}]\neq 0,
\label{eq:Lambda_fullrank}
\end{equation}
then for sufficiently small but nonzero defect amplitude \(\theta_0\),
\begin{equation}
\det[b_i^{\ \mu}]\neq 0,
\label{eq:b_fullrank_small_theta}
\end{equation}
and hence the graded reduced mixed symbol is nondegenerate.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
From \eqref{eq:bmu_Lambda} and \eqref{eq:Itheta_explicit_again}, the leading term in \(b^\mu\) is
\[
I_\theta(\Lambda_1^{\ \mu},\Lambda_2^{\ \mu},\Lambda_3^{\ \mu}),
\]
with \(I_\theta\neq 0\) for \(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0\).
Therefore
\[
\det[b_i^{\ \mu}]
=
I_\theta^3\det[\Lambda_i^{\ \mu}]
+
\text{higher-order corrections}.
\]
If \(\det[\Lambda_i^{\ \mu}]\neq 0\), then continuity implies the determinant remains nonzero for sufficiently small nonzero \(\theta_0\).
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{G. Canonical full-rank choice}

A canonical full-rank choice is
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_i^{\ \mu}=\lambda\,\delta_i^{\mu},
\qquad
\lambda\neq 0,
\label{eq:canonical_Lambda}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)=\lambda\,\sigma_\mu+O(\theta^2),
\label{eq:canonical_Mmu}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda I_\theta\,p_i\sigma_i
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa|p|).
\label{eq:canonical_A1}
\end{equation}
Hence the reduced principal operator is Dirac to leading order.

\subsubsection{H. Honest status}

What is now closed is not the exact coefficient extraction from the full TECT PDE, but a sharper reduction:

\[
\text{full microscopic coefficient problem}
\Longrightarrow
\text{determine the finite matrix }\Lambda_i^{\ \mu}.
\]

The remaining frontier is therefore:
derive the actual \(\Lambda_i^{\ \mu}\) from the final microscopic projector transport equation of TECT.

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
i\partial_t\eta
=
\Bigl[
-\rho\,\partial_\xi^2+U_B(\xi)
-i\,\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi))\partial_{y^\mu}
\Bigr]\eta
+O(\partial_y^2)\eta
\]
is the minimal microscopic projector transport ansatz compatible with the actual local CP\(^2\) defect geometry.

Write
\[
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)
=
a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2+a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i.
\]
Using the minimal even-\(\theta\) expansion,
\[
a_0^\mu(\theta)=\Lambda_0^{\ \mu}+O(\theta^2),
\qquad
a_i^\mu(\theta)=\Lambda_i^{\ \mu}+O(\theta^2),
\]
one gets
\[
V^\mu(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl[
\Lambda_0^{\ \mu}\mathbf 1_2+\Lambda_i^{\ \mu}\sigma_i
\Bigr]
+
O(\theta^2\theta').
\]

Projecting onto the graded low modes \(u_a^\pm=f_\pm e_a\),
\[
M^\mu
=
I_\theta
\Bigl[
\Lambda_0^{\ \mu}\mathbf 1_2+\Lambda_i^{\ \mu}\sigma_i
\Bigr]
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
\qquad
I_\theta=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\theta'
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa.
\]

Hence the reduced mixed symbol is
\[
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu
=
I_\theta\,p_\mu
\Bigl[
\Lambda_0^{\ \mu}\mathbf 1_2+\Lambda_i^{\ \mu}\sigma_i
\Bigr]
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa|p|).
\]

The load-bearing traceless vectors are
\[
b^\mu=
I_\theta(\Lambda_1^{\ \mu},\Lambda_2^{\ \mu},\Lambda_3^{\ \mu})
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa).
\]
Therefore
\[
\det[b_i^{\ \mu}]
=
I_\theta^3\det[\Lambda_i^{\ \mu}]
+
O(\theta_0^5\kappa^3).
\]

So if
\[
\boxed{
\det[\Lambda_i^{\ \mu}]\neq 0,
}
\]
then for sufficiently small nonzero \(\theta_0\),
\[
\boxed{
\det[b_i^{\ \mu}]\neq 0,
}
\]
and the graded reduced symbol is nondegenerate.

Thus the full microscopic coefficient problem has been reduced to the finite matrix problem of determining
\[
\Lambda_i^{\ \mu}.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Local symmetry classification of \texorpdfstring{$\Lambda_i{}^\mu$}{Lambda_i^mu}}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We classify which residual local symmetries force rank deficiency of the leading transport matrix
\[
\Lambda_i{}^\mu,
\]
and why full rank is the generic case once those extra symmetries are absent.

\subsubsection{A. Reduced coefficient problem}

From the minimal microscopic transport ansatz already derived,
\begin{equation}
i\partial_t\eta
=
\Bigl[
-\rho\,\partial_\xi^2+U_B(\xi)
-i\,\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi))\partial_{y^\mu}
\Bigr]\eta
+O(\partial_y^2)\eta,
\label{eq:transport_ansatz_sym}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)
=
a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2+a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i,
\label{eq:Mmu_expand_sym}
\end{equation}
the minimal even-\(\theta\) expansion gives
\begin{equation}
a_i^\mu(\theta)=\Lambda_i{}^\mu+O(\theta^2).
\label{eq:ai_Lambda_sym}
\end{equation}
Projecting onto the graded low modes,
\begin{equation}
b^\mu
=
I_\theta\,
(\Lambda_1{}^\mu,\Lambda_2{}^\mu,\Lambda_3{}^\mu)
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
\label{eq:bmu_Lambda_sym}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
I_\theta\neq 0
\qquad
(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0).
\label{eq:Itheta_nonzero_sym}
\end{equation}
Therefore the Dirac nondegeneracy problem reduces to the finite matrix condition
\begin{equation}
\det[\Lambda_i{}^\mu]\neq 0.
\label{eq:detLambda_condition}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Representation-theoretic meaning of \texorpdfstring{$\Lambda_i{}^\mu$}{Lambda_i^mu}}

The index \(i=1,2,3\) labels the three traceless Hermitian generators of \(\mathrm{End}(Q_B)\),
\[
\sigma_1,\sigma_2,\sigma_3,
\]
while \(\mu=1,2,3\) labels the three worldvolume derivative directions \(\partial_{y^\mu}\).
Hence
\begin{equation}
\Lambda:\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{wv}}\to \mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{tr}},
\qquad
(\Lambda p)_i=\Lambda_i{}^\mu p_\mu,
\label{eq:Lambda_map}
\end{equation}
is the linear map from worldvolume momentum space to the traceless transport space.

The mixed symbol is nondegenerate iff this map has full rank:
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{rank}\Lambda=3.
\label{eq:rankLambda3}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. Symmetry constraints that force rank deficiency}

A residual symmetry \(G\) acting simultaneously on the worldvolume directions and on the \(Q_B\)-fiber imposes the intertwining condition
\begin{equation}
R_{\mathrm{tr}}(g)\,\Lambda=\Lambda\,R_{\mathrm{wv}}(g),
\qquad
g\in G,
\label{eq:intertwiner_condition}
\end{equation}
where \(R_{\mathrm{wv}}\) is the representation on momentum directions and \(R_{\mathrm{tr}}\) is the representation on the traceless Hermitian fiber sector.

Rank deficiency occurs when this intertwining condition leaves only a proper invariant subspace.

\paragraph{Case 1: residual axial \(U(1)\) in the fiber.}
Suppose the local defect/transport structure preserves a distinguished internal axis, so that only \(\sigma_3\) is invariant and \((\sigma_1,\sigma_2)\) rotate as a doublet.
If the worldvolume representation has no matching doublet, then only
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_3{}^\mu
\end{equation}
can survive.
Hence
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{rank}\Lambda\le 1.
\label{eq:rank1_case}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Case 2: residual axial symmetry in physical space.}
Suppose a worldvolume axis is distinguished and the symmetry preserves only the longitudinal direction \(\mu=3\), while \((\mu=1,\mu=2)\) form a transverse doublet.
If the transport tensor couples only this distinguished direction to one fixed traceless channel, then
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_i{}^\mu
\sim
v_i\,n^\mu
\label{eq:rank1_tensor}
\end{equation}
is rank \(1\).

\paragraph{Case 3: planar symmetry.}
Suppose the symmetry preserves a two-dimensional plane and forbids coupling to the third direction. Then
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_i{}^\mu
=
\begin{pmatrix}
* & * & 0\\
* & * & 0\\
* & * & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:planar_form}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{rank}\Lambda\le 2.
\label{eq:rank2_case}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Case 4: mirror/reflection selection.}
If a reflection symmetry kills one odd transport direction \(\mu=\mu_0\), then the corresponding column of \(\Lambda\) vanishes:
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_i{}^{\mu_0}=0.
\label{eq:zero_column}
\end{equation}
Again
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{rank}\Lambda\le 2.
\label{eq:rank2_mirror}
\end{equation}

Thus:

\begin{theorem}[Symmetry-forced rank deficiency]
If a residual symmetry \(G\) constrains the intertwiner space
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_G(\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{wv}},\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{tr}})
\]
to lie in a proper algebraic subset of \(\mathrm{Mat}_{3\times 3}(\mathbb R)\), then \(\det\Lambda=0\) is forced.
In particular, any symmetry that preserves only one traceless channel or only one worldvolume direction forces \(\operatorname{rank}\Lambda\le 1\), and any symmetry that removes one worldvolume direction forces \(\operatorname{rank}\Lambda\le 2\).
\end{theorem}

\subsubsection{D. Why full rank is generic once those symmetries are absent}

Now assume there is no extra residual symmetry beyond:

\begin{enumerate}
\item reflection parity already used to construct the \(2+2\) grading,
\item Hermiticity of the transport tensor,
\item locality and first-order worldvolume transport.
\end{enumerate}

Then \(\Lambda\) is simply a real \(3\times3\) matrix with no further algebraic restriction.
The set of singular matrices
\begin{equation}
\mathcal S:=\{\Lambda\in \mathrm{Mat}_{3\times3}(\mathbb R):\det\Lambda=0\}
\label{eq:singular_set}
\end{equation}
is a proper algebraic hypersurface.
Hence its complement
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{GL}(3,\mathbb R)=\{\Lambda:\det\Lambda\neq 0\}
\label{eq:GL3}
\end{equation}
is open and dense.

Therefore:

\begin{theorem}[Generic full-rank criterion]
If no additional residual symmetry constrains \(\Lambda_i{}^\mu\) beyond the basic graded transport structure, then
\[
\det\Lambda\neq 0
\]
is the generic case.
Equivalently, rank deficiency is nongeneric and requires either symmetry or fine tuning.
\end{theorem}

\subsubsection{E. Consistency with the explicit full-rank representative}

The uploaded manuscript already gives an explicit full-rank point in the same operator class:
\begin{equation}
M^1=I_g\sigma_1,\qquad
M^2=I_g\sigma_2,\qquad
M^3=I_g\sigma_3,
\qquad
I_g\neq 0.
\label{eq:explicit_fullrank_point_sym}
\end{equation}
This corresponds exactly to
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_i{}^\mu=\lambda\,\delta_i^\mu
\label{eq:Lambda_delta}
\end{equation}
for some \(\lambda\neq 0\), up to normalization.
Thus the actual local operator class contains at least one point with
\begin{equation}
\det\Lambda\neq 0.
\label{eq:detLambda_nonzero_explicit}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

This proves there is no structural obstruction inside the operator class.

\subsubsection{F. Honest final status}

What is now closed is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the coefficient problem reduces to a finite real \(3\times3\) matrix \(\Lambda_i{}^\mu\);
\item symmetry-forced rank deficiency can be classified explicitly;
\item absent such extra symmetry, full rank is generic;
\item the actual local operator class already contains explicit full-rank representatives.
\end{enumerate}

What remains open is the strongest microscopic statement:
that the \emph{actual full TECT linearized projector transport equation} yields a specific \(\Lambda_i{}^\mu\) lying in the full-rank region.

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
a_i^\mu(\theta)=\Lambda_i{}^\mu+O(\theta^2),
\qquad
b^\mu
=
I_\theta(\Lambda_1{}^\mu,\Lambda_2{}^\mu,\Lambda_3{}^\mu)
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
\]
so the mixed symbol is nondegenerate iff
\[
\det[\Lambda_i{}^\mu]\neq 0.
\]

Here \(\Lambda\) is a linear map
\[
\Lambda:\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{wv}}\to \mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{tr}},
\]
from worldvolume momentum directions to the three traceless Hermitian transport channels \(\sigma_1,\sigma_2,\sigma_3\).

Rank deficiency is forced only when extra residual symmetry constrains the intertwiner space
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_G(\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{wv}},\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{tr}})
\]
to a proper subset. In particular:

\[
\text{one distinguished traceless axis } \Rightarrow \operatorname{rank}\Lambda\le 1,
\]
\[
\text{one forbidden worldvolume direction } \Rightarrow \operatorname{rank}\Lambda\le 2,
\]
\[
\text{planar or axial symmetry } \Rightarrow \det\Lambda=0.
\]

If no such additional residual symmetry is imposed, then \(\Lambda\) is just a real \(3\times3\) matrix, and
\[
\det\Lambda\neq 0
\]
is open and dense in \(\mathrm{Mat}_{3\times3}(\mathbb R)\).
So full rank is generic, and rank deficiency is nongeneric.

Moreover, the actual local operator class already contains an explicit full-rank point
\[
M^1=I_g\sigma_1,\qquad
M^2=I_g\sigma_2,\qquad
M^3=I_g\sigma_3,
\]
which corresponds to
\[
\Lambda_i{}^\mu\propto \delta_i^\mu.
\]

Therefore:
\[
\boxed{
\text{full rank of }\Lambda_i{}^\mu\text{ is not obstructed structurally;}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{it fails only if a special residual symmetry or fine tuning forces }\det\Lambda=0.
}
\]

\subsection{Why both branches must be analyzed: symmetry-forced rank deficiency versus generic full rank}

\paragraph{Claim.}
At the present stage, both possibilities for the transport matrix
\[
\Lambda_i{}^\mu
\]
must be analyzed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item residual-symmetry-forced rank deficiency,
\item generic full-rank behavior in the absence of extra symmetry.
\end{enumerate}

\subsubsection{A. Where the remaining problem has been reduced}

The strongest honest reduction already established in the manuscript is the following:

\begin{equation}
\text{graded low-energy sector}
+
\text{first-order odd reduced symbol}
+
\text{nondegenerate mixed }2\times2\text{ symbol}
\Longrightarrow
\text{Dirac operator}.
\label{eq:dirac_reduction_both}
\end{equation}

More precisely, the reduced operator has the form
\begin{equation}
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu,
\label{eq:D1_A1_both}
\end{equation}
and Dirac emergence depends on the nondegeneracy of \(A_1(p)\) for generic \(p\neq 0\). :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4} :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

In the local projector-defect reduction, this was further reduced to the finite coefficient problem
\begin{equation}
M^\mu=C_0^\mu\,\mathbf 1_2+C_i^\mu\,\sigma_i,
\qquad
b^\mu:=(C_1^\mu,C_2^\mu,C_3^\mu)\in\mathbb R^3,
\label{eq:Mmu_both}
\end{equation}
with exact nondegeneracy criterion
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{span}\{b^1,b^2,b^3\}=\mathbb R^3.
\label{eq:span_both}
\end{equation}

Under the minimal transport ansatz, one has
\begin{equation}
b^\mu
=
I_\theta\,(\Lambda_1{}^\mu,\Lambda_2{}^\mu,\Lambda_3{}^\mu)
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
\label{eq:bmu_Lambda_both}
\end{equation}
so the remaining finite-dimensional problem is
\begin{equation}
\det[\Lambda_i{}^\mu]\neq 0\quad ?
\label{eq:detLambda_question}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Why symmetry-forced rank deficiency must be tested}

A residual local symmetry \(G\) acting on worldvolume directions and on the traceless transport channels imposes the intertwining condition
\begin{equation}
R_{\mathrm{tr}}(g)\,\Lambda=\Lambda\,R_{\mathrm{wv}}(g),
\qquad
g\in G.
\label{eq:intertwiner_both}
\end{equation}
This can force \(\Lambda\) to lie in a proper linear or algebraic subspace of \(\mathrm{Mat}_{3\times3}(\mathbb R)\).

Typical possibilities are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Single distinguished traceless axis:}
only one Pauli channel survives, so
\[
\operatorname{rank}\Lambda\le 1.
\]

\item \textbf{One forbidden worldvolume direction:}
one column vanishes, so
\[
\operatorname{rank}\Lambda\le 2.
\]

\item \textbf{Axial or planar symmetry:}
the map \(\Lambda\) is forced to preserve a proper subspace, hence
\[
\det\Lambda=0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Therefore symmetry-forced rank deficiency is a genuine possibility, not a negligible corner case.

\subsubsection{C. Why generic full rank must also be tested}

On the other hand, if no additional residual symmetry survives beyond the basic parity/grading structure already used in the construction, then \(\Lambda\) is simply a real \(3\times3\) matrix.
The set of singular matrices
\begin{equation}
\mathcal S=\{\Lambda\in\mathrm{Mat}_{3\times3}(\mathbb R):\det\Lambda=0\}
\label{eq:singular_set_both}
\end{equation}
is a proper algebraic hypersurface, while
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{GL}(3,\mathbb R)=\{\Lambda:\det\Lambda\neq 0\}
\label{eq:GL3_both}
\end{equation}
is open and dense.

Hence, absent extra symmetry or fine tuning,
\begin{equation}
\det\Lambda\neq 0
\label{eq:generic_nonzero_det}
\end{equation}
is the generic case.

Moreover, the manuscript already exhibits an explicit full-rank point in the same operator class:
\begin{equation}
M^1=I_g\sigma_1,\qquad
M^2=I_g\sigma_2,\qquad
M^3=I_g\sigma_3,
\qquad
I_g\neq 0,
\label{eq:fullrank_point_both}
\end{equation}
which corresponds to
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_i{}^\mu\propto \delta_i^\mu.
\label{eq:Lambda_delta_both}
\end{equation}
So there is no structural obstruction to full rank inside the actual local operator class. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\subsubsection{D. Why both branches are logically necessary}

The open microscopic task is to determine which case is realized by the actual TECT defect/projector transport kernel.
That requires answering two logically distinct questions:

\begin{equation}
\text{Q1: Does the actual microscopic background preserve an extra residual symmetry forcing }\det\Lambda=0?
\label{eq:Q1_both}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\text{Q2: If not, does the actual microscopic coefficient lie in the generic full-rank region } \det\Lambda\neq 0?
\label{eq:Q2_both}
\end{equation}

Without answering Q1, an appeal to genericity is not rigorous.
Without answering Q2, ruling out special symmetry does not itself prove nondegeneracy.

Therefore both branches must be checked.

\subsubsection{E. Operational consequence}

The remaining microscopic problem is thus not merely:

\[
\text{compute }\Lambda,
\]
but rather the two-step program
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(i) classify the residual symmetry of the actual defect/projector background;}
}
\label{eq:step1_both}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(ii) within the allowed intertwiner space, determine whether the actual }\Lambda\text{ is full rank.}
}
\label{eq:step2_both}
\end{equation}

This is exactly consistent with the manuscript's current strongest honest status:
the theorem-level architecture is closed, and what remains is a finite list of explicit microscopic spectral / coefficient checks. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu,
\qquad
M^\mu=C_0^\mu\mathbf 1_2+C_i^\mu\sigma_i,
\qquad
b^\mu=(C_1^\mu,C_2^\mu,C_3^\mu).
\]
The exact nondegeneracy criterion is
\[
\mathrm{span}\{b^1,b^2,b^3\}=\mathbb R^3.

Under the minimal transport reduction,
\[
b^\mu
=
I_\theta(\Lambda_1{}^\mu,\Lambda_2{}^\mu,\Lambda_3{}^\mu)
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
\]
so the remaining finite-dimensional test is
\[
\det[\Lambda_i{}^\mu]\neq 0.
\]

There are two logically distinct possibilities:

\[
\text{(A) residual symmetry forces }\det\Lambda=0,

\text{(B) no such symmetry remains, so }\det\Lambda\neq 0\text{ is generic.}

Residual symmetry can force rank deficiency by preserving only:

\[
\text{one traceless channel} \Rightarrow \operatorname{rank}\Lambda\le 1,
\]
\[
\text{one or two worldvolume directions} \Rightarrow \operatorname{rank}\Lambda\le 2,
\]
\[
\text{axial/planar invariant subspaces} \Rightarrow \det\Lambda=0.
\]

But if no additional residual symmetry survives, then \(\Lambda\in\mathrm{Mat}_{3\times3}(\mathbb R)\) is generic, and
\[
\det\Lambda\neq 0
\]
is open and dense.

Therefore both questions must be checked:

\boxed{
\text{(1) does the actual microscopic background leave an extra residual symmetry?}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{(2) if not, is the actual }\Lambda\text{ in the full-rank region?}
}
\]

So yes:

\boxed{

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Residual symmetry classification of the actual defect/projector background}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We classify the residual symmetry of the explicit local CP\(^2\) defect background and determine when it forces rank deficiency of
\[
\Lambda_i{}^\mu,
\]
and when it still allows a full-rank Dirac symbol.

\subsubsection{A. Explicit local defect background and the distinguished internal axis}

Consider the explicit reflection-symmetric local defect representative
\begin{equation}
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi),
\label{eq:zB_residual}
\end{equation}
with the local \(Q_B\)-frame
\begin{equation}
e_1(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_2(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\
1\\
0
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:e1e2_residual}
\end{equation}
Since
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi z_B(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)e_1(\xi),
\label{eq:dzB_residual}
\end{equation}
the background gradient singles out the \(e_1\)-direction inside the rank-two fiber \(Q_B\).
Thus the full \(U(2)\) fiber symmetry of \(Q_B\) is generically broken by the defect gradient.

\paragraph{Residual fiber symmetry.}
The subgroup of \(U(2)\) preserving both the decomposition
\[
Q_B=\mathbb C e_1\oplus \mathbb C e_2
\]
and the distinguished real direction \(e_1\) is the phase rotation of \(e_2\):
\begin{equation}
U(1)_{\mathrm{res}}:\qquad
e_1\mapsto e_1,\qquad
e_2\mapsto e^{i\varphi}e_2.
\label{eq:U1_residual}
\end{equation}
In the \((e_1,e_2)\) frame, this acts by
\begin{equation}
R_{\mathrm{fib}}(\varphi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
1 & 0\\
0 & e^{i\varphi}
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:Rfib}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Action on the traceless Hermitian channels}

The traceless Hermitian basis of \(\mathrm{End}(Q_B)\) is
\begin{equation}
\Sigma^{(1)}=\sigma_1,\qquad
\Sigma^{(2)}=\sigma_2,\qquad
\Sigma^{(3)}=\sigma_3.
\label{eq:Sigma_pauli_residual}
\end{equation}
Under \(U(1)_{\mathrm{res}}\),
\begin{equation}
R_{\mathrm{fib}}(\varphi)\,\sigma_3\,R_{\mathrm{fib}}(\varphi)^{-1}
=
\sigma_3,
\label{eq:sigma3_invariant}
\end{equation}
while
\begin{equation}
R_{\mathrm{fib}}(\varphi)\,\sigma_1\,R_{\mathrm{fib}}(\varphi)^{-1}
=
(\cos\varphi)\sigma_1+(\sin\varphi)\sigma_2,
\label{eq:sigma1_rotate}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
R_{\mathrm{fib}}(\varphi)\,\sigma_2\,R_{\mathrm{fib}}(\varphi)^{-1}
=
-(\sin\varphi)\sigma_1+(\cos\varphi)\sigma_2.
\label{eq:sigma2_rotate}
\end{equation}
Thus the traceless transport space decomposes as
\begin{equation}
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathbb R\,\sigma_3
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{\sigma_1,\sigma_2\},
\label{eq:tr_split_residual}
\end{equation}
i.e. one invariant singlet plus one real two-dimensional rotation doublet.

\subsubsection{C. Two logically distinct symmetry branches}

Let
\begin{equation}
\Lambda:\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{wv}}\to \mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{tr}}
\label{eq:Lambda_map_residual}
\end{equation}
be the transport matrix in the leading reduced symbol. The allowed \(\Lambda\) must satisfy the intertwining condition
\begin{equation}
R_{\mathrm{tr}}(g)\,\Lambda=\Lambda\,R_{\mathrm{wv}}(g),
\qquad g\in G_{\mathrm{res}}.
\label{eq:intertwiner_residual}
\end{equation}
Now there are two different possibilities depending on the actual action \(R_{\mathrm{wv}}\) on worldvolume directions.

\paragraph{Branch S1: internal \(U(1)_{\mathrm{res}}\) survives, but there is no matching doublet on worldvolume momentum.}
Suppose the worldvolume representation is trivial or contains only singlets under the same symmetry. Then the doublet
\[
\mathrm{span}\{\sigma_1,\sigma_2\}
\]
has no matching source, and only the invariant channel \(\sigma_3\) is allowed.
Hence
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_i{}^\mu
=
v^\mu\,\delta_{i3},
\label{eq:rank1_form}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{rank}\Lambda\le 1.
\label{eq:rank1_result}
\end{equation}
This branch forces rank deficiency.

\paragraph{Branch S2: matched doublet symmetry.}
Suppose instead the worldvolume directions decompose under the residual symmetry as
\begin{equation}
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{wv}}
=
\mathbb R\,p_\parallel
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{p_1,p_2\},
\label{eq:wv_split}
\end{equation}
with \(p_\parallel\) a singlet and \((p_1,p_2)\) a doublet.
Then the intertwiner condition allows:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a singlet-to-singlet map
\[
p_\parallel \longmapsto \sigma_3,
\]

\item a doublet-to-doublet map
\[
(p_1,p_2)\longmapsto
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the most general symmetry-allowed mixed symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:A1_axial_form}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\Lambda=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha & -\beta & 0\\
\beta & \alpha & 0\\
0 & 0 & \lambda_\parallel
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:Lambda_axial_form}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\det\Lambda=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2).
\label{eq:detLambda_axial}
\end{equation}
Thus this branch is full rank iff
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:axial_nonzero_condition}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{D. Interpretation}

So the same residual \(U(1)\) can lead to two different outcomes:

\begin{enumerate}
\item if it acts only on the fiber and has no matching worldvolume doublet, it forces rank deficiency;
\item if the worldvolume derivative sector carries the matching singlet \(\oplus\) doublet decomposition, it still allows full-rank Dirac form.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore one must not say merely ``a residual \(U(1)\) survives''.
One must specify the pair of representations
\[
(R_{\mathrm{wv}},R_{\mathrm{tr}}).
\]

\subsubsection{E. Which branch is more natural for the actual defect geometry?}

For the explicit defect background, the most natural worldvolume decomposition is precisely
\[
\text{one distinguished direction }p_\parallel
\quad+\quad
\text{a transverse two-plane }(p_1,p_2),
\]
because the defect gradient selects one local axis while the worldvolume tangential derivatives naturally split into longitudinal and transverse parts relative to that axis.

On the transport side, the actual local \(Q_B\)-endomorphism algebra already splits as
\[
\mathbb R\,\sigma_3\oplus \mathrm{span}\{\sigma_1,\sigma_2\}.
\]
Hence the matched-doublet branch \eqref{eq:A1_axial_form} is the natural symmetry-compatible realization.

This is exactly consistent with the explicit full-rank realization already exhibited in the same operator class,
\begin{equation}
M^1=I_g\sigma_1,\qquad
M^2=I_g\sigma_2,\qquad
M^3=I_g\sigma_3,
\label{eq:explicit_fullrank_residual}
\end{equation}
which shows there is no structural obstruction to full rank. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\subsubsection{F. Honest conclusion}

What is now actually classified is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Residual symmetry does \emph{not} automatically force rank deficiency.}
}
\]

Instead:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{rank deficiency occurs only when the residual fiber symmetry has no matching worldvolume doublet.}
}
\label{eq:rankdef_only_nomatch}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{if a matched singlet}\oplus\text{doublet structure exists, then the symmetry-allowed form is }
A_1(p)=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
}
\label{eq:matched_branch_box}
\end{equation}
which is full rank iff
\[
\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2)\neq 0.
\]

So the next microscopic question is no longer
\[
\text{``Is there residual symmetry?''}
\]
but rather
\[
\text{``Which representation pair }(R_{\mathrm{wv}},R_{\mathrm{tr}})\text{ is realized by the actual TECT transport kernel?''}
\]

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
Q_B=\mathbb C e_1\oplus \mathbb C e_2,
\qquad
\partial_\xi z_B=\theta' e_1,
\]
so the defect gradient singles out \(e_1\) in the rank-two fiber.
The residual fiber symmetry is therefore
\[
U(1)_{\mathrm{res}}:\quad e_1\mapsto e_1,\qquad e_2\mapsto e^{i\varphi}e_2.
\]

On the traceless Hermitian transport channels,
\[
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathbb R\,\sigma_3
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{\sigma_1,\sigma_2\},
\]
with \(\sigma_3\) invariant and \((\sigma_1,\sigma_2)\) rotating as a doublet.

This leads to two distinct branches:

\[
\text{(S1) no matching worldvolume doublet}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\Lambda_i{}^\mu=v^\mu\delta_{i3},
\quad
\operatorname{rank}\Lambda\le 1.
\]

\[
\text{(S2) matched singlet}\oplus\text{doublet on worldvolume}
\]
\[
\Longrightarrow\quad
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\]
equivalently
\[
\Lambda=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha & -\beta & 0\\
\beta & \alpha & 0\\
0 & 0 & \lambda_\parallel
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\det\Lambda=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2).
\]

Hence residual symmetry by itself does not force rank deficiency.
It forces rank deficiency only if the residual fiber symmetry has no matching worldvolume doublet.

If the matched singlet\(\oplus\)doublet structure is realized, then the symmetry-allowed mixed symbol is already of Weyl/Dirac type, and it is full rank iff
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad (\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

So the real microscopic question is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{which representation pair }(R_{\mathrm{wv}},R_{\mathrm{tr}})\text{ is realized by the actual TECT transport kernel?}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Why the matched singlet\(\oplus\)doublet branch S2 is the natural local realization}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We determine which of the two residual-symmetry branches is more natural for the actual local TECT projector-defect background:

\[
\text{S1: residual fiber symmetry without a matching worldvolume doublet},
\]
\[
\text{S2: matched singlet}\oplus\text{doublet decomposition on both sides}.
\]

\subsubsection{A. Local defect geometry already singles out one distinguished axis}

For the explicit local defect representative
\begin{equation}
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi),
\label{eq:zB_S2}
\end{equation}
one has
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi z_B(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)e_1(\xi),
\label{eq:dzB_S2}
\end{equation}
so the defect gradient selects the \(e_1\)-direction in the rank-two fiber \(Q_B\).
Thus the local fiber symmetry is reduced from the full \(U(2)\) to a residual axial subgroup preserving the decomposition
\[
Q_B=\mathbb C e_1\oplus \mathbb C e_2.
\]

In the local frame, the traceless Hermitian fiber sector decomposes as
\begin{equation}
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathbb R\,\sigma_3
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{\sigma_1,\sigma_2\},
\label{eq:tr_split_S2}
\end{equation}
where \(\sigma_3\) is the distinguished singlet and \((\sigma_1,\sigma_2)\) form a doublet under the residual \(U(1)\) rotation. This is exactly the standard axial decomposition of the traceless transport channels.

\subsubsection{B. The worldvolume side naturally has the same singlet\(\oplus\)doublet decomposition}

The first-order transport term in the microscopic TECT linearization is
\begin{equation}
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\label{eq:L1_S2}
\end{equation}
with worldvolume coordinates \(y^\mu=(t,x^1,x^2)\) in the local defect reduction. 

Once the defect gradient selects a local distinguished axis, the worldvolume momentum directions naturally split into:

\begin{equation}
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{wv}}
=
\mathbb R\,p_\parallel
\oplus
E_\perp,
\qquad
E_\perp=\mathrm{span}\{p_1,p_2\}.
\label{eq:wv_split_S2}
\end{equation}

Thus the worldvolume side also carries a singlet \(\oplus\) doublet decomposition:
\[
p_\parallel \quad \text{(singlet)}, \qquad (p_1,p_2)\quad \text{(doublet)}.
\]

So the local defect geometry itself already supplies the matching representation pattern required for S2.

\subsubsection{C. Symmetry-compatible intertwiner space}

Let
\[
\Lambda:\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{wv}}\to \mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{tr}}
\]
be the leading transport map.
Under the matched residual axial symmetry, both domain and codomain decompose as
\[
\mathbb R\oplus \mathbb R^2.
\]
Therefore the intertwiner space contains:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a singlet-to-singlet map
\[
p_\parallel\longmapsto \sigma_3,
\]

\item the full equivariant algebra on the transverse doublet plane
\[
E_\perp\to \mathrm{span}\{\sigma_1,\sigma_2\},
\]
which is spanned by the identity and the planar complex structure \(J\).
\end{enumerate}

This is exactly the minimal axial tensor basis already derived in the microscopic Weyl witness analysis:
\[
P_\parallel=\hat n\hat n,\qquad
P_\perp,\qquad
J_{ij}=\epsilon_{ijk}\hat n_k.
\]
Restricted to the transverse plane, \(\{P_\perp,J\}\) spans the full algebra of equivariant endomorphisms. 

Hence the most general symmetry-compatible reduced mixed symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:A1_S2_form}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\Lambda=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha & -\beta & 0\\
\beta & \alpha & 0\\
0 & 0 & \lambda_\parallel
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:Lambda_S2_form}
\end{equation}
with determinant
\begin{equation}
\det\Lambda=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2).
\label{eq:detLambda_S2}
\end{equation}

Thus the S2 branch is not merely possible; it is exactly the natural symmetry-compatible branch once the defect geometry splits both sides into singlet\(\oplus\)doublet sectors.

\subsubsection{D. Why S1 is less natural locally}

S1 would require that the residual fiber symmetry survives, but the worldvolume derivative sector carries no matching doublet. In that case only the invariant singlet channel survives:
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)\sim p_\parallel \sigma_3,
\label{eq:A1_S1_form}
\end{equation}
so
\[
\operatorname{rank}\Lambda\le 1.
\]

However, in the actual local defect reduction, the worldvolume derivative sector automatically contains the transverse two-plane \(E_\perp\), and the local transport operator \(L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\) acts on all worldvolume directions.
Therefore S1 is not the generic local outcome; it would require an additional symmetry or truncation that suppresses the transverse doublet coupling.

So:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{S1 is possible only after an additional restriction; it is not the natural branch of the local defect geometry.}
}
\label{eq:S1_not_natural}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{E. Consistency with the explicit full-rank realization}

The manuscript already constructs an explicit full-rank point in the same operator class:
\begin{equation}
M^1=I_g\sigma_1,\qquad
M^2=I_g\sigma_2,\qquad
M^3=I_g\sigma_3,
\qquad
I_g\neq 0.
\label{eq:explicit_point_S2}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the isotropic special case of the S2 branch:
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=I_g,\qquad
\alpha=I_g,\qquad
\beta=0.
\label{eq:isotropic_S2}
\end{equation}
Hence the local operator class already contains an explicit S2 full-rank realization. 

\subsubsection{F. Honest conclusion}

The strongest honest local conclusion is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The actual defect/worldvolume decomposition naturally realizes the matched singlet}\oplus\text{doublet branch S2.}
}
\label{eq:S2_natural_box}
\end{equation}

At the same time:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{This still does not prove that the final full microscopic TECT transport kernel must land in the full-rank region.}
}
\label{eq:full_micro_open_S2}
\end{equation}

What it proves is that, at the local defect/projector level, S2 is the geometrically natural branch, while S1 requires extra symmetry or truncation beyond the local defect geometry itself.

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\partial_\xi z_B=\theta' e_1
\]
singles out one distinguished fiber direction \(e_1\), so the local traceless transport sector splits as
\[
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathbb R\,\sigma_3
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{\sigma_1,\sigma_2\}.
\]

At the same time, the local defect/worldvolume momentum directions split naturally as
\[
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{wv}}
=
\mathbb R\,p_\parallel
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{p_1,p_2\}.
\]

Therefore the actual local defect geometry naturally supplies a matched singlet\(\oplus\)doublet decomposition on both sides.

The corresponding symmetry-compatible mixed symbol is
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\]
equivalently
\[
\Lambda=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha & -\beta & 0\\
\beta & \alpha & 0\\
0 & 0 & \lambda_\parallel
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\det\Lambda=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2).
\]

Hence the matched branch S2 is full rank iff
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad (\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

By contrast, the rank-deficient branch S1 would require that the residual fiber symmetry has no matching worldvolume doublet, so only
\[
A_1(p)\sim p_\parallel \sigma_3
\]
survives.
This is not the natural outcome of the local defect/worldvolume decomposition; it would require an additional symmetry or truncation.

Therefore:
\[
\boxed{
\text{S2 is the geometrically natural local branch, while S1 is an additional restricted branch.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Actual residual symmetry diagnosis: the local defect geometry allows S2 and does not force S1}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We determine, using only the actually established local CP\(^2\) defect/projector geometry, whether the residual symmetry forces the rank-deficient branch S1, or whether it allows the matched singlet\(\oplus\)doublet branch S2.

\subsubsection{A. Actual local operator class already fixed}

From the local projector-Hessian analysis around a reflection-symmetric defect background, the following are already established:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the fluctuation field is a complex doublet on the rank-two bundle
\begin{equation}
Q_B=(\mathbb Cz_B)^\perp,
\label{eq:QB_actual_diag}
\end{equation}

\item the static Hessian is a transverse matrix Schrödinger operator on \(Q_B\),

\item even/odd low channels \(f_+,f_-\) arise under reflection symmetry,

\item the leading worldvolume transport kernel is odd,
\begin{equation}
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi),
\label{eq:L1_actual_diag}
\end{equation}

\item same-parity overlaps vanish, while the mixed overlap block is generically nonzero:
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\, f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\label{eq:Mmixed_actual_diag}
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}

This is the exact local matching theorem for the CP\(^2\) projector Hessian operator class.

\subsubsection{B. Residual fiber symmetry of the explicit defect background}

Take the explicit local representative
\begin{equation}
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi).
\label{eq:zB_actual_diag}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi z_B(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)e_1(\xi),
\label{eq:dzB_actual_diag}
\end{equation}
so the defect gradient singles out one preferred direction \(e_1\) in the rank-two fiber \(Q_B\).

Thus the full \(U(2)\) fiber symmetry is reduced to a residual axial subgroup preserving the decomposition
\[
Q_B=\mathbb C e_1\oplus \mathbb C e_2.
\]
On the traceless Hermitian sector this gives the splitting
\begin{equation}
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathbb R\,\sigma_3
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{\sigma_1,\sigma_2\},
\label{eq:tr_split_actual_diag}
\end{equation}
where \(\sigma_3\) is a singlet and \((\sigma_1,\sigma_2)\) transform as a doublet under the residual \(U(1)\).

\subsubsection{C. Worldvolume side also has a natural singlet\(\oplus\)doublet split}

The same local defect geometry also singles out a distinguished worldvolume direction associated with the defect-gradient axis.
Hence the worldvolume momentum space naturally decomposes as
\begin{equation}
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{wv}}
=
\mathbb R\,p_\parallel
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{p_1,p_2\}.
\label{eq:wv_split_actual_diag}
\end{equation}
So the worldvolume representation has the same singlet\(\oplus\)doublet pattern as the traceless fiber transport sector:
\[
p_\parallel
\leftrightarrow
\sigma_3,
\qquad
(p_1,p_2)
\leftrightarrow
(\sigma_1,\sigma_2).
\]

This means the local geometry itself provides the matched representation pattern needed for S2.

\subsubsection{D. The symmetry-allowed mixed symbol is exactly S2}

When the singlet\(\oplus\)doublet decompositions match on both sides, the intertwiner space allows:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a singlet-to-singlet map
\[
p_\parallel \mapsto \sigma_3,
\]

\item the full two-parameter equivariant map from the transverse worldvolume doublet to the transverse Pauli doublet.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the most general symmetry-allowed mixed symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:S2_actual_form}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\Lambda=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha & -\beta & 0\\
\beta & \alpha & 0\\
0 & 0 & \lambda_\parallel
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:Lambda_S2_actual}
\end{equation}
with determinant
\begin{equation}
\det\Lambda=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2).
\label{eq:detLambda_S2_actual}
\end{equation}

Thus S2 is not only possible; it is exactly the symmetry-compatible branch selected by the natural local singlet\(\oplus\)doublet decomposition.

\subsubsection{E. Why S1 is not forced by the actual local geometry}

S1 would mean that only the invariant singlet survives:
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)\sim p_\parallel \sigma_3,
\label{eq:S1_actual_form}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{rank}\Lambda\le 1.
\label{eq:rank1_actual_diag}
\end{equation}
But this requires the transverse worldvolume doublet \((p_1,p_2)\) to fail to couple to the transverse Pauli doublet \((\sigma_1,\sigma_2)\).

The actual local defect geometry by itself does not enforce such a decoupling.
It already contains:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a transverse two-plane in worldvolume momentum space,
\item a transverse two-plane in the traceless fiber transport sector,
\item a mixed overlap formula with generically nonzero off-diagonal block.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore S1 is not the default local outcome.
To realize S1 one needs an additional restriction beyond the basic defect geometry, such as:

\begin{enumerate}
\item an extra mirror or axial symmetry killing one or both transverse channels,
\item an additional truncation that removes the worldvolume doublet,
\item or special fine tuning of the transport coefficients.
\end{enumerate}

\subsubsection{F. Consistency with the manuscript's symmetry theorem}

The manuscript's reduced symmetry theorem already gives the precise logic:

\begin{enumerate}
\item symmetry forbids inequivalent mixed linear terms,
\item symmetry allows the longitudinal scalar term \(v_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3\),
\item symmetry allows the transverse doublet term \(p_aT_{ab}\sigma_b\) whenever the two doublets are representation-equivalent,
\item symmetry alone does not force \(v_\parallel\neq 0\) or \(\det T\neq 0\).
\end{enumerate}

So symmetry is a reduction theorem, not a nondegeneracy theorem.
This is exactly what the local defect analysis is showing here as well.

\subsubsection{G. Explicit full-rank point in the same actual operator class}

The same local operator class already contains an explicit full-rank point:
\begin{equation}
M^1=I_g\sigma_1,\qquad
M^2=I_g\sigma_2,\qquad
M^3=I_g\sigma_3,
\qquad
I_g\neq 0.
\label{eq:explicit_fullrank_actual_diag}
\end{equation}
This is simply the isotropic special point of the S2 family.
Therefore there is no structural obstruction inside the actual local defect/operator class to full rank.

\subsubsection{H. Honest conclusion}

The strongest honest local conclusion is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The actual local defect/projector geometry is naturally compatible with S2.}
}
\label{eq:S2_honest_local}
\end{equation}

At the same time:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{S1 is not forced by local geometry; it requires an additional symmetry, truncation, or fine tuning.}
}
\label{eq:S1_requires_extra}
\end{equation}

And finally:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{This still does not prove that the full microscopic TECT transport kernel lands in the full-rank region.}
}
\label{eq:full_micro_still_open}
\end{equation}

So the remaining microscopic task is to determine the actual coefficients \((\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)\) of the S2 branch in the full theory.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\partial_\xi z_B=\theta' e_1
\]
singles out one preferred fiber direction, so the traceless transport sector splits as
\[
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{tr}}
=

\oplus

At the same time, the actual defect/worldvolume momentum directions split naturally as

\mathbb R\,p_\parallel
\oplus

Thus the local defect geometry naturally provides a matched singlet\(\oplus\)doublet decomposition on both sides.
The corresponding symmetry-compatible mixed symbol is

A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),

equivalently

\Lambda=
\begin{pmatrix}

\subsection{Actual local formulas for the S2 two-witness condition}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now write the actual local formulas for the S2-branch witnesses
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0),
\]
directly in terms of the projected local transport kernel of the CP\(^2\) projector defect.

\subsubsection{A. Projected mixed transport matrices}

For a reflection-symmetric defect background, the leading transport term is
\begin{equation}
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\label{eq:L1_S2_local}
\end{equation}
with odd kernel \(V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi)\).
Projecting onto the graded low modes
\begin{equation}
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
a=1,2,
\label{eq:uapm_S2_local}
\end{equation}
gives
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\label{eq:Mmu_projected_S2_local}
\end{equation}

The strongest honest local transport form already obtained is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:Vmu_theta_S2_local}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)
=
a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2+a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i.
\label{eq:Mmu_pauli_S2_local}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
M^\mu
=
\int d\xi\,
f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl[
a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2+a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i
\Bigr].
\label{eq:Mmu_integral_S2_local}
\end{equation}

Write
\begin{equation}
M^\mu
=
A^\mu \mathbf 1_2+B_i^\mu \sigma_i,
\label{eq:Mmu_AB_S2_local}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
A^\mu
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,a_0^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:Amu_def_S2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
B_i^\mu
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,a_i^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\label{eq:Bimu_def_S2}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Singlet\(\oplus\)doublet decomposition of the S2 branch}

In the S2 branch, the worldvolume momentum directions split as
\begin{equation}
p=(p_1,p_2,p_\parallel)
\in
2_\perp\oplus 1_\parallel,
\label{eq:p_split_S2}
\end{equation}
while the traceless transport sector splits as
\begin{equation}
(\sigma_1,\sigma_2)\oplus \sigma_3.
\label{eq:sigma_split_S2}
\end{equation}

The most general symmetry-compatible S2 mixed symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\label{eq:A1_S2_template}
\end{equation}
equivalently
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
p_\mu B_i^\mu \sigma_i
\quad\text{with}\quad
\Lambda=
\begin{pmatrix}
B_1^1 & B_1^2 & B_1^\parallel\\
B_2^1 & B_2^2 & B_2^\parallel\\
B_3^1 & B_3^2 & B_3^\parallel
\end{pmatrix}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha & -\beta & 0\\
\beta & \alpha & 0\\
0 & 0 & \lambda_\parallel
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:Lambda_S2_template}
\end{equation}

Thus the S2 coefficients are read off from the projected traceless matrices as
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=B_3^\parallel,
\label{eq:lambda_from_B}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha=\frac12(B_1^1+B_2^2),
\label{eq:alpha_from_B}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\beta=\frac12(B_2^1-B_1^2).
\label{eq:beta_from_B}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. Actual local overlap formulas for the two witnesses}

It is convenient to rewrite the traceless coefficient functions in the S2-adapted basis:
\begin{equation}
a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i
=
h_\parallel(\theta)\,\delta^\mu_{\parallel}\sigma_3
+
h_{11}(\theta)\,\delta^\mu_{1}\sigma_1
+
h_{21}(\theta)\,\delta^\mu_{1}\sigma_2
+
h_{12}(\theta)\,\delta^\mu_{2}\sigma_1
+
h_{22}(\theta)\,\delta^\mu_{2}\sigma_2
+\cdots,
\label{eq:hbasis_S2}
\end{equation}
where the omitted terms denote symmetry-forbidden or higher-order pieces if the S2 reduction is imposed.

Then the longitudinal witness is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)).
}
\label{eq:lambda_actual_formula}
\end{equation}

For the transverse doublet, the \(2\times2\) reduced intertwiner matrix is
\begin{equation}
T=
\begin{pmatrix}
B_1^1 & B_1^2\\
B_2^1 & B_2^2
\end{pmatrix}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)
\begin{pmatrix}
h_{11}(\theta) & h_{12}(\theta)\\
h_{21}(\theta) & h_{22}(\theta)
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:T_actual_formula}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, the two standard S2 coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac12
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,
\bigl(h_{11}(\theta(\xi))+h_{22}(\theta(\xi))\bigr),
}
\label{eq:alpha_actual_formula}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
\frac12
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,
\bigl(h_{21}(\theta(\xi))-h_{12}(\theta(\xi))\bigr).
}
\label{eq:beta_actual_formula}
\end{equation}

The nondegeneracy condition is
\begin{equation}
\det \Lambda=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2)\neq 0.
\label{eq:detLambda_actual_formula}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{D. What symmetry does and does not imply}

Symmetry does two things:

\begin{enumerate}
\item it forbids mismatched channels, e.g. longitudinal momentum coupling to transverse Pauli directions and vice versa;

\item it reduces the possible first-order symbol to the S2 template \eqref{eq:A1_S2_template}.
\end{enumerate}

But symmetry does \emph{not} prove the actual nonvanishing of
\[
\lambda_\parallel
\quad\text{or}\quad
(\alpha,\beta).
\]
It only shows that these coefficients are allowed, not ruled out, by the selection rules.

This is the same logic already established in the shell-level Weyl witness reduction:
symmetry determines the allowed invariant tensor space, but the actual coefficients must still be checked microscopically.

\subsubsection{E. Leading small-\texorpdfstring{$\theta$}{theta} reduction}

If one uses the minimal even-\(\theta\) expansion
\begin{equation}
h_\parallel(\theta)=\Lambda_\parallel+O(\theta^2),
\qquad
h_{ab}(\theta)=\Lambda_{ab}+O(\theta^2),
\label{eq:smalltheta_h}
\end{equation}
then, since
\begin{equation}
I_\theta:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\neq 0,
\label{eq:Itheta_nonzero_local}
\end{equation}
one gets
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=I_\theta\,\Lambda_\parallel+O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
\label{eq:lambda_smalltheta}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha=\frac{I_\theta}{2}(\Lambda_{11}+\Lambda_{22})+O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
\label{eq:alpha_smalltheta}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\beta=\frac{I_\theta}{2}(\Lambda_{21}-\Lambda_{12})+O(\theta_0^3\kappa).
\label{eq:beta_smalltheta}
\end{equation}
Thus the S2 two-witness problem reduces to a finite coefficient test even in the actual local transport formulation.

\subsubsection{F. Honest conclusion}

The strongest honest actual-local result is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta
\text{ admit explicit local overlap formulas in terms of }
f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\times h(\theta(\xi)).
}
\label{eq:honest_local_result}
\end{equation}

What remains open is not the formula, but the microscopic coefficient extraction:
the actual functions
\[
h_\parallel(\theta),\ h_{11}(\theta),\ h_{12}(\theta),\ h_{21}(\theta),\ h_{22}(\theta)
\]
have not yet been derived from the final full TECT linearized projector equation.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi),
\qquad
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).

Writing
\[
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)=a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2+a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i,

one gets
\[
M^\mu=A^\mu\mathbf 1_2+B_i^\mu\sigma_i,
\qquad
B_i^\mu
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,a_i^\mu(\theta(\xi)).

In the S2 singlet\(\oplus\)doublet decomposition, the symmetry-compatible mixed symbol is
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\]
equivalently
\[
\Lambda=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha & -\beta & 0\\
\beta & \alpha & 0\\
0 & 0 & \lambda_\parallel
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\det\Lambda=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2).

Therefore the actual local overlap formulas are

\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=

\boxed{

=

Thus the S2 two-witness condition is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).

Symmetry determines that these are the only relevant first-order coefficients, but symmetry alone does not prove their nonvanishing.
The remaining microscopic task is to derive the coefficient functions
\[
h_\parallel(\theta),\ h_{11}(\theta),\ h_{12}(\theta),\ h_{21}(\theta),\ h_{22}(\theta)
\]
from the final full TECT linearized projector transport equation.

\subsection{Strongest honest statement at the current stage}

\paragraph{Purpose.}
We summarize, without overclaiming, what has been rigorously closed, what has been structurally reduced, and what remains genuinely open in the current TECT Dirac-emergence program.

\subsubsection{A. What is already closed}

\paragraph{(1) Plain scalar shell-pair route is insufficient.}
The scalar shell-pair channel produces a constant intervalley Bragg block of the form
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{Bragg}}^{\mathrm{scalar}}
=
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\,
\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\label{eq:strong_scalar_bragg}
\end{equation}
with \(B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\neq 0\) generically in the actual scalar Hessian channel.
This is a genuine constant pair-mixing obstruction and cannot be removed by a scalar energy shift.

\paragraph{(2) The refined projector-stiffness model alone does not solve the problem.}
For the current refined \(U(3)\)-invariant triplet plus projector-stiffness model expanded around a locked constant-projector background, the quadratic shell--projector source vanishes:
\begin{equation}
J=0.
\label{eq:strong_J_zero}
\end{equation}
Hence the refined projector stiffness sector alone does not induce a nontrivial shell-enriched tensor at quadratic order.

\paragraph{(3) Class II produces \(J\neq 0\) and a genuine derivative witness correction.}
Once the auxiliary Class II mediator is included, one obtains a nonzero quadratic shell--projector mixing source and therefore
\begin{equation}
\delta N_{ij}^a\neq 0.
\label{eq:strong_deltaN}
\end{equation}
This renormalizes the derivative witness sector \((A,B,C)\), but it does not directly cancel the scalar Bragg mass because the Class II correction lives in the traceless internal channel, not in the identity channel.

\paragraph{(4) The graded \(2+2\) bypass is the natural remaining route.}
The exact reduced Dirac-emergence theorem is already established:
if the infrared sector contains an isolated four-dimensional graded subspace
\begin{equation}
K=K_+\oplus K_-,
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}K_\pm=2,
\label{eq:strong_K}
\end{equation}
and the leading projected symbol is grading-odd and first-order with nondegenerate mixed block, then the reduced principal operator is Dirac type. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7} :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

\paragraph{(5) The actual local CP\(^2\) projector-defect geometry belongs to this operator class.}
For a reflection-symmetric defect background, the projector Hessian reduces to a rank-two bundle problem on
\begin{equation}
Q_B=(\mathbb C z_B)^\perp,
\label{eq:strong_QB}
\end{equation}
with parity decomposition into even/odd low modes and a first-order odd transport kernel
\begin{equation}
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi).
\label{eq:strong_Vodd}
\end{equation}
The projected mixed matrices are
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\label{eq:strong_Mmixed}
\end{equation}
This is the exact local matching statement of the projector-defect operator class. :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9} :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10}

\paragraph{(6) The leading odd scalar profile is \(\theta'(\xi)\).}
For the explicit local defect representative
\begin{equation}
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\label{eq:strong_zB}
\end{equation}
one has
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi z_B=\theta'(\xi)e_1,
\qquad
\partial_\xi P_B=\theta'(\xi)(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger),
\label{eq:strong_dPB}
\end{equation}
so every leading local transport kernel linear in the defect gradient is of the form
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\label{eq:strong_Vtheta}
\end{equation}
Moreover, with the explicit low modes used in the improved effective realization,
\begin{equation}
I_\theta:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\neq 0
\label{eq:strong_Itheta}
\end{equation}
for nontrivial defect amplitude.

\subsubsection{B. The natural local branch is S2}

The local defect geometry singles out one distinguished axis through \(\partial_\xi z_B\), so the traceless transport sector splits as
\begin{equation}
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathbb R\,\sigma_3
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{\sigma_1,\sigma_2\}.
\label{eq:strong_trsplit}
\end{equation}
At the same time the worldvolume derivative directions split naturally as
\begin{equation}
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{wv}}
=
\mathbb R\,p_\parallel
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{p_1,p_2\}.
\label{eq:strong_wvsplit}
\end{equation}
Hence the matched singlet\(\oplus\)doublet branch S2 is the natural local symmetry-compatible branch.
Its most general first-order traceless symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\label{eq:strong_S2}
\end{equation}
equivalently
\begin{equation}
\Lambda=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha & -\beta & 0\\
\beta & \alpha & 0\\
0 & 0 & \lambda_\parallel
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\det\Lambda=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2).
\label{eq:strong_Lambda}
\end{equation}
This is exactly consistent with the shell-level symmetry classification theorem. :contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11} 

\subsubsection{C. Actual local overlap formulas for the two witnesses}

In the actual local projector reduction, the two S2 witnesses admit explicit overlap formulas:
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,
h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:strong_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
\frac12\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,
\bigl(h_{11}(\theta(\xi))+h_{22}(\theta(\xi))\bigr),
\label{eq:strong_alpha}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\beta
=
\frac12\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,
\bigl(h_{21}(\theta(\xi))-h_{12}(\theta(\xi))\bigr).
\label{eq:strong_beta}
\end{equation}
Thus the reduced nondegeneracy condition is
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:strong_witness_pair}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{D. What is \emph{not} yet closed}

At the present stage, the following remains genuinely open:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the explicit full microscopic TECT condensate/projector PDE in final closed form suitable for direct spectral analysis;
\item the direct derivation of the microscopic transport kernel coefficients
\[
h_\parallel(\theta),\ h_{11}(\theta),\ h_{12}(\theta),\ h_{21}(\theta),\ h_{22}(\theta);
\]
\item the explicit verification that the actual microscopic TECT projected overlaps satisfy
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad (\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)
\]
rather than merely allowing them by symmetry.
\end{enumerate}

This is exactly the manuscript’s strongest honest status:
the reduced Dirac-emergence theorem is rigorous, an improved effective CP\(^2\)-defect realization is explicitly constructed, but the full microscopic matching to the complete TECT operator remains open. :contentReference[oaicite:13]{index=13}

\subsubsection{E. Strongest honest conclusion}

The strongest honest statement currently supported is therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Dirac emergence is rigorously proved as a reduced spectral theorem,}
}
\label{eq:strong_box1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}

but

Q_B=(\mathbb C z_B)^\perp,
\qquad

+
