\section{TECT Dirac-Emergence Master Context (Current Strongest Honest Statement)}

\subsection{Project goal}

The current goal is to determine whether TECT admits a \emph{microscopically justified} emergent Dirac operator in the defect/projector sector.

The program has now split into two logically distinct layers:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a \emph{rigorous reduced spectral theorem} for Dirac emergence;
\item a \emph{microscopic matching problem} for the actual TECT projector/defect transport coefficients.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{I. What is already closed}

\subsubsection{I.1 Plain scalar shell-pair route is insufficient}

The scalar shell-pair channel produces a genuine constant intervalley Bragg block
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{Bragg}}^{\mathrm{scalar}}
=
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\,
\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\neq 0
\ \text{generically}.
\label{eq:MC_scalar_Bragg}
\end{equation}
This cannot be removed by a scalar energy subtraction, so the plain scalar shell-pair route does \emph{not} yield a massless Dirac point.

\subsubsection{I.2 The refined projector-stiffness model alone does not induce the needed shell mixing}

For the current refined \(U(3)\)-invariant triplet plus projector-stiffness model around a locked constant-projector background, the quadratic shell--projector mixing source vanishes:
\begin{equation}
J=0.
\label{eq:MC_J_zero}
\end{equation}
Hence the projector-stiffness sector alone does not induce a nontrivial shell-enriched tensor at quadratic order.

\subsubsection{I.3 Class II yields a genuine derivative witness correction but does not remove the scalar Bragg mass}

With the auxiliary Class II mediator included, one obtains
\begin{equation}
\delta N_{ij}^a\neq 0,
\label{eq:MC_deltaN_nonzero}
\end{equation}
so the derivative witness sector \((A,B,C)\) is renormalized.

However, the Class II correction lives in the traceless internal sector and therefore does not directly cancel the identity-channel scalar Bragg obstruction
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]

\subsubsection{I.4 The natural remaining route is the graded \(2+2\) bypass}

There is a rigorous reduced theorem:

If the low-energy sector contains an isolated graded four-dimensional space
\begin{equation}
K=K_+\oplus K_-,
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}K_\pm=2,
\label{eq:MC_K_split}
\end{equation}
and the leading projected symbol is grading-odd and first-order, with nondegenerate mixed block, then the reduced principal operator is Dirac type.

Equivalently, the reduced operator has the form
\begin{equation}
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu,
\label{eq:MC_D1_form}
\end{equation}
and if \(A_1(p)\) is nondegenerate for generic \(p\neq 0\), then \(D_1(p)\) is a Dirac principal operator.

\subsection{II. Actual local CP\(^2\) projector-defect realization}

\subsubsection{II.1 Rank-two bundle structure}

For a local projector defect background
\begin{equation}
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B(\xi)^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B(\xi)^\dagger z_B(\xi)=1,
\label{eq:MC_PB}
\end{equation}
the physical tangent fluctuation lives in the rank-two complex bundle
\begin{equation}
Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp.
\label{eq:MC_QB}
\end{equation}

Thus the defect fluctuation problem is not scalar; it is already a rank-two bundle problem.

\subsubsection{II.2 Reflection-symmetric explicit representative}

A useful explicit local representative is
\begin{equation}
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi),
\qquad
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi).
\label{eq:MC_zB_explicit}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi z_B(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)e_1(\xi),
\label{eq:MC_dzB}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi P_B(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\bigl(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger\bigr).
\label{eq:MC_dPB}
\end{equation}
Hence every leading local transport kernel linear in the defect gradient factors through \(\theta'(\xi)\).

\subsubsection{II.3 Leading transport kernel}

The actual local first-order transport operator is of the form
\begin{equation}
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi),
\label{eq:MC_L1}
\end{equation}
and the strongest honest local form is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:MC_Vtheta}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)
=
a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2+a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i.
\label{eq:MC_Mtheta}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{II.4 Even/odd low modes and mixed overlap}

Using a local \(Q_B\)-frame \(e_a(\xi)\), define
\begin{equation}
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
a=1,2,
\label{eq:MC_u_pm}
\end{equation}
with \(f_+\) even and \(f_-\) odd.

Then the projected mixed matrices are
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\label{eq:MC_Mmixed}
\end{equation}
Same-parity overlaps vanish, while the mixed block is generically nonzero.

\subsubsection{II.5 Explicit nonzero overlap of the leading odd scalar profile}

The leading odd scalar profile is
\[
g_{\mathrm{lead}}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi).
\]
For the explicit low modes used in the effective realization,
\begin{equation}
I_\theta
:=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa,
\label{eq:MC_Itheta}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
I_\theta\neq 0
\qquad
(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0).
\label{eq:MC_Itheta_nonzero}
\end{equation}

Thus the actual local geometry already gives a nontrivial graded overlap scale.

\subsection{III. Residual symmetry and the natural S2 branch}

\subsubsection{III.1 Fiber-side singlet\(\oplus\)doublet decomposition}

Because \(\partial_\xi z_B=\theta' e_1\) singles out \(e_1\), the traceless Hermitian transport sector splits as
\begin{equation}
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathbb R\,\sigma_3
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{\sigma_1,\sigma_2\}.
\label{eq:MC_tr_split}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{III.2 Worldvolume-side singlet\(\oplus\)doublet decomposition}

The local defect/worldvolume geometry also naturally splits momentum directions into
\begin{equation}
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{wv}}
=
\mathbb R\,p_\parallel
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{p_1,p_2\}.
\label{eq:MC_wv_split}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{III.3 Natural S2 mixed symbol}

Therefore the natural local symmetry-compatible branch is the matched singlet\(\oplus\)doublet branch S2:
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:MC_S2_symbol}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\Lambda=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha & -\beta & 0\\
\beta & \alpha & 0\\
0 & 0 & \lambda_\parallel
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\det\Lambda=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2).
\label{eq:MC_Lambda_S2}
\end{equation}
Hence the S2 two-witness condition is
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:MC_two_witness}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{III.4 Why S1 is not the natural local branch}

The rank-deficient branch S1 would keep only
\[
A_1(p)\sim p_\parallel \sigma_3.
\]
But the local defect geometry already contains both the transverse worldvolume doublet \((p_1,p_2)\) and the transverse traceless transport doublet \((\sigma_1,\sigma_2)\).
Therefore S1 is not forced by the local geometry itself; it would require an additional symmetry, truncation, or fine tuning.

\subsection{IV. Actual local formulas for the S2 witnesses}

The local overlap formulas are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:MC_lambda_formula}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
\frac12
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,
\bigl(h_{11}(\theta(\xi))+h_{22}(\theta(\xi))\bigr),
\label{eq:MC_alpha_formula}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\beta
=
\frac12
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,
\bigl(h_{21}(\theta(\xi))-h_{12}(\theta(\xi))\bigr).
\label{eq:MC_beta_formula}
\end{equation}

Thus the two-witness problem has been reduced to a coefficient-extraction problem for the local transport tensor entries
\[
h_\parallel(\theta),\ h_{11}(\theta),\ h_{12}(\theta),\ h_{21}(\theta),\ h_{22}(\theta).
\]

\subsection{V. What remains genuinely open}

The remaining frontier is now sharply isolated:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the final full microscopic TECT condensate/projector PDE in a form suitable for direct spectral analysis;
\item the direct extraction of the microscopic coefficient functions
\[
h_\parallel(\theta),\ h_{11}(\theta),\ h_{12}(\theta),\ h_{21}(\theta),\ h_{22}(\theta);
\]
\item the direct microscopic proof that
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)
\]
in complete TECT rather than only in the explicit improved effective realization.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{VI. Strongest honest conclusion}

The strongest currently justified statement is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Dirac emergence is rigorously proved as a reduced spectral theorem,}
}
\label{eq:MC_conc1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{its hypotheses are explicitly realizable in an improved effective CP}^2\text{-defect model,}
}
\label{eq:MC_conc2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{and the actual local projector-defect geometry is naturally compatible with the S2 branch,}
}
\label{eq:MC_conc3}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the full microscopic matching to complete TECT, including the actual S2 coefficient extraction, remains open.}
}
\label{eq:MC_conc4}
\end{equation}

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\textbf{Closed:}
\]

1. The plain scalar shell-pair route is insufficient because it yields a genuine constant Bragg block
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2\neq 0.
\]

2. The refined projector-stiffness model alone gives
\[
J=0,
\]
so it does not induce the needed shell-enriched tensor.

3. Class II gives
\[
\delta N_{ij}^a\neq 0,
\]
hence renormalizes the derivative witness sector, but it does not cancel the scalar Bragg mass.

4. The graded \(2+2\) reduced theorem is rigorous:
if the leading reduced operator is grading-odd, first-order, and has nondegenerate mixed symbol, then the principal operator is Dirac type.

5. The actual local CP\(^2\) projector-defect geometry belongs to this operator class:
\[
Q_B=(\mathbb C z_B)^\perp,
\qquad
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\]

6. The natural local symmetry-compatible branch is S2:
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\]
with nondegeneracy condition
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad (\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\]

7. The actual local witness formulas are
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)),
\]
\[
\alpha
=
\frac12\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,(h_{11}(\theta(\xi))+h_{22}(\theta(\xi))),
\]
\[
\beta
=
\frac12\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,(h_{21}(\theta(\xi))-h_{12}(\theta(\xi))).
\]

\[
\textbf{Still open:}
\]

1. the final full microscopic TECT projector/condensate PDE suitable for direct spectral analysis;

2. the explicit microscopic extraction of
\[
h_\parallel(\theta),\ h_{11}(\theta),\ h_{12}(\theta),\ h_{21}(\theta),\ h_{22}(\theta);
\]

3. the direct microscopic proof that
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad (\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)
\]
in complete TECT.

Therefore:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Dirac emergence is rigorously proved as a reduced theorem and explicitly realizable in an improved effective CP}^2\text{-defect model,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the full microscopic S2 coefficient extraction in complete TECT remains open.}
}
\]

\subsection{Concrete microscopic ansatz for the projector transport equation}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We formulate a concrete microscopic ansatz for the transport sector of the projector-defect fluctuation equation, consistent with all previously established local structural results, and reduce the remaining coefficient problem to explicit overlap integrals.

\subsubsection{A. Structural input already fixed}

The local CP\(^2\) projector-defect analysis has already established the following:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the physical fluctuation field is a section
\begin{equation}
\eta(\xi,y)\in Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb Cz_B(\xi))^\perp,
\label{eq:eta_QB_concrete}
\end{equation}

\item the static quadratic Hessian is a transverse matrix Schrödinger operator on \(Q_B\), :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\item upon restoring slow worldvolume dependence, the leading transport term has the form
\begin{equation}
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi),
\label{eq:L1_concrete}
\end{equation}
with odd kernel built linearly from the transverse defect gradient, :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\item for the explicit defect representative
\begin{equation}
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\label{eq:zB_concrete}
\end{equation}
one has
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi z_B=\theta'(\xi)e_1,
\qquad
\partial_\xi P_B=\theta'(\xi)(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger),
\label{eq:dPB_concrete}
\end{equation}
so the leading local transport kernel must factor through \(\theta'(\xi)\).
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the strongest honest local transport form is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\label{eq:Vtheta_concrete}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Concrete microscopic ansatz}

We now take the minimal first-order microscopic transport ansatz
\begin{equation}
i\partial_t\eta
=
\Bigl[
-\rho\,D_\xi^2+U_B(\xi)
-i\,\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi))\,\partial_{y^\mu}
\Bigr]\eta
+
O(\partial_y^2)\eta.
\label{eq:microscopic_transport_ansatz}
\end{equation}
This is not yet derived from the final complete TECT PDE; it is the minimal microscopic ansatz consistent with all established local projector-defect structure. 

In a local \(Q_B\)-frame, decompose
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)
=
a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2+a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i.
\label{eq:Mmu_pauli_concrete}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. S2-adapted decomposition}

For the natural local S2 branch, decompose the worldvolume directions into
\[
p=(p_1,p_2,p_\parallel),
\]
and write the traceless part in the S2 basis:
\begin{equation}
a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i
=
h_\parallel(\theta)\,\delta^\mu_\parallel \sigma_3
+
h_{11}(\theta)\,\delta^\mu_1 \sigma_1
+
h_{21}(\theta)\,\delta^\mu_1 \sigma_2
+
h_{12}(\theta)\,\delta^\mu_2 \sigma_1
+
h_{22}(\theta)\,\delta^\mu_2 \sigma_2
+\cdots .
\label{eq:S2_hbasis_concrete}
\end{equation}
Then the local S2 witness formulas are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:lambda_concrete}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
\frac12
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,
\bigl(h_{11}(\theta(\xi))+h_{22}(\theta(\xi))\bigr),
\label{eq:alpha_concrete}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\beta
=
\frac12
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,
\bigl(h_{21}(\theta(\xi))-h_{12}(\theta(\xi))\bigr).
\label{eq:beta_concrete}
\end{equation}
This is the actual local form of the S2 two-witness condition.

\subsubsection{D. Minimal even-\texorpdfstring{$\theta$}{theta} expansion}

Because the local transport data are built from the projector background and the physical projector class does not distinguish \(\theta\) from \(-\theta\) at the level of the local scalar coefficient functions, the minimal consistent ansatz is an even expansion in \(\theta\):
\begin{equation}
h_\parallel(\theta)=\Lambda_\parallel+\Xi_\parallel\,\theta^2+O(\theta^4),
\label{eq:hparallel_expand}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
h_{ab}(\theta)=\Lambda_{ab}+\Xi_{ab}\,\theta^2+O(\theta^4),
\qquad a,b=1,2.
\label{eq:hab_expand}
\end{equation}
Similarly,
\begin{equation}
a_0^\mu(\theta)=\Lambda_0{}^\mu+\Xi_0{}^\mu\,\theta^2+O(\theta^4).
\label{eq:a0_expand_concrete}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{E. Reduction to explicit overlap integrals}

Insert \eqref{eq:hparallel_expand}--\eqref{eq:hab_expand} into \eqref{eq:lambda_concrete}--\eqref{eq:beta_concrete}.
Define
\begin{equation}
I_\theta:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi),
\label{eq:Itheta_concrete}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
I_{\theta^3}:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,\theta(\xi)^2.
\label{eq:Itheta3_concrete}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\Lambda_\parallel I_\theta+\Xi_\parallel I_{\theta^3}+O(\theta_0^5\kappa),
\label{eq:lambda_expand_concrete}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
\frac12(\Lambda_{11}+\Lambda_{22})I_\theta
+
\frac12(\Xi_{11}+\Xi_{22})I_{\theta^3}
+
O(\theta_0^5\kappa),
\label{eq:alpha_expand_concrete}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\beta
=
\frac12(\Lambda_{21}-\Lambda_{12})I_\theta
+
\frac12(\Xi_{21}-\Xi_{12})I_{\theta^3}
+
O(\theta_0^5\kappa).
\label{eq:beta_expand_concrete}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{F. Explicit evaluation of \texorpdfstring{$I_\theta$}{Itheta} and \texorpdfstring{$I_{\theta^3}$}{Itheta3}}

Using the explicit profiles
\begin{equation}
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\label{eq:theta_profile_concrete}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
f_+(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{\kappa}{2}}\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
f_-(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{3\kappa}{2}}\,\tanh(\kappa\xi)\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi),
\label{eq:fpm_concrete}
\end{equation}
one already has
\begin{equation}
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa.
\label{eq:Itheta_value_concrete}
\end{equation}

Now compute \(I_{\theta^3}\).
Since
\begin{equation}
\theta'(\xi)
=
-\theta_0\kappa\,\mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi)\tanh(\kappa\xi),
\label{eq:theta_prime_concrete}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\theta(\xi)^2=\theta_0^2\,\mathrm{sech}^2(\kappa\xi),
\label{eq:theta_sq_concrete}
\end{equation}
while
\begin{equation}
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)
=
\frac{\sqrt3\,\kappa}{2}\,\tanh(\kappa\xi)\mathrm{sech}^2(\kappa\xi),
\label{eq:fpfm_concrete}
\end{equation}
we get
\begin{align}
I_{\theta^3}
&=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\theta(\xi)^2
\nonumber\\
&=
-\frac{\sqrt3\,\theta_0^3\kappa^2}{2}
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}
d\xi\,
\tanh^2(\kappa\xi)\,\mathrm{sech}^5(\kappa\xi).
\label{eq:Itheta3_step1}
\end{align}
Set
\[
t=\tanh(\kappa\xi),\qquad dt=\kappa\,\mathrm{sech}^2(\kappa\xi)d\xi,
\qquad \mathrm{sech}(\kappa\xi)=\sqrt{1-t^2}.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
I_{\theta^3}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\,\theta_0^3\kappa}{2}
\int_{-1}^{1} t^2(1-t^2)^{3/2}\,dt.
\label{eq:Itheta3_step2}
\end{equation}
Using
\begin{equation}
\int_{-1}^{1} t^2(1-t^2)^{3/2}\,dt=\frac{\pi}{16},
\label{eq:Itheta3_integral}
\end{equation}
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta^3}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\,\theta_0^3\kappa.
}
\label{eq:Itheta3_value}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{G. Concrete witness expansion}

Substituting \eqref{eq:Itheta_value_concrete} and \eqref{eq:Itheta3_value} into \eqref{eq:lambda_expand_concrete}--\eqref{eq:beta_expand_concrete},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_\parallel
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\,\theta_0^3\kappa\,\Xi_\parallel
+O(\theta_0^5\kappa),
}
\label{eq:lambda_final_concrete}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\,\theta_0\kappa\,(\Lambda_{11}+\Lambda_{22})
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{64}\,\theta_0^3\kappa\,(\Xi_{11}+\Xi_{22})
+O(\theta_0^5\kappa),
}
\label{eq:alpha_final_concrete}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\,\theta_0\kappa\,(\Lambda_{21}-\Lambda_{12})
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{64}\,\theta_0^3\kappa\,(\Xi_{21}-\Xi_{12})
+O(\theta_0^5\kappa).
}
\label{eq:beta_final_concrete}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{H. Interpretation}

The remaining full microscopic coefficient problem has now been reduced to determining the finite coefficient data
\[
\Lambda_\parallel,\ \Lambda_{ab},\ \Xi_\parallel,\ \Xi_{ab}.
\]
At leading order in small defect amplitude \(\theta_0\), the two-witness condition becomes simply
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_{11}+\Lambda_{22},\ \Lambda_{21}-\Lambda_{12})\neq (0,0),
\label{eq:leading_witness_condition}
\end{equation}
since \(I_\theta\neq 0\).

\paragraph{Honest status.}
What has been achieved here is a concrete microscopic transport ansatz plus an explicit reduction of the S2 witness coefficients to finite overlap integrals with fully computed \(\theta\)-profile factors.
What remains open is the derivation of the actual microscopic numbers \(\Lambda_\parallel,\Lambda_{ab},\Xi_\parallel,\Xi_{ab}\) from the final complete TECT projector transport PDE.

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
i\partial_t\eta
=
\Bigl[
-\rho\,D_\xi^2+U_B(\xi)
-i\,\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi))\,\partial_{y^\mu}
\Bigr]\eta
+O(\partial_y^2)\eta
\]
is the minimal concrete microscopic ansatz consistent with the actual local projector-defect operator class.

Using the S2 decomposition,
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)),
\]
\[
\alpha
=
\frac12\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,(h_{11}(\theta(\xi))+h_{22}(\theta(\xi))),
\]
\[
\beta
=
\frac12\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,(h_{21}(\theta(\xi))-h_{12}(\theta(\xi))).
\]

With the minimal even-\(\theta\) expansion
\[
h_\parallel(\theta)=\Lambda_\parallel+\Xi_\parallel\theta^2+O(\theta^4),
\qquad
h_{ab}(\theta)=\Lambda_{ab}+\Xi_{ab}\theta^2+O(\theta^4),
\]
the witness coefficients reduce to
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\Lambda_\parallel I_\theta+\Xi_\parallel I_{\theta^3}+O(\theta_0^5\kappa),
\]
\[
\alpha
=
\frac12(\Lambda_{11}+\Lambda_{22})I_\theta
+
\frac12(\Xi_{11}+\Xi_{22})I_{\theta^3}
+O(\theta_0^5\kappa),
\]
\[
\beta
=
\frac12(\Lambda_{21}-\Lambda_{12})I_\theta
+
\frac12(\Xi_{21}-\Xi_{12})I_{\theta^3}
+O(\theta_0^5\kappa).
\]

For the explicit defect and low-mode profiles,
\[
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta^3}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\,\theta_0^3\kappa.
\]

Hence
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_\parallel
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\,\theta_0^3\kappa\,\Xi_\parallel
+O(\theta_0^5\kappa),
\]
\[
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\,\theta_0\kappa\,(\Lambda_{11}+\Lambda_{22})
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{64}\,\theta_0^3\kappa\,(\Xi_{11}+\Xi_{22})
+O(\theta_0^5\kappa),
\]
\[
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\,\theta_0\kappa\,(\Lambda_{21}-\Lambda_{12})
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{64}\,\theta_0^3\kappa\,(\Xi_{21}-\Xi_{12})
+O(\theta_0^5\kappa).
\]

Therefore, at leading order, the full microscopic S2 witness problem has been reduced to the finite coefficient test
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_{11}+\Lambda_{22},\ \Lambda_{21}-\Lambda_{12})\neq (0,0).
}
\]

\subsection{A minimal S2-compatible concrete ansatz for the microscopic projector transport operator}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We propose a concrete microscopic transport operator compatible with all previously established local projector-defect structure and the S2 symmetry reduction, and extract the three Weyl/Dirac witness coefficients explicitly.

\subsubsection{A. Structural constraints already fixed}

The actual local CP\(^2\) projector-defect analysis gives:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the transport term is first-order and odd:
\begin{equation}
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi),
\label{eq:L1_concrete_S2}
\end{equation}

\item the defect gradient factorizes through
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi z_B=\theta'(\xi)e_1,
\qquad
\partial_\xi P_B=\theta'(\xi)(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger),
\label{eq:dPB_factor_S2}
\end{equation}
hence the transport kernel must take the form
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:Vmu_theta_factor_S2}
\end{equation}

\item the local fiber \(Q_B(\xi)\) is complex rank \(2\), so the traceless Hermitian transport channels form a three-dimensional space.
\end{enumerate}

The shell/local symmetry reduction further shows that the natural symmetry-compatible Weyl form is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\label{eq:S2_target_form_again}
\end{equation}
with nondegeneracy condition
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:S2_witness_again}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Canonical local fiber basis}

Let the local orthonormal \(Q_B\)-frame be \((e_1,e_2)\).
Define the canonical traceless Hermitian basis
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_1:=e_1e_2^\dagger+e_2e_1^\dagger,
\label{eq:Sigma1_concrete}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_2:=-ie_1e_2^\dagger+ie_2e_1^\dagger,
\label{eq:Sigma2_concrete}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_3:=e_1e_1^\dagger-e_2e_2^\dagger.
\label{eq:Sigma3_concrete}
\end{equation}
In the local frame, these are exactly
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_i\leftrightarrow \sigma_i,
\qquad i=1,2,3.
\label{eq:Sigma_to_Pauli}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. Canonical worldvolume splitting}

Let the worldvolume momentum directions split as
\begin{equation}
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{wv}}
=
\mathbb R\,n^\mu
\oplus
E_\perp,
\label{eq:wv_split_concrete}
\end{equation}
where \(n^\mu\) is the distinguished longitudinal direction and \(E_\perp\) is the transverse two-plane.

Choose an orthonormal transverse frame \(E^\mu{}_a\) (\(a=1,2\)) on \(E_\perp\), and define the transverse complex-structure rotated frame
\begin{equation}
J^\mu{}_a:=\epsilon_{ab}E^\mu{}_b.
\label{eq:J_frame_concrete}
\end{equation}

Then the three canonical symmetry-compatible channels are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item longitudinal singlet:
\[
n^\mu\Sigma_3,
\]

\item transverse even doublet:
\[
E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a,
\qquad a=1,2,
\]

\item transverse odd doublet:
\[
J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a,
\qquad a=1,2.
\]
\end{enumerate}

\subsubsection{D. Minimal concrete transport ansatz}

We now propose the minimal S2-compatible microscopic transport kernel:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_\parallel\,n^\mu \Sigma_3
+\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:Vmu_minimal_S2}
\end{equation}

Here:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(\Lambda_\parallel\in\mathbb R\) is the longitudinal singlet coupling,
\item \(\Lambda_E\in\mathbb R\) is the transverse even coupling,
\item \(\Lambda_O\in\mathbb R\) is the transverse odd coupling.
\end{itemize}

This is the minimal concrete ansatz because:

\begin{enumerate}
\item it is linear in the actual local odd scalar profile \(\theta'(\xi)\),
\item it uses the actual local rank-two fiber endomorphism basis,
\item it realizes exactly the S2 singlet\(\oplus\)doublet structure and nothing more.
\end{enumerate}

\subsubsection{E. Projection to the graded \(2+2\) carrier}

Let
\begin{equation}
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
a=1,2.
\label{eq:u_pm_projected_S2}
\end{equation}
Then the mixed projected matrices are
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\label{eq:Mmu_projected_concrete}
\end{equation}
Substituting \eqref{eq:Vmu_minimal_S2},
\begin{equation}
M^\mu
=
I_\theta
\Bigl[
\Lambda_\parallel\,n^\mu \sigma_3
+\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr],
\label{eq:Mmu_after_projection}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
I_\theta:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi).
\label{eq:Itheta_projection}
\end{equation}

For the explicit defect and low-mode profiles already used,
\begin{equation}
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa.
\label{eq:Itheta_explicit_final}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{F. Reading off the S2 witnesses}

Choose worldvolume coordinates adapted to the splitting:
\[
p=(p_1,p_2,p_\parallel).
\]
Then the reduced mixed symbol is
\begin{align}
A_1(p)
&=p_\mu M^\mu \nonumber\\
&=
I_\theta\Bigl[
\Lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+\Lambda_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+\Lambda_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
\Bigr].
\label{eq:A1_from_concrete_ansatz}
\end{align}
Therefore the actual S2 witnesses are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=I_\theta\,\Lambda_\parallel,
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\,\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\,\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:witnesses_from_Lambda}
\end{equation}

Since \(I_\theta\neq 0\) for nontrivial defect amplitude, the nondegeneracy condition is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:Lambda_witness_condition}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{G. Determinant and Weyl/Dirac condition}

The coefficient matrix is
\begin{equation}
\Lambda=
\begin{pmatrix}
\Lambda_E & -\Lambda_O & 0\\
\Lambda_O & \Lambda_E & 0\\
0 & 0 & \Lambda_\parallel
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:Lambda_matrix_concrete}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\det\Lambda
=
\Lambda_\parallel(\Lambda_E^2+\Lambda_O^2).
\label{eq:detLambda_concrete}
\end{equation}
So the reduced symbol is nondegenerate iff
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_\parallel(\Lambda_E^2+\Lambda_O^2)\neq 0.
\label{eq:nondeg_concrete}
\end{equation}

If the opposite valley or doubled graded partner satisfies the standard pairing relation, this yields the Dirac principal operator after doubling.

\subsubsection{H. Honest status}

What is proved here is not the final microscopic TECT PDE, but something sharper than an abstract theorem:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a concrete S2-compatible microscopic transport ansatz has been written,
\item its projected witnesses are explicitly computable,
\item the Dirac nondegeneracy problem is reduced to the finite coefficient test
\[
\Lambda_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{enumerate}

What remains open is the derivation of the actual values of
\[
\Lambda_\parallel,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O
\]
from the complete microscopic TECT projector transport equation.

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi))
\]
must be odd and \(Q_B\)-endomorphism valued.

Using the canonical local \(Q_B\)-fiber basis
\[
\Sigma_1,\Sigma_2,\Sigma_3 \cong \sigma_1,\sigma_2,\sigma_3,
\]
and the canonical worldvolume singlet\(\oplus\)doublet splitting
\[
n^\mu,\qquad E^\mu{}_a,\qquad J^\mu{}_a=\epsilon_{ab}E^\mu{}_b,
\]
the minimal S2-compatible concrete transport ansatz is
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_\parallel\,n^\mu \Sigma_3
+\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\]

Projecting onto the graded low modes \(u_a^\pm=f_\pm e_a\) gives
\[
M^\mu
=
I_\theta
\Bigl[
\Lambda_\parallel\,n^\mu \sigma_3
+\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr],
\qquad
I_\theta=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi).
\]

Hence
\[
A_1(p)
=
I_\theta\Bigl[
\Lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+\Lambda_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+\Lambda_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
\Bigr].
\]

Therefore the actual S2 witnesses are
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=I_\theta\,\Lambda_\parallel,
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\,\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\,\Lambda_O.
}
\]

Since
\[
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa
\neq 0
\]
for nontrivial defect amplitude, the nondegeneracy condition is equivalently
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

The coefficient matrix is
\[
\Lambda=
\begin{pmatrix}
\Lambda_E & -\Lambda_O & 0\\
\Lambda_O & \Lambda_E & 0\\
0 & 0 & \Lambda_\parallel
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\det\Lambda=\Lambda_\parallel(\Lambda_E^2+\Lambda_O^2).
\]

Thus the full microscopic S2 witness problem has been reduced to a three-parameter finite coefficient test.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{A minimal microscopic transport operator generating the S2 witnesses}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We propose a concrete microscopic transport operator consistent with the actual local projector-defect structure and the S2 symmetry reduction, and extract the three witness coefficients
\[
\Lambda_\parallel,\qquad \Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O
\]
explicitly.

\subsubsection{A. Structural constraints from the actual local defect geometry}

The local CP\(^2\) projector-defect Hessian already fixes the following:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the low-energy transport operator has the first-order form
\begin{equation}
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\label{eq:L1_minimal_op}
\end{equation}

\item for a reflection-symmetric defect background, the transport kernel is odd,
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi),
\label{eq:Vodd_minimal_op}
\end{equation}

\item the leading local odd building blocks are linear in
\[
\partial_\xi P_B,\qquad \partial_\xi z_B,\qquad \theta'(\xi),
\]
hence the strongest honest local form is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:Vtheta_minimal_op}
\end{equation}

\item the local fiber \(Q_B(\xi)\) is complex rank \(2\), so its traceless Hermitian endomorphism algebra is three-dimensional.
\end{enumerate}
These are exactly the structural ingredients proved in the local projector-Hessian matching theorem. 

\subsubsection{B. Canonical local basis on the fiber and worldvolume}

Let \((e_1,e_2)\) be the local orthonormal frame of \(Q_B\), and define the canonical traceless Hermitian basis
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_1:=e_1e_2^\dagger+e_2e_1^\dagger,
\label{eq:Sigma1_minimal_op}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_2:=-ie_1e_2^\dagger+ie_2e_1^\dagger,
\label{eq:Sigma2_minimal_op}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_3:=e_1e_1^\dagger-e_2e_2^\dagger.
\label{eq:Sigma3_minimal_op}
\end{equation}
In the local frame,
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_i\leftrightarrow \sigma_i.
\label{eq:SigmaPauli_minimal_op}
\end{equation}

On the worldvolume side, use the natural S2-adapted splitting
\begin{equation}
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{wv}}
=
\mathbb R\,n^\mu
\oplus
E_\perp,
\label{eq:wv_split_minimal_op}
\end{equation}
where \(n^\mu\) is the distinguished longitudinal direction and \(E_\perp\) is the transverse two-plane.
Choose an orthonormal transverse frame \(E^\mu{}_a\) (\(a=1,2\)) and define the rotated frame
\begin{equation}
J^\mu{}_a:=\epsilon_{ab}E^\mu{}_b.
\label{eq:Jframe_minimal_op}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. Minimal S2-compatible transport ansatz}

The minimal S2-compatible transport kernel is then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_\parallel\, n^\mu \Sigma_3
+\Lambda_E\, E^\mu{}_a \Sigma_a
+\Lambda_O\, J^\mu{}_a \Sigma_a
\Bigr],
\qquad a=1,2.
}
\label{eq:Vmu_minimal_transport}
\end{equation}

This ansatz is minimal because it keeps exactly the three symmetry-allowed channels:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a longitudinal singlet \(n^\mu\Sigma_3\),
\item a transverse even doublet \(E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a\),
\item a transverse odd doublet \(J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a\).
\end{enumerate}

No additional first-order channel is required by the already established local geometry and S2 symmetry reduction.

\subsubsection{D. Projection onto the graded low-energy carrier}

Let the graded low modes be
\begin{equation}
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
a=1,2.
\label{eq:u_pm_minimal_transport}
\end{equation}
The projected mixed matrices are
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\label{eq:Mmu_projection_minimal_transport}
\end{equation}
Substituting \eqref{eq:Vmu_minimal_transport},
\begin{equation}
M^\mu
=
I_\theta
\Bigl[
\Lambda_\parallel\, n^\mu \sigma_3
+\Lambda_E\, E^\mu{}_a \sigma_a
+\Lambda_O\, J^\mu{}_a \sigma_a
\Bigr],
\label{eq:Mmu_projected_minimal_transport}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
I_\theta:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi).
\label{eq:Itheta_minimal_transport}
\end{equation}
For the explicit defect profile and low modes already used in the improved effective realization,
\begin{equation}
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa.
\label{eq:Itheta_value_minimal_transport}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{E. Reduced mixed symbol and direct identification of the witnesses}

Using worldvolume momenta
\[
p=(p_1,p_2,p_\parallel),
\]
the reduced mixed symbol becomes
\begin{align}
A_1(p)
&=p_\mu M^\mu \nonumber\\
&=
I_\theta\Bigl[
\Lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+\Lambda_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+\Lambda_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
\Bigr].
\label{eq:A1_minimal_transport}
\end{align}
Comparing with the canonical S2 template
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\label{eq:S2_template_minimal_transport}
\end{equation}
we read off
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=I_\theta\,\Lambda_\parallel,
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\,\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\,\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:witness_identification_minimal_transport}
\end{equation}

Since \(I_\theta\neq 0\) for nontrivial defect amplitude, the S2 two-witness condition is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:witness_condition_minimal_transport}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{F. Determinant and nondegeneracy}

The effective transport matrix in the S2 basis is
\begin{equation}
\Lambda=
\begin{pmatrix}
\Lambda_E & -\Lambda_O & 0\\
\Lambda_O & \Lambda_E & 0\\
0 & 0 & \Lambda_\parallel
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:Lambda_matrix_minimal_transport}
\end{equation}
with determinant
\begin{equation}
\det\Lambda
=
\Lambda_\parallel(\Lambda_E^2+\Lambda_O^2).
\label{eq:detLambda_minimal_transport}
\end{equation}
Thus the reduced symbol is nondegenerate exactly when
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_\parallel(\Lambda_E^2+\Lambda_O^2)\neq 0.
\label{eq:nondeg_condition_minimal_transport}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{G. Interpretation and honest status}

This construction is not yet a full microscopic derivation from the final TECT PDE.
Rather, it is the minimal concrete ansatz consistent with all currently established local structural facts:

\begin{enumerate}
\item oddness from the reflection-symmetric defect gradient,
\item rank-two local projector fiber \(Q_B\),
\item canonical three-dimensional traceless Hermitian fiber algebra,
\item natural S2 singlet\(\oplus\)doublet symmetry reduction.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the remaining microscopic problem is no longer one of operator-class identification.
It is the finite coefficient problem:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{determine the actual values of }
\Lambda_\parallel,\ \Lambda_E,\ \Lambda_O
\text{ from the full TECT projector transport dynamics.}
}
\label{eq:remaining_problem_minimal_transport}
\end{equation}

must be odd and \(Q_B\)-endomorphism valued.

Using the canonical local fiber basis
