%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{A more concrete microscopic transport ansatz using the primitive projector channel \texorpdfstring{$T(P)=3P-\mathbf 1_3$}{T(P)=3P-I}}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We refine the previous minimal S2-compatible transport ansatz by using the most canonical internal tensor induced by the CP\(^2\) defect projector,
\[
T(P)=3P-\mathbf 1_3,
\]
and determine how much of the desired S2 structure it can actually generate on the rank-two bundle \(Q_B\).

\subsubsection{A. Microscopic origin of the transport term}

In the local projector-defect linearization, the first-order transport contribution arises because derivatives act on the background projector.
The microscopic linearized transport term is schematically
\begin{equation}
T(\delta P)
=
-C_{ij}\Big[(\partial_iP_B)\partial_j\delta P+(\partial_jP_B)\partial_i\delta P\Big].
\label{eq:transport_linearized_primitive}
\end{equation}
Thus the transport kernel is built from two ingredients:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the background projector gradient \(\partial_\xi P_B\),
\item an internal tensor channel acting on projector fluctuations.
\end{enumerate}
:contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

\subsubsection{B. The primitive internal channel}

A canonically distinguished internal Hermitian traceless tensor induced by a CP\(^2\) projector is
\begin{equation}
T(P)=3P-\mathbf 1_3.
\label{eq:primitive_channel_def}
\end{equation}
Since \(P\) is a rank-one Hermitian projector, \(T(P)\) has eigenvalues
\[
2,-1,-1,
\]
is Hermitian, traceless, and pointwise invertible, and distinguishes the projector line \(\mathrm{im}\,P\) from its orthogonal complement \(\ker P\). :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

Therefore the most canonical concrete transport operator one can try is a defect-gradient coupling dressed by the primitive channel.

\subsubsection{C. Explicit defect background and restriction to \texorpdfstring{$Q_B$}{QB}}

Take the explicit local defect representative
\begin{equation}
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B(\xi)^\dagger.
\label{eq:PB_primitive}
\end{equation}
Let
\begin{equation}
Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp
\label{eq:QB_primitive}
\end{equation}
with local orthonormal frame
\begin{equation}
e_1(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_2(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\
1\\
0
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:frame_primitive}
\end{equation}
These satisfy
\begin{equation}
P_B e_1=0,
\qquad
P_B e_2=0,
\label{eq:PB_annihilates_Q}
\end{equation}
because \(e_1,e_2\in Q_B\).

Therefore, restricted to the \(Q_B\) fiber,
\begin{equation}
T(P_B)\big|_{Q_B}
=
(3P_B-\mathbf 1_3)\big|_{Q_B}
=
-\mathbf 1_{Q_B}.
\label{eq:primitive_restricted_Q}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{D. Consequence: the primitive channel alone gives only the identity on \texorpdfstring{$Q_B$}{QB}}

Equation \eqref{eq:primitive_restricted_Q} is decisive.
It implies that the primitive channel \(T(P_B)\) does \emph{not} generate a traceless Pauli-triplet structure on the rank-two fiber \(Q_B\).
Instead, on \(Q_B\) it collapses to a scalar multiple of the identity.

Thus any transport ansatz of the form
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\Lambda^\mu\,T(P_B)\big|_{Q_B}
\label{eq:too_primitive}
\end{equation}
becomes
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)=-\theta'(\xi)\,\Lambda^\mu\,\mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:primitive_identity_only}
\end{equation}
After projection onto the graded \(2+2\) carrier,
\begin{equation}
M^\mu
=
-I_\theta\,\Lambda^\mu\,\mathbf 1_2,
\label{eq:Mmu_identity_only}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
I_\theta=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\neq 0.
\label{eq:Itheta_again_primitive}
\end{equation}
Hence the mixed symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)= -I_\theta\,p_\mu\Lambda^\mu\,\mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:A1_identity_only}
\end{equation}

This is first-order and not a constant mass term, but it carries no traceless Pauli structure.

\subsubsection{E. Why this is insufficient for the full S2 branch}

The natural S2 branch requires the mixed symbol
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\label{eq:S2_needed_again}
\end{equation}
which needs one singlet traceless channel \(\sigma_3\) and a transverse traceless doublet \((\sigma_1,\sigma_2)\).

But the primitive projector channel restricted to \(Q_B\) yields only
\[
\mathbf 1_2,
\]
not \(\sigma_1,\sigma_2,\sigma_3\).

Therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T(P)=3P-\mathbf 1_3\ \text{alone cannot generate the full S2 Pauli-triplet transport structure on }Q_B.
}
\label{eq:primitive_insufficient_box}
\end{equation}

In particular, for the minimal S2 parameterization
\[
V^\mu(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_\parallel n^\mu\Sigma_3
+\Lambda_EE^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+\Lambda_OJ^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr],
\]
the primitive channel alone effectively gives
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_E=\Lambda_O=0
\quad\text{generically},
\label{eq:primitive_kills_doublet}
\end{equation}
because it contains no off-diagonal or traceless splitting inside \(Q_B\).

\subsubsection{F. Minimal refinement needed}

To obtain the full S2 structure, one needs a more refined internal channel than \(T(P)\) alone.
The minimal possibilities are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{frame-sensitive commutator channel:}
an operator built from \(P_B\) and \(\partial_\xi P_B\), such as
\[
[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B],
\]
which acts nontrivially on \(Q_B\);

\item \textbf{connection/gradient channel:}
an endomorphism built from the induced \(Q_B\)-connection or its frame-covariant derivative, which can distinguish \(e_1\) and \(e_2\);

\item \textbf{direct shell--projector derivative coupling:}
a UV term of the type already classified in the shell-enriched analysis,
\[
L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(2)}\sim \Lambda^a_{ij}(\partial_i\phi_0)(D_j\psi)\,\xi^a,
\]
whose internal label \(a\) directly spans the reduced Pauli sector.
\end{enumerate}
:contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\subsubsection{G. Honest conclusion}

The primitive channel \(T(P)=3P-\mathbf 1_3\) is canonical and extremely useful for topological and mirror-sector questions, but it is too coarse to generate the full S2 transport triplet on the rank-two tangent bundle \(Q_B\).

So the honest conclusion is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{primitive channel alone } \Rightarrow \text{identity-valued first-order transport only;}
}
\label{eq:primitive_honest1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{full S2 Weyl/Dirac transport requires an additional gradient-sensitive traceless }Q_B\text{-endomorphism channel.}
}
\label{eq:primitive_honest2}
\end{equation}

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
T(P)=3P-\mathbf 1_3
\]
is the canonical primitive Hermitian traceless tensor induced by a rank-one CP\(^2\) projector.

For the explicit defect background
\[
P_B=z_Bz_B^\dagger,
\qquad
Q_B=(\mathbb Cz_B)^\perp,
\]
and the local \(Q_B\)-frame \(e_1,e_2\), one has
\[
P_Be_1=0,
\qquad
P_Be_2=0.
\]
Therefore
\[
T(P_B)\big|_{Q_B}
=
(3P_B-\mathbf 1_3)\big|_{Q_B}
=
-\mathbf 1_{Q_B}.
\]

Hence a transport kernel built only from the primitive channel takes the form
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\Lambda^\mu T(P_B)\big|_{Q_B}
=
-\theta'(\xi)\Lambda^\mu \mathbf 1_2.
\]
After projection,
\[
M^\mu=-I_\theta\Lambda^\mu\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
A_1(p)=-I_\theta\,p_\mu\Lambda^\mu\,\mathbf 1_2.
\]

This is first-order but carries no traceless Pauli structure.
Therefore the primitive channel alone cannot generate the full S2 symbol
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]

So:
\[
\boxed{
T(P)=3P-\mathbf 1_3 \text{ alone is too coarse for the full S2 Weyl/Dirac transport triplet on }Q_B.
}
\]

A full S2 realization requires an additional gradient-sensitive traceless \(Q_B\)-endomorphism channel, such as one built from
\[
[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B],
\]
the induced frame/connection structure, or a direct shell--projector derivative coupling carrying the reduced Pauli label.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{The commutator channel \texorpdfstring{$\mathcal T_\xi=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B]$}{Txi=i[P,dP]} and its induced action on the tangent bundle}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now analyze the first genuinely gradient-sensitive internal channel
\[
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B]
\]
for the explicit CP\(^2\) defect background, and determine what structure it induces on the rank-two tangent bundle \(Q_B\).

\subsubsection{A. Why this is the natural next channel}

The primitive Hermitian traceless tensor
\[
T(P)=3P-\mathbf 1_3
\]
is canonical but too coarse on \(Q_B\), since
\[
T(P_B)\big|_{Q_B}=-\mathbf 1_{Q_B}.
\]
So it cannot produce the full traceless transport triplet on the tangent bundle. :contentReference[oaicite:0]{index=0}

On the other hand, the microscopic defect connection in the Callias construction is explicitly
\[
A_i=[P,\partial_iP],
\]
and for the affine Higgs field \(\Phi=\mu(3P-\mathbf 1_3)\) one has
\[
D_i\Phi=0.
\]
Thus the commutator channel \([P,\partial_iP]\) is not ad hoc; it is already a canonically distinguished gradient-sensitive object in the microscopic projector geometry. :contentReference[oaicite:1]{index=1}

At the same time, the local projector-Hessian transport kernel is known to be built linearly from \(\partial_\xi P_B\) and related gradient tensors. 
Hence
\[
\mathcal T_\xi=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B]
\]
is the next minimal channel to test.

\subsubsection{B. Explicit defect background and frame}

Take the explicit reflection-symmetric defect representative
\begin{equation}
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B(\xi)^\dagger.
\label{eq:zB_comm}
\end{equation}
Let the orthonormal local frame of
\[
Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp
\]
be
\begin{equation}
e_1(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_2(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\
1\\
0
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:e1e2_comm}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi z_B(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)e_1(\xi),
\label{eq:dz_comm}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi P_B
=
(\partial_\xi z_B)z_B^\dagger+z_B(\partial_\xi z_B)^\dagger
=
\theta'(\xi)\bigl(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger\bigr).
\label{eq:dP_comm}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. Exact computation of the commutator channel}

Now compute
\begin{align}
[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B]
&=
z_Bz_B^\dagger\,
\theta'(\xi)\bigl(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger\bigr)
-
\theta'(\xi)\bigl(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger\bigr)\,
z_Bz_B^\dagger.
\label{eq:comm_start}
\end{align}
Using
\[
z_B^\dagger e_1=0,\qquad e_1^\dagger z_B=0,\qquad z_B^\dagger z_B=1,
\]
we get
\begin{equation}
P_B\,\partial_\xi P_B
=
\theta'(\xi)\,z_Be_1^\dagger,
\qquad
(\partial_\xi P_B)\,P_B
=
\theta'(\xi)\,e_1z_B^\dagger.
\label{eq:products_comm}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B]
=
\theta'(\xi)\bigl(z_Be_1^\dagger-e_1z_B^\dagger\bigr).
\label{eq:comm_final}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal T_\xi
=
i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B]
=
i\theta'(\xi)\bigl(z_Be_1^\dagger-e_1z_B^\dagger\bigr).
}
\label{eq:Txi_final}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{D. Geometric meaning}

The operator \(\mathcal T_\xi\) exchanges the projector line \(\mathbb Cz_B\) and the distinguished tangent direction \(\mathbb Ce_1\).
Indeed,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal T_\xi z_B
=
i\theta'(\xi)\bigl(z_Be_1^\dagger z_B-e_1z_B^\dagger z_B\bigr)
=
-i\theta'(\xi)e_1,
\label{eq:Txi_on_z}
\end{equation}
while
\begin{equation}
\mathcal T_\xi e_1
=
i\theta'(\xi)\bigl(z_Be_1^\dagger e_1-e_1z_B^\dagger e_1\bigr)
=
+i\theta'(\xi)z_B.
\label{eq:Txi_on_e1}
\end{equation}
Also,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal T_\xi e_2=0.
\label{eq:Txi_on_e2}
\end{equation}

Thus \(\mathcal T_\xi\) is not an endomorphism of \(Q_B\); it is an off-block generator between \(\mathbb Cz_B\) and \(\mathbb Ce_1\), annihilating \(e_2\).

\subsubsection{E. Direct restriction to \texorpdfstring{$Q_B$}{QB}}

Let \(\Pi_Q=\mathbf 1_3-P_B\) be the projector onto \(Q_B\).
Then
\begin{equation}
\Pi_Q \mathcal T_\xi \Pi_Q = 0.
\label{eq:Txi_Q_restriction_zero}
\end{equation}
Indeed, for any \(v\in Q_B\), \(\mathcal T_\xi v\in \mathbb Cz_B\), so projecting back to \(Q_B\) gives zero.

Therefore the commutator channel itself is not yet a \(Q_B\)-endomorphism transport tensor.

\subsubsection{F. Induced quadratic channel on \texorpdfstring{$Q_B$}{QB}}

However, \(\mathcal T_\xi^2\) \emph{is} block-preserving.
Using \eqref{eq:Txi_on_z}--\eqref{eq:Txi_on_e2},
\begin{equation}
\mathcal T_\xi^2 z_B
=
\theta'(\xi)^2 z_B,
\label{eq:Txi2_on_z}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\mathcal T_\xi^2 e_1
=
\theta'(\xi)^2 e_1,
\label{eq:Txi2_on_e1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\mathcal T_\xi^2 e_2=0.
\label{eq:Txi2_on_e2}
\end{equation}
Hence, restricted to \(Q_B\),
\begin{equation}
\Pi_Q \mathcal T_\xi^2 \Pi_Q
=
\theta'(\xi)^2\,\Pi_{e_1},
\label{eq:Txi2_Q}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\Pi_{e_1}=e_1e_1^\dagger.
\]

In the local \(Q_B\)-frame \((e_1,e_2)\),
\begin{equation}
\Pi_{e_1}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
1 & 0\\
0 & 0
\end{pmatrix}
=
\frac12(\mathbf 1_2+\sigma_3).
\label{eq:Pi_e1_sigma3}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_Q \mathcal T_\xi^2 \Pi_Q
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\bigl(\mathbf 1_2+\sigma_3\bigr).
}
\label{eq:Txi2_sigma3}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{G. Consequence for transport structure}

This shows that the commutator channel is much stronger than the primitive channel \(3P-\mathbf 1_3\).

\begin{itemize}
\item The primitive channel restricted to \(Q_B\) gives only
\[
-\mathbf 1_2.
\]

\item The induced quadratic commutator channel gives
\[
\frac12(\mathbf 1_2+\sigma_3),
\]
so it contains a genuine traceless splitting \(\sigma_3\) on \(Q_B\).
\end{itemize}

Hence the commutator channel naturally generates the longitudinal singlet part of the S2 structure.

\subsubsection{H. But not yet the full S2 triplet}

Equation \eqref{eq:Txi2_sigma3} still singles out only the \(e_1/e_2\) splitting.
So it naturally produces the \(\sigma_3\) channel, but not the transverse doublet \((\sigma_1,\sigma_2)\).

Therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal T_\xi=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B]
\text{ is sufficient to generate a gradient-sensitive }\sigma_3\text{-type channel,}
}
\label{eq:Txi_sigma3_box}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{it is not by itself sufficient to produce the full }(\sigma_1,\sigma_2,\sigma_3)\text{ S2 triplet.}
}
\label{eq:Txi_not_full_triplet}
\end{equation}

To obtain the transverse doublet, one still needs an additional frame-sensitive or worldvolume-plane-sensitive channel, e.g.

\begin{enumerate}
\item a connection/frame-twist channel,
\item a worldvolume transverse complex-structure channel,
\item or a direct shell--projector derivative coupling carrying the reduced Pauli doublet label.
\end{enumerate}

\subsubsection{I. Honest conclusion}

The commutator channel is the first genuinely successful refinement beyond the primitive \(3P-\mathbf 1_3\) channel:

\[
3P-\mathbf 1_3 \Rightarrow \text{identity only on }Q_B,
\]
whereas
\[
i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B]
\Rightarrow \text{after induced projection, } \mathbf 1_2+\sigma_3.
\]

So the gradient-sensitive commutator channel captures the distinguished tangent splitting of the defect geometry and provides a natural microscopic source for the longitudinal witness \(\lambda_\parallel\).

But a full Weyl/Dirac S2 symbol still requires one more ingredient for the transverse doublet.

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B]
\]
is the natural first gradient-sensitive internal channel beyond the primitive tensor \(3P-\mathbf 1_3\).

For the explicit CP\(^2\) defect background,
\[
\partial_\xi P_B
=
\theta'(\xi)(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger),
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal T_\xi
=
i\theta'(\xi)(z_Be_1^\dagger-e_1z_B^\dagger).
}
\]

Its action is
\[
\mathcal T_\xi z_B=-i\theta'(\xi)e_1,
\qquad
\mathcal T_\xi e_1=+i\theta'(\xi)z_B,
\qquad
\mathcal T_\xi e_2=0.
\]
So \(\mathcal T_\xi\) is an off-block operator between the projector line \(\mathbb Cz_B\) and the distinguished tangent direction \(\mathbb Ce_1\).

Direct restriction to \(Q_B\) gives
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi\Pi_Q=0.
\]
But the induced quadratic channel is
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q
=
\theta'(\xi)^2\,\Pi_{e_1}
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\bigl(\mathbf 1_2+\sigma_3\bigr).
\]

Therefore the commutator channel, unlike the primitive channel, generates a genuine traceless splitting on \(Q_B\), namely a natural \(\sigma_3\)-type channel.

So:
\[
\boxed{
i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B]
\text{ is a genuine gradient-sensitive microscopic source for the longitudinal singlet witness.}
}
\]

However, it still does not generate the full transverse doublet \((\sigma_1,\sigma_2)\) by itself.
Hence:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the commutator channel improves the primitive channel, but a full S2 Weyl/Dirac triplet still needs one additional transverse doublet source.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Minimal composite transport operator generating the full S2 triplet}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We construct the minimal composite transport operator that generates the full S2 triplet
\[
(\sigma_1,\sigma_2,\sigma_3)
\]
on the graded low-energy sector, combining the commutator-induced singlet channel with the transverse doublet source.

\subsubsection{A. What the previous channels achieved}

\paragraph{Primitive projector channel.}
The canonical primitive internal tensor
\begin{equation}
T(P)=3P-\mathbf 1_3
\label{eq:Tprimitive_comp}
\end{equation}
is Hermitian, traceless, and pointwise invertible on \(\mathbb C^3\). 
However, on the tangent bundle
\[
Q_B=(\mathbb Cz_B)^\perp,
\]
it reduces to
\begin{equation}
T(P_B)\big|_{Q_B}=-\mathbf 1_{Q_B},
\label{eq:Tprimitive_Q}
\end{equation}
so it produces only an identity-valued first-order transport and no Pauli triplet.

\paragraph{Commutator channel.}
The canonical gradient-sensitive channel is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B].
\label{eq:Tcomm_def}
\end{equation}
This is natural because the Callias connection is exactly
\[
A_i=[P,\partial_iP].
\]


For the explicit defect background,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal T_\xi
=
i\theta'(\xi)\bigl(z_Be_1^\dagger-e_1z_B^\dagger\bigr),
\label{eq:Tcomm_explicit}
\end{equation}
so \(\mathcal T_\xi\) is an off-block operator exchanging \(\mathbb Cz_B\) and \(\mathbb Ce_1\), while annihilating \(e_2\).

Direct restriction gives
\begin{equation}
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi\Pi_Q=0,
\label{eq:Tcomm_direct_zero}
\end{equation}
but the induced quadratic channel gives
\begin{equation}
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q
=
\theta'(\xi)^2\Pi_{e_1}
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\bigl(\mathbf 1_2+\sigma_3\bigr).
\label{eq:Tcomm_sq}
\end{equation}

Thus the commutator channel naturally produces a \(\sigma_3\)-type splitting, but not the transverse Pauli doublet \((\sigma_1,\sigma_2)\).

\subsubsection{B. Need for a transverse doublet source}

The symmetry-compatible S2 reduced symbol has the exact form
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\label{eq:S2_full_again_comp}
\end{equation}
with nondegeneracy criterion
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:S2_nondeg_again_comp}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

Hence a full microscopic transport operator must supply:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a longitudinal singlet channel \(\sigma_3\),
\item a transverse even channel \((p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)\),
\item a transverse odd channel \((-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)\).
\end{enumerate}

The commutator-induced channel provides the first one naturally.
The remaining two require an explicit transverse doublet source.

\subsubsection{C. Canonical transverse doublet source}

Let \(n^\mu\) denote the distinguished longitudinal worldvolume direction, and let \(E^\mu{}_a\) (\(a=1,2\)) be an orthonormal frame of the transverse two-plane.
Define the rotated transverse frame
\begin{equation}
J^\mu{}_a:=\epsilon_{ab}E^\mu{}_b.
\label{eq:Jtransverse_comp}
\end{equation}
On the fiber, use the canonical traceless basis
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_1,\Sigma_2,\Sigma_3 \cong \sigma_1,\sigma_2,\sigma_3.
\label{eq:Sigma_basis_comp}
\end{equation}

The minimal transverse doublet source is then
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\perp}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a+\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr],
\qquad a=1,2.
\label{eq:Vperp_comp}
\end{equation}
This is the minimal S2-compatible first-order transverse doublet source.

\subsubsection{D. Why the singlet must carry an odd prefactor}

A naive singlet term from \(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q\) would be
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{naive}}(\xi)
=
\lambda_c\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
\label{eq:naive_singlet}
\end{equation}
But after projection onto the graded low modes, the overlap integral would be proportional to
\begin{equation}
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^2.
\label{eq:bad_integral}
\end{equation}
Now:
\[
f_+ \text{ is even},\qquad
f_- \text{ is odd},\qquad
\theta'^2 \text{ is even},
\]
so the integrand is odd. Therefore
\begin{equation}
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'^2=0.
\label{eq:bad_integral_zero}
\end{equation}
Hence the naive quadratic commutator singlet does \emph{not} contribute to the first-order mixed symbol.

Therefore a viable longitudinal singlet source must include one additional odd factor.
The simplest choice is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\parallel}(\xi)
=
\lambda_c\,\theta'(\xi)\,\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q\,n^\mu.
\label{eq:good_singlet}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:Tcomm_sq},
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\parallel}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu(\mathbf 1_2+\sigma_3).
\label{eq:good_singlet_explicit}
\end{equation}
Its traceless part is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{tr}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\label{eq:good_singlet_traceless}
\end{equation}
Now \(f_+f_-\theta'^3\) is even, so the overlap need not vanish.

\subsubsection{E. Minimal composite S2 transport operator}

Combining the longitudinal commutator-induced singlet with the transverse doublet source, the minimal composite transport operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{comp}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr],
\qquad a=1,2.
}
\label{eq:Vcomp_final}
\end{equation}

This is the minimal first-order transport operator that uses:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the actual commutator geometry for the longitudinal singlet,
\item the canonical transverse doublet structure for the Pauli doublet.
\end{enumerate}

\subsubsection{F. Projection to the graded low-energy carrier}

Project onto the graded low modes
\begin{equation}
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
a=1,2.
\label{eq:u_modes_comp}
\end{equation}
The mixed matrices are
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu_{\mathrm{comp}}(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\label{eq:M_comp}
\end{equation}
Define the overlap integrals
\begin{equation}
I_\theta:=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi),
\label{eq:Itheta_comp}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
I_{\theta'^3}:=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)^3.
\label{eq:Itheta3prime_comp}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
M^\mu
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
I_\theta\Bigl[
\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a+\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr].
\label{eq:M_comp_final}
\end{equation}

Therefore the reduced mixed symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\label{eq:A1_comp}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\,\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\,\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:witness_comp}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{G. Explicit evaluation of \texorpdfstring{$I_{\theta'^3}$}{I(theta'^3)}}

Using the explicit profiles
\[
f_+(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{\kappa}{2}}\sech(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
f_-(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{3\kappa}{2}}\tanh(\kappa\xi)\sech(\kappa\xi),
\]
and
\[
\theta'(\xi)=-\theta_0\kappa\,\sech(\kappa\xi)\tanh(\kappa\xi),
\]
we compute
\begin{align}
I_{\theta'^3}
&=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'^3 \nonumber\\
&=
-\frac{\sqrt3\,\theta_0^3\kappa^4}{2}
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}
d\xi\,
\tanh^4(\kappa\xi)\sech^5(\kappa\xi).
\label{eq:I3prime_step1}
\end{align}
Set
\[
t=\tanh(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
dt=\kappa\sech^2(\kappa\xi)d\xi,
\qquad
\sech(\kappa\xi)=\sqrt{1-t^2}.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3}{2}
\int_{-1}^{1} t^4(1-t^2)^{3/2}\,dt.
\label{eq:I3prime_step2}
\end{equation}
The integral is strictly positive, so
\begin{equation}
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0
\qquad
(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0).
\label{eq:I3prime_nonzero}
\end{equation}
Thus the longitudinal witness produced by the commutator-induced channel is generically nonzero whenever \(\lambda_c\neq 0\).

\subsubsection{H. Final nondegeneracy condition}

Since
\[
I_\theta\neq 0,\qquad I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0
\]
for nontrivial defect amplitude, the S2 two-witness condition becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:final_comp_condition}
\end{equation}

So the full S2 triplet is generated by:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the commutator-induced channel for the longitudinal singlet,
\item the transverse doublet source for the Pauli doublet.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Honest status.}
This is still a concrete microscopic ansatz, not the final derived TECT PDE.
But it is stronger than the earlier abstract reduction because it identifies a specific minimal composite operator that produces all three S2 witness coefficients explicitly.

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\mathcal T_\xi=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B]
\]
is the first genuinely gradient-sensitive internal channel beyond the primitive tensor \(3P-\mathbf 1_3\).

Direct restriction gives
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi\Pi_Q=0,
\]
but the induced quadratic channel is
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\bigl(\mathbf 1_2+\sigma_3\bigr).
\]

A naive singlet source proportional to \(\theta'^2\sigma_3\) fails at first order because
\[
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'^2=0
\]
by parity.

Therefore the minimal viable longitudinal singlet source is
\[
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\]

Combining this with the transverse doublet source, the minimal composite S2 transport operator is
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{comp}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\]

Projecting onto the graded low modes gives
\[
M^\mu
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
I_\theta\Bigl[
\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a+\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr],
\]
hence
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\,\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\,\Lambda_O.
}
\]

Since
\[
I_\theta\neq 0,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0
\]
for nontrivial defect amplitude, the final S2 nondegeneracy condition reduces to
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

Thus the minimal full S2 triplet is generated by:

\[
\text{longitudinal singlet from the commutator-induced channel,}
\]
\[
\text{transverse doublet from the worldvolume-plane traceless source.}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{A concrete minimal microscopic action term generating the three S2 witnesses}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now choose one explicit microscopic transport term, compatible with the actual local projector-defect geometry and the S2 reduction, and compute the three witness coefficients
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \beta
\]
as explicit constants.

\subsubsection{A. Structural inputs already fixed}

The local CP\(^2\) projector-defect analysis establishes:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the leading transport is first-order and odd,
\begin{equation}
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi),
\label{eq:L1_action}
\end{equation}
with the transport kernel built linearly from the background projector gradient, :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\item the canonical gradient-sensitive internal channel is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B],
\label{eq:Txi_action}
\end{equation}
which is natural because the projector connection itself is
\begin{equation}
A_i=[P,\partial_iP],
\label{eq:Ai_action}
\end{equation}
in the microscopic Callias/projector geometry, :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\item the reduced symmetry-compatible S2 symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:S2_target_action}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}
\end{enumerate}

\subsubsection{B. Canonical local basis}

Let \((e_1,e_2)\) be the local orthonormal frame of
\[
Q_B=(\mathbb C z_B)^\perp.
\]
Define the canonical traceless Hermitian basis
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_1:=e_1e_2^\dagger+e_2e_1^\dagger,
\label{eq:Sigma1_action}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_2:=-ie_1e_2^\dagger+ie_2e_1^\dagger,
\label{eq:Sigma2_action}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_3:=e_1e_1^\dagger-e_2e_2^\dagger.
\label{eq:Sigma3_action}
\end{equation}
In the local frame these are exactly \(\sigma_1,\sigma_2,\sigma_3\).

On the worldvolume side, choose the natural S2-adapted basis:
\begin{equation}
n^\mu \quad \text{(longitudinal singlet)},
\qquad
E^\mu{}_a \quad (a=1,2)\ \text{(transverse frame)},
\qquad
J^\mu{}_a:=\epsilon_{ab}E^\mu{}_b.
\label{eq:wv_basis_action}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. Commutator-induced singlet}

From the explicit defect computation,
\begin{equation}
\Pi_Q \mathcal T_\xi^2 \Pi_Q
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\bigl(\mathbf 1_2+\sigma_3\bigr).
\label{eq:Txi2_action}
\end{equation}
Its traceless part is
\begin{equation}
(\Pi_Q \mathcal T_\xi^2 \Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\sigma_3.
\label{eq:Txi2tr_action}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\theta'(\xi)\,(\Pi_Q \mathcal T_\xi^2 \Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^3}{2}\sigma_3
\label{eq:Txi3_action}
\end{equation}
is the minimal odd longitudinal singlet source.

\subsubsection{D. Minimal concrete transport action}

We now propose the concrete microscopic transport term
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{trans}}^{\min}
=
-i\,\eta^\dagger
\Big[
g_c\,\theta'(\xi)\,(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
+
g_E\,\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
g_O\,\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Big]\partial_{y^\mu}\eta.
}
\label{eq:Ltrans_min_action}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:Txi3_action}, this becomes
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{trans}}^{\min}
=
-i\,\eta^\dagger
\Big[
\frac{g_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu \sigma_3
+
g_E\,\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
g_O\,\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Big]\partial_{y^\mu}\eta.
\label{eq:Ltrans_explicit_action}
\end{equation}

This is the minimal concrete S2-compatible transport action because:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the longitudinal singlet comes from the actual commutator geometry,
\item the transverse doublet comes from the minimal worldvolume-plane traceless source,
\item no additional first-order channel is included.
\end{enumerate}

\subsubsection{E. Projection onto the graded low modes}

Let
\begin{equation}
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
a=1,2.
\label{eq:u_pm_action}
\end{equation}
The projected mixed matrices are
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\label{eq:Mmu_action}
\end{equation}
Define
\begin{equation}
I_\theta:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi),
\label{eq:Itheta_action}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
I_{\theta'^3}:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^3.
\label{eq:Itheta3prime_action}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
M^\mu
=
\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
I_\theta\Bigl[
g_E\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
g_O\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr].
\label{eq:Mmu_final_action}
\end{equation}

Hence the reduced mixed symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\label{eq:A1_final_action}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta.
}
\label{eq:witnesses_action}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{F. Explicit evaluation of the overlap integrals}

For the explicit defect profile
\begin{equation}
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\sech(\kappa\xi),
\label{eq:theta_profile_action}
\end{equation}
and the explicit low modes
\begin{equation}
f_+(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{\kappa}{2}}\,\sech(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
f_-(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{3\kappa}{2}}\,\tanh(\kappa\xi)\sech(\kappa\xi),
\label{eq:fpm_action}
\end{equation}
one already has
\begin{equation}
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa.
\label{eq:Itheta_value_action}
\end{equation}

Now compute \(I_{\theta'^3}\).
Using
\begin{equation}
\theta'(\xi)
=
-\theta_0\kappa\,\sech(\kappa\xi)\tanh(\kappa\xi),
\label{eq:theta_prime_action}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)
=
\frac{\sqrt3\,\kappa}{2}\,\tanh(\kappa\xi)\sech^2(\kappa\xi),
\label{eq:fpfm_action}
\end{equation}
we obtain
\begin{align}
I_{\theta'^3}
&=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^3
\nonumber\\
&=
-\frac{\sqrt3\,\theta_0^3\kappa^4}{2}
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}
d\xi\,
\tanh^4(\kappa\xi)\sech^5(\kappa\xi).
\label{eq:I3prime_step1_action}
\end{align}
Set
\[
t=\tanh(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
dt=\kappa\,\sech^2(\kappa\xi)\,d\xi,
\qquad
\sech(\kappa\xi)=\sqrt{1-t^2}.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3}{2}
\int_{-1}^{1} t^4(1-t^2)^{3/2}\,dt.
\label{eq:I3prime_step2_action}
\end{equation}
Using
\begin{equation}
\int_{-1}^{1} t^4(1-t^2)^{3/2}\,dt=\frac{3\pi}{128},
\label{eq:t4_integral_action}
\end{equation}
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:I3prime_value_action}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{G. Explicit witness coefficients}

Substituting \eqref{eq:Itheta_value_action} and \eqref{eq:I3prime_value_action} into \eqref{eq:witnesses_action},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:lambda_final_action}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:alpha_beta_final_action}
\end{equation}

Thus the S2 nondegeneracy condition
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad (\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0)
\]
reduces exactly to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:gc_gE_gO_condition}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{H. Honest conclusion}

This is still a concrete microscopic ansatz, not the final derived complete TECT PDE.
But it is now a very sharp one:
a single explicit transport action term has been chosen, and the three S2 witnesses have been computed all the way down to explicit numerical profile factors.

Therefore the remaining open microscopic problem is no longer structural.
It is simply whether complete TECT dynamics actually generates nonzero
\[
g_c,\qquad g_E,\qquad g_O.
\]

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{trans}}^{\min}
=
-i\,\eta^\dagger
\Big[
g_c\,\theta'(\xi)\,(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
+
g_E\,\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
g_O\,\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Big]\partial_{y^\mu}\eta
\]
is a concrete minimal microscopic transport action compatible with the local projector-defect geometry and the S2 symmetry reduction.

Using
\[
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\sigma_3,
\]
this becomes
\[
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{trans}}^{\min}
=
-i\,\eta^\dagger
\Big[
\frac{g_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
g_E\,\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
g_O\,\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Big]\partial_{y^\mu}\eta.
\]

After projection onto the graded low modes,
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta,
\]
with
\[
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\]

Hence the full S2 nondegeneracy condition reduces to the simple finite test
\[
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

So the remaining microscopic question is just whether complete TECT dynamics actually generates nonzero \(g_c,g_E,g_O\).

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{TECT Dirac-Emergence Master Context (Latest Snapshot with Concrete Transport Ansatz)}

\subsection{0. Working rules for the project}

\begin{itemize}
\item Conversation language: Korean.
\item Mathematical derivations: English \LaTeX.
\item Focus: rigorous derivation, honest separation of what is proved / reduced / still open.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{1. Global research target}

The current target is:

\[
\text{derive an emergent massless Dirac operator from the actual TECT defect/projector sector.}
\]

The program now has two layers:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a \emph{reduced spectral theorem layer}, already essentially closed;
\item a \emph{microscopic coefficient extraction layer}, still open.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{2. What is already closed}

\subsubsection{2.1 Plain scalar shell-pair route fails}

The scalar shell-pair channel yields a genuine constant Bragg block
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{Bragg}}^{\mathrm{scalar}}
=
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\,
\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\neq 0
\ \text{generically}.
\label{eq:MC2_scalar_Bragg}
\end{equation}
This is a true constant pair-mixing obstruction and cannot be removed by a simple scalar shift.
Hence the plain scalar shell-pair route does \emph{not} yield a massless Dirac point.

\subsubsection{2.2 Refined projector-stiffness model alone fails}

For the current refined \(U(3)\)-invariant triplet plus projector-stiffness model around a locked constant-projector background,
\begin{equation}
J=0.
\label{eq:MC2_J_zero}
\end{equation}
Therefore the projector-stiffness sector alone does not induce the needed shell--projector mixing at quadratic order.

\subsubsection{2.3 Class II gives derivative witnesses but not identity-channel cancellation}

With the auxiliary Class II mediator included, one obtains a genuine shell-enriched correction
\begin{equation}
\delta N_{ij}^a\neq 0.
\label{eq:MC2_deltaN}
\end{equation}
Thus the derivative witness sector is renormalized.
However, this correction lives in the traceless internal channel and therefore does not directly cancel the identity-channel scalar Bragg obstruction
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]

\subsubsection{2.4 The natural remaining route is the graded \(2+2\) bypass}

The reduced theorem is:

if there exists an isolated four-dimensional infrared sector
\begin{equation}
K=K_+\oplus K_-,
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}K_\pm=2,
\label{eq:MC2_K_split}
\end{equation}
and the projected leading symbol is grading-odd, first-order, and nondegenerate, then the reduced principal operator is Dirac.

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu,
\label{eq:MC2_D1}
\end{equation}
and nondegeneracy of \(A_1(p)\) for generic \(p\neq 0\) implies Dirac emergence.

\subsection{3. Actual local CP\(^2\) projector-defect geometry}

\subsubsection{3.1 Rank-two tangent bundle}

For a defect background
\begin{equation}
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B(\xi)^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B^\dagger z_B=1,
\label{eq:MC2_PB}
\end{equation}
the physical tangent fluctuation lives in
\begin{equation}
Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp.
\label{eq:MC2_QB}
\end{equation}
Thus the defect fluctuation problem is already a rank-two bundle problem, not a scalar one.

\subsubsection{3.2 Explicit reflection-symmetric representative}

A useful explicit local representative is
\begin{equation}
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\sech(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi).
\label{eq:MC2_zB}
\end{equation}
Choose the local \(Q_B\)-frame
\begin{equation}
e_1(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_2(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\
1\\
0
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:MC2_frame}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi z_B=\theta'(\xi)e_1,
\qquad
\partial_\xi P_B=\theta'(\xi)(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger).
\label{eq:MC2_dPB}
\end{equation}
Hence every leading local transport kernel linear in the defect gradient must factor through \(\theta'(\xi)\).

\subsubsection{3.3 Local transport kernel}

The actual local first-order transport operator has the form
\begin{equation}
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi).
\label{eq:MC2_L1}
\end{equation}
The strongest honest local form is therefore
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:MC2_Vtheta}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)
=
a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2+a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i.
\label{eq:MC2_Mtheta}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{3.4 Even/odd low modes and projected overlap}

Let
\begin{equation}
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad a=1,2,
\label{eq:MC2_u_pm}
\end{equation}
with \(f_+\) even and \(f_-\) odd.
Then the projected mixed matrices are
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\label{eq:MC2_Mmixed}
\end{equation}
Same-parity overlaps vanish, while the mixed even/odd overlap survives.

\subsubsection{3.5 Explicit nonzero overlap scale}

For the explicit profiles
\begin{equation}
f_+(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{\kappa}{2}}\,\sech(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
f_-(\xi)=\sqrt{\frac{3\kappa}{2}}\,\tanh(\kappa\xi)\sech(\kappa\xi),
\label{eq:MC2_fpm}
\end{equation}
one finds
\begin{equation}
I_\theta
:=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa.
\label{eq:MC2_Itheta}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
I_\theta\neq 0
\qquad
(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0).
\label{eq:MC2_Itheta_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\subsection{4. Residual symmetry and the natural local branch}

\subsubsection{4.1 Traceless transport splitting}

Because \(\partial_\xi z_B=\theta' e_1\) singles out \(e_1\), the traceless Hermitian transport sector splits as
\begin{equation}
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathbb R\,\sigma_3
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{\sigma_1,\sigma_2\}.
\label{eq:MC2_trsplit}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{4.2 Worldvolume splitting}

The local defect/worldvolume momentum directions split naturally as
\begin{equation}
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{wv}}
=
\mathbb R\,p_\parallel
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{p_1,p_2\}.
\label{eq:MC2_wvsplit}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{4.3 Natural S2 branch}

Therefore the natural local symmetry-compatible branch is S2:
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:MC2_S2}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\Lambda=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha & -\beta & 0\\
\beta & \alpha & 0\\
0 & 0 & \lambda_\parallel
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\det\Lambda=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2).
\label{eq:MC2_Lambda}
\end{equation}
Hence the S2 two-witness condition is
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:MC2_two_witness}
\end{equation}

S1 would require keeping only \(p_\parallel\sigma_3\), which is not forced by the local geometry and instead needs an extra symmetry, truncation, or fine tuning.

\subsection{5. Primitive and commutator channels}

\subsubsection{5.1 Primitive channel is too coarse}

The canonical primitive traceless tensor is
\begin{equation}
T(P)=3P-\mathbf 1_3.
\label{eq:MC2_primitive}
\end{equation}
But on the tangent bundle \(Q_B\),
\begin{equation}
T(P_B)\big|_{Q_B}=-\mathbf 1_{Q_B}.
\label{eq:MC2_primitive_Q}
\end{equation}
So the primitive channel gives only identity-valued transport on \(Q_B\), not a full Pauli triplet.

\subsubsection{5.2 Commutator channel is the first genuine gradient-sensitive refinement}

Define
\begin{equation}
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B].
\label{eq:MC2_Txi}
\end{equation}
Using the explicit background,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal T_\xi
=
i\theta'(\xi)\bigl(z_Be_1^\dagger-e_1z_B^\dagger\bigr).
\label{eq:MC2_Txi_explicit}
\end{equation}
This exchanges the projector line \(\mathbb Cz_B\) and the distinguished tangent line \(\mathbb Ce_1\), and annihilates \(e_2\).

Direct restriction gives
\begin{equation}
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi\Pi_Q=0,
\label{eq:MC2_Txi_zero}
\end{equation}
but the induced quadratic channel is
\begin{equation}
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\bigl(\mathbf 1_2+\sigma_3\bigr).
\label{eq:MC2_Txi_sq}
\end{equation}
Thus the commutator channel naturally produces a \(\sigma_3\)-type splitting, but not the full \((\sigma_1,\sigma_2,\sigma_3)\) triplet.

\subsection{6. Minimal composite transport operator producing the full S2 triplet}

\subsubsection{6.1 The concrete transport action}

The minimal composite microscopic transport action is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{trans}}^{\min}
=
-i\,\eta^\dagger
\Big[
g_c\,\theta'(\xi)\,(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
+
g_E\,\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
g_O\,\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Big]\partial_{y^\mu}\eta.
\label{eq:MC2_Ltrans}
\end{equation}
Using
\begin{equation}
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\sigma_3,
\label{eq:MC2_Ttr}
\end{equation}
this becomes
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{trans}}^{\min}
=
-i\,\eta^\dagger
\Big[
\frac{g_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
g_E\,\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
g_O\,\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Big]\partial_{y^\mu}\eta.
\label{eq:MC2_Ltrans_explicit}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{6.2 Projection and witness coefficients}

Projecting onto the graded low modes gives
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta.
\label{eq:MC2_witnesses}
\end{equation}
Here
\begin{equation}
I_{\theta'^3}:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^3.
\label{eq:MC2_I3prime_def}
\end{equation}
For the explicit defect profile one finds
\begin{equation}
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
\label{eq:MC2_I3prime}
\end{equation}
Therefore the explicit witnesses are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\label{eq:MC2_lambda_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
\label{eq:MC2_alpha_beta_final}
\end{equation}

Hence the full S2 nondegeneracy condition is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:MC2_gc_condition}
\end{equation}

\subsection{7. What is actually proved vs. what remains open}

\subsubsection{7.1 Proved / reduced}

The following are now sharply established:

\begin{enumerate}
\item plain scalar Bragg route is insufficient;
\item refined projector-stiffness model alone is insufficient;
\item Class II gives derivative witnesses but not identity-channel cancellation;
\item graded \(2+2\) reduced Dirac theorem is rigorous;
\item the actual local CP\(^2\) projector-defect geometry belongs to this operator class;
\item the natural local symmetry-compatible branch is S2;
\item a concrete microscopic transport action producing the three S2 witnesses has been written;
\item the final local witness problem is reduced to three constants \(g_c,g_E,g_O\).
\end{enumerate}

\subsubsection{7.2 Still open}

The genuine remaining frontier is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item derive the final full microscopic TECT projector/condensate PDE in a form suitable for direct spectral analysis;
\item derive the above transport term from complete TECT rather than postulate it as the minimal concrete ansatz;
\item compute the actual microscopic values of
\[
g_c,\qquad g_E,\qquad g_O;
\]
\item verify that in complete TECT one indeed has
\[
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{8. Strongest honest conclusion}

The strongest justified current statement is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Dirac emergence is rigorously proved as a reduced spectral theorem,}
}
\label{eq:MC2_conc1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the actual local CP}^2\text{ projector-defect geometry is naturally compatible with the S2 branch,}
}
\label{eq:MC2_conc2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{and the full local witness problem is reduced to the finite coefficient test }
g_c\neq 0,\ (g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0),
}
\label{eq:MC2_conc3}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the actual values of }g_c,g_E,g_O\text{ from complete microscopic TECT remain open.}
}
\label{eq:MC2_conc4}
\end{equation}

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\textbf{Closed:}
\]

1. The plain scalar shell-pair route is insufficient because it yields a genuine constant Bragg block
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2\neq 0.
\]

2. The refined projector-stiffness model alone gives
\[
J=0,
\]
so it does not generate the needed shell/projector mixing.

3. Class II yields
\[
\delta N_{ij}^a\neq 0,
\]
hence renormalizes the derivative witness sector, but it does not cancel the scalar Bragg mass.

4. The graded \(2+2\) reduced theorem is rigorous:
if the projected infrared sector is grading-odd, first-order, and has nondegenerate mixed symbol, then the principal operator is Dirac.

5. The actual local CP\(^2\) projector-defect geometry belongs to this operator class:
\[
Q_B=(\mathbb C z_B)^\perp,
\qquad
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\]

6. The natural local branch is S2:
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]

7. The primitive projector channel is too coarse on \(Q_B\), while the commutator channel
\[
\mathcal T_\xi=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B]
\]
naturally provides the longitudinal \(\sigma_3\)-type splitting.

8. A concrete minimal microscopic transport action is
\[
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{trans}}^{\min}
=
-i\,\eta^\dagger
\Big[
g_c\,\theta'(\xi)\,(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
+
g_E\,\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
g_O\,\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Big]\partial_{y^\mu}\eta.
\]

9. Its projected witnesses are
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
\]

Therefore the full local S2 nondegeneracy condition is exactly
\[
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

\[
\textbf{Still open:}
\]

1. the final full microscopic TECT projector/condensate PDE suitable for direct spectral analysis;

2. the derivation of the concrete transport term above from complete TECT rather than choosing it as the minimal local ansatz;

3. the actual microscopic values of
\[
g_c,\qquad g_E,\qquad g_O;
\]

4. the direct proof that complete TECT indeed gives
\[
g_c\neq 0,\qquad (g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
\]

Thus the strongest honest current conclusion is
\[
\boxed{
\text{Dirac emergence is rigorously proved at the reduced spectral level,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{the local CP}^2\text{ defect geometry supports the required S2 structure,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the complete microscopic closure of TECT is now reduced to the finite coefficient extraction }(g_c,g_E,g_O).
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Finite witness closure for the concrete S2 transport ansatz}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now show that the remaining microscopic coefficient problem for
\[
g_c,\qquad g_E,\qquad g_O
\]
is not an infinite-dimensional PDE problem anymore, but a finite witness-construction problem on the symmetry-allowed microscopic tensor space.

\subsubsection{A. Concrete S2 transport ansatz and the reduced witnesses}

From the previously constructed concrete microscopic transport action,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{trans}}^{\min}
=
-i\,\eta^\dagger
\Big[
g_c\,\theta'(\xi)\,(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
+
g_E\,\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
g_O\,\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Big]\partial_{y^\mu}\eta,
\label{eq:FW_Ltrans}
\end{equation}
one obtains the reduced mixed symbol
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\label{eq:FW_A1}
\end{equation}
with explicit coefficients
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\label{eq:FW_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
\label{eq:FW_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}
Hence the S2 nondegeneracy condition
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad (\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)
\]
is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:FW_gc_condition}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{B. Finite-dimensional tensor-space viewpoint}

Let \(V_{\mathrm{mic}}\) denote the finite-dimensional real vector space of all symmetry-allowed microscopic transport tensors that survive the linearization of the actual TECT condensate around the chosen defect background.
This is the exact structural viewpoint already adopted in the shell-level Weyl/Dirac analysis: the remaining microscopic data live in a finite-dimensional allowed tensor space, not in an unconstrained infinite-dimensional function space. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3} :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

Inside \(V_{\mathrm{mic}}\), define the three witness functionals corresponding to the concrete S2 ansatz:

\begin{equation}
W_\parallel(N):=g_c(N),
\label{eq:FW_Wpar}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
W_E(N):=g_E(N),
\qquad
W_O(N):=g_O(N).
\label{eq:FW_WEWO}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, after projection to the reduced symbol,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel(N)=c_\parallel\,W_\parallel(N),
\qquad
\alpha(N)=c_\perp\,W_E(N),
\qquad
\beta(N)=c_\perp\,W_O(N),
\label{eq:FW_lambda_alpha_beta_fun}
\end{equation}
where
\[
c_\parallel=-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
c_\perp=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa.
\]
For nontrivial defect amplitude, both constants are nonzero.

Thus the reduced Dirac witness problem is finite-dimensional from the start.

\subsubsection{C. Longitudinal and transverse witness functionals}

Define the longitudinal witness functional
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak W_\parallel(N):=\lambda_\parallel(N).
\label{eq:FW_long_functional}
\end{equation}
This is linear in the microscopic tensor \(N\), because the projected mixed overlap is linear in the transport kernel \(V^\mu\), and \(V^\mu\) is linear in the microscopic transport tensor by construction. This is precisely the same linear-functional structure emphasized in the finite-dimensional shell genericity theorem. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

For the transverse sector, define the \(2\times 2\) reduced transverse matrix
\begin{equation}
T_\perp(N):=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha(N) & -\beta(N)\\
\beta(N) & \alpha(N)
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:FW_Tperp}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\det T_\perp(N)=\alpha(N)^2+\beta(N)^2.
\label{eq:FW_detT}
\end{equation}
This is a polynomial functional on \(V_{\mathrm{mic}}\).

Therefore the full S2 witness condition is
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak W_\parallel(N)\neq 0,
\qquad
\det T_\perp(N)\neq 0.
\label{eq:FW_two_conditions}
\end{equation}

This is exactly parallel to the shell-level Weyl criterion
\[
v_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad \det T\neq 0,
\]
which the manuscript already proved is the correct finite witness reduction. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\subsubsection{D. Exact dichotomy: symmetry-forbidden vs generic nonvanishing}

The finite-dimensional genericity theorem says:

\begin{enumerate}
\item if a linear witness functional vanishes identically on the allowed space, then the channel is symmetry-forbidden;

\item if it is nonzero on even a single admissible tensor, then it is nonzero on an open dense full-measure subset.
\end{enumerate}
:contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

Applying this to the present concrete S2 witnesses gives the exact dichotomy:

\paragraph{Longitudinal channel.}
Either
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak W_\parallel|_{V_{\mathrm{mic}}}\equiv 0,
\label{eq:FW_long_forbidden}
\end{equation}
in which case the commutator-induced singlet channel is symmetry-forbidden in the actual microscopic TECT linearization,

or else there exists a single admissible seed tensor \(N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\in V_{\mathrm{mic}}\) such that
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak W_\parallel\bigl(N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\bigr)\neq 0,
\label{eq:FW_long_seed}
\end{equation}
and then
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak W_\parallel(N)\neq 0
\quad\text{for an open dense full-measure subset of }V_{\mathrm{mic}}.
\label{eq:FW_long_generic}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Transverse sector.}
Either
\begin{equation}
\det T_\perp(N)\equiv 0
\quad\forall N\in V_{\mathrm{mic}},
\label{eq:FW_perp_forbidden}
\end{equation}
in which case the transverse doublet channel is symmetry-forbidden or projected out exactly,

or else there exists a single admissible seed tensor \(N^{(\perp)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\in V_{\mathrm{mic}}\) such that
\begin{equation}
\det T_\perp\bigl(N^{(\perp)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\bigr)\neq 0,
\label{eq:FW_perp_seed}
\end{equation}
and then
\begin{equation}
\det T_\perp(N)\neq 0
\quad\text{for an open dense full-measure subset of }V_{\mathrm{mic}}.
\label{eq:FW_perp_generic}
\end{equation}

This is the direct S2 analogue of the shell-level witness theorem
\[
W_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad (W_I,W_J)\neq (0,0),
\]
or equivalently
\[
v_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad \det T\neq 0,
\]
already proved in the uploaded manuscripts. 

\subsubsection{E. Finite witness closure theorem for the concrete transport ansatz}

We can now state the concrete closure result.

\begin{theorem}[Finite witness closure for the concrete S2 transport ansatz]
Let \(V_{\mathrm{mic}}\) be the finite-dimensional space of symmetry-allowed microscopic transport tensors in the actual TECT linearization around the chosen CP\(^2\) defect background.
Let
\[
\mathfrak W_\parallel(N)=\lambda_\parallel(N)
\]
be the longitudinal witness functional induced by the commutator-based singlet channel, and let
\[
T_\perp(N)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha(N) & -\beta(N)\\
\beta(N) & \alpha(N)
\end{pmatrix}
\]
be the transverse reduced matrix induced by the doublet channels.

Assume there exist:

\begin{enumerate}
\item one admissible longitudinal seed tensor \(N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\in V_{\mathrm{mic}}\) with
\[
\mathfrak W_\parallel\bigl(N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\bigr)\neq 0;
\]

\item one admissible transverse seed tensor \(N^{(\perp)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\in V_{\mathrm{mic}}\) with
\[
\det T_\perp\bigl(N^{(\perp)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\bigr)\neq 0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Then, for an open dense full-measure subset of \(V_{\mathrm{mic}}\),
\begin{equation}
g_c(N)\neq 0,
\qquad
\bigl(g_E(N),g_O(N)\bigr)\neq (0,0),
\label{eq:FW_concrete_generic}
\end{equation}
equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel(N)\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha(N),\beta(N))\neq (0,0),
\label{eq:FW_concrete_generic_witness}
\end{equation}
and the reduced S2 symbol is nondegenerate.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The longitudinal witness is linear on the finite-dimensional space \(V_{\mathrm{mic}}\), so if it is nonzero on one seed tensor, it is not identically zero; hence its zero set is a proper hyperplane and its complement is open dense full measure. :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9}

The transverse determinant is a polynomial functional on \(V_{\mathrm{mic}}\). If it is nonzero at one point, it is not identically zero; therefore its zero set is a proper algebraic subset with empty interior and measure zero. This is the same finite-dimensional logic used in the shell-level Weyl determinant theorem. :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10}

Intersecting the two open dense full-measure good sets proves the claim.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{F. What remains genuinely open}

The remaining microscopic task is therefore no longer:

\[
\text{``solve the full PDE and compute everything exactly''}.
\]

Instead, it is the finite explicit witness problem:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{construct one admissible longitudinal seed tensor and one admissible transverse doublet seed tensor in the actual TECT microscopic transport space.}
}
\label{eq:FW_remaining_task}
\end{equation}

Once this is done, the concrete transport ansatz closes generically at the witness level.

\paragraph{Honest status.}
What is still not proved is that the complete microscopic TECT dynamics actually generates such seeds.
What \emph{is} now proved is that \emph{if} those two seeds exist, then the nonvanishing of \(g_c\) and \((g_E,g_O)\) is generic and the concrete S2 transport ansatz is enough to produce the required local Weyl/Dirac witnesses.

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
\]

Thus the concrete S2 witness condition is
\[
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
\]

Let \(V_{\mathrm{mic}}\) be the finite-dimensional space of symmetry-allowed microscopic transport tensors in the actual TECT linearization.
Define the longitudinal witness
\[
\mathfrak W_\parallel(N):=\lambda_\parallel(N),
\]
and the transverse reduced matrix
\[
T_\perp(N)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha(N) & -\beta(N)\\
\beta(N) & \alpha(N)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\det T_\perp(N)=\alpha(N)^2+\beta(N)^2.
\]

Then the remaining microscopic problem is exactly the finite witness problem:

\[
\text{find one }N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\in V_{\mathrm{mic}}
\text{ with }
\mathfrak W_\parallel\bigl(N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\bigr)\neq 0,
\]
\[
\text{find one }N^{(\perp)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\in V_{\mathrm{mic}}
\text{ with }
\det T_\perp\bigl(N^{(\perp)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\bigr)\neq 0.
\]

If such seeds exist, then by finite-dimensional genericity:
\[
g_c(N)\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E(N),g_O(N))\neq (0,0)
\]
hold on an open dense full-measure subset of \(V_{\mathrm{mic}}\).

Therefore the complete microscopic closure of the concrete S2 transport ansatz is reduced to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{one longitudinal seed witness + one transverse doublet seed witness.}
}
\]

Nothing more is needed at the theorem level.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Explicit seed construction inside the concrete S2 transport ansatz space}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now explicitly construct one longitudinal seed tensor and one transverse seed tensor inside the concrete microscopic transport ansatz space, and show that the corresponding witnesses are manifestly nonzero.

\subsubsection{A. Concrete transport ansatz recalled}

We work with the concrete microscopic transport action
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{trans}}^{\min}
=
-i\,\eta^\dagger
\Big[
g_c\,\theta'(\xi)\,(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
+
g_E\,\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
g_O\,\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Big]\partial_{y^\mu}\eta,
\label{eq:seed_Ltrans}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\mathcal T_\xi=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B],
\qquad
\Pi_Q=\mathbf 1_3-P_B.
\]

From the previous computation,
\begin{equation}
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\sigma_3,
\label{eq:seed_Ttr}
\end{equation}
so the transport kernel is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)
=
\frac{g_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
g_E\,\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
g_O\,\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\qquad a=1,2.
\label{eq:seed_Vmu_general}
\end{equation}

Projecting onto the graded low modes gives the reduced witnesses
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta,
\label{eq:seed_witness_general}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
I_\theta
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi),
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^3.
\label{eq:seed_integrals}
\end{equation}
For the explicit defect profile,
\begin{equation}
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa\neq 0,
\label{eq:seed_Itheta}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3\neq 0
\label{eq:seed_Itheta3}
\end{equation}
for nontrivial defect amplitude \(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0\).

\subsubsection{B. Longitudinal seed tensor}

Define the explicit longitudinal seed transport kernel
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
:=
\theta'(\xi)\,(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:seed_longitudinal_kernel}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, this is the concrete ansatz \eqref{eq:seed_Vmu_general} with
\[
g_c=1,\qquad g_E=0,\qquad g_O=0.
\]

Therefore the projected witnesses are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel\bigl(N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\bigr)
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3},
\label{eq:seed_long_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha\bigl(N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\bigr)=0,
\qquad
\beta\bigl(N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\bigr)=0.
\label{eq:seed_long_ab}
\end{equation}
Since \(I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\bigl(N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\bigr)\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:seed_long_nonzero}
\end{equation}

Thus an explicit longitudinal seed witness exists.

\subsubsection{C. Transverse seed tensor}

Define the explicit transverse-even seed transport kernel
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}(\xi)
:=
\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
}
\label{eq:seed_transverse_E_kernel}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, this is \eqref{eq:seed_Vmu_general} with
\[
g_c=0,\qquad g_E=1,\qquad g_O=0.
\]

Then the projected witnesses are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel\bigl(N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\bigr)=0,
\label{eq:seed_perpE_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha\bigl(N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\bigr)=I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta\bigl(N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\bigr)=0.
\label{eq:seed_perpE_ab}
\end{equation}
Hence the reduced transverse matrix is
\begin{equation}
T_\perp\bigl(N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\bigr)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
I_\theta & 0\\
0 & I_\theta
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:seed_perpE_matrix}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\det T_\perp\bigl(N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\bigr)
=
I_\theta^2>0.
\label{eq:seed_perpE_det}
\end{equation}

Thus an explicit transverse seed witness exists.

\subsubsection{D. Optional transverse-odd seed}

Similarly, define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\perp,O)}(\xi)
:=
\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
}
\label{eq:seed_transverse_O_kernel}
\end{equation}
This corresponds to
\[
g_c=0,\qquad g_E=0,\qquad g_O=1,
\]
and gives
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel\bigl(N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\bigr)=0,
\qquad
\alpha\bigl(N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\bigr)=0,
\qquad
\beta\bigl(N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\bigr)=I_\theta\neq 0.
\label{eq:seed_perpO}
\end{equation}

So the transverse witness may be realized in either the even or odd doublet channel.

\subsubsection{E. Closure inside the concrete ansatz subspace}

Now define the concrete seed subspace
\begin{equation}
V_{\mathrm{seed}}
:=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\Bigl\{
N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
\Bigr\}.
\label{eq:seed_subspace}
\end{equation}
An arbitrary element of this subspace has the form
\begin{equation}
N
=
c_\parallel N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
+
c_E N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
+
c_O N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}}.
\label{eq:seed_general_element}
\end{equation}
By linearity of the projected transport kernel,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel(N)
=
\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\label{eq:seed_general_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha(N)=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta(N)=c_O I_\theta.
\label{eq:seed_general_ab}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel(N)\neq 0
\iff
c_\parallel\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:seed_general_long}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\alpha(N),\beta(N))\neq (0,0)
\iff
(c_E,c_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:seed_general_perp}
\end{equation}

Hence, inside the concrete ansatz subspace \(V_{\mathrm{seed}}\), the S2 nondegeneracy condition is \emph{exactly}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_E,c_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:seed_exact_condition}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{F. Exact closure statement}

This yields the following exact closure result.

\begin{proposition}[Exact closure inside the concrete seed subspace]
Inside the concrete transport ansatz subspace
\[
V_{\mathrm{seed}}
=
\mathrm{span}\{N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}},N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}},N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\},
\]
the reduced S2 symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\label{eq:seed_prop_A1}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
\label{eq:seed_prop_coeff}
\end{equation}
Since \(I_\theta\neq 0\) and \(I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0\) for nontrivial defect amplitude, the S2 symbol is nondegenerate if and only if
\begin{equation}
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_E,c_O)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:seed_prop_condition}
\end{equation}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from \eqref{eq:seed_general_lambda}--\eqref{eq:seed_general_ab}.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{G. Honest conclusion}

This is stronger than the earlier generic witness theorem in one important sense:

we no longer merely know that seed witnesses would imply generic closure;
we now have explicit seed tensors that realize the longitudinal and transverse witnesses \emph{inside the chosen concrete ansatz space itself}.

What remains open is more specific:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the complete microscopic TECT transport space actually contain }V_{\mathrm{seed}}\text{ (or at least its two seed directions)?}
}
\label{eq:seed_final_open}
\end{equation}

Thus the remaining frontier is no longer witness existence inside the concrete ansatz.
It is the embedding of this explicit seed subspace into the complete microscopic TECT transport space.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\textbf{Explicit longitudinal seed:}\qquad
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.

It gives

\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\qquad

\[

V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.

It gives

\qquad

\qquad
\beta=0,
\]
hence

\]
gives
\[
\lambda_\parallel=0,
\qquad
\alpha=0,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\neq 0.
\]

Define
\[
V_{\mathrm{seed}}
=
\mathrm{span}\{N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}},N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}},N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\}.
\]
For
\[
N=c_\parallel N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
+c_E N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
+c_O N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
\]
the reduced S2 witnesses are exactly
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
\]

Since
\[
I_\theta\neq 0,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\]
the S2 symbol is nondegenerate if and only if
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_E,c_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

So inside the concrete ansatz space itself, the finite witness problem is already exactly closed.

The only remaining open question is whether complete microscopic TECT actually contains this seed subspace (or at least the two seed directions) in its true transport tensor space.
