\subsection{Embedding of the explicit seed subspace into the allowed microscopic transport space}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We show that the explicit seed subspace
\[
V_{\mathrm{seed}}
=
\mathrm{span}\Bigl\{
N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
\Bigr\}
\]
is not an arbitrary effective construction, but can be embedded into the class of symmetry-allowed microscopic TECT transport couplings already identified in the uploaded derivations.

\subsubsection{A. Allowed microscopic carrier structure}

The microscopic classification theorem already established that any UV source able to induce a first-order enriched tensor must carry simultaneously:

\begin{enumerate}
\item one spatial derivative index \(i\) or \(j\),
\item one internal reduced-shell/tangent index \(a\).
\end{enumerate}

More precisely, the generic target quadratic mixing form is
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(2)}
=
\Lambda^a_{ij}(\partial_i\phi_0)(D_j\psi)\,\xi^a+\text{h.c.}
\label{eq:embed_target}
\end{equation}
and this already implies that the UV extension must introduce an \((i,a)\)-carrier. Pure scalar or pure projector corrections are insufficient. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

At lowest derivative order, the minimal viable local classes are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item direct shell--projector derivative couplings (Class I),
\item heavy auxiliary internal vector mediators \(X_i^a\) (Class II),
\item connection-like mediators \(A_i^a\) (Class III).
\end{enumerate}


Thus the allowed microscopic transport space already contains exactly the type of tensor carrier our explicit seeds require.

\subsubsection{B. Shell-level minimal witness basis}

The shell-level Weyl reduction already identified the minimal symmetry-compatible microscopic tensor family:
\begin{equation}
N_{ij}^{3}=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\label{eq:shell_A_tensor}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
N_{ij}^{1}=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\label{eq:shell_BC1_tensor}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
N_{ij}^{2}=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\label{eq:shell_BC2_tensor}
\end{equation}
for which the reduced coefficients satisfy
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel\propto A,
\qquad
\alpha\propto B,
\qquad
\beta\propto C.
\label{eq:shell_ABC_reduce}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, the local Weyl/Dirac problem is exactly the finite coefficient test
\begin{equation}
A\neq 0,
\qquad
(B,C)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:shell_ABC_condition}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

This provides the precise microscopic template with which the explicit defect/projector seeds should be compared.

\subsubsection{C. Defect/projector version of the same three channels}

In the local CP\(^2\) defect geometry, the natural S2 splitting is

\[
\text{longitudinal singlet} \leftrightarrow \sigma_3,
\qquad
\text{transverse doublet} \leftrightarrow (\sigma_1,\sigma_2).
\]

The explicit seed transport kernels we constructed are:

\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\label{eq:embed_seed_long}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\label{eq:embed_seed_even}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\perp,O)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\label{eq:embed_seed_odd}
\end{equation}

These are the exact defect/projector analogues of the shell-level tensors \eqref{eq:shell_A_tensor}--\eqref{eq:shell_BC2_tensor}:

\begin{equation}
A \ \leftrightarrow\ N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
\qquad
B \ \leftrightarrow\ N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
\qquad
C \ \leftrightarrow\ N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}}.
\label{eq:embed_dictionary}
\end{equation}

So the seed subspace \(V_{\mathrm{seed}}\) is exactly the defect/projector realization of the already-proved three-parameter microscopic witness basis.

\subsubsection{D. Explicit embedding through Class I}

Class I already allows direct local derivative couplings of the form
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(I)}
=
\Lambda^a_{ij}(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger)T_a\Psi\,(T_a\partial_jP)
+\text{h.c.}
\label{eq:ClassI_embed}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

After expansion around the locked background and reduction to the tangent channel \(\xi^a\), this produces the target structure
\[
(\partial_i\phi_0)(D_j\psi)\,\xi^a.
\]
Now choose the coefficient tensors \(\Lambda^a_{ij}\) in the three basis forms
\begin{equation}
\Lambda^{3}_{ij}=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\label{eq:embed_Lambda3}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\Lambda^{1}_{ij}=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\label{eq:embed_Lambda1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\Lambda^{2}_{ij}=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
\label{eq:embed_Lambda2}
\end{equation}
These are symmetry-allowed by the microscopic shell-level analysis and already generate the three reduced coefficients \((\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)\). 

Therefore Class I already contains a microscopic three-dimensional subspace whose reduced defect/projector image is isomorphic to \(V_{\mathrm{seed}}\).

\subsubsection{E. Explicit embedding through Class II}

Class II introduces a heavy auxiliary internal vector mediator \(X_i^a\):
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(II)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+\alpha X_i^a(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger T_a\Psi+\text{h.c.})
+\beta X_i^a\partial_i\delta P^a\psi.
\label{eq:ClassII_embed}
\end{equation}
Eliminating \(X_i^a\) generates precisely the target first-order enriched structure
\[
(\partial_i\phi_0)(\partial_j\psi)\,\xi^a,
\]
hence a nonzero \(\delta N^a_{ij}\). :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

Now choose the shell/projector current carried by \(X_i^a\) to project onto the same three basis tensors \eqref{eq:embed_Lambda3}--\eqref{eq:embed_Lambda2}.
Then the reduced low-energy transport coefficients again span the same three-dimensional space \((A,B,C)\), hence the same seed subspace.

Therefore Class II also admits an embedding of \(V_{\mathrm{seed}}\).

\subsubsection{F. Embedding theorem}

We may now state the exact result.

\begin{theorem}[Embedding of the explicit seed subspace]
Assume the true microscopic TECT transport sector contains at least one of the minimal viable UV extension classes identified in the classification theorem, namely Class I or Class II.

Then there exists a three-dimensional microscopic tensor subspace
\[
V_{\mathrm{mic}}^{(3)}\subset V_{\mathrm{mic}}
\]
whose reduced defect/projector image is isomorphic to
\[
V_{\mathrm{seed}}
=
\mathrm{span}\Bigl\{
N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
\Bigr\}.
\]

Equivalently, the longitudinal seed witness and the transverse doublet seed witnesses can be realized by admissible microscopic transport tensors.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Class I and Class II both supply the required \((i,a)\)-carrier structure \eqref{eq:embed_target}. The shell-level witness analysis already proved that the three tensors \eqref{eq:embed_Lambda3}--\eqref{eq:embed_Lambda2} form the minimal symmetry-compatible microscopic basis controlling the reduced coefficients \((\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)\). 

The explicit defect/projector seeds \eqref{eq:embed_seed_long}--\eqref{eq:embed_seed_odd} are exactly the local projector realization of those three channels under the dictionary \eqref{eq:embed_dictionary}. Hence the reduced image of the three-dimensional microscopic basis is isomorphic to \(V_{\mathrm{seed}}\).
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{G. Honest final status}

What is now genuinely closed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the finite witness problem is explicitly solved inside the concrete ansatz space;
\item the seed subspace \(V_{\mathrm{seed}}\) is compatible with the already-classified allowed microscopic UV carrier structures;
\item if complete TECT realizes Class I or Class II, then the explicit seed directions are admissible microscopic transport directions.
\end{enumerate}

What is still open:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{which minimal UV class (if any) is actually realized by the true full microscopic TECT dynamics.}
}
\label{eq:embed_open}
\end{equation}

So the remaining frontier is no longer witness construction or local operator structure.
It is a model-selection / microscopic-realization question.

\subsection{Why Class II is the natural microscopic choice for TECT at the current stage}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now justify why the Class II UV completion --- the heavy auxiliary internal vector mediator \(X_i^a\) --- is the most natural microscopic carrier for the remaining TECT Dirac-emergence problem, and reinterpret the previously constructed concrete witness coefficients in that language.

\subsubsection{A. The remaining problem requires an \texorpdfstring{$(i,a)$}{(i,a)} carrier}

The final local witness problem was reduced to three coefficients
\[
g_c,\qquad g_E,\qquad g_O,
\]
appearing in the concrete transport action
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{trans}}^{\min}
=
-i\,\eta^\dagger
\Big[
g_c\,\theta'(\xi)\,(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
+
g_E\,\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
g_O\,\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Big]\partial_{y^\mu}\eta.
\label{eq:classII_Ltrans_min}
\end{equation}
This action requires a microscopic source carrying simultaneously:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a spatial / derivative index \(i\) or \(j\),
\item an internal reduced-shell / tangent index \(a\).
\end{enumerate}

The classification theorem already established that any viable UV completion must provide exactly such an \((i,a)\)-carrier, and that pure scalar or pure projector corrections are insufficient. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

\subsubsection{B. Why Class II is the most natural realization of the required carrier}

The minimal viable classes already identified are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Class I: direct shell--projector derivative coupling,
\item Class II: heavy auxiliary internal vector mediator \(X_i^a\),
\item Class III: connection-like mediator.
\end{enumerate}


Among them, Class II is the most natural present choice because the mediator
\begin{equation}
X_i^a
\label{eq:classII_X}
\end{equation}
already carries the exact index structure needed for the enriched first-order tensor:
one spatial index \(i\) and one internal index \(a\).

The Class II UV action has the schematic form
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(II)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+\alpha\,X_i^a J_i^a(\Psi)
+\beta\,X_i^a K_i^a(P,\delta P),
\label{eq:classII_schematic}
\end{equation}
where \(J_i^a(\Psi)\) is the shell/current source and \(K_i^a(P,\delta P)\) is the projector/tangent source.
Eliminating \(X_i^a\) generates an effective interaction of the target type
\[
(\partial_i\phi_0)(D_j\psi)\,\xi^a,
\]
and the document already verified that this leads to a nonzero shell-enriched tensor
\begin{equation}
\delta N_{ij}^a\neq 0.
\label{eq:classII_deltaN_again}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

Thus Class II is not merely allowed; it is precisely the minimal UV carrier structure matching the final reduced witness problem.

\subsubsection{C. Comparison with the other classes}

\paragraph{Pure scalar / pure projector corrections.}
These fail because they do not carry the required \((i,a)\) structure. They cannot produce the enriched mixed tensor needed for the first-order reduced symbol. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\paragraph{Primitive projector channel \(3P-\mathbf 1_3\).}
This is a useful internal tensor, but on \(Q_B\) it reduces to the identity, so by itself it is too coarse to generate the full S2 Pauli triplet.

\paragraph{Class I.}
Class I also works in principle:
\[
L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(2)}=\Lambda^a_{ij}(\partial_i\phi_0)(D_j\psi)\xi^a+\text{h.c.}
\]
But it inserts the needed carrier tensor \(\Lambda^a_{ij}\) directly by hand. It is therefore less explanatory microscopically than Class II, where the same tensor is generated dynamically by integrating out \(X_i^a\). :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\paragraph{Class III.}
Class III is plausible but currently less explicit in the present derivation chain. At this stage it is weaker as a concrete closure candidate than Class II.

Therefore the natural priority ordering is:
\[
\text{Class II} \;>\; \text{Class I} \;>\; \text{Class III},
\]
for the current TECT closure problem.

\subsubsection{D. Reinterpretation of the seed subspace in Class II language}

Previously we constructed the explicit seed subspace
\begin{equation}
V_{\mathrm{seed}}
=
\mathrm{span}\Bigl\{
N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
\Bigr\}.

The shell-level minimal witness basis is

\qquad
N_{ij}^{2}=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\label{eq:classII_ABC}
\end{equation}
and it reduces exactly to
\[
\lambda_\parallel\propto A,\qquad
\alpha\propto B,\qquad
\beta\propto C.
\]
:contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

In the Class II interpretation, these three channels correspond naturally to the three internal mediator directions:
\begin{equation}
X_i^3 \leftrightarrow \text{longitudinal singlet seed},
\label{eq:classII_X3}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}

Hence the explicit defect/projector seed basis is exactly the local realization of the Class II carrier decomposition.

\subsubsection{E. Interpretation of \texorpdfstring{$g_c,g_E,g_O$}{g_c,g_E,g_O}}

Under this reading, the three witness coefficients in the concrete transport action

g_c,\qquad g_E,\qquad g_O

g_c\neq 0,

\section{Dirac Emergence via the Class II Microscopic Carrier}

\subsection{Logical status}

In this section we separate three layers of the argument:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a rigorously proved reduced spectral theorem;
\item a local geometric compatibility statement for the CP\(^2\) projector-defect sector;
\item a concrete Class II microscopic ansatz yielding explicit low-energy witnesses.
\end{enumerate}

Only the first item is claimed as a theorem in the strict reduced-operator sense.
The second is a local structural proposition.
The third is a concrete microscopic ansatz proposition, not yet a derivation from the final complete TECT PDE.

\subsection{The reduced graded Dirac theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Reduced graded \(2+2\) Dirac emergence]
Let \(K\subset H\) be an isolated four-dimensional infrared sector with a grading
\[
K=K_+\oplus K_-,
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}K_\pm=2.
\]
Assume the projected leading operator takes the form
\[
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu,
\]
and assume \(A_1(p)\) is nondegenerate for generic \(p\neq 0\).
Then the reduced principal symbol is Dirac type.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The grading forces the diagonal blocks to vanish.
The first-order mixed symbol defines a Clifford-type linearization once it is nondegenerate.
After a linear change of momenta and a unitary change of graded basis, one obtains the canonical Dirac form.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Local CP\(^2\) projector-defect geometry}

Let the explicit local defect background be
\[
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi),
\qquad
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\sech(\kappa\xi),
\]
with projector
\[
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B(\xi)^\dagger.
\]
Its tangent bundle is
\[
Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp.
\]
Choose the local orthonormal frame
\[
e_1(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_2(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\
1\\
0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Then
\[
\partial_\xi z_B=\theta'(\xi)e_1,
\qquad
\partial_\xi P_B=\theta'(\xi)(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger).
\]

\begin{proposition}[Local odd transport structure]
In the local projector-defect sector, the leading first-order transport operator has the form
\[
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi),
\]
and the strongest honest local form is
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\]
where \(\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\) is a Hermitian \(Q_B\)-endomorphism.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Reflection symmetry makes \(P_B\) even and \(\partial_\xi P_B\) odd.
The leading transport term is linear in the background gradient and first-order in worldvolume derivatives.
Therefore it factors through \(\theta'(\xi)\), and its fiber action is an endomorphism of \(Q_B\).
\end{proof}

In a local \(Q_B\)-frame, write
\[
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)=a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2+a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i.
\]

\subsection{Natural S2 local branch}

The defect gradient singles out one preferred tangent direction \(e_1\), so the traceless fiber sector splits as
\[
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathbb R\,\sigma_3
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{\sigma_1,\sigma_2\}.
\]
The worldvolume momentum directions split naturally as
\[
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{wv}}
=
\mathbb R\,p_\parallel
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{p_1,p_2\}.
\]

\begin{proposition}[Natural local S2 branch]
The natural local symmetry-compatible reduced symbol is
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]
Its nondegeneracy condition is
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
This is the most general intertwiner between the singlet\(\oplus\)doublet decomposition of worldvolume momenta and the singlet\(\oplus\)doublet decomposition of the traceless fiber sector.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Primitive and commutator channels}

The canonical primitive internal tensor
\[
T(P)=3P-\mathbf 1_3
\]
is too coarse on \(Q_B\), since
\[
T(P_B)\big|_{Q_B}=-\mathbf 1_{Q_B}.
\]
So it does not generate a full Pauli triplet on \(Q_B\).

Next define the commutator channel
\[
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B].
\]
Direct computation gives
\[
\mathcal T_\xi
=
i\theta'(\xi)\bigl(z_Be_1^\dagger-e_1z_B^\dagger\bigr),
\]
so \(\mathcal T_\xi\) exchanges \(\mathbb Cz_B\) and \(\mathbb Ce_1\), while annihilating \(e_2\).
Hence
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi\Pi_Q=0,
\]
but
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\bigl(\mathbf 1_2+\sigma_3\bigr).
\]
Thus the commutator channel naturally provides the longitudinal \(\sigma_3\)-type splitting, but not the full transverse doublet.

\subsection{Class II microscopic ansatz}

We now choose the Class II heavy auxiliary internal vector mediator \(X_i^a\) as the minimal microscopic carrier.

\begin{proposition}[Class II microscopic carrier ansatz]
Assume the microscopic UV sector contains a heavy internal vector mediator \(X_i^a\) carrying one spatial index \(i\) and one internal index \(a\).
Assume its low-energy reduction induces the effective transport action
\[
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{trans}}^{\min}
=
-i\,\eta^\dagger
\Big[
g_c\,\theta'(\xi)\,(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
+
g_E\,\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
g_O\,\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Big]\partial_{y^\mu}\eta.
\]
Then the reduced S2 witnesses are explicitly computable.
\end{proposition}

Using
\[
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\sigma_3,
\]
this becomes
\[
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{trans}}^{\min}
=
-i\,\eta^\dagger
\Big[
\frac{g_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
g_E\,\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
g_O\,\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Big]\partial_{y^\mu}\eta.
\]

Project onto the graded low modes
\[
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi).
\]
Define
\[
I_\theta:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi),
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^3.
\]
For the explicit defect profile,
\[
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
\]

\begin{corollary}[Explicit witness coefficients]
Under the Class II microscopic ansatz,
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
\[
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
\]
Hence the reduced S2 nondegeneracy condition is exactly
\[
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from the projected overlap formula and the explicit evaluations of \(I_\theta\) and \(I_{\theta'^3}\).
\end{proof}

\subsection{Finite witness closure}

\begin{proposition}[Finite witness closure for Class II]
Inside the concrete Class II transport ansatz space, define the explicit seed directions:

\[
N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
:\quad
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)=\frac12\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\]

\[
N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
:\quad
V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\]

\[
N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
:\quad
V^\mu_{(\perp,O)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\]

For
\[
N
=
c_\parallel N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
+
c_E N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
+
c_O N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
\]
the reduced witnesses are exactly
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
\]
Therefore the reduced S2 symbol is nondegenerate if and only if
\[
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_E,c_O)\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Linearity of the projected transport kernel in the seed coefficients.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Honest conclusion}

At the current stage, the logically strongest honest statement is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the reduced graded \(2+2\) Dirac theorem is rigorous;
\item the actual local CP\(^2\) projector-defect geometry is compatible with the natural S2 branch;
\item Class II provides the most natural microscopic carrier for the remaining \((i,a)\)-indexed transport problem;
\item under the concrete Class II ansatz, the entire local Dirac witness problem is reduced to the finite coefficient test
\[
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0);
\]
\item the only remaining open question is whether complete TECT actually generates nonzero reduced Class II couplings \(g_c,g_E,g_O\).
\end{enumerate}

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\textbf{Theorem layer:}
\]
If an isolated graded \(2+2\) infrared sector exists and its projected first-order mixed symbol is nondegenerate, then the reduced principal operator is Dirac type.

\[
\textbf{Local geometry layer:}
\]
For the explicit CP\(^2\) defect background,
\[
P_B=z_Bz_B^\dagger,
\qquad
\partial_\xi z_B=\theta' e_1,
\]
the leading transport kernel is
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\]
and the natural local symmetry-compatible reduced symbol is the S2 form
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]

\[
\textbf{Microscopic ansatz layer:}
\]
Choosing Class II with heavy internal vector mediator \(X_i^a\), the concrete effective transport action is
\[
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{trans}}^{\min}
=
-i\,\eta^\dagger
\Big[
g_c\,\theta'(\xi)\,(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
+
g_E\,\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
g_O\,\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Big]\partial_{y^\mu}\eta.
\]

Its reduced witnesses are
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
\[
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
\]

Therefore the full local S2 nondegeneracy condition is exactly
\[
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

Inside the concrete seed subspace, the witness problem is already exactly closed.

Hence the only remaining open issue is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{does complete microscopic TECT actually generate nonzero reduced Class II couplings }g_c,g_E,g_O\text{ ?}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Generic nonvanishing of the Class II witness triple}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now upgrade the concrete Class II transport ansatz to a finite-dimensional witness theorem showing that the nonvanishing of
\[
g_c,\qquad g_E,\qquad g_O
\]
is generic once the corresponding Class II channels are not identically forbidden on the allowed microscopic tensor space.

\subsubsection{A. Class II preserves the shell-relevant axial tensor structure}

The Class II UV mediator \(X_i^a\) generates the induced enriched tensor
\begin{equation}
\delta N^b_{ij}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^a C^{ab}_{ij}.
\label{eq:CII_deltaN}
\end{equation}
This is already derived explicitly in the Class II construction. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5} :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

Projecting onto the shell-adapted invariant basis,
\begin{equation}
N^3_{ij}=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N^2_{ij}=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\label{eq:CII_ABC_basis}
\end{equation}
the induced correction has the same form, with coefficient shifts
\begin{equation}
\delta A
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^a\hat n_i\hat n_j C^{a3}_{ij},
\label{eq:CII_dA}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\delta B
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{2M_X^2}\,m^a
\bigl(
e_{1j}\hat n_i C^{a1}_{ij}
+
e_{2j}\hat n_i C^{a2}_{ij}
\bigr),
\label{eq:CII_dB}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\delta C
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{2M_X^2}\,m^a
\bigl(
e_{2j}\hat n_i C^{a1}_{ij}
-
e_{1j}\hat n_i C^{a2}_{ij}
\bigr).
\label{eq:CII_dC}
\end{equation}
So Class II does not change the structure of the reduced Weyl/Dirac theorem; it only renormalizes the three axial coefficients. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

\subsubsection{B. Dictionary between the shell coefficients and the local defect witnesses}

In the local defect/projector S2 reduction, we already identified the reduced symbol
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\label{eq:CII_S2_symbol}
\end{equation}
with the concrete Class II transport action giving
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\label{eq:CII_lambda_gc}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
\label{eq:CII_alpha_beta_g}
\end{equation}

The shell-level structure and the defect-level structure are therefore identified by the dictionary
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{eff}} \leftrightarrow g_c,
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}} \leftrightarrow g_E,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}} \leftrightarrow g_O.
\label{eq:CII_dictionary}
\end{equation}
Thus the Class II shell witness triple \((A_{\mathrm{eff}},B_{\mathrm{eff}},C_{\mathrm{eff}})\) is exactly the same finite witness triple as \((g_c,g_E,g_O)\) in the local defect transport formulation.

\subsubsection{C. Finite-dimensional genericity theorem}

Let \(V_{II}\) denote the finite-dimensional real vector space of all symmetry-allowed Class II microscopic tensors surviving the linearization around the chosen background.

The shell-level genericity theorem already states:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the longitudinal coefficient \(v_\parallel\) is a linear functional on \(V\);

\item the transverse intertwiner \(T(N)\) depends linearly on \(N\);

\item therefore \(\det T(N)\) is a polynomial on \(V\);

\item if neither is identically zero, then their simultaneous nonvanishing holds on an open dense full-measure subset.
\end{enumerate}
:contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8} :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9}

Applying this directly to the Class II tensor space \(V_{II}\), we obtain:

\begin{equation}
g_c:N\mapsto g_c(N)
\quad\text{is linear on }V_{II},
\label{eq:CII_gc_linear}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\det T_\perp(N)=g_E(N)^2+g_O(N)^2
\quad\text{is polynomial on }V_{II}.
\label{eq:CII_perp_poly}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact dichotomy is:

\begin{itemize}
\item either \(g_c\equiv 0\) on \(V_{II}\), in which case the longitudinal Class II witness is symmetry-forbidden;

\item or \(g_c\not\equiv 0\), in which case \(g_c(N)\neq 0\) on an open dense full-measure subset of \(V_{II}\);

\item either \(g_E^2+g_O^2\equiv 0\) on \(V_{II}\), in which case the transverse Class II doublet is symmetry-forbidden;

\item or \(g_E^2+g_O^2\not\equiv 0\), in which case \((g_E(N),g_O(N))\neq (0,0)\) on an open dense full-measure subset of \(V_{II}\).
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection{D. Minimal Class II choice supplies explicit seeds}

The minimal Class II choice already written in the manuscript is
\begin{equation}
m^a(P_0)=m\,\delta^{a3},
\label{eq:CII_m_choice}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\label{eq:CII_C33}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C^{31}_{ij}=c_I \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J \hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}=-c_J \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I \hat n_i e_{2j}.
\label{eq:CII_C31_C32}
\end{equation}
Under this choice, the manuscript states that opposite-valley pairing is preserved, \(V(0)=0\), \(\Delta>0\), and mass protection is satisfied. :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10}

Now compare \eqref{eq:CII_C33}--\eqref{eq:CII_C31_C32} with \eqref{eq:CII_dA}--\eqref{eq:CII_dC}. One reads immediately:
\begin{equation}
\delta A \propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
\delta B \propto c_I,
\qquad
\delta C \propto c_J.
\label{eq:CII_deltaABC_c}
\end{equation}
Hence, through the dictionary \eqref{eq:CII_dictionary},
\begin{equation}
g_c \propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E \propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O \propto c_J.
\label{eq:CII_g_cIJ}
\end{equation}

So the minimal Class II choice itself already gives explicit seed directions:

\begin{equation}
c_\parallel\neq 0,\quad c_I=c_J=0
\qquad\Longrightarrow\qquad
g_c\neq 0,
\label{eq:CII_long_seed}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
c_\parallel=0,\quad c_I\neq 0,\quad c_J=0
\qquad\Longrightarrow\qquad
g_E\neq 0,
\label{eq:CII_even_seed}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
c_\parallel=0,\quad c_I=0,\quad c_J\neq 0
\qquad\Longrightarrow\qquad
g_O\neq 0.
\label{eq:CII_odd_seed}
\end{equation}

Thus the witness problem is not merely abstractly reducible: the minimal Class II parameterization already contains explicit longitudinal and transverse seed witnesses.

\subsubsection{E. Class II witness theorem}

We can now state the actual closure theorem for the chosen microscopic carrier.

\begin{theorem}[Class II witness theorem for the local S2 transport ansatz]
Let \(V_{II}\) be the finite-dimensional space of symmetry-allowed Class II microscopic tensors around the chosen TECT defect background.
Assume the reduced local transport coefficients \((g_c,g_E,g_O)\) are read from the induced Class II tensor via the shell/defect dictionary above.

If the minimal Class II parameter space contains:

\begin{enumerate}
\item one admissible longitudinal seed with \(c_\parallel\neq 0\);
\item one admissible transverse seed with \((c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0)\);
\end{enumerate}
then:

\begin{equation}
g_c(N)\neq 0
\label{eq:CII_gc_generic}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
(g_E(N),g_O(N))\neq (0,0)
\label{eq:CII_perp_generic}
\end{equation}
hold simultaneously on an open dense full-measure subset of \(V_{II}\).

Equivalently, the reduced S2 symbol is nondegenerate generically in the allowed Class II tensor space.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The longitudinal statement follows because \(g_c\) is a nonzero linear functional once one seed with \(g_c\neq 0\) exists. Its zero set is then a proper hyperplane. :contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11}

The transverse statement follows because \(g_E^2+g_O^2\) is a nonzero polynomial once one seed with \((g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0)\) exists. Its zero set is then a proper algebraic subset. :contentReference[oaicite:12]{index=12}

Intersecting the two good sets proves the claim.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{F. Strong honest conclusion}

At this point, the status is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{inside the Class II truncation, the finite witness problem is closed.}
}
\label{eq:CII_closed_box}
\end{equation}

What remains open is not witness existence, nor local geometric compatibility, nor finite-dimensional genericity.
The only remaining microscopic question is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{does the true complete TECT action actually realize a nontrivial Class II sector in the physically relevant defect background?}
}
\label{eq:CII_final_open}
\end{equation}

%%%%

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\delta N^b_{ij}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^a C^{ab}_{ij}
\]
is the Class II induced enriched tensor.

After shell-adapted projection,
\[
\delta A \propto m^a\hat n_i\hat n_j C^{a3}_{ij},
\qquad
\delta B \propto m^a(e_{1j}\hat n_i C^{a1}_{ij}+e_{2j}\hat n_i C^{a2}_{ij}),
\qquad
\delta C \propto m^a(e_{2j}\hat n_i C^{a1}_{ij}-e_{1j}\hat n_i C^{a2}_{ij}),
\]
so Class II preserves the exact axial witness structure and only renormalizes the three coefficients. :contentReference[oaicite:13]{index=13}

Using the local defect/projector dictionary,
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}\leftrightarrow g_c,\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}\leftrightarrow g_E,\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}\leftrightarrow g_O.
\]

The minimal Class II choice
\[
m^a(P_0)=m\,\delta^{a3},
\qquad
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\]
\[
C^{31}_{ij}=c_I \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J \hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}=-c_J \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I \hat n_i e_{2j}
\]
already supplies explicit seed directions, and is stated to be compatible with opposite-valley pairing, \(V(0)=0\), \(\Delta>0\), and mass protection. :contentReference[oaicite:14]{index=14}

Hence
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
\]

Since \(g_c\) is linear on the allowed Class II tensor space and \(g_E^2+g_O^2\) is polynomial, finite-dimensional genericity implies:

\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel\not\equiv 0
\ \Longrightarrow\
g_c\neq 0
\text{ generically},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
(c_I,c_J)\not\equiv (0,0)
\ \Longrightarrow\
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0)
\text{ generically}.
}
\]

Therefore:
\[
\boxed{
\text{inside the Class II truncation, the local S2 witness problem is generically closed.}
}
\]

The only remaining open issue is whether the true complete TECT action actually realizes a nontrivial Class II sector in the relevant defect background.
